It includes the positioning of furnaces, handling equipment and auxiliary facilities to improve material flow and energy efficiency.
[C21C 5/54] Processes yielding slags of special composition -- C21C 5/54 covers processes in carbon-steel manufacturing that deliberately produce slags having a defined chemical composition, such as those tailored for specific refining or heat-treatment functions. It relates to the production of plain mild, medium-carbon or cast steel where the slag's makeup is engineered for desired metallurgical effects.
[C21C 5/56] Manufacture of steel by other methods -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Also methods starting from scrap (with/without preheating) not treated in electric (arc) furnaces
[C21C 5/562] starting from scrap -- C21C 5/562 defines methods for producing carbon-steel by using scrap as the primary feedstock, covering the melting, refining and casting operations needed to obtain plain mild steel, medium-carbon steel or cast steel. It falls under the metallurgy hierarchy for processing pig-iron into wrought iron or steel.
[C21C 5/565] Preheating of scrap  apparatus for preheating scrap in general  F27D13/002 -- The CPC entry C21C 5/565 concerns apparatus and methods for preheating scrap metal before it is melted in pig-iron or carbon-steel production, covering general preheating devices used in refining and the manufacture of plain, medium-carbon or cast steel.
[C21C 5/567] operating in a continuous way -- The classification C21C 5/567 covers continuous-process manufacturing of carbon-steel such as plain mild, medium-carbon or cast steel, falling under processing of pig-iron within metallurgy. It pertains to operations performed in a nonstop or flow-through manner rather than batch production.
[C21C 7/00] Treating molten ferrous alloys, e.g. steel, not covered by groups -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Treatments of refining or alloying by means of the treatment agents, the form thereof, purpose or the circumstances.  Metallic, carbonaceous or exothermic treatment agents.  Loose or compacted agents or cored wires.  Treatments in a ladle, under pressure or in a current of streaming metal;  special treatments of the slag.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Treating molten metals during moulding -> B22D - Remelting of ferrous alloys -> C22B
[C21C 7/0006] Adding metallic additives -- C21C 7/0006 covers methods of treating molten ferrous alloys, such as steel, by adding metallic additives that are not specified in other groups. It relates to processes for refining or manufacturing wrought iron or steel where the additive improves composition, properties, or performance of the melt. This entry falls under the metallurgy hierarchy for processing pig-iron.
[C21C 7/0025] Adding carbon material -- This subclass concerns methods of introducing carbonaceous material into molten ferrous alloys during processing, such as steel, to modify composition and properties. It includes techniques for adding carbon sources like coke, graphite or carbon powders directly to the melt, excluding processes covered by other specific groups.
[C21C 7/0037] by injecting powdered material -- The subclass C21C 7/0037 covers processes for treating molten ferrous alloys in which powdered material is injected into the melt, such as during refining, alloying or de-oxygenation, and is not classified elsewhere in the processing of pig-iron hierarchy.
[C21C 7/0043] into the falling stream of molten metal -- C21C 7/0043 covers methods for treating molten ferrous alloys as they flow in a falling stream, such as pouring molten steel onto a moving belt, into a trough or over a cascade. The techniques aim to refine the metal, adjust temperature, remove inclusions or add alloying elements while the metal is in free fall.
[C21C 7/005] using exothermic reaction compositions -- C21C 7/005 covers methods of treating molten ferrous alloys, such as steel, by introducing compositions that undergo an exothermic reaction. The heat generated by the reaction is used to modify the melt's temperature, chemistry or microstructure during processes like refining, deoxidation or temperature control, without falling within more specific sub-groups of the classification.
[C21C 7/0056] using cored wires -- C21C 7/0056 relates to the use of cored wires for treating molten ferrous alloys such as steel, for example during refining, casting or other processing steps. It covers methods where the wire delivers alloying elements, fluxes or other additives directly into the melt.
[C21C 7/0068] by introducing material into a current of streaming metal -- This CPC subclass covers treating molten ferrous alloys by introducing material into a flowing metal stream, such as adding alloying elements, inoculants or other agents while the metal is moving, facilitating refining, deoxidation or property modification.
[C21C 7/0075] Treating in a ladle furnace, e.g. up-/reheating of molten steel within the ladle -- The CPC code C21C 7/0075 relates to the processing of pig-iron within the broader field of chemistry and metallurgy. It specifically covers the treatment of molten ferrous alloys, such as steel, in a ladle furnace, including up-heating or reheating operations performed in the ladle.
[C21C 7/0081] Treating and handling under pressure -- The subclass C21C 7/0081 covers methods and apparatus for treating molten ferrous alloys while they are subjected to pressure, such as pressurised ladle operations, pressure casting or other techniques that manipulate the melt under confined conditions to modify its composition, temperature or solidification behaviour.
[C21C 7/0087] Treatment of slags covering the steel bath, e.g. for separating slag from the molten metal -- C21C 7/0087 covers methods for handling slag that rests on the surface of molten steel, aimed at separating the slag from the metal during processing. It includes techniques such as mechanical removal, slag-covering agents, and bath agitation to improve metal purity and operational efficiency.
[C21C 7/04] Removing impurities by adding a treating agent -- C21C 7/04 covers procedures for removing undesirable elements from molten ferrous alloys by adding a treating agent during refining. The methods are applied to pig-iron, steel or other molten metals to extract impurities such as sulfur, phosphorus or carbon that are not addressed by other specific groups. This falls under the broader category of processing pig-iron and manufacturing wrought-iron or steel.
[C21C 7/06] Deoxidising, e.g. killing -- C21C 7/06 is a CPC subclass within chemistry-metallurgy dealing with the processing of pig-iron and steel. It covers techniques for deoxidising, or "killing," molten ferrous alloys by removing dissolved oxygen during refining.
[C21C 7/064] Dephosphorising -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Including specifically disclosed agents for desulfurising and dephosphorising
[C21C 7/0645] Agents used for dephosphorising or desulfurising -- This subclass covers chemical agents added to molten ferrous alloys, such as steel or pig-iron, to reduce phosphorus or sulfur levels during refining. It includes dephosphorising and desulphurising compounds and mixtures used for treating molten metal not covered by other groups.
[C21C 7/068] Decarburising -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Including stainless steels
[C21C 7/0685] of stainless steel -- C21C 7/0685 refers to methods for treating molten ferrous alloys that are specifically stainless steel. It covers refining, deoxidation, alloying, temperature control and other processes applied to the melt before solidification, excluding steps already covered in related groups. The code classifies inventions related to the production or improvement of stainless-steel quality.
[C21C 7/072] Treatment with gases -- C21C 7/072 covers processes for treating molten ferrous alloys, such as steel, by introducing gases to effect reactions, remove impurities or modify composition. It includes gas-blowing, oxygen-lancing, and similar treatments that are not specified in other groups, and is used for refining, decarburizing, or alloying molten metal during production.
[C21C 7/076] Use of slags or fluxes as treating agents -- C21C 7/076 covers the use of slags or fluxes as treating agents for molten ferrous alloys such as steel, where the treatment method is not captured by more specific groups. It includes processes that modify the composition, cleanliness or properties of the melt by adding these substances during refining, casting or other high-temperature operations.
[C21C 7/10] Handling in a vacuum -- C21C 7/10 covers techniques for manipulating molten ferrous alloys such as steel in a vacuum environment. It includes vacuum-ladles, vacuum transport and pouring operations, and related equipment designed to prevent oxidation and improve metal quality during refining or casting.
[C21D] MODIFYING THE PHYSICAL STRUCTURE OF FERROUS METALS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  General methods or devices for heat treatment, e.g. hardening, annealing, heating, quenching or tempering.  Heat treatment adapted for particular articles, e.g. springs, pipes, drills, rollers or wires; furnaces therefor.  Heat treatment of cast-iron or of ferrous alloys.  Changing the physical properties of ferrous metals by deformation, by deformation combined or followed by heat treatment or by other methods.  Diffusion processes for extraction of non-metals, e.g. decarburising; furnaces therefor.  Process control or regulation for heat treatments.  The term "ferrous alloys" refers to alloys based essentially on iron.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Chemical descaling -> C23 - Cementation by diffusion processes -> C23C - Surface treatment of metallic material -> C23F17/00  **Glossary:** - Alloy: A composition of plural elements at least one of which is a free metal. It also includes material containing any combination of fibres, filaments, whiskers and particles, e.g. carbides, diamond, oxides, borides, nitrides, silicides, or other metal compounds, e.g. oxynitrides or sulfides embedded in a metallic matrix. - Cast iron: Ferrous alloy which solidifies with a eutectic, with a carbon content of 2.1-4 wt%. - Steel: Ferrous alloy with a carbon content of 0.2-2.1wt%. - Air hardening steel: Steel which does not require quenching from a high temperature to harden but which is hardened by cooling in air from above its critical temperature range. - Sub-critical annealing/Stress relief annealing: Heat treatment for relieving or dissipating stresses in weldments, heavily machined parts, castings, forgings by heating them, uniformly heated through, and air cooled/slow cooled with subsequent finishing or heat treatment. - Oil-hardening: Process of hardening a ferrous alloy by heating within or above the transformation range and quenching in oil. - Decarburization: Subjecting the steel to high temperatures and heat treating in a media containing air, oxygen or hydrogen to remove carbon at the surface. - Recrystallization: After all metal crystals have been dissolved by heating enough to lose its structural strength, the metal temperature then falls, allowing the crystals to re-form. - Spheroidizing: Heating the carbon steel to approximately 700 °C for over 30 hours to form spheroidite, to soften higher carbon steels and allow more formability. - Aging or ageing: A process in which the hardness or strength of a metal alloy having a constituent in supersaturated solid solution is increased over time as the constituent precipitates out as a secondary phase containing the constituent. When occurring at room temperature the process is termed "natural aging", while a process that occurs when subjecting the metal alloy to elevated temperature is termed "artificial aging". Aging for a longer time than that corresponding to maximum strength or hardness at the particular temperature is termed "over-ageing". - Hardening: The increase in resistance to deformation. - Precipitation hardening: As the quenched alloy ages, a new material precipitates out of the metallic crystal lattice, filling in abutting spaces, and increasing hardness. - Normalizing: A process of heating metallic material above its critical temperature and cooling in air thereby establishing a fine uniform grain size and improving the microstructural uniformity. - Quenching: The rapid cooling of metallic material either from elevated temperature to room temperature or cooling of metal to sub-ambient temperature, at a specific rate, with a given medium. - Tempering: Heating of a previously quenched or normalized metallic material to an elevated temperature, and then cooling under suitable conditions to obtain the desired mechanical properties. - Martempering: Heat treatment of steel involving austenitisation of steel followed by quenching in heat extracting medium (e.g. salt), at a rate fast enough to avoid the formation of ferrite, pearlite or bainite to a temperature slightly above the martensite start (Ms) point. - Austempering: Isothermal heat treatment applied to steel and cast iron, involves holding the metallic material at the quenching temperature for an extended period of time in order to produce a lower bainite microstructure for steels and a structure of acicular ferrite and high carbon, stabilized austenite known as ausferrite for cast-irons. - Case Hardening: Heat treatment or combination of heat treatments of surface hardening involving a change in the composition of the outer layer of an iron-base alloy in which the surface is made harder by inward diffusion of a gas or liquid followed by appropriate thermal treatment.
[C21D 1/00] General methods or devices for heat treatment, e.g. annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods and devices for heat treatments: annealing, hardening or quenching of ferrous alloys.
[C21D 10/00] Modifying the physical properties by methods other than heat treatment or deformation -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Modifying the physical properties by laser shock processing, ultrasonic treatment and other methods other than heat treatment or deformation.
[C21D 10/005] by laser shock processing -- C21D 10/005 addresses the modification of ferrous metal physical properties by laser shock processing, a technique that uses high-energy laser pulses to generate shock waves that alter surface microstructure, hardness, residual stress and fatigue resistance without employing heat treatment or deformation.
[C21D 1/02] Hardening articles or materials formed by forging or rolling, with no further heating beyond that required for the formation
[C21D 1/04] with simultaneous application of supersonic waves, magnetic or electric fields -- C21D 1/04 pertains to heat-treatment processes for ferrous metals that employ supersonic (ultrasonic) vibrations concurrently with magnetic or electric fields. The simultaneous fields are used to modify the metal's microstructure during operations such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering, improving material properties.
[C21D 1/06] Surface hardening -- C21D 1/06 relates to methods and apparatus for surface hardening of ferrous metals, employing heat-treatment processes such as annealing, quenching, tempering or case hardening to increase hardness at the material's exterior while preserving a tougher core. This subclass falls within the broader fields of chemistry, metallurgy and the modification of ferrous metal structures.
[C21D 1/08] with flames -- C21D 1/08 covers heat-treatment operations on ferrous metals that employ a flame as the heating source, such as flame-hardening, flame-annealing, flame-quenching or flame-tempering. The classification applies to processes where the metal is directly heated by a combustible or fuel-gas flame to alter its microstructure and mechanical properties.
[C21D 1/09] by direct application of electrical or wave energy -- C21D 1/09 covers processes that alter the micro-structure of iron-based alloys by applying electrical energy or electromagnetic waves directly to the material, such as induction heating, resistance heating, laser treatment or ultrasonic irradiation. These methods are used for annealing, hardening, quenching, tempering or other heat-treatment operations without intermediate heating media.
[C21D 1/10] by electric induction -- A method or device for heat treating ferrous metals by electric induction, covering processes such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering that use induced electromagnetic fields to control temperature and microstructure. It falls under the CPC subclass C21D 1/10 within the metallurgy hierarchy.
[C21D 11/00] Process control or regulation for heat treatments -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Control and regulation of heat treatments.
[C21D 11/005] for cooling -- The C21D 11/005 subgroup relates to methods and apparatus for controlling the cooling phase of heat-treatment operations on ferrous metals. It covers techniques, sensors and control systems that regulate cooling rates, temperature gradients and quench conditions to achieve specific microstructures and mechanical properties.
[C21D 1/18] Hardening -- C21D 1/18 pertains to general heat-treatment techniques for ferrous metals that increase hardness, such as annealing, quenching, tempering and related processes, as well as the devices used to perform them. It falls within the metallurgy subclass dealing with physical-structure modification of steel and iron alloys.
[C21D 1/185] from an intercritical temperature -- C21D 1/185 covers heat-treatment steps that begin at an intercritical temperature, i.e., a temperature between the lower and upper transformation ranges of steel where both austenite and ferrite coexist. The classification applies to processes such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering that start from this mixed-phase condition to achieve desired microstructures and mechanical properties in ferrous alloys.
[C21D 1/19] by interrupted quenching -- Interrupted quenching is a heat-treatment technique for ferrous metals where the cooling (quench) is paused or partially reversed to temper the material before it reaches the fully hardened state. This controlled interruption refines the microstructure, balancing hardness with toughness and reducing distortion or cracking.
[C21D 1/20] Isothermal quenching, e.g. bainitic hardening -- C21D 1/20 covers processes that quench ferrous metals at a constant temperature rather than by rapid cooling, notably bainitic hardening. The classification includes techniques where the material is held isothermally to achieve desired microstructures and mechanical properties, falling under general heat-treatment methods such as annealing, hardening, quenching and tempering.
[C21D 1/22] Martempering -- C21D 1/22 Martempering describes a heat-treatment technique for ferrous alloys in which a part is quenched from the austenitizing temperature to a temperature just above the martensite start point, held there to equalize temperature, then cooled to form martensite; this reduces thermal stress, limits distortion and improves mechanical properties. The process is used to obtain a fine microstructure while avoiding the cracking associated with conventional rapid quenching.
[C21D 1/25] Hardening, combined with annealing between 300 degrees Celsius and 600 degrees Celsius, i.e. heat refining ("Vergüten") -- This CPC subclass covers processes that harden ferrous metal while simultaneously annealing it at temperatures between 300 and 600 °C, known as heat refining or Vergüten. It falls under general heat-treatment methods for modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals.
[C21D 1/26] Methods of annealing -- C21D 1/26 covers techniques for annealing ferrous metals, involving heating and controlled cooling to reduce hardness, relieve internal stresses, and improve ductility. The methods may include various heating sources, temperature regimes, and post-treatment steps applied to steel and cast iron.
[C21D 1/28] Normalising -- Normalising is a heat-treatment process for ferrous metals that refines grain structure, relieves internal stresses and improves mechanical properties by heating the material above its critical temperature and then allowing it to cool in still air. The method produces a uniform, fine-grained microstructure, increasing ductility and toughness.
[C21D 1/30] Stress-relieving -- Stress-relieving refers to a heat-treatment step for ferrous metals that reduces internal residual stresses produced during manufacturing or previous heat-treatment operations. The material is heated to a temperature below the transformation range and then held before cooling, allowing the stresses to relax without significantly altering the metal's microstructure. This improves dimensional stability and mechanical performance.
[C21D 1/32] Soft annealing, e.g. spheroidising -- Soft annealing, also called spheroidising, is a heat-treatment process for ferrous alloys that converts cementite into rounded particles, lowering hardness and enhancing ductility and machinability. The metal is held at a sub-critical temperature long enough for carbides to coalesce, then cooled slowly.
[C21D 1/34] Methods of heating -- C21D 1/34 covers general methods and devices for heating ferrous metals, including annealing, hardening, quenching and tempering. It addresses techniques and equipment used to apply heat to modify the physical structure of steel and other iron alloys.
[C21D 1/38] Heating by cathodic discharges -- C21D 1/38 concerns heating ferrous metals by cathodic discharge, where a negatively charged electrode creates a plasma or arc that transfers heat to the metal surface, allowing annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering without direct flame.
[C21D 1/40] Direct resistance heating -- C21D 1/40 pertains to direct resistance heating used to alter the physical structure of ferrous metals during heat-treatment operations such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering. The method passes an electric current through the workpiece itself, generating heat internally for rapid, controllable temperature changes.
[C21D 1/42] Induction heating -- C21D 1/42 classifies inventions that use induction heating to treat ferrous metals, including processes such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering. The entry covers apparatus, control methods and techniques that generate heat by electromagnetic induction to modify the metal's microstructure.
[C21D 1/44] in heat-treatment baths -- This CPC subclass covers the use of bath-type equipment for heat-treating ferrous metals, including annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering carried out in liquid media. It relates to general methods and devices that employ heat-treatment baths to modify the physical structure of steel or other ferrous alloys.
[C21D 1/46] Salt baths -- C21D 1/46 refers to the use of molten salt baths as a medium for heat-treating ferrous metals. It covers methods and apparatus that employ liquid salts to carry out annealing, hardening, quenching, tempering or similar thermal processes on steel and related alloys. This classification groups techniques that provide controlled heating and cooling via the conductive properties of the salt mixture.
[C21D 1/48] Metal baths -- This subclass refers to metal baths employed in heat-treatment operations such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering of ferrous metals, where the workpiece is immersed in a liquid or molten metal to transfer heat. It encompasses apparatus and methods that use metal baths for surface hardening, alloying or other thermal modifications of steel and related alloys.
[C21D 1/50] Oil baths -- C21D 1/50 refers to oil baths used as heating media in heat-treatment processes such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering of ferrous metals. Oil baths provide uniform temperature control and are applied in metallurgical operations to modify the physical structure of steel and cast iron.
[C21D 1/52] with flames -- C21D 1/52 covers heat-treatment processes for ferrous metals that use direct flame as the heating source, such as flame-annealing, flame-hardening, flame-quenching or flame-tempering. It includes methods and devices that employ flames to modify the microstructure and mechanical properties of steel and other iron alloys.
[C21D 1/53] Heating in fluidised beds -- C21D 1/53 relates to heating ferrous metals in fluidised-bed furnaces as part of heat-treatment operations such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering. The technique uses a stream of heated gas to suspend solid particles, creating a uniform, high-efficiency heat environment that transfers energy quickly and evenly to the metal workpiece.
[C21D 1/54] Determining when the hardening temperature has been reached by measurement of magnetic or electrical properties -- This classification covers techniques for detecting when a ferrous metal has reached its hardening temperature by monitoring changes in its magnetic or electrical characteristics, allowing precise control of heat-treatment processes such as annealing, hardening, quenching and tempering.
[C21D 1/55] Hardenability tests, e.g. end-quench tests -- The C21D 1/55 entry covers methods for evaluating the hardenability of ferrous metals, such as end-quench tests that determine how deep a material can be hardened after heat treatment. It is used to assess the effectiveness of annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering processes.
[C21D 1/56] characterised by the quenching agents -- C21D 1/56 covers heat-treatment techniques for ferrous metals where the process is defined by the type of quenching agent employed. It includes methods such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering that use specific liquids, gases or polymeric media to control cooling rates and resulting material properties.
[C21D 1/58] Oils -- C21D 1/58 covers the use of oils as heat-treatment media for ferrous metals, including their formulation, properties and methods of application in processes such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering. It pertains to oils that facilitate temperature control and surface protection during these metallurgical operations.
[C21D 1/60] Aqueous agents -- Aqueous agents are water-based substances used in the heat-treating or surface-modifying of ferrous metals, such as during annealing, hardening, quenching, tempering or related processes. They may include water, steam, lubricating emulsions or other liquid formulations that affect cooling rates, protect against oxidation, or aid in the uniformity of temperature changes. This subclass groups the chemical compositions and applications of these water-based treatments.
[C21D 1/607] Molten salts -- Molten salts are employed as heat-transfer media or reaction environments in heat-treatment processes such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering of ferrous metals, enabling rapid and uniform temperature control. Their high thermal stability and capacity to dissolve metal compounds facilitate efficient modification of the physical structure of steels.
[C21D 1/613] Gases -- C21D 1/613 pertains to the use of gases in heat-treatment operations that alter the physical structure of ferrous metals. It includes methods and devices where gases serve as protective, reactive or quenching media during annealing, hardening, tempering or similar processes, influencing cooling rates and surface chemistry.
[C21D 1/62] Quenching devices -- C21D 1/62 covers devices used to quench ferrous metal workpieces after heat treatment. It includes apparatus for rapid cooling such as spray, immersion or mist systems designed to control cooling rates and prevent distortion. The classification falls under methods for modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals in metallurgy.
[C21D 1/63] for bath quenching -- C21D 1/63 covers techniques that cool heated ferrous alloys by immersing them in a liquid quench bath. It includes apparatus and processes that control the bath composition, temperature and agitation to achieve rapid heat removal for hardening, tempering or annealing. The classification is used for patents describing bath quenching methods and related equipment.
[C21D 1/64] with circulating liquids -- C21D 1/64 covers heat-treatment processes for ferrous metals that employ circulating liquids, such as oil, water or other cooling/heating fluids, to control annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering. The classification applies to devices and methods where the liquid is actively circulated around the workpiece to achieve uniform temperature changes.
[C21D 1/667] for spray quenching -- C21D 1/667 defines spray quenching, a heat-treatment process in which a ferrous workpiece is rapidly cooled by a directed spray of water, oil or other fluid to achieve hardening, tempering or other property changes. The technique is used to modify the physical structure of steels and other iron-based alloys.
[C21D 1/673] for die quenching -- C21D 1/673 covers techniques and apparatus for die quenching, a rapid cooling process applied to steel dies during heat treatment to achieve desired hardness and dimensional stability. It falls under the subclass of modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals, focusing on heat-treatment methods such as annealing, hardening, quenching and tempering.
[C21D 1/68] Temporary coatings or embedding materials applied before or during heat treatment -- C21D 1/68 relates to the use of temporary protective or embedding layers applied to ferrous metal workpieces before or during heat-treatment operations such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering, in order to shield surfaces, control the treatment environment, or maintain shape; the coatings are removed after the heat-treatment process.
[C21D 1/70] while heating or quenching -- C21D 1/70 relates to processes in which heating and quenching are performed in the same operation or in immediate succession, such as applying a rapid cooling medium while the material is still at elevated temperature. It covers equipment or control methods that combine these steps for steel or other ferrous alloys.
[C21D 1/72] during chemical change of surfaces -- C21D 1/72 covers methods or apparatuses for heat-treating ferrous metals-such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering-while a chemical alteration of the surface is occurring, for example during case hardening, carburizing or other surface-chemical processes.
[C21D 1/74] Methods of treatment in inert gas, controlled atmosphere, vacuum or pulverulent material -- C21D 1/74 covers heat-treatment processes for ferrous metals that are carried out in inert gases, controlled atmospheres, vacuum or with pulverulent media. The methods include annealing, hardening, quenching, tempering and related procedures designed to modify the metal's physical structure under these protected environments.
[C21D 1/76] Adjusting the composition of the atmosphere -- The CPC subclass C21D 1/76 covers techniques for adjusting the composition of the gas atmosphere during heat-treatment operations on ferrous metals, such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering. It includes methods of introducing, removing or regulating inert, oxidizing or reducing gases to control surface condition and mechanical properties.
[C21D 1/763] using a catalyst -- C21D 1/763 relates to the use of a catalyst in processes that modify the physical structure of ferrous metals, such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering. It covers methods and devices where a catalyst promotes or accelerates heat-treatment reactions, enhancing efficiency or the resulting material properties.
[C21D 1/767] with forced gas circulation -- C21D 1/767 covers heat-treatment processes for ferrous metals-such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering-where a gas is deliberately circulated or forced through the workpiece or furnace to enhance heat transfer and control temperature gradients.
[C21D 1/773] under reduced pressure or vacuum -- C21D 1/773 covers heat-treatment processes for ferrous metals that are performed under reduced-pressure or vacuum conditions. It includes methods such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering where the low-pressure atmosphere is used to limit oxidation, decarburisation or gas absorption, and the related equipment for maintaining the vacuum during treatment.
[C21D 1/78] Combined heat-treatments not provided for above -- A combined heat-treatment involves applying two or more heat-treatment operations-such as annealing, hardening, quenching, tempering, or similar processes-in a single sequence or simultaneously to obtain a microstructure or property that cannot be achieved by any of the individual treatments alone. This entry covers any such integrated procedures that are not specifically enumerated in the preceding classifications for modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals.
[C21D 1/785] Thermocycling -- C21D 1/785 - Thermocycling covers methods that repeatedly heat and cool ferrous metals to alter their microstructure, improving properties such as hardness and toughness. It is used in heat-treatment processes like annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering to achieve desired mechanical performance.
[C21D 1/82] Descaling by thermal stresses -- C21D 1/82 covers techniques that remove oxide scale or other surface layers from ferrous metals by applying rapid temperature changes that generate thermal stresses, causing the scale to crack and detach. The methods include localized heating, cooling, or combined cycles and can be integrated with annealing or quenching operations.
[C21D 1/84] Controlled slow cooling -- The CPC subclass C21D 1/84 relates to controlled slow cooling of ferrous metals within heat-treatment operations such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering. It defines methods or devices that gradually lower temperature under regulated conditions to adjust the metal's microstructure and mechanical properties.
[C21D 2201/00] Treatment for obtaining particular effects -- The CPC subclass C21D 2201/00 covers methods of treating ferrous metals to produce particular effects, including surface modifications, heat-treatment or other physical-structure alterations that impart desired properties such as increased hardness, corrosion resistance or magnetic behavior. It falls under chemistry → metallurgy → modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals.
[C21D 2201/01] Shape memory effect -- C21D 2201/01 covers processes that induce or exploit the shape memory effect in ferrous alloys, a phenomenon where the material returns to a predetermined shape after deformation when heated. It falls under treatments for modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals in the CPC hierarchy.
[C21D 2201/02] Superplasticity -- Superplasticity is a metallurgical treatment that enhances the ductility of ferrous metals, allowing them to undergo exceptionally large elongations before failure. It involves modifying the physical structure of the metal to achieve specific mechanical effects such as improved formability and strain-rate sensitivity.
[C21D 2201/03] Amorphous or microcrystalline structure -- Methods for producing an amorphous or microcrystalline structure in ferrous metals, typically by rapid cooling, quenching or similar treatments that alter the metal's physical structure to achieve specific mechanical or physical properties.
[C21D 2201/04] Single or very large crystals -- C21D 2201/04 covers processes that produce single-crystal or unusually large-grain structures in ferrous metals, typically by specialized heat-treatment, solid-ification or deformation techniques. The classification is used for methods that modify the metal's physical structure to achieve specific mechanical or magnetic properties.
[C21D 2201/05] Grain orientation -- C21D 2201/05 concerns processes that control or modify the grain orientation in ferrous metals to achieve desired material properties such as strength, ductility, or magnetic behavior. It covers treatments like rolling, annealing, or thermo-mechanical processing that align crystallographic grains in a specific direction. The classification is used for patents involving the manipulation of microstructure to obtain particular effects.
[C21D 2211/00] Microstructure comprising significant phases -- The C21D 2211/00 entry covers patents that describe ferrous-metal microstructures containing one or more distinct, significant phases. It includes methods for identifying, characterising, or engineering these phases to influence material properties, and relates to the broader field of modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals.
[C21D 2211/001] Austenite -- Austenite is the face-centered cubic phase of iron-carbon alloys that forms at elevated temperatures and can retain austenitic structure at room temperature through alloying. It imparts high ductility and toughness, serving as a matrix that can transform into other phases during cooling, and is a key microstructural component in many stainless and high-strength steels.
[C21D 2211/002] Bainite -- Bainite is a tempered microstructure that forms in steel when austenite is cooled at intermediate rates, producing a mixture of ferrite plates and fine carbide precipitates. It yields a balance of high strength and good toughness, making it valuable for wear-resistant and structural components. The classification covers methods for inducing or characterising this phase within ferrous alloys.
[C21D 2211/003] Cementite -- C21D 2211/003 classifies cementite, the iron-carbon carbide Fe₃C, as a distinct microstructural phase in ferrous alloys. It is used to identify and study the presence, distribution, and effects of this hard, brittle constituent on the mechanical properties of steels and cast irons. This entry falls under chemistry → metallurgy → modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals → microstructure comprising significant phases.
[C21D 2211/004] Dispersions -- The CPC subclass C21D 2211/004, titled "Dispersions," covers inventions that create or modify a micro-structure in ferrous metals by introducing a second phase-such as particles, fibers or precipitates-distributed throughout the base metal to improve properties like strength, wear resistance or corrosion behavior. It falls under chemistry-metallurgy fields dealing with physical-structure modifications of iron-based alloys.
[C21D 2211/005] Ferrite -- Ferrite is a microstructural phase of iron-carbon alloys consisting of essentially pure iron with a body-centered cubic crystal structure. In the Cooperative Patent Classification it appears under modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals, denoting a material whose significant phase is ferrite, often targeted for its magnetic and mechanical properties.
[C21D 2211/006] Graphite -- C21D 2211/006 classifies the presence and characteristics of graphite as a distinct phase within the microstructure of ferrous metals. It covers the identification, morphology, distribution and influence of graphite inclusions on the alloy's mechanical and physical properties. This code is used for patents describing how graphite is formed, controlled or modified in steel and cast iron.
[C21D 2211/007] Ledeburite -- Ledeburite is a eutectic microstructure found in high-carbon ferrous alloys, consisting of a lamellar mixture of cementite and austenite that forms on solidification. The C21D 2211/007 subclass covers patents dealing with the identification, formation, or alteration of this phase within metal microstructures.
[C21D 2211/008] Martensite -- Martensite is the hard, needle-like microstructure that forms in ferrous alloys when austenite is rapidly cooled, producing a supersaturated carbon-in-iron solid solution. It is a significant phase in the microstructural classification of modified steel and other iron-based metals.
[C21D 2211/009] Pearlite -- C21D 2211/009 Pearlite describes the lamellar microstructure of steel composed of alternating ferrite and cementite layers, a significant phase combination that determines key mechanical properties. It falls under modifying the physical structure of ferrous-metal alloys, focusing on how this microstructure influences strength, hardness and ductility.
[C21D 2221/00] Treating localised areas of an article -- C21D 2221/00 refers to processes for treating specific, limited regions of a ferrous metal component, such as localized heating, cooling, mechanical working, or chemical treatment, to alter its physical structure without affecting the whole part. The methods are applied to improve properties like hardness, strength, or corrosion resistance in targeted zones.
[C21D 2221/01] End parts (e.g. leading, trailing end) -- The classification covers processes that treat the ends of ferrous metal articles, such as leading or trailing edges, to modify their surface or structure by localized treatment.
[C21D 2221/02] Edge parts -- Edge parts are peripheral elements of a ferrous metal article such as flanges, rims, or edge reinforcements that are produced by locally treating the material to modify its physical structure. The process typically involves shaping, hardening, coating or otherwise altering a confined region of the metal to improve strength, wear resistance or sealing performance.
[C21D 2221/10] Differential treatment of inner with respect to outer regions, e.g. core and periphery, respectively -- The C21D 2221/10 subclass covers methods that treat the interior of a ferrous metal article differently from its exterior, such as applying distinct heat, mechanical, or chemical processes to the core versus the surface. It is used for localized differential treatment aimed at modifying the physical structure of the material in specific regions.
[C21D 2241/00] Treatments in a special environment -- The CPC entry C21D 2241/00 covers processes that treat ferrous metal workpieces in specially controlled environments such as inert atmospheres, vacuum or protective gases to alter their physical structure, for example by influencing hardness, grain size or surface properties during heat-treatment, annealing or similar operations.
[C21D 2241/01] under pressure -- C21D 2241/01 classifies methods of treating ferrous metals under pressure to alter their physical structure, including pressure-assisted heat treatment, forging or deformation processes performed in a pressurized environment.
[C21D 2241/02] Hot isostatic pressing -- Hot isostatic pressing is a heat-treatment process that subjects ferrous metal parts to high temperature and high-pressure inert gas, typically argon, in a sealed chamber. The uniform pressure eliminates internal voids, refines grain structure and improves mechanical properties, making it a key method for densifying and repairing components with complex geometries. It is classified under C21D 2241/02 for modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals in a special environment.
[C21D 2241/03] in zero gravity (e.g. in space) -- It refers to methods or processes for modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals conducted in a zero-gravity environment such as space, encompassing metallurgical treatments performed under weightless conditions.
[C21D 2251/00] Treating composite or clad material -- C21D 2251/00 covers processes for treating composite or clad ferrous metal structures, such as bonding, coating, or heat treatment to improve mechanical or corrosion properties. The methods involve modifying the physical structure of the metal layers in composites or clad products.
[C21D 2251/02] Clad material -- C21D 2251/02 covers the treatment of composite or clad ferrous metal materials, focusing on processes that modify the physical structure of a base metal by bonding it with a different metal layer. It includes methods for producing, joining, or reinforcing such clad products and is situated under the metallurgy branch of the CPC system.
[C21D 2251/04] Welded or brazed overlays -- The C21D 2251/04 class covers processes for creating welded or brazed overlay layers on ferrous substrates. It includes techniques that bond a protective or functional metal coating to a base material by welding or brazing, improving surface hardness, corrosion resistance or wear performance while the underlying metal remains unchanged.
[C21D 2261/00] Machining or cutting being involved -- C21D 2261/00 covers machining or cutting operations that alter the physical structure of ferrous metals, such as steel and cast iron, by removing material, shaping, or forming parts. The classification is used for patents describing processes like turning, milling, drilling or grinding that modify metal form.
[C21D 2281/00] Making use of special physico-chemical means -- The CPC subclass C21D 2281/00 covers processes for altering the physical structure of ferrous metals by applying special physico-chemical means such as electromagnetic fields, ultrasonic energy, plasma, or other non-mechanical treatments that induce changes in grain size, phase distribution or surface characteristics. It is used for techniques that modify metal properties without traditional mechanical working.
[C21D 2281/01] Seed crystals being used -- C21D 2281/01 concerns the introduction of seed crystals into ferrous metals during processing to control grain nucleation and growth, thereby tailoring the material's microstructure and properties. This subclass falls under methods that modify the physical structure of ferrous metals using special physico-chemical means.
[C21D 2281/02] temperature gradient -- The C21D 2281/02 subclass covers the use of temperature gradients as a special physico-chemical means for modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals, such as shaping, hardening or refining grain size through controlled heating or cooling patterns. It falls under metallurgy methods that alter metal microstructure by applying spatial temperature differentials.
[C21D 3/00] Diffusion processes for extraction of non-metals -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Diffusion processes for extraction of non-metals and furnaces thereof.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Local protective coatings -> C21D1/72
[C21D 3/02] Extraction of non-metals -- C21D 3/02 covers methods that use diffusion to separate non-metallic elements from ferrous metals, typically by heating the metal to allow the non-metal to migrate to the surface or into a carrier gas for collection. The processes are applied in steelmaking and metallurgical refining to recover elements such as carbon, sulfur or phosphorus.
[C21D 3/04] Decarburising -- Decarburising is the diffusion-controlled removal of carbon from ferrous metals, usually by exposing the material to an oxidising or inert atmosphere at elevated temperatures. The process reduces carbon content to improve ductility, machinability or to prepare steel for further heat-treatment steps.
[C21D 3/06] Extraction of hydrogen -- C21D 3/06 covers methods for extracting hydrogen from ferrous metal matrices, typically involving diffusion-based techniques that remove hydrogen generated during processing or service. The classification is used for patents describing treatments that mitigate hydrogen-induced embrittlement or recover hydrogen for reuse in metallurgical operations.
[C21D 3/08] Extraction of nitrogen -- C21D 3/08 covers processes that remove nitrogen from ferrous metals by diffusion, typically involving heating in a controlled atmosphere or vacuum to drive the nitrogen out of the steel matrix. The techniques are used to improve mechanical properties and reduce brittleness caused by dissolved nitrogen. This subclass falls under metallurgical methods for modifying the physical structure of iron-based alloys.
[C21D 3/10] Furnaces therefor -- C21D 3/10 covers furnaces designed for diffusion processes that extract non-metallic elements from ferrous metals, facilitating modification of the metal's physical structure. The classification pertains to equipment and methods used in metallurgical treatments where diffusion is employed to remove impurities or alloying elements.
[C21D 5/00] Heat treatments of cast-iron -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Heat treatments of cast iron alloys i.e. ferrous alloy which solidifies with a eutectic, with Carbon 2.1%-4% by weight percent.
[C21D 5/02] improving the malleability of grey cast-iron -- C21D 5/02 concerns heat-treatment methods applied to cast-iron, particularly grey cast-iron, to improve its malleability. It includes processes such as annealing, normalizing or tempering that modify the microstructure, reducing brittleness and enhancing ductility for subsequent forming operations.
[C21D 5/04] of white cast-iron -- The code C21D 5/04 covers heat treatment techniques applied to white cast-iron, a type of cast iron characterized by a hard, cementite-rich microstructure. It includes processes such as annealing, normalising or tempering that transform the brittle white cast-iron into more ductile or wear-resistant forms.
[C21D 5/06] Malleabilising -- C21D 5/06 covers malleabilising techniques for cast-iron, chiefly heat-treatment processes that convert the as-cast, brittle structure into a tougher, more ductile form. It is a subcategory of modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals within the broader metallurgy and chemistry sections.
[C21D 5/08] with oxidation of carbon -- C21D 5/08 covers heat-treatment methods applied to cast-iron in which carbon is oxidised, such as decarburisation or controlled oxidation processes that modify the metal's surface and bulk composition to improve hardness, wear resistance or other mechanical properties. This subclass falls under metallurgy techniques for altering the physical structure of ferrous metals.
[C21D 5/10] in gaseous agents -- C21D 5/10 covers heat-treatment processes for cast-iron that are carried out in a gaseous environment. The gas may serve to remove or introduce elements, control oxidation or provide a protective atmosphere during annealing, normalizing, or similar treatments that alter the metal's physical structure.
[C21D 5/12] in solid agents -- The C21D 5/12 subclass covers heat-treatment methods for cast-iron that employ solid agents such as powders, fragments or inserts to alter the metal's microstructure. Techniques include solid-phase carburising, nitriding, alloying or decarburisation, where the solid material diffuses into the cast-iron surface during the thermal cycle.
[C21D 5/14] Graphitising -- C21D 5/14 - Graphitising refers to a heat-treatment process applied to cast-iron in which the carbon present is transformed into graphite, improving the material's machinability, wear resistance and reducing brittleness. This treatment is classified under modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals in the Cooperative Patent Classification.
[C21D 5/16] Packing agents -- Packing agents are materials placed around or within cast-iron components during heat-treatment processes such as annealing or normalising to control the atmosphere, reduce oxidation, and influence surface hardness or decarburisation. They may be inorganic powders, ceramics, or refractory compounds that pack the furnace chamber and provide a protective barrier.
[C21D 6/00] Heat treatment of ferrous alloys -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Heat treatment of ferrous alloys: iron-based alloys and all types of steels such as low alloy steels, dual-phase steels, tool steels, spring steels, maraging steels, stainless steels, ferritic, austenitic, martensitic, bainitic or pearlitic.  **Glossary:** - Hardening by cooling below 0 degrees Celsius: Controlled cooling below 0° C in order to alter the material microstructure, and enhance its strength and wear properties.
[C21D 6/001] containing Ni  C21D6/004  takes precedence
[C21D 6/002] containing Cr  C21D6/004  takes precedence -- C21D 6/002 refers to heat-treatment methods applied to ferrous alloys that contain chromium as an alloying element. The subclass falls under metallurgy and the modification of the physical structure of ferrous metals. It has been replaced by the more specific subclass C21D 6/004.
[C21D 6/004] containing Cr and Ni -- C21D 6/004 covers heat treatment processes for ferrous alloys that contain chromium and nickel, focusing on methods of modifying their physical structure such as annealing, quenching or tempering. The classification is applied to patents describing treatment of steel alloys with these elements to achieve specific mechanical properties.
[C21D 6/005] containing Mn -- C21D 6/005 relates to heat-treatment methods applied to ferrous alloys that contain manganese. It falls under the subclass for modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals and addresses thermal processes used to develop specific mechanical properties in Mn-alloyed steels.
[C21D 6/007] containing Co -- The C21D 6/007 subclass covers heat-treatment processes applied to ferrous alloys in which cobalt is present as an alloying element. It includes methods such as annealing, quenching, tempering and other thermal cycles designed to alter hardness, strength, grain structure or other physical properties of cobalt-containing steels and cast irons. This entry falls under the broader hierarchy of chemistry → metallurgy → modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals.
[C21D 6/008] containing Si -- C21D 6/008 designates heat-treatment operations performed on ferrous alloys that contain silicon. The code is used for processes such as annealing, quenching, or tempering where silicon is present to modify hardness, strength, or other physical properties of the steel.
[C21D 6/02] Hardening by precipitation -- C21D 6/02 covers precipitation hardening of ferrous alloys, a heat-treatment technique that raises hardness by forming finely dispersed compound particles within the metal matrix during controlled heating and cooling. The subclass includes the procedures, temperature regimes and alloying element selections used to achieve the desired strength and wear-resistance in steel and other iron-based materials.
[C21D 6/04] Hardening by cooling below 0 degrees Celsius -- C21D 6/04 covers heat-treatment processes that harden ferrous alloys by cooling them to sub-zero temperatures, typically through quenching in liquid media such as brine, oil or dry ice. The method increases hardness and strength by promoting rapid martensitic transformation while limiting grain growth.
[C21D 7/00] Modifying the physical properties of iron or steel by deformation -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Cold working and hot working deformation process of iron and steel.
[C21D 7/02] by cold working -- C21D 7/02 covers methods that alter the physical properties of iron or steel through deformation applied at temperatures below the material's recrystallisation point, commonly known as cold working. Techniques include rolling, drawing, forging or bending that produce strain hardening, dimensional changes or improved mechanical performance without heating the metal.
[C21D 7/04] of the surface -- C21D 7/04 covers methods for altering the surface of iron or steel by deformation to change its physical properties. It includes treatments such as rolling, forging, shot peening or surface mechanical attrition that modify hardness, strength or fatigue resistance without adding material. The entry is classified under chemistry - metallurgy - modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals - modifying the physical properties of iron or steel by deformation.
[C21D 7/06] by shot-peening or the like -- C21D 7/06 covers methods for altering the physical properties of iron or steel through deformation techniques such as shot-peening or similar surface-impact processes. It falls within the Cooperative Patent Classification hierarchy under Chemistry → Metallurgy → Modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals, specifically addressing deformation-based property modification.
[C21D 7/08] by burnishing or the like -- C21D 7/08 covers methods of improving the physical properties of iron or steel by deforming the material through burnishing or comparable techniques. These processes involve surface smoothing or compressive work to enhance hardness, strength, or wear resistance without changing composition. It falls within the metallurgy subclass dealing with modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals.
[C21D 7/10] of the whole cross-section, e.g. of concrete reinforcing bars -- C21D 7/10 concerns methods that alter the physical properties of iron or steel by deforming the entire cross-section, for example when shaping concrete reinforcing bars.
[C21D 7/105] of concrete reinforcing bars -- The subclass C21D 7/105 covers methods of deforming iron or steel to alter its physical properties specifically for concrete reinforcing bars, commonly known as rebar. It includes processes such as rolling, drawing, or other cold-working techniques that shape and strengthen the bars before they are embedded in concrete structures.
[C21D 7/12] by expanding tubular bodies -- In the CPC, class C21D 7/12 covers techniques for improving the physical characteristics of iron or steel through deformation that expands tubular components, such as pipes or rods. The entry includes processes like tube expansion, swaging or other methods that enlarge the diameter to alter strength, ductility or other material properties.
[C21D 7/13] by hot working -- The CPC subclass C21D 7/13 addresses methods of hot-working iron or steel to alter their physical properties through deformation. It lies within the hierarchy of chemistry, metallurgy, and modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals.
[C21D 8/00] Modifying the physical properties of ferrous metals or ferrous alloys by deformation combined with, or followed by, heat treatment -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Modifying the physical properties by deformation combined with, or followed by, heat treatment during manufacturing processes of plates or strips, plates or strips for deep drawing, rods or wires, tubular bodies or articles with special electromagnetic properties.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Hardening articles or materials formed by forging or rolling with no further heating beyond that required for the formation -> C21D1/02  **Glossary:** - Hot rolling: Rolling occurs in the austenite region of the phase diagram of the steel (above approximately 900⁰C). - Warm rolling: Rolling occurs in the ferrite region of the phase diagram of the steel (approximately 600⁰C to 800⁰C). - Cold rolling: Rolling occurs below the ferrite region (below 600⁰C).

[C21D 8/0289] Application of a tension-inducing coating -- Group C21D8/0289 is impacted by reclassification into groups C21D8/04 - C21D8/0494 . Groups C21D8/0289 and C21D8/04 - C21D8/0494 should be considered in order to perform a complete search.
[C21D 8/0294] involving a localised treatment -- Group C21D8/0294 is impacted by reclassification into groups C21D8/04 - C21D8/0494 . Groups C21D8/0294 and C21D8/04 - C21D8/0494 should be considered in order to perform a complete search.
[C21D 8/04] to produce plates or strips for drawing, e.g. for deep-drawing -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Modifying the physical properties by deformation combined with, or followed by, heat treatment of ferrous alloys, during manufacturing of plates or strips for deep-drawing.
[C21D 8/041] involving a particular fabrication or treatment of ingot or slab -- The code C21D 8/041 covers methods that modify the physical properties of ferrous metals or alloys by deforming an ingot or slab and then applying heat treatment, or by combining deformation with subsequent heating. It relates to specific fabrication or treatment operations applied to the bulk material to achieve desired structural changes.
[C21D 8/0415] Rapid solidification; Thin strip casting -- Rapid solidification and thin-strip casting are processes that quickly solidify molten steel into thin ribbons or strips, producing a highly refined microstructure and enabling subsequent deformation and heat-treatment to tailor strength, toughness and wear resistance of ferrous alloys.
[C21D 8/0421] characterised by the working steps -- The C21D 8/0421 subclass covers methods that alter the physical properties of ferrous metals or alloys by first deforming the material and then applying heat treatment, with the classification defined by the particular sequence of working steps used during the process.
[C21D 8/0426] Hot rolling -- This CPC subclass covers hot rolling, a deformation process applied to ferrous metals or alloys at elevated temperatures, often combined with or followed by heat treatment to modify their physical structure and properties. It falls under the metallurgy hierarchy for modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals.
[C21D 8/0431] Warm rolling -- Warm rolling is a deformation technique applied to ferrous metals at temperatures above ambient but below the recrystallization range, allowing shape change while limiting excessive grain growth. The process is often combined with or followed by heat treatment to refine microstructure and enhance mechanical properties.
[C21D 8/0436] Cold rolling -- Cold rolling is a deformation process in which ferrous metal sheet or strip is passed repeatedly through a set of rollers at or near room temperature to reduce its thickness. The work-hardening produced is usually relieved by a subsequent heat-treatment such as annealing, giving the material the desired strength and ductility.
[C21D 8/0442] Flattening; Dressing; Flexing -- A CPC subclass for ferrous-metal workpieces that are flattened, dressed or flexed, using deformation that may be combined with or followed by heat treatment to alter physical properties. It addresses processes such as flattening rolls, surface dressing or bending operations applied to steels and other ferrous alloys.
[C21D 8/0447] characterised by the heat treatment -- C21D 8/0447 covers ferrous metals or alloys whose physical properties are altered by deformation followed by or combined with heat treatment. It includes processes such as annealing, quenching, tempering or other thermal cycles applied after rolling, forging, extrusion or similar shaping steps to achieve the desired structural changes.
[C21D 8/0452] with application of tension -- This subclass covers methods that modify the physical properties of ferrous metals or alloys by applying tensile deformation, optionally followed by heat treatment, to achieve the desired structural changes.
[C21D 8/0457] with diffusion of elements, e.g. decarburising, nitriding -- C21D 8/0457 covers processes that modify ferrous metals or alloys by deformation followed by heat-treatment involving diffusion of elements such as carbon removal or nitrogen insertion, e.g. decarburising and nitriding, to change surface or bulk properties.
[C21D 8/0463] following hot rolling -- This subclass deals with processes applied after hot rolling of ferrous metals, where deformation is followed by additional heat treatment to adjust properties such as strength, hardness, or ductility. The methods include annealing, normalizing, quenching, tempering, or similar treatments performed after the hot rolling step. This is used to refine the microstructure and achieve desired mechanical characteristics.
[C21D 8/0468] between cold rolling steps -- C21D 8/0468 covers a method in which a ferrous metal or alloy is cold rolled and then subjected to a further cold-rolling pass before any heat treatment, i.e., successive deformation steps are performed without intervening annealing. This subclass falls under modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals by deformation combined with or followed by heat treatment.
[C21D 8/0473] Final recrystallisation annealing -- This CPC entry C21D 8/0473 titled Final recrystallisation annealing covers the heat-treatment step applied after deformation of ferrous metals or alloys to complete recrystallisation, restore a uniform grain structure and relieve internal stresses. It sits within the hierarchy of chemistry, metallurgy and modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals.

[C21D 8/0484] Application of a separating or insulating coating -- C21D 8/0484 covers the application of a separating or insulating coating to ferrous metals or alloys that have been deformed and heat-treated, aiming to modify surface properties such as corrosion resistance, electrical insulation or wear protection. The coating may be applied by spraying, dipping, electroplating or other methods and serves to isolate the metal from its environment or adjacent parts.
[C21D 8/0489] Application of a tension-inducing coating -- It relates to applying a coating that generates tensile stress in ferrous metals or alloys, typically before or after deformation and subsequent heat treatment to enhance strength, fatigue life, or dimensional stability. The coating acts as a source of internal tension, modifying the metal's microstructure during the heat-affected processes.

It is situated under Chemistry → Metallurgy → Modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals, code C21D 8/0494.

It includes methods such as rolling, forging, or extrusion combined with annealing, normalizing, or quenching to achieve desired microstructural changes.
[C21D 8/1211] Rapid solidification; Thin strip casting -- C21D 8/1211 covers rapid solidification techniques such as thin-strip casting for ferrous alloys, where the melt is cooled at very high rates to create fine-grained structures and altered mechanical properties. These methods are used to modify the metal's physical structure before or after deformation and heat treatment.
[C21D 8/1216] characterised by the working steps -- C21D 8/1216 is a CPC subclass that deals with methods for altering the physical properties of ferrous metals or alloys through deformation combined with, or followed by, heat treatment, where the defining feature of the classification is the particular sequence of working steps employed.
[C21D 8/1222] Hot rolling -- Hot rolling is a thermomechanical process in which ferrous metals or alloys are passed through rollers at temperatures above their recrystallization point, producing a permanent shape change and refining the microstructure. The combined deformation and subsequent cooling adjust hardness, ductility and strength, making the material suitable for further manufacturing steps.
[C21D 8/1227] Warm rolling -- Warm rolling is the deformation of ferrous metals or alloys at temperatures above room-temperature but below the recrystallization range, allowing shape change with reduced forces while preserving certain mechanical properties. The process combines rolling with controlled heating to improve ductility and influence grain structure, thereby modifying the material's physical properties.
[C21D 8/1233] Cold rolling -- C21D 8/1233 Cold rolling deals with the deformation of ferrous metals or alloys by passing them through rollers at ambient temperature to reduce thickness and alter mechanical properties, often followed by heat treatment to further modify micro-structure and improve strength or ductility.
[C21D 8/1238] Flattening; Dressing; Flexing -- C21D 8/1238 covers processes that flatten, dress or flex ferrous metals and alloys, using deformation-often followed by heat treatment-to alter their physical structure and properties such as hardness, strength or ductility. This subclass falls under modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals within the metallurgy and chemistry sections of the Cooperative Patent Classification.
[C21D 8/1244] characterised by the heat treatment -- This subclass covers methods for altering the physical properties of ferrous metals or alloys by first deforming the material and then applying a heat-treatment operation such as annealing, quenching or tempering. The defining feature is that the heat treatment follows the deformation and serves to modify characteristics like hardness, strength or ductility. It applies to steels and other ferrous alloys processed by forging, rolling, extrusion or similar deformation techniques.
[C21D 8/125] with application of tension -- The entry covers processes that modify the physical properties of ferrous metals or alloys by applying tensile forces, usually as part of deformation and subsequent heat treatment. It pertains to methods such as stretching, drawing, or pulling to achieve desired microstructure or mechanical characteristics.
[C21D 8/1255] with diffusion of elements, e.g. decarburising, nitriding -- This subclass C21D 8/1255 covers processes that modify ferrous metals by deformation followed by heat treatment where elements diffuse into the material, such as decarburising or nitriding. [C21D 8/1272] Final recrystallisation annealing -- Final recrystallisation annealing is a post-deformation heat treatment applied to ferrous metals or alloys to complete the recrystallisation process, allowing new strain-free grains to grow and restoring ductility and dimensional stability after working. This step typically follows deformation and earlier annealing stages to refine the microstructure and improve mechanical properties.
