[C22C 2026/001] Fullerenes -- C22C 2026/001 covers inventions related to fullerenes, the closed-cage carbon molecules such as C60 and C70. The classification includes methods for their synthesis, purification, functionalisation and applications in materials, electronics, medicine and energy storage.
[C22C 2026/002] Carbon nanotubes -- C22C 2026/002 pertains to carbon nanotubes, including their synthesis, structural variants such as single-walled and multi-walled forms, functionalisation, and characterization. The subclass also covers methods for processing, assembling, and incorporating nanotubes into composites, devices, and other materials, as well as their specific physical, chemical, and mechanical properties.
[C22C 2026/003] Cubic boron nitrides only -- C22C 2026/003 covers inventions that deal exclusively with cubic boron nitride, a synthetic super-hard material used in cutting tools and abrasives. The subgroup includes methods of producing, processing, shaping or applying cubic BN, as well as articles consisting solely of this compound, without reference to other materials. It is a narrow refinement of the broader C22C class for inorganic synthesis.
[C22C 2026/005] with additional metal compounds being borides -- This CPC subgroup covers metallurgical processes in which borides are introduced as additional metal compounds, typically during the production of titanium, zirconium or other refractory metal alloys, to modify the alloy's structure, hardness or corrosion-resistance. It specifies the use of boride-containing additives in the preparation of metallic alloys or composites.
[C22C 2026/006] with additional metal compounds being carbides -- C22C 2026/006 covers metallurgical processes in which carbide formation is assisted by the addition of other metal compounds that are themselves carbides, such as incorporating silicon carbide, tungsten carbide or similar materials into a reaction mixture to modify composition, structure or properties of the resulting carbide product.
[C22C 2026/007] with additional metal compounds being nitrides -- C22C 2026/007 designates inventions that involve metal compounds specifically in the form of nitrides, where a metal is bonded to nitrogen. The subgroup covers the preparation, processing or use of such metal nitride materials, which are commonly applied as hard coatings, catalysts or semiconductor components.
[C22C 2026/008] with additional metal compounds other than carbides, borides or nitrides -- This CPC subclass covers metallurgical processes in which additional metal compounds are introduced, excluding carbides, borides and nitrides. It includes the use of metal oxides, sulfides, halides, oxysulfides and similar substances as additives, fluxes or catalysts to modify the composition, structure or properties of alloys, powders or coatings.
[C22C 2047/005] Working of filaments or rods into fibre reinforced metal by mechanical deformation -- This CPC subclass (C22C 2047/005) relates to processes that embed filaments or rods into a metal matrix to form fibre-reinforced metal by mechanical deformation such as drawing, rolling, extrusion or similar shaping operations. It covers the working steps that create the composite material, rather than the production of the filaments, rods or the metal itself.
[C22C 2047/205] placing wires inside grooves of a metal layer -- C22C 2047/205 covers processes in which conductive wires are positioned within channels or grooves machined or formed in a metal layer, securing the wires by the surrounding metal and enabling integrated, low-profile interconnections in electronic components.
[C22C 21/00] Alloys based on aluminium -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Aluminium based alloys i.e. with Al as the major constituent i.e. the base of the alloy  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Amorphous alloys -> C22C45/08 - Laminates -> B32B
[C22C 21/003] containing at least 2.6% of one or more of the elements: tin, lead, antimony, bismuth, cadmium, and titanium -- This subclass covers aluminium-based alloys that incorporate a minimum of 2.6 % by weight of one or more of tin, lead, antimony, bismuth, cadmium or titanium. The specification applies to metallurgical compositions where these elements are intentionally added to modify properties such as strength, corrosion resistance, or machinability.
[C22C 21/006] containing Hg -- The CPC subclass C22C 21/006 covers aluminium-based alloys that incorporate mercury as a constituent element. It relates to the metallurgical field, specifically to the composition and properties of aluminium alloys where mercury is intentionally added, often to modify fluidity, wettability or other performance characteristics.
[C22C 21/02] with silicon as the next major constituent -- C22C 21/02 classifies aluminium-based alloys in which silicon is the second most abundant element, covering compositions, preparation methods and characteristic properties of these silicon-containing aluminium alloys. It is used to index patents dealing with the formulation, processing or applications of such alloys, distinguishing them from other aluminium alloy groups where different major constituents predominate.
[C22C 21/04] Modified aluminium-silicon alloys -- The CPC subclass C22C 21/04 covers aluminium-silicon alloys that have been modified by additional elements or treatments to change their properties. It includes alloys where silicon is the principal alloying element and the composition is altered with other metals, additives, heat treatment, or mechanical processing to improve strength, corrosion resistance, or casting characteristics.
[C22C 21/06] with magnesium as the next major constituent -- C22C 21/06 denotes aluminium alloys whose next major constituent is magnesium, defining the composition range and related processing features for these Al-Mg alloy systems within the Cooperative Patent Classification used by the EPO and USPTO.
[C22C 21/08] with silicon -- C22C 21/08 covers aluminium alloys that contain silicon as a principal alloying element. These silicon-aluminium alloys are mainly used in casting to lower melting temperature, improve fluidity and enhance wear resistance.
[C22C 21/10] with zinc as the next major constituent -- C22C 21/10 classifies aluminium alloys in which zinc is the second most important element, covering their composition, metallurgical characteristics and processing methods. The group includes alloy families where zinc contributes significantly to strength, corrosion resistance and heat-treatability, and it is used for aerospace, automotive and structural applications.
[C22C 21/12] with copper as the next major constituent -- C22C 21/12 refers to aluminium-based alloys in which copper is the next major constituent, covering the composition, preparation methods, and characteristic properties of such alloys. It is a subcategory of metallurgy dealing specifically with aluminium alloys where copper plays a primary alloying role.
[C22C 21/14] with silicon -- C22C 21/14 covers aluminium alloys that contain silicon as a principal alloying element. These alloys are used for castings and components requiring good fluidity, low density, and high strength, such as engine blocks and aerospace parts. The classification falls under chemistry - metallurgy - alloys - alloys based on aluminium.
[C22C 21/16] with magnesium -- C22C 21/16 designates aluminum alloys that incorporate magnesium as a principal alloying element. These alloys are engineered to improve strength, corrosion resistance and formability, and are used in automotive, aerospace and structural applications.
[C22C 21/18] with zinc -- C22C 21/18 designates aluminium alloys that contain zinc as an alloying element. These alloys are covered in the Cooperative Patent Classification system used by the EPO and USPTO, falling under the chemistry-metallurgy-alloys hierarchy.
[C22C 22/00] Alloys based on manganese -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Manganese based alloys i.e. with Mn as the major constituent i.e. the base of the alloy  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Amorphous alloys -> C22C45/00 - Laminates -> B32B
[C22C 2200/00] Crystalline structure -- C22C 2200/00 refers to the crystalline structure of alloys, covering the arrangement of atoms in the crystal lattice, phase configurations, grain boundaries and related micro-structural features that determine material properties. It is used to classify inventions dealing with analysis, modification or control of alloy crystal structures in metallurgy.
[C22C 2200/02] Amorphous -- The C22C 2200/02 entry covers amorphous alloys, which are metallic materials that lack a long-range crystalline lattice and instead possess a disordered, glass-like atomic arrangement. This subclass is used to classify inventions related to the composition, production, and properties of such non-crystalline metal alloys.
[C22C 2200/04] Nanocrystalline -- Nanocrystalline refers to materials composed of crystals with grain sizes typically below 100 nanometers, giving them distinctive mechanical, electrical and catalytic properties compared with coarse-grained counterparts. In the CPC alloy section, this subgroup covers the preparation, characterization and applications of such fine-grained metallic and alloy structures, particularly where crystalline arrangements influence performance.
[C22C 2200/06] Quasicrystalline -- Quasicrystalline refers to alloys whose atomic arrangement is ordered yet non-periodic, displaying symmetries forbidden in conventional crystals such as five-fold axes. The class covers the definition, structural characteristics, synthesis methods, and typical properties and uses of these aperiodic crystalline materials.
[C22C 2202/00] Non-ferrous alloys, i.e. alloys based essentially on metals other than iron
[C22C 2202/02] Magnetic -- C22C 2202/02 designates non-ferrous alloys that possess magnetic properties, covering compositions and treatments that give metals such as copper, aluminum, nickel or their combinations a measurable response to magnetic fields. The entry is used for patents involving magnetic behavior in alloys that are not primarily iron-based.
[C22C 2202/04] Hydrogen absorbing -- C22C 2202/04 classifies non-ferrous alloy compositions that are capable of absorbing hydrogen, covering materials designed for hydrogen storage or for use where hydrogen uptake affects performance, such as magnesium-based, aluminium-based or other light-metal alloys whose properties are influenced by hydrogen absorption.
[C22C 2204/00] End product comprising different layers, coatings or parts of cermet -- C22C 2204/00 designates cermet end products that are composed of two or more distinct layers, coatings or separate parts integrated into a single component. The classification applies to items in which a ceramic-metal composite is combined with additional material layers to achieve specific mechanical, thermal or wear-resistant properties. It falls under the hierarchy Chemistry > Metallurgy > Alloys.
[C22C 23/00] Alloys based on magnesium -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Magnesium based alloys i.e. with Mg as the major constituent i.e. the base of the alloy.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Amorphous alloys -> C22C45/005 - Laminates -> B32B
[C22C 23/02] with aluminium as the next major constituent -- C22C 23/02 classifies magnesium alloys in which aluminium is the next major constituent, covering their composition, manufacturing methods and characteristic properties. The subclass is used to catalogue inventions related to lightweight Mg-Al systems employed in aerospace, automotive and other engineering applications.
[C22C 23/04] with zinc or cadmium as the next major constituent -- C22C 23/04 covers magnesium alloys in which zinc or cadmium is the next most abundant element - these materials are developed for lightweight structural use, providing a balance of strength, corrosion resistance and machinability.
[C22C 23/06] with a rare earth metal as the next major constituent -- Magnesium alloys in which a rare-earth metal (such as yttrium, cerium or lanthanum) serves as the second principal component are covered by C22C 23/06. These alloys exploit the combined light weight of magnesium and the strengthening, corrosion-resistant and high-temperature properties imparted by the rare-earth element, making them suitable for aerospace, automotive and electronic applications.
[C22C 24/00] Alloys based on an alkali or an alkaline earth metal -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Alkali or alkaline earth metal based alloys i.e. with Li, Na, K, Rb, Cs, Fr, Ca, Sr, Ba, Ra as the major constituent i.e. the base of the alloy.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Amorphous alloys -> C22C45/00 - Laminates -> B32B
[C22C 25/00] Alloys based on beryllium -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Beryllium based alloys i.e. with Be as the major constituent i.e. the base of the alloy.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Amorphous alloys -> C22C45/06 - Laminates -> B32B

[C22C 27/00] Alloys based on rhenium or a refractory metal not mentioned in groups -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Rhenium or refractory metal based alloys other than Ti-, Zr- based alloys i.e. with Re, V, Cr, Nb, Mo, Hf, Ta, W as the major constituent i.e. the base of the alloy.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Amorphous alloys -> C22C45/00 , C22C45/006 , C22C45/10 - Laminates -> B32B - Magnetic media/MRAM/head laminates -> G11B , G11C
[C22C 27/02] Alloys based on vanadium, niobium, or tantalum -- C22C 27/02 defines alloys whose principal matrix is vanadium, niobium or tantalum, all refractory transition metals, together with other elements to achieve specific mechanical, thermal or corrosion-resistant properties. These compositions fall under the broader category of alloys based on rhenium or other refractory metals not listed elsewhere.
[C22C 27/025] alloys based on vanadium -- C22C 27/025 classifies alloy compositions in which vanadium is the principal constituent, covering binary and multicomponent systems designed for high-temperature strength, corrosion resistance or other specialized properties. The subclass is nested under alloys based on rhenium or other refractory metals not otherwise listed, and relates to the metallurgical characteristics and processing of vanadium-based alloys.
[C22C 27/04] Alloys based on tungsten or molybdenum -- C22C 27/04 relates to alloys whose principal component is tungsten or molybdenum, often combined with other refractory metals. The subclass is applied to patents describing the composition, manufacture, or treatment of these alloys when they are not covered by more specific CPC groups.
[C22C 27/06] Alloys based on chromium -- C22C 27/06 covers alloys whose primary component is chromium, falling under the chemistry-metallurgy-alloys branch for alloys based on rhenium or other refractory metals not listed elsewhere. It specifies compositions and treatments where chromium provides the principal metallic matrix or phase. This classification is used by the EPO and USPTO to index patents on chromium-based alloy inventions.
[C22C 28/00] Alloys based on a metal not provided for in groups -- **Definition:** This place covers:  alloys not otherwise provided for, such as alloys based on Ga, Ge, In, Rare earth metals etc.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Amorphous alloys -> C22C45/00 - Laminates -> B32B - Alloys based on non-metals (such asB, Si, Se, Te-based alloys) -> C01B , C01D , C01G
[C22C 29/00] Alloys based on carbides, oxides, nitrides, borides, or silicides, e.g. cermets, or other metal compounds, e.g. oxynitrides, sulfides -- **Definition:** This place covers:  alloys containing more than 50wt% of carbides, oxides, nitrides, borides, oxynitrides, sulfides etc., i.e. cermets  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Cubic or wurtzitic boron nitrides -> C22C26/00 - Laminates -> B32B - Magnetic media/head laminates -> G11B
[C22C 29/005] comprising a particular metallic binder -- C22C 29/005 in the Cooperative Patent Classification covers alloys that incorporate a specific metallic binder within carbide, oxide, nitride, boride or silicide matrices such as cermets and related metal compounds. It pertains to the formulation and use of a defined binder material to hold the refractory particles together.
[C22C 29/02] based on carbides or carbonitrides -- C22C 29/02 refers to alloys whose principal solid phases are metal carbides or carbonitrides, often combined with metallic matrices to form cermets or related composites used for wear-resistant, high-temperature or cutting-tool applications.
[C22C 29/04] based on carbonitrides -- C22C 29/04 covers alloys whose principal constituent is a metal carbonitride, i.e., compounds containing both carbon and nitrogen bound to a metal. It includes compositions where carbonitrides are used as matrix or reinforcement phases to impart hardness, wear resistance, or high-temperature stability, often in cermet-type materials.
[C22C 29/06] based on carbides, but not containing other metal compounds -- C22C 29/06 classifies metal alloys whose primary constituent is a carbide phase, excluding those that also contain other metal compounds such as oxides, nitrides, borides, silicides or similar. These carbide-based alloys are typically employed for high-temperature strength, wear resistance or cutting-tool applications, and the code separates them from cermets or composite materials that combine carbides with additional metal compounds.
[C22C 29/062] based on B 4 C -- This CPC subclass covers metal alloys whose principal reinforcing phase is boron carbide (B4C), used as hard particles in cermets or metal matrix composites. It includes the compositions, manufacturing methods, and applications where B4C provides wear resistance, high hardness, or thermal stability.
[C22C 29/065] based on SiC -- C22C 29/065 covers alloys that incorporate silicon carbide as a principal component, forming metal-carbide composites such as cermets for high-temperature, wear-resistant or cutting-tool applications. The classification includes formulations where SiC is combined with metals or other compounds to enhance hardness, thermal stability, and corrosion resistance.
[C22C 29/067] comprising a particular metallic binder -- This CPC subclass C22C 29/067 covers alloys that contain a specified metallic binder which holds together carbides, oxides, nitrides, borides, silicides or related metal compounds such as cermets and oxynitrides. It addresses the composition and preparation of such binder-containing alloys.
[C22C 29/08] based on tungsten carbide -- C22C 29/08 designates alloys in which tungsten carbide is the main constituent, typically combined with metallic binders to form hard, wear-resistant materials such as cutting tools and wear parts. The subclass is part of the broader group covering carbides, oxides, nitrides, borides and silicide-based alloys.
[C22C 29/10] based on titanium carbide -- C22C 29/10 pertains to alloys whose principal phase is titanium carbide, encompassing cermets and related metal compounds that incorporate TiC. These materials are employed in cutting tools, wear-resistant parts, and other high-temperature applications where hardness and corrosion resistance are required.
[C22C 29/12] based on oxides -- This subclass covers metal alloys whose primary binding phase is an oxide, including oxide-based cermets, oxynitrides and related compounds. It pertains to the production, composition and use of such oxide-derived alloys within the broader category of carbide, oxide, nitride, boride or silicide alloys.
[C22C 29/14] based on borides -- C22C 29/14 is a CPC subclass for metal alloys whose primary component is a boride, covering materials such as cermets and other compounds where boron combines with metals. It falls under the hierarchy Chemistry → Metallurgy → Alloys → Alloys based on carbides, oxides, nitrides, borides, or silicides.
[C22C 29/16] based on nitrides -- C22C 29/16 covers alloys whose principal component is a metal nitride, including metal-nitride composites and cermets designed for high-temperature, wear-resistant, or hard-coating applications. It falls under Chemistry → Metallurgy → Alloys based on carbides, oxides, nitrides, borides or silicides.
[C22C 29/18] based on silicides -- C22C 29/18 covers metal alloys whose principal constituent is a silicide, including both binary and complex silicide phases used for high-temperature, wear-resistant or hard-coating applications. The classification includes cermet-type materials and any alloy where silicide formation defines the structure or properties.
[C22C 3/00] Removing material from alloys to produce alloys of different constitution -- **Definition:** This place covers:  methods of separation of constituents of alloys such as purification, recovery, removing of undesirable material(s) etc.
[C22C 30/00] Alloys containing less than 50% by weight of each constituent -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Alloys of multiple bases, i.e. with more than one element as major constituents.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Amorphous alloys -> C22C45/00 - Laminates -> B32B - Magnetic media/ head laminates -> G11B
[C22C 30/02] containing copper -- C22C 30/02 covers alloys that contain copper and where each constituent makes up less than 50 % by weight of the total composition. It falls under the hierarchy CHEMISTRY-METALLURGY-ALLOYS-Alloys containing less than 50% by weight of each constituent. The classification is used by the Cooperative Patent Classification system shared by the EPO and USPTO.
[C22C 30/04] containing tin or lead -- C22C 30/04 designates alloys in which no individual component exceeds 50 % by weight and that contain tin or lead. These are covered under the metallurgy subclass for mixed-metal compositions, typically used where the properties of tin or lead-such as low melting point, corrosion resistance, or lubricity-are desired in a multi-element alloy.
[C22C 3/005] Separation of the constituents of alloys -- C22C 3/005 covers methods for separating the individual components of metallic alloys, typically by removing one or more phases to obtain a material with a different composition. Techniques may include mechanical, chemical or electrolytic processes that isolate constituent metals for recycling or re-alloying.
[C22C 30/06] containing zinc -- C22C 30/06 classifies alloys that include zinc as a constituent, where every element in the alloy is present at less than 50 % by weight. It falls under the hierarchy Chemistry → Metallurgy → Alloys → Alloys containing less than 50 % by weight of each constituent, and is used to patent zinc-bearing alloy compositions and related processes.
[C22C 32/00] Non-ferrous alloys containing at least 5% by weight but less than 50% by weight of oxides, carbides, borides, nitrides, silicides or other metal compounds, e.g. oxynitrides, sulfides, whether added as such or formed -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Dispersion hardened alloys with less than 5wt% of dispersed compounds, e.g. ODS aluminium are also classified in this group.

[C22C 32/0015] with only single oxides as main non-metallic constituents -- The code C22C 32/0015 designates non-ferrous alloys that contain between 5 % and 50 % by weight of metal compounds, but where the only non-metallic component is a single oxide. These alloys may include oxides, carbides, borides, nitrides, silicides or other compounds, yet for this subgroup the main non-metallic constituent is limited to one type of oxide.
[C22C 32/0021] Matrix based on noble metals, Cu or alloys thereof -- C22C 32/0021 refers to non-ferrous alloy compositions where the continuous phase, or matrix, is formed primarily of a noble metal, copper, or an alloy of copper, typically containing 5-50% by weight of secondary metal compounds such as oxides, carbides, borides, nitrides or silicides. The classification is used for patents concerning the preparation, structure or use of such matrices.
[C22C 32/0026] Matrix based on Ni, Co, Cr or alloys thereof -- Group C22C32/0026 is impacted by reclassification into groups C22C1/059 and C22C33/0261 . Groups C22C32/0026 , C22C1/059 and C22C33/0261 should be considered in order to perform a complete search.

[C22C 32/0047] with carbides, nitrides, borides or silicides as the main non-metallic constituents -- Groups C22C32/0047 , C22C32/0052 , C22C32/0057 , C22C32/0063 , C22C32/0068 , C22C32/0073 and C22C32/0078 are impacted by reclassification into group C22C1/059 . [C22C 32/0052] only carbides -- It covers non-ferrous alloy compositions in which carbides are the sole added metal compound, present in an amount of at least 5 % but less than 50 % by weight of the alloy. [C22C 32/0057] based on B 4 C -- A non-ferrous alloy in which boron carbide is the primary matrix and which contains from 5 % to less than 50 % by weight of oxides, carbides, borides, nitrides, silicides or similar metal compounds such as oxynitrides or sulfides, either added directly or formed in-situ. [C22C 32/0063] based on SiC -- This CPC subclass covers non-ferrous alloy compositions in which silicon carbide is the primary constituent, with the alloy containing between 5 % and 50 % by weight of SiC or related compounds such as oxides, carbides or nitrides. [C22C 32/0068] only nitrides -- This subclass covers non-ferrous alloys that contain from 5 % to less than 50 % by weight of metal nitrides as the sole type of compound introduced or formed in the alloy, such as nitrides of titanium, aluminium or other metals, without other oxides, carbides, borides, silicides or similar phases.

[C22C 33/00] Ferrous alloys, i.e. alloys based on iron -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods of making ferrous alloys, cast irons, amorphous ferrous alloys not provided in any of C21D , C22B , C21B . Use of master alloys for the production of ferrous alloys.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Powder metallurgy methods -> C22C33/02 , B22F
[C22C 33/003] making amorphous alloys -- The C22C 33/003 subclass covers processes for producing amorphous ferrous alloys, which are iron-based metals that lack a long-range crystalline structure. It includes rapid solidification, melt-spinning and related techniques that yield non-crystalline alloys with unique magnetic, mechanical or corrosion-resistant properties.
[C22C 33/006] compositions used for making ferrous alloys -- The CPC entry C22C 33/006 covers compositions employed in the production of ferrous alloys, that is, iron-based alloy materials. It includes formulations of metallic or non-metallic constituents designed to achieve specific properties in steel and other iron alloys.
[C22C 33/02] by powder metallurgy -- C22C 33/02 classifies ferrous alloys that are manufactured by powder-metallurgy techniques, including processes such as compaction, sintering, hot isostatic pressing and other methods that form solid metal parts from metal powders. It covers iron-based alloy compositions and related treatments aimed at achieving specific mechanical or physical properties.
[C22C 33/0207] Using a mixture of prealloyed powders or a master alloy  mixtures of metal powder in general  B22F1/09
[C22C 33/0214] comprising P or a phosphorus compound -- C22C 33/0214 designates ferrous (iron-based) alloys that contain elemental phosphorus or a phosphorus-containing compound. The inclusion of phosphorus is used to influence the alloy's hardness, strength, wear resistance or corrosion behaviour, and the subclass falls under the metallurgy of ferrous alloys in the CPC system.
[C22C 33/0221] comprising S or a sulfur compound -- The subclass C22C 33/0221 covers ferrous alloys that contain sulfur or a sulfur-containing compound as an alloying element. It includes steels, cast irons and other iron-based materials in which sulfur is added to influence properties such as machinability, strength, or wear resistance.
[C22C 33/0228] comprising other non-metallic compounds or more than 5% of graphite -- C22C 33/0228 refers to ferrous alloys-iron-based alloys-that incorporate additional non-metallic compounds or contain more than five percent graphite. It falls under the hierarchy of Chemistry → Metallurgy → Alloys → Ferrous alloys in the Cooperative Patent Classification used by the EPO and USPTO.
[C22C 33/0235] Starting from compounds, e.g. oxides  manufacture of articles starting from powder comprising reducible metal compounds in general  B22F3/001
[C22C 33/0242] using the impregnating technique  impregnating articles in general  B22F3/26
[C22C 33/025] having an intermetallic of the REM-Fe type which is not magnetic -- The CPC subclass C22C 33/025 relates to ferrous alloys that incorporate an intermetallic compound of a rare-earth metal (REM) and iron, specifically when the resulting material is not magnetic. It is used to classify metalworking or alloy-design inventions where a non-magnetic REM-Fe phase is purposefully introduced.
[C22C 33/0257] characterised by the range of the alloying elements -- C22C 33/0257 is a CPC subclass within the ferrous alloys group that covers patents where the alloy is defined by the range of its alloying elements. It applies to iron-based alloys whose composition is specified by particular proportions of elements such as carbon, nickel, chromium or other additives.
[C22C 33/0261] Matrix based on Fe for ODS steels -- Group C22C33/0261 is incomplete pending reclassification of documents from group C22C32/0026 . Groups C22C32/0026 and C22C33/0261 should be considered in order to perform a complete search.
[C22C 33/0264] the maximum content of each alloying element not exceeding 5% -- The CPC subclass C22C 33/0264 covers ferrous alloys in which no individual alloying element exceeds five percent by weight. It specifies low-alloy compositions of iron-based materials, used to define steels and cast irons with minimal additive levels.
[C22C 33/0271] with only C, Mn, Si, P, S, As as alloying elements, e.g. carbon steel -- C22C 33/0271 designates ferrous alloys that contain only carbon, manganese, silicon, phosphorus, sulfur and arsenic as alloying elements, representing typical carbon-steel compositions. It is situated in the hierarchy chemistry → metallurgy → alloys → ferrous alloys.
[C22C 33/0278] with at least one alloying element having a minimum content above 5% -- This CPC subclass covers ferrous alloys that contain at least one alloying element present in a proportion greater than five percent by weight. It pertains to iron-based materials where the added element significantly influences the alloy's properties such as strength, corrosion resistance or heat resistance. The classification is used for patents concerning the composition and processing of such high-content alloyed steels and cast irons.
[C22C 33/0285] with Cr, Co, or Ni having a minimum content higher than 5% -- The CPC subclass C22C 33/0285 covers ferrous alloys that contain chromium, cobalt or nickel with each of those elements present at a minimum of more than 5 % by weight, focusing on the composition of iron-based alloys rather than specific manufacturing steps.
[C22C 33/0292] with more than 5% preformed carbides, nitrides or borides -- The subclass C22C 33/0292 covers ferrous alloys-iron-based materials-containing more than five percent preformed carbide, nitride or boride particles. It is used to classify high-performance steels and other iron alloys where these hard phases are intentionally added to enhance wear resistance, hardness or strength.
[C22C 33/04] by melting -- C22C 33/04 concerns the production of ferrous alloys by melting. It includes methods where iron-based alloys are formed through the melting of metallic components, such as casting and refining operations carried out in furnaces.
[C22C 33/06] using master alloys -- The subclass C22C 33/06 covers the use of master alloys in the preparation or treatment of ferrous alloys. It includes methods where a pre-alloyed master material is added to a molten iron melt to introduce alloying elements, adjust composition or improve properties.
[C22C 33/08] Making cast-iron alloys -- The entry C22C 33/08 covers processes for producing cast-iron alloys, which are ferrous alloys based on iron with a high carbon content. It includes methods of melting, alloying, and casting that achieve the desired composition, microstructure, and mechanical properties in the final cast product.
[C22C 33/10] including procedures for adding magnesium -- The C22C 33/10 subclass pertains to ferrous alloys-metallic materials based on iron-in which magnesium is incorporated, covering both the resulting alloy compositions and the specific processes used to add magnesium during production. This entry falls under the chemistry-metallurgy-alloys hierarchy of the Cooperative Patent Classification used by the EPO and USPTO.
[C22C 33/12] by fluidised injection -- C22C 33/12 covers the production of ferrous alloys by fluidised injection, where molten metal or alloying components are introduced into a fluidised bed to form the alloy. This method is classified under Chemistry → Metallurgy → Alloys → Ferrous alloys in the CPC system.

[C22C 35/005] based on iron, e.g. ferro-alloys -- C22C 35/005 refers to master alloys for iron or steel based on iron. These are ferro-alloys, used in metallurgy. They are classified under alloys.
[C22C 37/00] Cast-iron alloys -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Cast iron alloy compositions  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Steel alloy compositions -> C22C38/00
[C22C 37/04] containing spheroidal graphite -- This CPC subclass covers cast-iron alloys in which the graphite present is spheroidal rather than flake, typical of ductile or nodular iron. It includes compositions, treatments and manufacturing methods that produce or utilize round graphite particles to improve strength, ductility and machinability.
[C22C 37/06] containing chromium -- C22C 37/06 covers cast-iron alloys that contain chromium as an alloying element. The presence of chromium enhances corrosion resistance, hardness and wear resistance, making these alloys useful for engine components, pumps, and other wear-critical castings.
[C22C 37/08] with nickel -- The C22C 37/08 subclass covers cast-iron alloys that incorporate nickel as an alloying element. Nickel addition enhances corrosion resistance, hardenability and strength, making these alloys suitable for components such as engine parts, valves and wear-resistant castings.
[C22C 37/10] containing aluminium or silicon -- C22C 37/10 covers cast-iron alloys that contain aluminium or silicon as alloying elements. These alloys are employed where enhanced fluidity, corrosion resistance or specific mechanical properties are required, such as in engine blocks, pipe fittings and other cast components.
[C22C 38/00] Ferrous alloys, e.g. steel alloys -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Iron based alloys and all types of steels (low alloy steels, dual-phase steels, tool steels, spring steels, maraging steels, stainless steels, ferritic, austenitic, martensitic, bainitic, pearlitic etc.).  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Cast irons -> C22C37/00 - Amorphous alloys -> C22C45/02 , C22C45/008
[C22C 38/001] containing N -- The CPC subclass C22C 38/001 refers to steel alloys that incorporate nitrogen as an alloying element. It covers compositions, processing methods and resulting properties of ferrous alloys where nitrogen is added to improve strength, hardness or corrosion resistance. This subclass falls under Chemistry → Metallurgy → Alloys → Ferrous alloys, steel alloys.

It falls under CPC subclass C22C 38, which addresses ferrous alloys containing various alloying elements.
[C22C 38/004] Very low carbon steels, i.e. having a carbon content of less than 0,01% -- C22C 38/004 covers very low carbon steels containing less than 0.01% carbon. These ferrous alloys are designed for high ductility and weldability, making them suitable for applications that require excellent formability. The subclass sits within the metallurgy alloys section of the CPC system.
[C22C 38/005] containing rare earths, i.e. Sc, Y, Lanthanides -- C22C 38/005 covers ferrous alloys, such as steel, that are alloyed with rare-earth elements like scandium, yttrium or the lanthanides. These rare-earth additions are used to modify the microstructure, improve strength, corrosion resistance or high-temperature performance, and are disclosed in processes and compositions for producing such enhanced steels.
[C22C 38/007] containing silver -- C22C 38/007 designates ferrous alloys, such as steels, that incorporate silver as an alloying element. The subclass includes compositions, preparation methods and properties of silver-bearing steel alloys, as well as their specific applications where the presence of silver imparts desired characteristics.
[C22C 38/008] containing tin -- The CPC subgroup C22C 38/008 covers ferrous alloys, particularly steel, that incorporate tin as a component of the composition. Inclusion of tin is disclosed for purposes such as improving corrosion resistance, wear resistance or machinability, and the subgroup lies within the hierarchy Chemistry - Metallurgy - Alloys - Ferrous alloys.
[C22C 38/02] containing silicon -- C22C 38/02 covers ferrous alloy compositions that include silicon as a principal constituent. [C22C 45/10] with molybdenum, tungsten, niobium, tantalum, titanium, or zirconium as the major constituent -- C22C 45/10 covers amorphous metal alloys in which molybdenum, tungsten, niobium, tantalum, titanium or zirconium constitute the principal component of the material. The classification falls under chemistry → metallurgy → alloys → amorphous alloys and relates to the composition and preparation of these non-crystalline alloys.
[C22C 47/00] Alloys containing fibres or filaments -- The CPC subclass C22C 47/00 covers metal alloys that incorporate reinforcing fibres or filaments, forming composite materials in which a metallic matrix is strengthened by added fibrous elements. It includes alloys with metallic, ceramic or polymeric fibres used to improve mechanical properties such as strength, stiffness or wear resistance.
[C22C 47/02] Pretreatment of the fibres or filaments -- C22C 47/02 covers processes applied to reinforcement fibres or filaments before they are incorporated into metal-matrix alloys, such as cleaning, surface activation, coating or chemical modification intended to improve adhesion and the performance of the resulting composite.
[C22C 47/025] Aligning or orienting the fibres -- C22C 47/025 covers methods for aligning or orienting reinforcing fibres or filaments within metal alloys, such as during casting, extrusion, rolling, or heat-treatment, to achieve desired directional properties in fibre-reinforced metal composites.
[C22C 47/04] by coating, e.g. with a protective or activated covering -- C22C 47/04 covers methods for applying a protective or functional coating to fiber-reinforced metal alloys, such as adding a barrier layer, corrosion-resistant film or catalytic surface. The coating may be applied by painting, spraying, electrophoretic deposition or other surface-treatment techniques to improve durability, wear resistance or activity.
[C22C 47/06] by forming the fibres or filaments into a preformed structure, e.g. using a temporary binder to form a mat-like element -- C22C 47/06 covers methods for producing metal alloys that incorporate fibers or filaments which are first arranged into a defined shape, such as a mat formed with a temporary binder, before being consolidated into the final composite.
[C22C 47/062] from wires or filaments only -- C22C 47/062 concerns alloys in which the reinforcing component consists exclusively of wires or filaments, detailing the composition, manufacturing and application of such fiber-reinforced metal matrices. It falls under the CPC hierarchy Chemistry - Metallurgy - Alloys - Alloys containing fibres or filaments.
[C22C 47/064] Winding wires -- The CPC subclass C22C 47/064 covers methods and apparatus for winding wires onto a core or form, typically in the manufacture of coils, transformers, or other wire-wound components. It includes techniques for arranging metallic or alloy wires, potentially with fibers, to create uniform winding patterns and maintain tension. This classification falls under alloys containing fibres or filaments in the metallurgical chemistry hierarchy.
[C22C 47/066] Weaving wires -- C22C 47/066 covers methods and apparatus for weaving metal wires, especially when the wires form part of fiber-reinforced or filament-containing alloys. It includes techniques for interlacing wires to produce mesh, fabrics, or reinforced structures used in engineering and textile applications.
[C22C 47/068] Aligning wires -- The C22C 47/068 subclass addresses techniques for positioning or aligning wires within metal alloys that incorporate fibers or filaments, typically to enhance mechanical strength, electrical conductivity, or other functional properties of the composite material. It is part of the hierarchy CHEMISTRY → METALLURGY → ALLOYS → Alloys containing fibres or filaments.
[C22C 47/08] by contacting the fibres or filaments with molten metal, e.g. by infiltrating the fibres or filaments placed in a mould -- This subclass concerns the production of metal alloys that incorporate fibers or filaments by bringing the reinforcing material into direct contact with molten metal. Typical methods involve infiltrating a pre-arranged fiber network placed in a mold so that the metal fills the spaces and solidifies around the fibers, creating a fiber-reinforced metal matrix.
[C22C 47/10] Infiltration in the presence of a reactive atmosphere -- C22C 47/10 covers techniques for infiltrating fibre-reinforced metal alloys in which a reactive gas-such as oxygen, nitrogen, or hydrogen-is present during the infiltration of a molten metal or alloy into the fibre or filament network, affecting wetting, bonding, or resulting in in-situ compound formation within the composite.
[C22C 47/12] Infiltration or casting under mechanical pressure -- A process for producing fibre- or filament-reinforced metal alloys in which the liquid metal is forced into the reinforcement by applying mechanical pressure, such as in pressure die casting, squeeze casting or other high-pressure infiltration methods, to achieve full wetting and densification of the composite.
[C22C 47/14] by powder metallurgy, i.e. by processing mixtures of metal powder and fibres or filaments -- C22C 47/14 designates alloys that contain fibres or filaments and are manufactured by powder-metallurgy, i.e. by mixing metal powder with reinforcing fibres or filaments and then consolidating the blend into a solid alloy.
[C22C 47/16] by thermal spraying of the metal, e.g. plasma spraying
[C22C 47/18] using a preformed structure of fibres or filaments -- C22C 47/18 relates to metallurgical processes for producing alloys that incorporate fibres or filaments, specifically where a pre-formed fibrous structure is used as a template or reinforcement during alloy formation. The classification covers methods that integrate these pre-shaped fiber networks into the metal matrix to achieve composite properties.
[C22C 47/20] by subjecting to pressure and heat an assembly comprising at least one metal layer or sheet and one layer of fibres or filaments -- C22C 47/20 covers processes that form metal-matrix composites by applying pressure and heat to an assembly that includes at least one metal sheet or layer together with a layer of fibres or filaments, thereby bonding the metal and reinforcement into a single structure. This subclass is used for methods that consolidate metal and fiber layers through hot-pressing or similar techniques.
[C22C 49/00] Alloys containing metallic or non-metallic fibres or filaments -- Alloys that incorporate metallic or non-metallic fibres or filaments as reinforcement or functional elements are classified under C22C 49/00. The entry covers composite metal systems where the filament phase is dispersed within a matrix alloy to improve mechanical, thermal or wear properties, and includes methods of producing such fibre-reinforced metal alloys.
[C22C 49/02] characterised by the matrix material -- C22C 49/02 covers alloys that incorporate metallic or non-metallic fibers or filaments and are defined primarily by the nature of the matrix material that binds the reinforcements. It includes compositions where a metal, ceramic or polymer matrix provides the continuous phase in which the fibers are embedded, influencing the alloy's overall properties. This subclass distinguishes such materials from other fiber-reinforced alloys based on the matrix composition rather than the fibers themselves.
[C22C 49/04] Light metals -- C22C 49/04 defines the subclass for light metals within the CPC hierarchy for alloys containing metallic or non-metallic fibres or filaments. It covers compositions, processing and applications of low-density metals such as aluminium, magnesium, titanium and their alloys, especially when combined with reinforcing fibres.
[C22C 49/06] Aluminium
[C22C 49/08] Iron group metals -- The C22C 49/08 entry covers alloys that incorporate metallic or non-metallic fibres or filaments and are based on iron-group metals such as iron, cobalt, nickel and their alloys, defining their composition and structural characteristics for patent classification.
[C22C 49/10] Refractory metals -- C22C 49/10 designates refractory metals, a sub-category of alloys that incorporate metallic or non-metallic fibres or filaments. It covers high-melting-point metals such as tungsten, molybdenum, tantalum, niobium and chromium used in high-temperature or harsh-environment applications.
[C22C 49/11] Titanium -- C22C 49/11 refers to titanium alloys that include metallic or non-metallic fibers or filaments. These composite alloys combine titanium's high strength-to-weight ratio with the reinforcing effect of fibers, improving stiffness, wear resistance or thermal stability for aerospace, medical implants and other high-performance applications.
[C22C 49/12] Intermetallic matrix material -- The CPC subclass C22C 49/12 defines intermetallic matrix materials, which are alloys whose continuous phase consists of an intermetallic compound and that incorporate metallic or non-metallic fibres or filaments. These composites combine the high temperature and strength characteristics of intermetallics with the reinforcement benefits of the fibres, and are employed in applications such as aerospace and high-performance engineering.
[C22C 49/14] characterised by the fibres or filaments -- Alloys in which metallic or non-metallic fibres or filaments are incorporated as a defining feature, forming reinforced metal matrix composites. The classification covers the preparation, composition and properties of such fibre-reinforced alloys, where the presence of the fibres or filaments is the principal characteristic.

[C22F] CHANGING THE PHYSICAL STRUCTURE OF NON-FERROUS METALS AND NON-FERROUS ALLOYS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Changing the physical (metallurgical) structure of non-ferrous metals or alloys by heat treatment or by hot or cold working;  Changing the physical structure of non-ferrous metals or alloys by special physical methods, e.g. treatment with neutrons.  The term "non-ferrous alloys" refers to alloys based essentially on metals other than iron.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Working metallic powder, powder metallurgical apparatus or processes -> B22F , C22C1/04 - Heat treatment, e.g. annealing, quenching, tempering, adapted for particular metallic articles; furnaces therefor -> C21D9/00 - Electrolytic production or refining of metals -> C25C - Single crystals or homogeneous polycrystalline material with defined structure; production thereof -> C30B  **Glossary:** - Alloy: A composition of plural elements at least one of which is a free metal. It also includes material containing any combination of fibres, filaments, whiskers and particles, e.g. carbides, diamond, oxides, borides, nitrides, silicides, or other metal compounds, e.g. oxynitrides or sulfides embedded in a metallic matrix - Recrystallization: After all metal crystals have been dissolved by heating enough to lose its structural strength, the metal temperature then falls, allowing the crystals to re-form - Aging (or ageing): A process in which the hardness or strength of a metal alloy having a constituent in supersaturated solid solution is increased over time as the constituent precipitates out as a secondary phase containing the constituent. When occurring at room temperature the process is termed "natural aging", while a process that occurs when subjecting the metal alloy to elevated temperature is termed "artificial aging". Aging for a longer time than that corresponding to maximum strength or hardness at the particular temperature is termed "over-ageing". - Hardening: The increase in resistance to deformation - Precipitation hardening: As the quenched alloy ages, a new material precipitates out of the metallic crystal lattice, filling in abutting spaces, and increasing hardness - Normalizing: A process of heating metallic material above its critical temperature and cooling in air thereby establishing a fine uniform grain size and improving the microstructural uniformity - Quenching: The rapid cooling of metallic material either from elevated temperature to room temperature or cooling of metal to sub-ambient temperature, at a specific rate, with a given medium. - Tempering: Heating of a previously quenched or normalized metallic material to an elevated temperature, and then cooling under suitable conditions to obtain the desired mechanical properties.
[C22F 1/00] Changing the physical structure of non-ferrous metals or alloys by heat treatment or by hot or cold working -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods of changing the physical structure of non-ferrous metals or alloys by heat treatment or by hot or cold working which are not covered in any of B22F , B21B , B21J , C21D , C25C .  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Methods of making alloys by powder metallurgy -> B22F - Heat treatment, e.g. annealing, quenching, tempering, adapted for particular metallic articles; furnaces therefor -> C21D9/00  **Glossary:** - SMA alloys (shape memory alloys): alloys having the ability when originally shaped at a first temperature and reshaped at a second temperature to undergo a reversible thermoelastic transition and resume its original shape when returned to the first temperature or an intermediate temperature - Quenching: Cooling of metallic material at a specific rate, with a given medium.
[C22F 1/002] by rapid cooling or quenching; cooling agents used therefor -- C22F 1/002 covers methods of changing the physical structure of non-ferrous metals or alloys by rapid cooling or quenching, including the selection and use of cooling agents such as water, oil, gases or other media to achieve the desired heat-treatment effect.
[C22F 1/004] Heat treatment in fluid bed -- This subcategory covers heat-treatment processes in which non-ferrous metals or alloys are heated in a fluidized bed of gas or liquid to modify their microstructure, improve mechanical properties, or relieve stresses. It includes fluid-bed annealing, tempering and case-hardening.
[C22F 1/006] Resulting in heat recoverable alloys with a memory effect -- C22F 1/006 covers methods that produce heat-recoverable non-ferrous alloys exhibiting a shape-memory effect, created by heat treatment or hot and cold working that alter the alloy's physical structure. It falls under the broader category of changing the physical structure of non-ferrous metals and alloys, specifically within metallurgy and chemistry.
[C22F 1/008] Using a protective surface layer -- C22F 1/008 covers processes that apply a protective surface layer to non-ferrous metals or alloys during heat treatment or hot or cold working. The layer is intended to improve corrosion resistance, wear performance or other surface properties while the material's physical structure is being altered. This subclass falls under metallurgy techniques for changing the structure of non-ferrous metals.
[C22F 1/02] in inert or controlled atmosphere or vacuum -- The CPC subclass C22F 1/02 covers processes that modify the physical structure of non-ferrous metals or alloys by heat treatment or deformation while the material is kept in an inert, controlled atmosphere or a vacuum, preventing unwanted reactions with the surrounding gases. This includes annealing, quenching, tempering, or working operations performed under such protective conditions.
[C22F 1/04] of aluminium or alloys based thereon -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods of changing the physical structure of aluminium or aluminium alloys by heat treatment or by hot or cold working which are not covered in any of B22F , B21B , B21J , C21D , C25C .  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Methods of making alloys by powder metallurgy -> B22F - Heat treatment, e.g. annealing, quenching, tempering, adapted for particular metallic articles; furnaces therefor -> C21D9/00 - Making aluminium alloys by powder metallurgy -> C22C1/0408 - C22C1/0416
[C22F 1/043] of alloys with silicon as the next major constituent
[C22F 1/047] of alloys with magnesium as the next major constituent -- C22F 1/047 covers processes that modify the physical structure of non-ferrous alloys whose principal component is a metal other than magnesium and whose next major constituent is magnesium. It includes heat-treatment and hot or cold working techniques applied to such magnesium-containing alloys to achieve desired properties.
[C22F 1/05] of alloys of the Al-Si-Mg type, i.e. containing silicon and magnesium in approximately equal proportions -- C22F 1/05 classifies processes for altering the physical structure of non-ferrous alloys, specifically Al-Si-Mg alloys containing silicon and magnesium in roughly equal amounts, using heat treatment or hot/cold working. The entry falls under the broader category of metallurgy and the sub-group for changing physical structure of non-ferrous metals.
[C22F 1/053] of alloys with zinc as the next major constituent -- C22F 1/053 concerns methods for changing the physical structure of non-ferrous alloys in which zinc is the next major constituent, covering heat-treatment, hot working or cold working techniques that modify grain size, phase distribution or mechanical properties of such zinc-containing alloys.
[C22F 1/057] of alloys with copper as the next major constituent -- This CPC subclass covers methods for altering the physical structure of non-ferrous metal alloys that have copper as the next major constituent, using heat treatment or hot or cold working. It belongs to the metallurgy group dealing with changing the structure of non-ferrous metals and alloys.

[C22F 1/11] of chromium or alloys based thereon -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods of changing the physical structure of chromium or chromium alloys by heat treatment or by hot or cold working which are not covered in any of B22F , B21B , B21J , C21D , C25C .  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Methods of making alloys by powder metallurgy -> B22F - Heat treatment, e.g. annealing, quenching, tempering, adapted for particular metallic articles; furnaces therefor -> C21D9/00 - Making alloys by powder metallurgy -> C22C1/04 , C22C1/045

[C22F 1/14] of noble metals or alloys based thereon -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods of changing the physical structure of noble metals or alloys based thereon by heat treatment or by hot or cold working which are not covered in any of B22F , B21B , B21J , C21D , C25C .  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Methods of making alloys by powder metallurgy -> B22F - Heat treatment, e.g. annealing, quenching, tempering, adapted for particular metallic articles; furnaces therefor -> C21D9/00 - Making alloys by powder metallurgy -> C22C1/04 , C22C1/0466  **Glossary:** - Noble metal based alloys: alloys with the noble metal (Ag, Au, platinum group) as the major constituent i.e. the base of the alloy
[C22F 1/16] of other metals or alloys based thereon -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods of changing the physical structure of other metals or alloys based thereon, i.e. with Zn, Cd, Ti, Zr by heat treatment or by hot or cold working which are not covered in any of B22F , B21B , B21J , C21D , C25C .  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Methods of making alloys by powder metallurgy -> B22F - Heat treatment, e.g. annealing, quenching, tempering, adapted for particular metallic articles; furnaces therefor -> C21D9/00 - Making alloys by powder metallurgy -> C22C1/04
[C22F 1/165] of zinc or cadmium or alloys based thereon -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods of changing the physical structure of zinc or cadmium or alloys based thereon, by heat treatment or by hot or cold working which are not covered in any of B22F , B21B , B21J , C21D , C25C .  .  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Methods of making alloys by powder metallurgy -> B22F - Heat treatment, e.g. annealing, quenching, tempering, adapted for particular metallic articles; furnaces therefor -> C21D9/00 - Making alloys by powder metallurgy -> C22C1/04 , C22C1/0483
[C22F 1/18] High-melting or refractory metals or alloys based thereon -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods of changing the physical structure of refractory metal based alloys other than Ti-, Zr- based alloys i.e. with Re, V, Cr, Nb, Mo, Hf, Ta, W as the major constituent i.e. the base of the alloy, by heat treatment or by hot or cold working which are not covered in any of B22F , B21B , B21J , C21D , C25C .  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Methods of making alloys by powder metallurgy -> B22F - Heat treatment, e.g. annealing, quenching, tempering, adapted for particular metallic articles; furnaces therefor -> C21D9/00 - Making alloys by powder metallurgy -> C22C1/04 , C22C1/045

[C22F 3/00] Changing the physical structure of non-ferrous metals or alloys by special physical methods, e.g. treatment with neutrons -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods of changing the physical structure of non-ferrous metals or alloys by heat treatment or by hot or cold working which are not covered in any of B22F , B21B , B21J , C21D , C25C .  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Methods of making alloys by powder metallurgy -> B22F - Heat treatment, e.g. annealing, quenching, tempering, adapted for particular metallic articles; furnaces therefor -> C21D9/00
[C22F 3/02] by solidifying a melt controlled by supersonic waves or electric or magnetic fields -- C22F 3/02 covers processes for altering the microstructure of non-ferrous metals or alloys by solidifying a molten material while it is subjected to supersonic (ultrasonic) waves or to electric or magnetic fields. These methods use acoustic or electromagnetic energy to influence crystal growth and improve material properties.
[C23] COATING METALLIC MATERIAL -- C23 covers the chemical processes and apparatus for depositing metallic layers onto a substrate, including electroplating, electroless plating, vapor deposition and related treatment methods, as well as the compositions used for coating metallic material.
[C23C] COATING METALLIC MATERIAL -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Hot-dipping or immersion processes and apparatus for applying the coating material in the molten state without affecting the shape.  Coating by spraying, casting, by vacuum evaporation, by sputtering or by ion implantation and the different aspects of chemical coating which includes  Chemical coating by decomposition of either gaseous compounds, liquid or solid compounds, solutions or suspensions of the coating forming compounds, without leaving reaction products of surface material in the coating.  Coating starting from inorganic powder.  Coating with metallic material characterized only by the composition of the metallic material.  Chemical surface treatment of metallic materials, leaving reaction products of surface material in the coating.  All coatings referred to in this subclass are either "for metallic materials" or "by metallic material," with the exception of PVD (by vacuum evaporation, by sputtering or by ion implantation), and CVD (an aspect included in "the different aspects of chemical coating").  Solid state diffusion into metallic material surfaces.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Making metal-coated products by extrusion -> B21C23/22 - Covering with metal by connecting pre-existing layers to articles -> B21D39/00 , B23K - Metallizing of glass -> C03C - Metallizing mortars, concrete, artificial stone, ceramics or natural stone -> C04B41/00 - Enameling of, or applying a vitreous layer to, metals -> C23D - Treating metal surfaces or coating of metals by electrolysis or electrophoresis -> C25D - Single-crystal film growth -> C30B - Metallizing textiles -> D06M11/83 - Decorating textiles by locally metallizing -> D06Q1/04  **Glossary:** - Metallic Material: covers: Metals; Alloys which are metallic composite materials containing a substantial proportion of fibers or other somewhat larger particles; ceramic compositions containing free metal bonded to carbides, diamond, oxides, borides, nitrides or silicides, e.g. cermets, or other metal compounds, e.g. oxynitrides or sulfides, other than as macroscopic reinforcing agents.
[C23C 10/00] Solid state diffusion of only metal elements or silicon into metallic material surfaces -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The diffusion of metal elements or silicon into a metal or metal alloy surface by contact with either a reactive gas, a liquid (e.g. salt or metal melts) or a solid (e.g. powders, pastes).  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Diffusion of non-metal elements other than silicon into a metal or metal alloy surface -> C23C8/00 - Diffusion of at least one non-metal element other than silicon and at least one metal element or silicon into metallic material surfaces -> C23C12/00 - Coating by evaporation, by sputtering or by ion implantation of the coating forming material -> C23C14/00 - Electroless plating -> C23C18/00 - Conversion or passivation coatings obtained by reaction of the metallic surface with a reactive liquid, e.g. chromate, and/or silicate conversion coatings -> C23C22/00 - Conversion coatings obtained by electrolytic surface reaction, e.g. anodisation, chromatising -> C25D11/00 - Process or apparatus specially adapted for the manufacture or treatment of semiconductors devices, e.g. doping of semiconductors -> H10P  **Glossary:** - Ferrous surfaces: Surfaces containing a majority of iron per weight, such as but not limited to steel and cast iron
[C23C 10/02] Pretreatment of the material to be coated -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Pretreatments of the material to be coated, an operation being considered as pre-treatment when it is specially adapted for, but quite distinct from, the coating process concerned and constitutes an independent operation.  For example:
[C23C 10/04] Diffusion into selected surface areas, e.g. using masks -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Masking elements such as casings, shields, fixtures or blocking elements, as well as masking layers or tapes.  Treatments on selected surface areas also not involving masking elements.
[C23C 10/06] using gases -- C23C 10/06 covers methods that employ gases to introduce metal or silicon atoms into the surface of a metallic substrate by solid-state diffusion, forming a coating without melting the substrate. The technique relies on gas-phase transport of the diffusing species.
[C23C 10/08] only one element being diffused -- This CPC subclass concerns processes where a single element, either a metal or silicon, is diffused into a metallic substrate via solid-state diffusion to form a coating. It falls under the broader categories of chemistry and metallic material coatings, with code C23C 10/08.
[C23C 10/10] Chromising -- C23C 10/10 covers the process of chromising, where chromium or silicon atoms are diffused in solid-state into the surface of a metallic workpiece to form a protective coating. The method involves diffusion of only metal elements or silicon into the substrate without the use of a liquid or vapor phase coating. This subclass falls within the broader categories of chemistry and metallic material coating.
[C23C 10/12] of ferrous surfaces -- C23C 10/12 covers solid-state diffusion processes in which metal elements or silicon are introduced into the surfaces of ferrous (iron-based) materials, forming thin diffusion-controlled coatings without melting the substrate. It addresses methods for metallurgically enhancing hardness, wear resistance or corrosion protection of steel parts.
[C23C 10/14] more than one element being diffused in one step -- C23C 10/14 concerns solid-state diffusion processes in which two or more metallic elements or silicon are simultaneously introduced into a metallic surface in a single step, forming a diffusion-based coating on the material.
[C23C 10/16] more than one element being diffused in more than one step -- C23C 10/16 relates to solid-state diffusion processes in which two or more metallic or silicon elements are introduced into a metallic surface, carried out in successive diffusion steps to form a layered or combined coating.
[C23C 10/18] using liquids, e.g. salt baths, liquid suspensions -- C23C 10/18 covers processes that employ liquids-such as salt baths or liquid suspensions-to achieve solid-state diffusion of metal elements or silicon into the surfaces of metallic materials, forming a coating. It falls under the broader categories of chemistry and coating metallic material, specifying the use of liquid media for diffusion-based surface treatment.
[C23C 10/20] only one element being diffused -- C23C 10/20 covers processes in which a single metallic element or silicon is introduced into the surface of a metallic substrate by solid-state diffusion. The classification applies to diffusion treatments that involve only one diffusing species, without additional alloying or co-diffusion.
[C23C 10/22] Metal melt containing the element to be diffused -- This subclass deals with coating processes in which the metal to be deposited is provided as a melt that already includes the element to be diffused. The molten alloy is applied to the substrate and, during solid-state diffusion, the element migrates into the surface, forming a metallurgical coating.
[C23C 10/24] Salt bath containing the element to be diffused -- This CPC subclass covers processes where a molten salt bath containing the element to be diffused is used to introduce that element into a metallic workpiece by solid-state diffusion. The method enables diffusion of metals or silicon into the surface without applying a separate coating, and is applied in coating metallic materials.
[C23C 10/26] more than one element being diffused -- C23C 10/26 covers solid-state diffusion processes in which two or more elements, such as metals or silicon, are simultaneously diffused into the surface of a metallic substrate to form a coating. The classification pertains to methods that create mixed-element surface layers rather than a single-element diffusion.
[C23C 10/28] using solids, e.g. powders, pastes -- C23C 10/28 covers processes that employ solid materials such as powders or pastes to introduce metal elements or silicon into the surface of a metallic substrate by solid-state diffusion, forming a coating without using liquid or gaseous media.
[C23C 10/30] using a layer of powder or paste on the surface -- C23C 10/30 refers to processes that place a layer of powder or paste on a metallic surface and then induce solid-state diffusion of metal elements or silicon into that surface, typically by heating below the melting point. The technique creates alloyed or hardened surface layers without melting the base material.
[C23C 10/32] Chromising -- Chromising is a solid-state diffusion process that introduces chromium, or chromium-containing alloys, into the surface of a metallic substrate, typically steel, to form a hard, corrosion-resistant layer. The method involves high-temperature treatment without melting the base metal, allowing only metal elements or silicon to migrate into the surface. It is classified under C23C 10/32 for coating metallic materials by diffusion of metal elements.
[C23C 10/34] Embedding in a powder mixture, i.e. pack cementation -- This CPC subclass covers pack-cementation processes in which a workpiece is embedded in a powder mixture and heated so that only metal elements or silicon diffuse from the powder into the surface, forming a solid-state metallic coating.
[C23C 10/36] only one element being diffused -- C23C 10/36 concerns solid-state diffusion where a single metal element or silicon is introduced into the surface of a metallic material, altering its composition by diffusion without involving other elements. This process is used for surface modification and coating of metallic substrates.
[C23C 10/38] Chromising -- Chromising is a solid-state diffusion process in which chromium or silicon atoms are driven into the surface of a metallic material, typically steel, to form a hard, corrosion-resistant layer. The treatment involves heating the workpiece in contact with a chromium-bearing source, allowing only metal elements or silicon to diffuse without melting the substrate.
[C23C 10/40] of ferrous surfaces -- The CPC subclass C23C 10/40 covers processes that employ solid-state diffusion of metallic elements or silicon to form a coating on ferrous surfaces, altering the surface composition without melting the substrate. It pertains to metallic material coatings where diffusion is the primary mechanism for creating a protective or functional layer on steel or other iron-based alloys.
[C23C 10/42] in the presence of volatile transport additives, e.g. halogenated substances -- C23C 10/42 covers processes that create metallic coatings by solid-state diffusion of metal elements or silicon into a substrate surface while using volatile transport additives, such as halogenated compounds, to facilitate the diffusion and improve coating uniformity. This subclass falls under coating metallic material in the chemistry sector and specifies the use of these additives to enhance the diffusion-driven coating formation.
[C23C 10/44] Siliconising -- The CPC subclass C23C 10/44, titled Siliconising, relates to solid-state diffusion of silicon, or solely metal elements, into metallic surfaces to create a coating. It is classified under chemistry for coating metallic material and addresses the process of embedding silicon into the substrate by diffusion.
[C23C 10/46] of ferrous surfaces -- C23C 10/46 relates to coating ferrous (iron-based) surfaces by solid-state diffusion of metals or silicon, where the diffusing element penetrates the substrate without melting to form a surface alloy or diffusion layer. The classification includes heat-treatment or other processes that enable the element to migrate and bond to the iron surface.
[C23C 10/48] Aluminising -- C23C 10/48 covers aluminising, a solid-state diffusion process where aluminum, other metals or silicon are introduced into the surface of a metallic substrate to form a protective coating. The method is used to improve the corrosion resistance and wear properties of the base metal.
[C23C 10/50] of ferrous surfaces -- This CPC subclass concerns solid-state diffusion processes that introduce only metal elements or silicon into the surface of ferrous (iron-based) materials to form a coating. It covers methods where the diffusing species are applied without melting, typically by heat treatment or similar techniques.
[C23C 10/52] more than one element being diffused in one step -- This subgroup covers solid-state diffusion processes in which two or more metal elements or silicon are simultaneously introduced into a metallic surface, forming alloyed layers or coatings in a single diffusion step.
[C23C 10/54] Diffusion of at least chromium -- The C23C 10/54 subclass covers solid-state diffusion processes in which chromium atoms migrate into the surface of a metallic material or coating, typically to form a protective or functional layer. It is limited to diffusion of chromium alone (or alongside silicon) without the involvement of other alloying elements. This falls under the broader chemistry category of metallic material coatings.
[C23C 10/56] and at least aluminium -- The C23C 10/56 subclass covers solid-state diffusion processes in which aluminium, alone or together with other metal elements or silicon, penetrates the surface of a metallic substrate. It pertains to methods that introduce these elements into the coating layer to modify surface properties such as hardness, wear resistance, or corrosion protection. This classification is used for patents dealing with diffusion-based metallic coatings.
[C23C 10/58] more than one element being diffused in more than one step -- C23C 10/58 classifies processes in which two or more different elements are introduced into a metallic or silicon surface by solid-state diffusion using more than one diffusion step, creating multi-element alloyed coatings. It covers sequential diffusion treatments that combine several elements to modify the surface composition.
[C23C 10/60] After-treatment -- C23C 10/60 covers after-treatment processes in which only metal elements or silicon diffuse in solid state into the surface of a metallic coating. The treatment modifies the coating's properties-such as hardness, wear resistance or adhesion-through heat-induced interdiffusion without adding other materials.
[C23C 12/00] Solid state diffusion of at least one non-metal element other than silicon and at least one metal element or silicon into metallic material surfaces -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The diffusion of at least one non-metal elements other than silicon and at least one metal element or silicon into a metal or metal alloy surface by contact with either a reactive gas, a liquid (e.g. salt or metal melts) or a solid (e.g. powders, pastes).  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Diffusion of only non-metal elements other than silicon into a metallic surface -> C23C8/00 - Diffusion of only metal elements or silicon into a metallic surface -> C23C10/00 - Coating by evaporation, by sputtering or by ion implantation of the coating forming material -> C23C14/00 - Electroless plating -> C23C18/00 - Conversion or passivation coatings obtained by reaction of the metallic surface with a reactive liquid, e.g. chromate, and/or silicate conversion coatings -> C23C22/00 - Conversion coatings obtained by electrolytic surface reaction, e.g. anodisation, chromatising -> C25D11/00 - Process or apparatus specially adapted for the manufacture or treatment of semiconductors devices, e.g. doping of semiconductors -> H10P
[C23C 12/02] Diffusion in one step -- This CPC subclass C23C 12/02 covers one-step solid-state diffusion processes where at least one non-metal element other than silicon and at least one metal element or silicon are introduced into the surface of a metallic substrate to form a coating. It pertains to coating metallic materials by diffusion without intermediate layers.
[C23C 14/00] Coating by vacuum evaporation, by sputtering or by ion implantation -- **Definition:** This place covers:
[C23C 14/0005] Separation of the coating from the substrate -- C23C 14/0005 covers methods for removing a metallic coating that has been applied to a substrate by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. The classification addresses techniques to separate the deposited layer from the underlying material without damaging either component. It is relevant for recycling, repair or analysis of coated parts.
[C23C 14/001] Coating on a liquid substrate -- C23C 14/001 covers methods for forming a metallic coating on a liquid surface, typically by depositing metal atoms or ions onto a liquid substrate using vacuum-evaporation, sputtering, or ion-implantation techniques. The process creates a thin, continuous metallic film that adheres to the liquid medium for applications such as reflective coatings or functional liquid interfaces.
[C23C 14/0015] characterized by the colour of the layer -- The CPC subclass C23C 14/0015 covers metallic coatings applied by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation where the defining feature of the product is the colour of the deposited layer. It is used to classify inventions whose performance or identification relies on the visual hue of the metallic film.
[C23C 14/0021] Reactive sputtering or evaporation -- The subclass C23C 14/0021 covers coating metallic substrates by vacuum evaporation or sputtering while a reactive gas is present, causing the deposited metal to chemically react during film formation. It includes processes that form oxide, nitride or other compound layers by adjusting the gas atmosphere as the metal is vaporized or sputtered.
[C23C 14/0026] Activation or excitation of reactive gases outside the coating chamber -- The CPC entry C23C 14/0026 covers methods that activate or excite reactive gases before they enter the coating chamber in metallic coating processes such as vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation. It addresses pre-treatment of gases to improve film formation or deposition characteristics on the substrate.
[C23C 14/0031] Bombardment of substrates by reactive ion beams -- C23C 14/0031 covers methods in which a substrate is bombarded with reactive ion beams during vacuum deposition, sputtering or ion implantation to form a coating. The technique uses energetic ions that react with the surface to create metallic or compound layers with tailored composition and structure.
[C23C 14/0036] Reactive sputtering -- Reactive sputtering is a vacuum deposition technique in which a metallic target is bombarded by ions in the presence of a reactive gas, forming a compound or alloy film on the substrate. The process combines physical sputtering with chemical reaction, allowing precise control of composition, thickness and properties of coatings such as nitrides, oxides or carbides. It falls under the CPC subclass for coating metallic material by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation.
[C23C 14/0042] Controlling partial pressure or flow rate of reactive or inert gases with feedback of measurements -- C23C 14/0042 covers the regulation of the partial pressure or flow rate of reactive or inert gases during metallic coating processes such as vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation, using real-time measurement feedback to adjust gas supply and maintain desired film properties. This subclass falls under the broader category of coating metallic material in the Chemistry CPC scheme.
[C23C 14/0047] Activation or excitation of reactive gases outside the coating chamber -- C23C 14/0047 covers methods that energise or activate reactive gases before they enter a vacuum-deposition chamber, such as by plasma-generation, electric discharge or heating, to enhance film formation during coating by evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. These preparatory gas-activation steps are performed outside the coating chamber to modify the chemical reactivity of the gases used in metallic coating processes.
