[C23C 14/0052] Bombardment of substrates by reactive ion beams -- The CPC subclass C23C 14/0052 covers processes where a substrate is struck with reactive ion beams to form or modify a coating, typically in vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation operations on metallic surfaces. It is used to create chemically active layers or to incorporate elements into the coating.
[C23C 14/0057] using reactive gases other than O 2 , H 2 O, N 2 , NH 3  or CH 4 -- C23C 14/0057 covers processes for coating metallic substrates by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation that employ reactive gases not limited to oxygen, water, nitrogen, ammonia or methane, allowing alternative chemical reactions during film formation. This subclass falls within the chemistry domain under coating metallic material techniques.
[C23C 14/0063] characterised by means for introducing or removing gases -- C23C 14/0063 covers metallic coating processes by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation that incorporate methods for introducing or removing gases during deposition. It includes techniques that control the gas atmosphere to influence film composition, thickness or adhesion, such as gas-injection, pumping or venting steps.
[C23C 14/0068] characterised by means for confinement of gases or sputtered material, e.g. screens, baffles -- C23C 14/0068 classifies metallic coating processes performed by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation that employ devices to confine gases or the sputtered material, such as screens or baffles. These confinement means help control deposition and improve coating uniformity.
[C23C 14/0073] by exposing the substrates to reactive gases intermittently -- This CPC subclass relates to coating metallic substrates by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation where the workpiece is periodically exposed to reactive gases, allowing the formation of compound or alloy layers on the surface. The intermittent gas exposure controls the chemistry of the deposited film and is used to tailor properties such as hardness, corrosion resistance or conductivity.
[C23C 14/0078] by moving the substrates between spatially separate sputtering and reaction stations -- The subclass covers metallic coatings formed by sputtering in which the workpiece is transferred from a sputtering zone to a separate reaction station for further processing, such as post-sputtering chemical treatment or ion implantation. It applies to vacuum-evaporation or sputtering methods that involve moving the substrate between distinct spatial stations during coating.
[C23C 14/0084] Producing gradient compositions -- The code C23C 14/0084 covers methods for producing metallic coatings whose composition varies gradually across the layer, such as gradient alloys created by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation techniques. It addresses the design and control of compositional profiles in coated metal parts.
[C23C 14/0089] in metallic mode -- C23C 14/0089 covers the deposition of metallic coatings where the coating material is introduced in a metallic form, such as a metal vapor or ion, onto a substrate by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. It applies to processes that retain the metallic nature of the deposited layer throughout the coating operation.
[C23C 14/0094] in transition mode -- The C23C 14/0094 subclass covers metallic coatings applied by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation while the substrate is in a transition mode, meaning its temperature, phase or other condition is changing during deposition; it addresses the control of coating processes under such non-steady-state conditions.
[C23C 14/02] Pretreatment of the material to be coated
[C23C 14/021] Cleaning or etching treatments -- C23C 14/021 covers cleaning or etching processes applied to metallic coatings that have been deposited by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering, or ion-implantation methods. The classification includes chemical, plasma or physical treatments used to remove contaminants, oxides or surface irregularities before further processing or to modify surface properties. It is a subcategory of coating metallic material within the broader chemistry field.
[C23C 14/022] by means of bombardment with energetic particles or radiation -- C23C 14/022 covers coating metallic materials by means of bombardment with energetic particles or radiation, such as vacuum evaporation, sputtering, or ion implantation. This subclass falls under the broader categories of chemistry and metallic material coatings in the Cooperative Patent Classification system used by the EPO and USPTO.
[C23C 14/024] Deposition of sublayers, e.g. to promote adhesion of the coating  C23C14/027  takes precedence
[C23C 14/025] Metallic sublayers -- C23C 14/025 pertains to metallic sublayers employed in coating processes such as vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. It covers the deposition of intermediate metal films that serve to enhance adhesion, corrosion resistance or other functional properties of the final coating.
[C23C 14/027] Graded interfaces -- Graded interfaces are transitional layers in metallic coatings where the composition, structure or mechanical properties change continuously from the substrate to the surface. They are produced by adjusting parameters during vacuum-based deposition methods such as sputtering, evaporation or ion implantation, creating a smooth gradient that improves adhesion, reduces stress and tailors functional performance. This concept falls under CPC code C23C 14/027 for coatings of metallic material applied by vacuum techniques.
[C23C 14/028] Physical treatment to alter the texture of the substrate surface, e.g. grinding, polishing -- C23C 14/028 covers physical processes such as grinding, polishing or other mechanical treatments used to modify the surface texture of a metallic substrate, often before or after coating operations like vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. The focus is on altering the substrate's topography to improve adhesion, finish or functional properties of the subsequent metallic coating.
[C23C 14/04] Coating on selected surface areas, e.g. using masks -- C23C 14/04 covers techniques for depositing metallic coatings only on designated portions of a substrate, typically by using masks, patterned shields or similar means to protect other areas during vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation processes, enabling selective surface treatment.
[C23C 14/042] using masks -- C23C 14/042 refers to the use of masks in metallic coating processes performed by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. It covers techniques where a physical or patterned mask shields portions of the substrate to achieve selective deposition or patterned coatings on metallic surfaces.
[C23C 14/044] using masks to redistribute rather than totally prevent coating, e.g. producing thickness gradient
[C23C 14/046] Coating cavities or hollow spaces, e.g. interior of tubes; Infiltration of porous substrates -- This CPC subclass covers methods for depositing metallic coatings onto the interior surfaces of cavities, tubes or other hollow spaces and for infiltrating porous substrates with metal, typically using vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation techniques.
[C23C 14/048] using irradiation by energy or particles -- C23C 14/048 covers the use of energetic radiation or particle beams to deposit or modify metallic coatings, including methods such as electron-beam evaporation, ion-beam sputtering, laser or plasma assisted deposition, and ion implantation. The subclass addresses processes where irradiation provides the energy for coating formation on a substrate.
[C23C 14/06] characterised by the coating material -- C23C 14/06 covers metallic coating processes where the primary distinguishing feature is the material that is deposited, independent of the specific vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation technique used. The subclass is applied when the coating's composition, such as a particular metal or alloy, defines the patent subject matter.
[C23C 14/0605] Carbon -- C23C 14/0605 covers the application of carbon as a coating on metallic substrates using vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation processes. It falls under the chemistry category for metallic coating materials, focusing on thin-film carbon layers formed by these physical deposition methods.
[C23C 14/0611] Diamond -- Diamond coatings applied to metal surfaces via vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation provide extreme hardness, wear resistance and thermal conductivity while maintaining chemical inertness, making them suitable for cutting tools, wear-protected components and heat-spread applications.
[C23C 14/0617] AIII BV compounds, where A is Al, Ga, In or Tl and B is N, P, As, Sb or Bi -- The subclass C23C 14/0617 relates to metallic coatings produced by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation that use group-III-V compounds. It specifically covers compounds where the group-III element is aluminium, gallium, indium or thallium and the group-V element is nitrogen, phosphorus, arsenic, antimony or bismuth.
[C23C 14/0623] Sulfides, selenides or tellurides -- The CPC subclass C23C 14/0623 covers the use of sulfide, selenide or telluride compounds as metallic coatings applied by vacuum-based processes such as evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. These techniques produce thin films for protective, decorative or functional purposes, commonly in electronics, optics or related fields.
[C23C 14/0629] of zinc, cadmium or mercury -- C23C 14/0629 designates the use of zinc, cadmium or mercury as coating materials applied by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation processes. It is part of the Chemistry section, under metallic material coatings, and addresses thin-film deposition of these specific metals.
[C23C 14/0635] Carbides -- C23C 14/0635 designates the use of carbide compounds as protective coatings on metallic substrates applied by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation. It covers the deposition of carbide layers to improve hardness, wear resistance and corrosion protection.
[C23C 14/0641] Nitrides  C23C14/0617  takes precedence -- C23C 14/0641 covers the formation of nitride compounds as metallic coatings that are deposited by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation techniques. It falls under the chemistry category for metallic material coatings and is specific to nitride-type layers, with the broader subclass C23C 14/0617 taking precedence over it.
[C23C 14/0647] Boron nitride -- The CPC entry C23C 14/0647 covers the use of boron nitride as a protective or functional coating applied to metallic substrates by vacuum-based techniques such as evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation. It falls under the broader category of metallic material coatings within the chemistry field.
[C23C 14/0652] Silicon nitride -- C23C 14/0652 covers the deposition of silicon nitride films onto metallic substrates by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation processes. It relates to methods for forming protective or functional silicon nitride coatings on metals, typically used to enhance wear resistance, thermal stability or electrical properties.
[C23C 14/0658] Carbon nitride -- C23C 14/0658 covers carbon-nitride layers applied as metallic coatings by physical vapor deposition techniques such as vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. It pertains to the formation, composition and properties of carbon-nitride films used to modify surface hardness, wear resistance or optical characteristics.
[C23C 14/0664] Carbonitrides -- C23C 14/0664 pertains to carbonitride compounds, especially metal carbonitrides, employed as protective or functional coatings. It addresses the composition, preparation and properties of these films when applied by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation, covering uses such as hardness enhancement, corrosion resistance or optical modification.
[C23C 14/067] Borides -- C23C 14/067 covers the formation of boride coatings on metals using vacuum-deposition techniques such as evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. These boride layers provide hard, wear-resistant surfaces for applications like cutting tools, hard-facing and protective finishes on metallic components.
[C23C 14/0676] Oxynitrides -- Oxynitrides are metal-based compounds containing oxygen and nitrogen that form hard, corrosion-resistant coatings applied through vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation techniques. The classification covers processes and compositions where these mixed-anion layers are deposited to improve surface durability, wear resistance and thermal stability of metallic substrates.
[C23C 14/0682] Silicides -- C23C 14/0682 covers the formation of silicide layers on metallic substrates using vacuum-based techniques such as evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. The classification applies to processes that create a silicide coating to modify surface properties like hardness, corrosion resistance or electrical conductivity. It is part of the broader group dealing with metallic material coatings applied by vacuum deposition methods.
[C23C 14/0688] Cermets, e.g. mixtures of metal and one or more of carbides, nitrides, oxides or borides -- The CPC subclass C23C 14/0688 covers cermets-composite materials formed from a metal matrix combined with one or more carbides, nitrides, oxides or borides-used as metallic coatings applied by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation techniques.
[C23C 14/0694] Halides -- The CPC subclass C23C 14/0694 covers the use of halide compounds-such as metal chlorides, bromides or iodides-as source materials for metallic coatings produced by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation processes. It pertains to metallic coating applications where the halide serves either as the evaporant, target material or as an additive to modify the deposited film's composition or properties.
[C23C 14/08] Oxides -- C23C 14/08 relates to the deposition of oxide layers on metallic substrates by vacuum-based techniques such as evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation, forming protective or functional coatings. It falls under the broader chemistry category of coating metallic material, specifically addressing oxide coatings applied through these high-vacuum processes.
[C23C 14/081] of aluminium, magnesium or beryllium -- C23C 14/081 covers methods for applying metallic coatings by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation specifically to aluminium, magnesium or beryllium substrates, falling under the broader chemistry category of coating metallic materials. This entry defines the technical features of such thin-film processes for those three metals.
[C23C 14/082] of alkaline earth metals
[C23C 14/083] of refractory metals or yttrium -- This CPC subclass covers methods of applying a coating to metallic substrates by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation when the coating material is a refractory metal or yttrium, falling under the broader categories of chemistry and metallic material coatings.
[C23C 14/085] of iron group metals -- C23C 14/085 covers processes that apply coatings of iron-group metals-such as iron, cobalt or nickel-by vacuum-based methods including evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. The classification is used for patents describing how these metallic layers are deposited onto a substrate to achieve specific surface properties.
[C23C 14/086] of zinc, germanium, cadmium, indium, tin, thallium or bismuth -- C23C 14/086 covers metallic coatings applied by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation, specifically using zinc, germanium, cadmium, indium, tin, thallium or bismuth.
[C23C 14/087] of copper or solid solutions thereof -- This subclass covers the deposition of copper or copper-based solid-solution coatings onto substrates by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation techniques, including the preparation, composition and characteristics of such metallic coatings.
[C23C 14/088] of the type ABO 3  with A representing alkali, alkaline earth metal or Pb and B representing a refractory or rare earth metal -- The subclass C23C 14/088 covers the deposition of perovskite-type oxides of the formula ABO₃, where A is an alkali, alkaline-earth element or lead and B is a refractory or rare-earth metal, applied as metallic coatings by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation.
[C23C 14/10] Glass or silica -- This subclass covers the use of glass or silica as a coating material applied to metallic substrates by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation techniques.
[C23C 14/12] Organic material -- C23C 14/12 designates organic substances employed as coatings on metal substrates where the coating is applied using vacuum-based techniques such as evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. The code falls under chemistry, specifically metallic coating methods, and covers polymers, resins and other organic films that form protective, functional or decorative layers on metals.
[C23C 14/14] Metallic material, boron or silicon -- This CPC subclass covers the use of metallic boron or silicon as coating materials applied by physical-vapor-deposition techniques such as vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. It includes the processes, equipment and treatment steps for forming such metallic layers on various substrates.
[C23C 14/16] on metallic substrates or on substrates of boron or silicon -- C23C 14/16 covers deposition of metallic, boron or silicon substrates using vacuum-based techniques such as evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. The classification pertains to methods that form coatings directly on these substrates by physical vapor processes.
[C23C 14/165] by cathodic sputtering -- C23C 14/165 classifies processes that apply a metallic coating by cathodic sputtering, a vacuum-based technique in which a target serving as the cathode is bombarded with ions, causing metal atoms to be ejected and deposited as a thin film on the workpiece.
[C23C 14/18] on other inorganic substrates -- C23C 14/18 relates to processes that apply metallic coatings to inorganic substrates using vacuum-based techniques such as evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation, where the substrate is not a metal but another inorganic material.
[C23C 14/185] by cathodic sputtering -- This subclass deals with the use of cathodic sputtering to deposit metallic coatings. It includes processes where a target material is bombarded by ions from a cathode, causing atoms to be ejected and deposited onto a substrate under vacuum. It falls within the broader category of coating metallic material by vacuum evaporation, sputtering, or ion implantation.
[C23C 14/20] on organic substrates -- The CPC subgroup C23C 14/20 covers processes for depositing metallic coatings on organic substrates using vacuum-based techniques such as evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation. It includes the preparation of thin metal films on plastics, paper, wood or other non-metallic materials, focusing on the methods and parameters that achieve uniform, adherent layers.
[C23C 14/205] by cathodic sputtering -- The CPC entry C23C 14/205 covers the deposition of metallic coatings through cathodic sputtering, a physical-vapor-deposition process in which a negatively charged target (cathode) is bombarded by ions, causing metal atoms to be ejected and to condense as a thin film on a substrate.
[C23C 14/22] characterised by the process of coating -- This CPC subclass C23C 14/22 covers metallic coatings applied through vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation processes. It falls under chemistry, coating metallic material, specifically methods that use vacuum-based techniques to deposit a metal layer onto a substrate.
[C23C 14/221] Ion beam deposition  C23C14/46 ,  C23C14/48  take precedence
[C23C 14/223] specially adapted for coating particles -- C23C 14/223 refers to methods and apparatus specially adapted for applying metallic coatings to individual particles by vacuum-based techniques such as evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. It falls under the broader class of metallic material coatings within chemistry, focusing on particle-scale deposition processes.
[C23C 14/225] Oblique incidence of vaporised material on substrate -- C23C 14/225 covers methods of applying metallic coatings by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation in which the vaporised material strikes the substrate at an oblique angle. The angle of incidence is deliberately controlled to affect film thickness uniformity, microstructure and adhesion, and the subclass falls under chemistry and metallic-coating technologies.
[C23C 14/226] in order to form films with columnar structure -- This CPC subclass covers techniques for producing metallic coatings with a columnar micro-structure using vacuum-based processes such as evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. The methods focus on controlling deposition parameters to create vertically aligned columns that improve properties like hardness or thermal resistance. It falls under the broader chemistry group for metallic coating processes.
[C23C 14/228] Gas flow assisted PVD deposition -- C23C 14/228 classifies processes for depositing metallic coatings by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation in which a gas flow is employed to assist the deposition, improving film uniformity, adhesion or rate. It falls under coating metallic materials and specifies gas-assisted physical vapour deposition techniques.
[C23C 14/24] Vacuum evaporation -- C23C 14/24 refers to methods of applying metallic coatings by vacuum evaporation, including sputtering and ion-implantation techniques. It covers processes in which a metal is vaporised in a vacuum and condensed onto a substrate to form a thin, uniform coating.
[C23C 14/243] Crucibles for source material  C23C14/28 ,  C23C14/30  take precedence -- C23C 14/243 covers crucibles that contain source material during vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation processes for applying metallic coatings. It falls under the chemistry hierarchy for coating metallic material, but more specific subclasses C23C 14/28 and C23C 14/30 have priority over this entry.
[C23C 14/246] Replenishment of source material -- C23C 14/246 covers techniques for continuously or periodically feeding additional material to the source used in vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation coating processes, ensuring a stable deposition rate and composition. The replenishment may be performed by material addition, re-loading, or in-situ regeneration of the target.
[C23C 14/26] by resistance or inductive heating of the source -- C23C 14/26 refers to processes for applying metallic coatings by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation in which the source material is heated through resistance or inductive heating, enabling the deposition of a metallic layer onto a substrate.
[C23C 14/28] by wave energy or particle radiation -- The C23C 14/28 subclass covers metallic coatings applied using wave energy such as laser or electron-beam radiation, or directed particle radiation like ion beams, rather than conventional vacuum evaporation or sputtering. Techniques include laser cladding, electron-beam deposition and other radiation-based deposition processes.
[C23C 14/30] by electron bombardment -- C23C 14/30 classifies metallic coating processes that employ electron bombardment, typically electron-beam evaporation, to vaporise a metal source in vacuum and deposit a thin film on a substrate. The subclass falls under coating by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation and covers apparatus and techniques that use an electron beam to generate the coating material.
[C23C 14/32] by explosion -- C23C 14/32 covers the application of metallic coatings through vacuum-based techniques such as evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation when the coating material is delivered by an explosive process, enabling rapid deposition of metallic layers.
[C23C 14/325] Electric arc evaporation -- C23C 14/325 covers the use of electric-arc evaporation to apply metallic coatings. In this vacuum-deposition method an electric arc vaporises the metal source, and the resulting vapour condenses on a substrate to form a thin film. The classification applies to processes and apparatuses that employ this technique for producing metallic coatings.
[C23C 14/34] Sputtering -- C23C 14/34 covers the sputtering process, a vacuum-based technique for depositing metallic coatings. It involves ejecting atoms from a target material by bombarding it with energetic particles and allowing those atoms to condense on a substrate, forming a thin, uniform metallic layer. This method is used for creating precise coatings in electronics, optics and surface engineering.
[C23C 14/3407] Cathode assembly for sputtering apparatus, e.g. Target -- The subclass C23C 14/3407 covers cathode assemblies, such as targets, employed in sputtering apparatus for depositing metallic coatings by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation, focusing on the design and configuration of the cathode that holds the material to be sputtered.
[C23C 14/3414] Metallurgical or chemical aspects of target preparation, e.g. casting, powder metallurgy -- This subclass covers the preparation of targets used in vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation processes, focusing on metallurgical and chemical methods such as casting, powder metallurgy and related treatments. It includes techniques for forming, shaping and treating the material that will serve as the source of deposited metal.
[C23C 14/3421] using heated targets -- C23C 14/3421 covers methods of applying metallic coatings by vacuum processes in which the source material, or target, is heated before or during evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. Heating the target raises its vapor pressure or improves plasma generation, enabling more uniform and adherent metal layers on the substrate.
[C23C 14/3428] using liquid targets -- This CPC subclass covers the use of liquid targets to deposit metallic coatings in vacuum processes such as evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. It is situated under chemistry → coating metallic material → coating by vacuum evaporation, by sputtering or by ion implantation (C23C 14/3428).
[C23C 14/3435] Applying energy to the substrate during sputtering -- This CPC subgroup covers methods in which a substrate receives energy while a coating is deposited by sputtering, the energy being applied to modify film formation, for example by substrate heating, substrate-bias voltage or ion implantation during the deposition process.
[C23C 14/3442] using an ion beam -- An ion-beam process for applying a metallic coating, wherein the beam is directed onto a substrate to deposit or modify the surface under vacuum. This technique falls within the coating of metallic materials by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation, as defined in the Cooperative Patent Classification C23C 14/3442.
[C23C 14/345] using substrate bias -- C23C 14/345 relates to coating metallic substrates by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation in which a bias voltage is applied to the workpiece during deposition. The substrate bias is used to modify film growth, improve adhesion, control stress, density or composition of the coating. This subgroup falls under chemistry → coating metallic material → coating by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation.
[C23C 14/3457] using other particles than noble gas ions  C23C14/0036 ,  C23C14/46  take precedence -- This CPC subclass deals with metallic coating processes that employ vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation using particles other than noble-gas ions. It is situated under the broader coating metallic material category and supersedes the related subclasses C23C 14/0036 and C23C 14/46.
[C23C 14/3464] using more than one target  C23C14/56  takes precedence
[C23C 14/3471] Introduction of auxiliary energy into the plasma -- The subclass covers methods that apply an additional energy source-such as electrical, magnetic, radio-frequency, microwave or laser energy-to the plasma during vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation coating of metallic materials, thereby modifying plasma characteristics and influencing film formation.
[C23C 14/3478] using electrons, e.g. triode sputtering -- C23C 14/3478 refers to coating metallic materials by vacuum techniques that employ electrons, such as triode sputtering, where an electron stream liberates metal atoms for deposition on a substrate. It is a sub-class of coating by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation within the chemistry area.
[C23C 14/3485] using pulsed power to the target -- C23C 14/3485 is a Cooperative Patent Classification sub-group covering the application of pulsed-power techniques to the target during vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation processes for metallic coatings. It falls under the broader chemistry field for coating metallic material, specifically the methods that employ rapid, high-energy pulses to enhance film deposition.
[C23C 14/3492] Variation of parameters during sputtering -- The C23C 14/3492 class covers sputter coating processes in which the operating conditions-such as power, pressure, gas composition, substrate bias, or target-to-substrate distance-are altered during a single deposition run to modify film structure, composition, or properties. It includes methods that intentionally vary these parameters to achieve graded layers, tailored stress profiles, or functional gradients in metallic or alloy coatings applied by vacuum evaporation, sputtering, or ion implantation.
[C23C 14/35] by application of a magnetic field, e.g. magnetron sputtering -- This subclass relates to methods of forming metallic coatings using vacuum sputtering where a magnetic field is employed to confine plasma and enhance deposition, exemplified by magnetron sputtering. It includes any coating technique that relies on magnetic field assistance during sputtering.
[C23C 14/351] using a magnetic field in close vicinity to the substrate -- It covers the use of a magnetic field positioned close to the substrate during vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation of metallic coatings, guiding charged particles or plasma to affect film growth and properties.
[C23C 14/352] using more than one target  C23C14/56  takes precedence
[C23C 14/354] Introduction of auxiliary energy into the plasma -- C23C 14/354 covers coating methods in which auxiliary energy such as radio-frequency, microwave, laser or other power sources is introduced into the plasma during vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation of metallic materials. The added energy modifies plasma characteristics to improve film adhesion, density, uniformity or composition.
[C23C 14/355] using electrons, e.g. triode sputtering -- This CPC subclass covers the application of metallic coatings by electron-driven processes, notably triode sputtering, within vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation techniques. It sits under chemistry → coating metallic material → coating metallic material → coating by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation.
[C23C 14/357] Microwaves, e.g. electron cyclotron resonance enhanced sputtering -- This subclass covers coating processes in which microwaves, such as those generated by electron cyclotron resonance, are used to enhance sputtering during vacuum deposition of metallic films. It pertains to methods where microwave energy assists material removal and film formation on substrates.
[C23C 14/358] Inductive energy -- C23C 14/358 relates to the use of inductive energy in vacuum-based metal coating processes such as evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. It covers techniques where magnetic fields or inductively generated plasma provide the energy to vaporise or ionise the coating material, enabling deposition onto a substrate. The classification is used for patents describing inductively coupled coating apparatus or methods.
[C23C 14/46] by ion beam produced by an external ion source -- C23C 14/46 relates to applying metallic coatings using an ion beam generated by an external ion source, a technique that directs accelerated ions onto a substrate to form a thin film. This method falls under vacuum-based deposition processes such as sputtering and ion implantation and is used to achieve precise, uniform metallic layers on various materials.
[C23C 14/48] Ion implantation -- C23C 14/48 covers the use of ion implantation to form or modify a coating on a metallic substrate. The technique accelerates ions onto the surface, embedding them to alter composition, hardness, wear resistance, corrosion behavior or other surface properties without melting the base material. It is classified within coating processes that employ vacuum techniques such as sputtering or evaporation.
[C23C 14/50] Substrate holders -- C23C 14/50 classifies devices that hold or support substrates while metallic coatings are applied using vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation techniques. Such substrate holders maintain precise positioning, alignment and thermal control during the coating process, enabling uniform metal film deposition on the workpiece.
[C23C 14/505] for rotation of the substrates -- The CPC subgroup C23C 14/505 covers techniques for applying metallic coatings by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation in which the substrate is rotated during the deposition. Rotating the workpiece improves uniformity of film thickness and properties across the surface, and the entry addresses the specific mechanical arrangements and process parameters required for such rotation.
[C23C 14/52] Means for observation of the coating process -- C23C 14/52 designates devices or systems employed to observe and monitor metallic coatings applied by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation, providing real-time information on film thickness, uniformity or composition during the deposition process.
[C23C 14/54] Controlling or regulating the coating process -- C23C 14/54 covers methods and devices for controlling or regulating the coating process when applying metallic layers by vacuum evaporation, sputtering, or ion implantation. It falls under the chemistry subclass for metallic material coatings, focusing on process control to ensure uniform thickness, composition, and properties.
[C23C 14/541] Heating or cooling of the substrates -- C23C 14/541 relates to methods for heating, cooling or otherwise controlling the temperature of a substrate during metallic coating processes performed by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation, where substrate temperature is adjusted to influence film properties, adhesion, stress or microstructure.
[C23C 14/542] Controlling the film thickness or evaporation rate -- This CPC subclass concerns processes for controlling the thickness of a deposited metallic film or the rate at which material is evaporated during vacuum-based coating methods such as evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. It covers monitoring, feedback and adjustment techniques used to achieve desired film properties.
[C23C 14/543] using measurement on the vapor source -- C23C 14/543 covers processes for depositing metallic coatings by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation that incorporate measurement of the vapor source, such as monitoring temperature, pressure, composition or flux to control film growth. The classification is part of the CPC hierarchy for chemical coating of metallic materials, emphasizing analytical control of the source to achieve desired coating properties.
[C23C 14/544] using measurement in the gas phase -- C23C 14/544 covers methods for applying metallic coatings by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation in which the composition, pressure or other properties of the surrounding gas are measured during the coating process.
[C23C 14/545] using measurement on deposited material -- C23C 14/545 covers techniques for evaluating a metallic coating deposited by vacuum evaporation, sputtering, or ion implantation, focusing on measurements performed on the deposited layer. It includes methods to assess thickness, composition, adhesion, stress, micro-structure or other physical properties of the coating after or during its formation. This subclass is used to classify inventions that improve or apply such measurement processes.
[C23C 14/546] using crystal oscillators -- The CPC subclass C23C 14/546 covers processes that employ crystal oscillators in the deposition of metallic coatings applied by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. It includes the use of quartz crystal microbalances or similar resonators to monitor or control film thickness, deposition rate, or material properties during coating.
[C23C 14/547] using optical methods -- This CPC subgroup covers the use of optical techniques to monitor, control or characterize metallic coatings applied by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation processes. It includes methods such as spectroscopic ellipsometry, reflectometry or interferometry for assessing film thickness, uniformity or composition during or after deposition.
[C23C 14/548] Controlling the composition -- The CPC subclass C23C 14/548 covers techniques for controlling the composition of metallic coatings applied by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation. It includes methods that adjust alloy ratios, add dopants, create compositional gradients or monitor the coating's makeup during deposition to achieve the desired material properties.
[C23C 14/56] Apparatus specially adapted for continuous coating -- C23C 14/56 covers equipment designed specifically for the continuous application of metallic coatings using vacuum-based processes such as evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. The class includes machines that maintain a steady coating line, controlling material flux and substrate movement to achieve uniform metallic layers.
[C23C 14/562] for coating elongated substrates -- C23C 14/562 covers methods of applying metallic coatings to elongated substrates such as wires, rods or tubes by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. The class is used for patents that address coating processes aimed at long, thin components rather than bulk shapes.
[C23C 14/564] Means for minimising impurities in the coating chamber such as dust, moisture, residual gases -- The CPC subclass C23C 14/564 covers devices or procedures designed to reduce contaminants-such as dust, moisture or residual gases-inside vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation chambers used for metallic coating processes. It focuses on means that keep the coating environment clean to improve film quality.
[C23C 14/566] using a load-lock chamber -- This sub-group covers processes for applying metallic coatings by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation that incorporate a load-lock chamber to introduce and remove work pieces without breaking the vacuum in the main coating chamber. The load-lock isolates the coating environment, improving throughput and reducing contamination. It is used for efficient, continuous production of metallic coatings.
[C23C 14/568] Transferring the substrates through a series of coating stations  C23C14/562  takes precedence -- C23C 14/568 covers methods and apparatus for transporting workpieces through a series of vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation coating stations, such as conveyors, rollers or robotic handlers that enable successive metal-film deposition. It is a subcategory of C23C 14/562, which defines the broader coating process for metallic materials.
[C23C 14/58] After-treatment -- C23C 14/58 concerns post-deposition operations applied to metallic coatings produced by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation; it includes annealing, surface cleaning, oxidation, laser treatment or other modifications performed after the coating has been laid down.
[C23C 14/5806] Thermal treatment -- C23C 14/5806 covers thermal treatment steps applied to metallic coatings that have been deposited by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. It includes heating, annealing, tempering or other heat-based processes used to modify microstructure, relieve stress, improve adhesion or promote diffusion in the coated layer. The classification is part of the chemistry group for metallic coating technologies.
[C23C 14/5813] using lasers -- The subclass C23C 14/5813 covers the application of laser technology to metal-coating processes that rely on vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation. It includes methods where laser radiation assists in the removal, transport or activation of metallic material to form thin films on a substrate.
[C23C 14/582] using electron bombardment -- C23C 14/582 concerns coating metallic substrates by vacuum processes in which a beam of electrons is directed at the coating material to cause evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation, thereby depositing a thin film onto the target surface.
[C23C 14/5826] Treatment with charged particles  C23C14/582  takes precedence -- C23C 14/5826 is a CPC subclass that deals with post-treatment of metallic coatings using charged particles such as ions or plasma. It falls under the hierarchy of chemistry, metallic coating materials, and specifically coating by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation, and it refines the broader C23C 14/582 category on charged-particle treatments.
[C23C 14/5833] Ion beam bombardment -- C23C 14/5833 covers the use of ion-beam bombardment to treat or form metallic coatings, typically performed in vacuum environments such as evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation processes. The class addresses the energetic ion impact that modifies surface composition, structure or adhesion of the deposited metal layer.
[C23C 14/584] Non-reactive treatment -- C23C 14/584 covers non-reactive treatments applied to metallic coatings formed by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation. It includes physical processes such as annealing, ion-beam mixing, surface smoothing or hardening that modify the coating without chemical reaction. The class is used to classify patents dealing with post-deposition physical modification of metal films.
[C23C 14/5846] Reactive treatment -- C23C 14/5846 covers reactive treatment of metallic coatings produced by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation, where the deposited layer is subsequently exposed to a reactive gas, plasma or ion beam to alter its composition, structure or surface properties. This includes processes such as nitriding, carburizing or oxidation that enhance hardness, wear resistance or functional performance of the coating.
[C23C 14/5853] Oxidation -- This CPC subclass covers oxidation processes applied to metallic coatings formed through vacuum-deposition techniques such as evaporation, sputtering, or ion implantation. It includes methods where oxidation is used to modify the surface composition, structure, or properties of the metal coating.
[C23C 14/586] Nitriding -- C23C 14/586 nitriding covers the formation of a nitride coating on metallic substrates using vacuum-based techniques such as evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation, to improve surface hardness, wear resistance and corrosion protection.
[C23C 14/5866] Treatment with sulfur, selenium or tellurium -- This CPC subclass covers post-deposition treatments of metallic films formed by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation in which the surface is reacted with sulfur, selenium or tellurium. The purpose is to alter the coating's chemical or physical characteristics, such as corrosion resistance, hardness, conductivity or lubricity, by forming chalcogenide layers or compounds on the metal surface.
[C23C 14/5873] Removal of material -- The subclass C23C 14/5873 concerns techniques for eliminating part of a metallic coating that has been applied by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering or ion-implantation. It covers processes such as ion-beam milling, plasma etching or chemical stripping that selectively remove material from the coated surface.
[C23C 14/588] by mechanical treatment
[C23C 14/5886] Mechanical treatment  involving removal of material  C23C14/588 -- C23C 14/5886 covers mechanical processes used to remove material from metallic coatings applied by vacuum evaporation, sputtering or ion implantation. It includes grinding, polishing, abrasive blasting and similar techniques to thin, shape or clean the coating or underlying substrate.
[C23C 14/5893] Mixing of deposited material -- This subclass deals with methods that intentionally blend two or more metals while they are being deposited onto a substrate by vacuum-evaporation, sputtering, or ion-implantation. It includes co-evaporation, simultaneous or alternating sputter sources, and ion-beam mixing to form alloy or graded coatings directly during film growth.
[C23C 16/00] Chemical deposition or plating by decomposition -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Chemical coating by decomposition of gaseous compounds, without leaving reaction products of surface material in the coating, e.g. chemical vapour deposition (CVD), chemical coating by decomposition of gaseous compounds using electric discharge (plasma coating), using non excited gas phase coating.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Reactive sputtering or vacuum evaporation -> C23C14/00
[C23C 16/003] Coating on a liquid substrate -- C23C 16/003 covers the deposition of metallic coatings on a liquid substrate, where a metal layer is formed on the surface of a liquid by chemical decomposition or plating methods. It is applied in processes such as coating molten baths, producing continuous metal foils, or forming alloy layers on liquid media.
[C23C 16/006] characterized by the colour of the layer -- This subclass covers metal coating processes by chemical decomposition where the resulting layer is defined primarily by its colour. It includes methods and products where colour of the deposited metallic or oxide film is a distinguishing technical feature, such as tinted plating or coloured anodic films.
[C23C 16/01] on temporary substrates, e.g. substrates subsequently removed by etching -- This CPC subclass covers methods of depositing a metallic coating onto a temporary substrate that is later removed, usually by chemical etching, allowing the creation of free-standing metal layers. It falls under chemical deposition or plating by decomposition within the broader field of coating metallic material.
[C23C 16/02] Pretreatment of the material to be coated -- C23C 16/02 denotes the pretreatment of a metal substrate before a chemical deposition or plating process that proceeds by decomposition of a coating compound. The entry covers cleaning, etching, activation, or other surface-conditioning steps applied to the material to be coated.
[C23C 16/0209] by heating -- C23C 16/0209 covers techniques for forming metallic coatings by chemically decomposing a precursor and using heat to drive the deposition. The heating supplies the energy required to break down the compound and deposit the metal onto a substrate.
[C23C 16/0218] in a reactive atmosphere  C23C16/0227  takes precedence -- The CPC subclass C23C 16/0218 covers chemical deposition or plating processes in which the metallic coating is formed within a reactive atmosphere, such as oxidising, nitriding or sulfidising gases, affecting the reaction path and product composition. It is nested under the broader group for deposition by decomposition and is superseded by the more specific subclass C23C 16/0227.
[C23C 16/0227] by cleaning or etching -- C23C 16/0227 covers processes for metallic coatings formed by chemical deposition or decomposition in which the substrate surface is prepared through cleaning or etching steps. The cleaning or etching removes contaminants, oxides or modifies surface morphology to improve adhesion before the plating reaction.
[C23C 16/0236] by etching with a reactive gas
[C23C 16/0245] by etching with a plasma -- This subclass covers methods that form or modify a metal coating by removing material with a plasma-etch step, usually after a chemical deposition or plating by decomposition process. It is part of the coating metallic material group within the chemistry sector of the Cooperative Patent Classification.
[C23C 16/0254] Physical treatment to alter the texture of the surface, e.g. scratching or polishing -- C23C 16/0254 concerns physical techniques applied to a metallic coating deposited by chemical decomposition in order to modify its surface texture. Methods such as scratching, polishing, grinding or other mechanical abrasion are covered, enabling control of roughness, smoothness or patterning after the plating step.
[C23C 16/0263] Irradiation with laser or particle beam -- This subclass pertains to the production of metallic coatings by chemically decomposing a precursor using a laser or particle beam, which initiates deposition of metal onto a substrate. It falls under chemical deposition or plating by decomposition within the broader area of coating metallic materials.
[C23C 16/0272] Deposition of sub-layers, e.g. to promote the adhesion of the main coating -- The C23C 16/0272 sub-class concerns the application of thin intermediary layers before the primary metallic coating to improve adhesion. It covers methods for depositing such sub-layers, often by chemical or electrochemical means, and includes related process parameters that enhance the bond between the substrate and the final coating.
[C23C 16/0281] of metallic sub-layers  C23C16/029  takes precedence
[C23C 16/029] Graded interfaces -- The subclass C23C 16/029 concerns methods for producing metallic coatings in which the composition or structure varies continuously through the thickness, creating graded interfaces. Such techniques modify properties like hardness, corrosion resistance or thermal behavior by controlling the gradual transition of material phases during chemical deposition or plating.
[C23C 16/04] Coating on selected surface areas, e.g. using masks -- C23C 16/04 designates processes for applying a metallic coating only to selected areas of a substrate, typically by employing masks or other selective coverings during chemical deposition or plating by decomposition. It is situated in the chemistry hierarchy under coating metallic material and chemical deposition or plating by decomposition.
[C23C 16/042] using masks -- The CPC subclass C23C 16/042 covers methods of chemical deposition or plating by decomposition in which a mask is applied to define the areas to be plated or protected. Masking techniques include physical barriers, patterned films or resist layers that prevent deposition on selected portions of the substrate, enabling selective coating of metallic surfaces.
[C23C 16/045] Coating cavities or hollow spaces, e.g. interior of tubes; Infiltration of porous substrates -- The CPC subclass C23C 16/045 covers methods for applying metallic coatings to the interior of cavities, hollow spaces such as tube interiors, and porous substrates. It includes processes that deposit metal by chemical decomposition and techniques that infiltrate porous materials to achieve a uniform coating.
[C23C 16/047] using irradiation by energy or particles -- C23C 16/047 covers methods of forming metal or alloy coatings in which the deposition process is initiated or driven by irradiation, such as laser, electron-beam, plasma, or other energetic particles. The energy source decomposes a precursor or vapor, causing metallic material to deposit onto a substrate. This subclass lies within chemical deposition or plating by decomposition of a coating metallic material.
[C23C 16/06] characterised by the deposition of metallic material -- C23C 16/06 covers processes in which a metallic layer is formed by chemical decomposition of a precursor rather than by electrolytic reduction. The method deposits the metal directly onto a substrate through chemical reactions such as electroless plating, chemical vapor deposition, or similar techniques.
[C23C 16/08] from metal halides -- The C23C 16/08 subclass relates to chemical deposition or plating by decomposition in which a metallic coating is formed from metal halide precursors that decompose on a substrate surface. It covers methods that generate a metal layer by reducing or thermally breaking down metal halides, falling under the broader category of coating metallic material.
[C23C 16/10] Deposition of chromium only -- C23C 16/10 designates methods for depositing a pure chromium layer by chemical decomposition, such as electroless chromium plating, without co-deposition of other metals. The process is used to form protective or decorative metallic coatings on substrates.
[C23C 16/12] Deposition of aluminium only -- This CPC subclass covers processes in which aluminium is deposited on a substrate exclusively by chemical decomposition methods such as chemical vapor deposition or electroless plating, without the involvement of other metals. It is part of the chemical deposition or plating by decomposition group within metallic coating technologies.
[C23C 16/14] Deposition of only one other metal element -- This CPC subclass covers processes where a single foreign metal is deposited onto a substrate by chemical decomposition of a precursor, such as electroless plating or chemical vapor deposition, without simultaneous co-deposition of additional metals. It applies to coating metallic material using a single-metal deposition step.
[C23C 16/16] from metal carbonyl compounds -- This subclass covers processes that form metallic coatings by decomposing metal carbonyl compounds, using the volatile organometallic precursor to deposit a metal layer onto a substrate. It is part of the broader area of chemical deposition or plating by decomposition within coating metallic material.
[C23C 16/18] from metallo-organic compounds -- A method of chemically depositing a metallic coating in which a metallo-organic precursor decomposes to form the metal on a substrate. It falls under chemistry, coating metallic material, and chemical deposition or plating by decomposition. This subclass covers processes that use organometallic compounds as the source of the deposited metal.
[C23C 16/20] Deposition of aluminium only -- C23C 16/20 covers methods for depositing aluminium as the sole metal onto a substrate, typically through chemical deposition or plating processes where aluminium is formed by decomposition of a precursor. It is a subclass of coating metallic material within the chemistry section.
[C23C 16/22] characterised by the deposition of inorganic material, other than metallic material -- C23C 16/22 covers processes where inorganic, non-metallic materials are deposited onto a substrate by chemical decomposition, such as plating with oxides, nitrides, carbides or other ceramic compounds. These methods are used to form protective or functional coatings without involving metallic plating.
[C23C 16/24] Deposition of silicon only -- C23C 16/24 covers processes that deposit silicon alone onto a substrate, typically by chemical decomposition of silicon-containing precursors. It falls under the broader category of chemical deposition or plating by decomposition within metallic coating technologies. This subclass is used to classify patents dealing with silicon-only plating techniques.
[C23C 16/26] Deposition of carbon only -- C23C 16/26 pertains to methods for depositing a carbon layer on a substrate by chemical decomposition, such as chemical-vapor-deposition of carbon films. It falls under chemical deposition or plating by decomposition within the broader field of coating metallic materials.
[C23C 16/27] Diamond only -- C23C 16/27 covers chemical deposition or plating by decomposition in which the only coating material applied is diamond. It includes processes such as chemical vapor deposition that deposit a pure diamond layer on a substrate without any additional metallic or ceramic components.
[C23C 16/271] using hot filaments -- C23C 16/271 covers processes that use a heated filament to decompose volatile compounds, causing metallic material to be deposited as a coating on a substrate. The hot-filament method is employed in chemical vapor deposition and related plating techniques where the filament supplies the thermal energy for the reaction.
[C23C 16/272] using DC, AC or RF discharges -- This CPC subgroup covers metallic coating processes in which a source material is decomposed by an electric discharge-direct current, alternating current or radio-frequency-to deposit the metal onto a substrate as part of chemical deposition or plating.
[C23C 16/274] using microwave discharges -- C23C 16/274 covers the use of microwave-generated discharges to effect chemical deposition or plating of metallic materials. The subclass records processes in which microwave energy creates a plasma that decomposes a precursor, allowing a metal coating to be formed on a substrate. This falls under the broader CPC group for coating metallic material by decomposition.
[C23C 16/275] using combustion torches -- C23C 16/275 covers the deposition of metallic or alloy coatings by chemically decomposing a precursor material with the heat of a combustion torch. It includes processes where a flame or torch breaks down metal-containing compounds, allowing the metal to plate or coat a substrate directly from the gas phase. This subclass falls under chemical deposition or plating by decomposition within the broader field of coating metallic materials.
[C23C 16/276] using plasma jets -- This subgroup covers methods where plasma jets are employed to decompose precursor compounds, depositing metallic or alloy coatings onto substrates. It relates to chemical deposition by decomposition using plasma jet technology, typically for thin-film or coating formation.
[C23C 16/277] using other elements in the gas phase besides carbon and hydrogen; using other elements besides carbon, hydrogen and oxygen in case of use of combustion torches; using other elements besides carbon, hydrogen and inert gas in case of use of plasma jets -- The subclass C23C 16/277 covers chemical deposition or plating processes in which the gas-phase reactants contain elements other than carbon and hydrogen; for combustion-torch methods it also includes cases where oxygen is present, and for plasma-jet methods it encompasses the use of additional inert gases. This entry addresses the use of such extra elements to form metallic coatings by decomposition.
[C23C 16/278] doping or introduction of a secondary phase in the diamond -- This subclass covers methods for incorporating dopants or secondary phases into diamond during its formation or surface modification, typically by chemical vapor deposition or other decomposition processes to alter electrical, optical, or mechanical properties. It includes techniques for introducing elements or compounds into the diamond lattice or as coatings.
[C23C 16/279] control of diamond crystallography -- C23C 16/279 covers techniques for controlling the crystal structure of diamond formed by chemical deposition or plating processes that involve decomposition of a precursor, such as adjusting conditions to achieve desired diamond facets or grain orientation.
[C23C 16/28] Deposition of only one other non-metal element -- This subclass covers processes that chemically deposit a single non-metal element onto a metallic substrate by decomposition of a precursor, creating a pure elemental coating such as carbon, nitrogen, silicon or similar. It excludes methods that form alloys or mixed-element layers, focusing only on the deposition of one non-metal element as the coating material.
[C23C 16/30] Deposition of compounds, mixtures or solid solutions, e.g. borides, carbides, nitrides -- The CPC subclass C23C 16/30 covers methods for depositing compounds, mixtures or solid solutions such as borides, carbides and nitrides onto metallic surfaces by chemical decomposition. It falls under the broader categories of chemistry and metallic coating.
[C23C 16/301] AIII BV compounds, where A is Al, Ga, In or Tl and B is N, P, As, Sb or Bi
[C23C 16/303] Nitrides -- The CPC class C23C 16/303 covers processes for forming metallic nitrides on substrates by chemical deposition or plating through decomposition of nitrogen-containing compounds. It includes methods such as vapor-phase nitriding, plasma-assisted nitriding, and other techniques that generate nitride layers for corrosion resistance, hardness, or other surface properties. This subclass falls under chemistry, specifically coating metallic materials by chemical deposition.
[C23C 16/305] Sulfides, selenides, or tellurides -- C23C 16/305 covers coating processes in which a metallic layer is formed from sulfide, selenide or telluride compounds that decompose to deposit the metal. It includes methods of chemical deposition or plating where these chalcogenide precursors are used to generate the metallic coating on a substrate.
[C23C 16/306] AII BVI compounds, where A is Zn, Cd or Hg and B is S, Se or Te -- C23C 16/306 is a CPC subgroup for chemical deposition or plating by decomposition that uses AII BVI compounds, where A is zinc, cadmium or mercury and B is sulfur, selenium or tellurium, to form metallic coatings. This entry falls under the broader chemistry field and the coating metallic material category, focusing on specific binary metal-chalcogenide precursors for plating processes.
[C23C 16/308] Oxynitrides -- Oxynitrides are inorganic compounds containing oxygen, nitrogen and one or more metal elements, used as hard, wear-resistant or corrosion-protective coatings. In the CPC class C23C 16/308 they are produced by chemical deposition or plating processes in which a precursor decomposes on a substrate, forming a mixed oxide-nitride layer that combines the properties of both oxides and nitrides.
[C23C 16/32] Carbides -- C23C 16/32 covers the formation of carbide layers on metallic substrates by chemical decomposition, typically via vapor-phase or solution-phase deposition techniques. It includes processes for applying protective or functional carbide coatings, such as titanium, tungsten or silicon carbides, through methods like chemical vapor deposition, plasma-enhanced CVD or related plating procedures.
[C23C 16/325] Silicon carbide -- This CPC subgroup covers methods for applying a silicon-carbide coating to metallic objects by chemical decomposition, such as chemical vapor deposition or related plating techniques. It includes the formation of protective, wear-resistant or conductive SiC layers on steel, aluminum and other alloys.
[C23C 16/34] Nitrides -- C23C 16/34 covers the formation of nitride layers on metal substrates by chemical deposition or plating processes that decompose precursor compounds. It includes methods such as chemical vapor deposition, plasma-enhanced deposition, and other decomposition-based techniques used to create metallic nitride coatings for corrosion resistance, hardness, or functional surface properties. This subclass falls under the broader coating metallic material category within the Chemistry section of the CPC.
[C23C 16/342] Boron nitride -- C23C 16/342 covers the chemical deposition or plating-by-decomposition of boron nitride onto metallic substrates. The class details methods that form a boron-nitride coating through gaseous or liquid precursors that decompose and react on the surface, producing a protective or functional metallic coating.
[C23C 16/345] Silicon nitride -- C23C 16/345 covers the deposition of silicon nitride films by chemical decomposition, typically using chemical vapor deposition or related gas-phase methods, to form protective or functional coatings on metallic substrates. It includes processes that generate silicon nitride from volatile precursors and apply the resulting layer for wear resistance, corrosion protection, or thermal barrier applications.
[C23C 16/347] Carbon nitride -- C23C 16/347 covers the formation of carbon-nitride coatings by chemical deposition or plating processes that involve decomposition of precursors. It pertains to metallic substrates that receive a carbon-nitride layer, typically through methods such as chemical vapor deposition. The classification is part of the CPC group for coating metallic material within chemistry.
[C23C 16/36] Carbonitrides -- C23C 16/36 covers the formation of carbonitride layers on metal or other substrates by chemical or electrolytic decomposition, typically as protective or hard-wear coatings. The classification includes processes, reagents and equipment used to deposit carbon-rich nitride compounds that enhance surface hardness, corrosion resistance and lubricity.
[C23C 16/38] Borides -- C23C 16/38 pertains to the chemical deposition or plating of boride layers on metal substrates, where borides are formed by decomposition of precursor compounds. It includes methods, baths and treatments used to create hard, wear-resistant boride coatings for applications such as cutting tools, protective surfaces and electronic components.
[C23C 16/40] Oxides -- C23C 16/40 covers the formation of oxide layers on metal substrates by chemical decomposition methods, including thermal oxidation, anodic oxidation and other chemical deposition techniques that produce oxide coatings for protective, decorative or functional purposes.
[C23C 16/401] containing silicon -- C23C 16/401 relates to chemical deposition or plating of metallic materials in which silicon is incorporated into the coating. It covers processes such as electroless plating, chemical vapor deposition or other wet-chemical methods that produce silicon-containing metallic layers on a substrate.
[C23C 16/402] Silicon dioxide -- C23C 16/402 covers processes in which silicon dioxide is formed or applied by chemical decomposition as a coating on metallic substrates. It includes methods such as thermal or chemical vapor deposition that deposit SiO₂ layers for protective or functional purposes.
[C23C 16/403] of aluminium, magnesium or beryllium -- The CPC code C23C 16/403 pertains to methods for chemically depositing metallic coatings by decomposition that specifically involve aluminium, magnesium or beryllium. It covers processes such as chemical-vapor or thermal-decomposition plating where organometallic or other precursors are broken down to form a thin layer of one of these metals on a substrate. This classification falls under chemical deposition or plating by decomposition within coating metallic material.
[C23C 16/404] of alkaline earth metals -- This subclass covers processes for depositing alkaline earth metals onto a substrate by chemical decomposition of a suitable precursor, such as reducing compounds or organometallics, within the broader field of metallic coating. It includes methods where the metal is formed in situ from a compound and applied as a coating.
[C23C 16/405] of refractory metals or yttrium -- C23C 16/405 covers methods of chemically depositing or plating refractory metals and yttrium onto a substrate by decomposition of a volatile precursor compound that releases the metal on the surface. It falls under the coating of metallic material category in the CPC hierarchy.
[C23C 16/406] of iron group metals -- This CPC subclass covers methods of forming metallic coatings by chemical decomposition using iron-group metals such as iron, cobalt or nickel. It includes chemical vapor deposition, electroless plating and related techniques where a metal-containing precursor decomposes on the substrate to produce a metallic layer.
[C23C 16/407] of zinc, germanium, cadmium, indium, tin, thallium or bismuth -- C23C 16/407 covers methods for chemically depositing or plating metallic layers of zinc, germanium, cadmium, indium, tin, thallium or bismuth using decomposition reactions. The classification falls under the broader group for coating metallic materials and pertains to chemical deposition processes.
[C23C 16/408] of copper or solid solutions thereof -- The subclass C23C 16/408 covers chemical deposition or plating processes in which copper or solid-solution alloys containing copper are deposited onto a substrate, including electro-plating, electroless plating and related methods that form copper-based metallic coatings.
[C23C 16/409] of the type ABO 3  with A representing alkali, alkaline earth metal or lead and B representing a refractory metal, nickel, scandium or a lanthanide -- This CPC subclass C23C 16/409 covers chemical deposition or plating processes that form coatings of perovskite-type oxides with the formula ABO3, where the A-site is an alkali metal, alkaline-earth metal or lead and the B-site is a refractory metal, nickel, scandium or a lanthanide. The method relies on decomposition of precursor compounds to create the metallic coating.
[C23C 16/42] Silicides -- C23C 16/42 covers methods for forming silicide coatings on metal substrates by chemical deposition or plating using decomposition reactions. It includes processes that generate a silicide layer through thermal or chemical breakdown of silicon-containing precursors. The classification is used for patents on producing protective or functional silicide films on metallic parts.
[C23C 16/44] characterised by the method of coating -- The C23C 16/44 subclass concerns metallic coatings formed by chemical deposition or plating through decomposition, where the invention is identified primarily by the specific coating method employed rather than by the composition of the coating or the substrate. It falls under the chemistry hierarchy for coating metallic material and addresses processes that are characterised by how the coating is applied.
[C23C 16/4401] Means for minimising impurities, e.g. dust, moisture or residual gas, in the reaction chamber -- The CPC sub-group C23C 16/4401 covers devices or methods that reduce contaminants such as dust, moisture or residual gases inside the reaction chamber used for chemical deposition or plating by decomposition. It includes sealing, venting, filtration, drying or other control mechanisms that maintain a clean environment and improve coating quality.
[C23C 16/4402] Reduction of impurities in the source gas -- C23C 16/4402 covers techniques for removing contaminants from source gases used in chemical deposition or plating by decomposition, aiming to improve coating purity and performance. The entry addresses purification methods that reduce impurity levels before the gas is introduced into the deposition process.
[C23C 16/4404] Coatings or surface treatment on the inside of the reaction chamber or on parts thereof -- This subclass covers methods and materials for applying protective or functional metallic coatings to the interior surfaces of reaction vessels or their components, typically by chemical deposition or plating processes. It includes treatments that improve corrosion resistance, catalyst support, or reaction control inside the chamber.
[C23C 16/4405] Cleaning of reactor or parts inside the reactor by using reactive gases -- This subclass deals with methods that employ reactive gases to remove deposits, residues, or scale from reactors or internal components involved in chemical deposition or plating processes. It includes gas-phase reactions that chemically dissolve or volatilize contaminants without disassembly. Used in metal coating operations to maintain reactor performance.
[C23C 16/4407] Cleaning of reactor or reactor parts by using wet or mechanical methods -- C23C 16/4407 covers procedures for cleaning reactors or reactor components employing wet chemicals, rinsing, or mechanical actions such as brushing or scrubbing. The methods are intended to remove residues and prepare surfaces before or after metallic coating processes that involve chemical deposition or plating by decomposition.
[C23C 16/4408] by purging residual gases from the reaction chamber or gas lines -- This subclass covers methods of chemical deposition or plating by decomposition in which residual gases are removed by purging the reaction chamber or associated gas lines. The technique aims to improve film quality and process control by eliminating unwanted gases before or during the plating reaction.
[C23C 16/4409] characterised by sealing means -- This subclass of the CPC covers processes for depositing a metal coating by chemical decomposition in which the deposited layer is sealed, for example by a protective overlayer or a sealing step that isolates the coating from the environment. It relates to metallic-material coating methods where sealing means are integral to the deposition.
[C23C 16/4411] Cooling of the reaction chamber walls  C23C16/45572  takes precedence -- C23C 16/4411 covers techniques for cooling the walls of reaction chambers during chemical deposition or plating by decomposition of metallic materials. It is a sub-group of the broader coating metallic material class that deals with chemical deposition methods, and is superseded in priority by the related subclass C23C 16/45572.
[C23C 16/4412] Details relating to the exhausts, e.g. pumps, filters, scrubbers, particle traps -- The classification C23C 16/4412 pertains to chemical deposition or plating by decomposition and covers exhaust handling components such as pumps, filters, scrubbers and particle traps used to treat or remove gases and residues generated during metallic coating processes.
[C23C 16/4414] Electrochemical vapour deposition [EVD] -- C23C 16/4414 designates electrochemical vapour deposition, a technique that merges electrochemical reactions with vapor-phase transport to form metallic coatings on a substrate. The process typically involves generating a metal-containing vapor at an electrode surface and driving its reduction to deposit a thin, uniform metallic film.
[C23C 16/4415] Acoustic wave CVD -- C23C 16/4415 covers a chemical vapor deposition technique in which acoustic waves are employed to induce or enhance the decomposition of precursor gases, forming metallic or alloy coatings on a substrate. The method falls under coating metallic material by chemical deposition or plating through decomposition.
[C23C 16/4417] Methods specially adapted for coating powder -- This CPC subclass details processes that apply a metallic coating to powder particles, typically using chemical deposition or decomposition methods such as vapor-phase techniques. The focus is on achieving uniform metal layers on the powder to impart desired properties for further manufacturing or functional use.
[C23C 16/4418] Methods for making free-standing articles  C23C16/01  takes precedence -- This subclass deals with processes that produce self-supporting metallic or alloy articles directly from a chemical deposition or plating reaction, without using a substrate or mold. It includes techniques where the deposited material separates from the plating bath as a discrete piece, such as free-standing foils, ribbons, or shaped forms, and follows the broader C23C16/01 category.
[C23C 16/442] using fluidised bed process -- This CPC subclass covers methods of depositing a metallic coating by chemical decomposition where the reactants are introduced into a fluidised-bed reactor. The fluidised-bed provides high heat and mass transfer, allowing uniform plating of metals onto substrates. It falls under chemical deposition or plating by decomposition within the broader coating metallic material field.
[C23C 16/448] characterised by the method used for generating reactive gas streams, e.g. by evaporation or sublimation of precursor materials -- This sub-group of C23C 16/448 covers coating metallic materials where the reactive gas used for deposition is produced by heating a solid or liquid precursor to evaporate or sublimate it, generating a gas stream that reacts on the substrate. It classifies processes such as physical vapor deposition and thermal decomposition of precursors to form metallic coatings.
[C23C 16/4481] by evaporation using carrier gas in contact with the source material  C23C16/4486  takes precedence
[C23C 16/4482] by bubbling of carrier gas through liquid source material -- This subclass pertains to chemical deposition or plating by decomposition in which a carrier gas is bubbled through a liquid source of the metallic material, causing the material to decompose and form a coating on a substrate.
[C23C 16/4483] using a porous body -- C23C 16/4483 covers methods of depositing metallic coatings by chemical decomposition that employ a porous substrate or structure to receive the deposited material, enabling uniform plating or formation of a coating within the pores. This sub-group is used for processes such as electroless plating or chemical vapor deposition where a porous body acts as a carrier or scaffold for the metallic layer.
[C23C 16/4485] by evaporation without using carrier gas in contact with the source material  C23C16/4486  takes precedence
[C23C 16/4486] by producing an aerosol and subsequent evaporation of the droplets or particles -- The CPC subclass C23C 16/4486 covers chemical deposition or plating methods that create a metallic coating by forming an aerosol and then evaporating the droplets or particles, leaving the metal to deposit on the substrate. It is situated under coating metallic material, chemical deposition by decomposition.
[C23C 16/4487] by using a condenser -- This CPC subgroup concerns chemical deposition or plating processes that utilize a condenser to facilitate the decomposition of plating solutions and the subsequent formation of a metallic coating. It falls within the chemistry field under coating metallic material, specifically the chemical deposition or plating by decomposition category.
[C23C 16/4488] by  in situ  generation of reactive gas by chemical or electrochemical reaction -- This subclass covers methods that form metallic coatings by generating a reactive gas directly at the workpiece through a chemical or electrochemical reaction, which then decomposes to deposit metal, relying on in-situ gas generation rather than an externally supplied gaseous precursor.
[C23C 16/452] by activating reactive gas streams before introduction into the reaction chamber, e.g. by or addition of reactive species -- This CPC subclass covers methods of chemical deposition or plating that pre-activate reactive gas streams before they enter the reaction chamber, such as by adding reactive species or using plasma activation. It includes techniques that modify the gas composition or energy to improve deposition efficiency.
[C23C 16/453] passing the reaction gases through burners or torches, e.g. atmospheric pressure CVD -- A process in which the reactive gases are delivered through burners or torches to effect deposition, most commonly atmospheric-pressure chemical vapor deposition, used to form metallic or alloy coatings on substrates. This method controls the reaction zone by directing the gas flow, allowing precise coating formation without the need for reduced pressure environments.
[C23C 16/455] characterised by the method used for introducing gases into reaction chamber or for modifying gas flows in reaction chamber -- This subclass deals with metallic coating processes performed by chemical deposition or plating through decomposition, where the defining feature is the technique used to introduce gases into the reaction chamber or to modify gas flow during the operation.
