[C23C 16/45502] Flow conditions in reaction chamber -- The subclass C23C 16/45502 addresses the flow conditions inside reaction chambers used for chemical deposition or plating by decomposition, covering aspects such as gas or liquid velocity, turbulence, pressure, agitation and residence time that affect metallic coating formation. It pertains to the design and control of fluid dynamics within vapor-deposition, electro-plating or related reactors to achieve uniform and high-quality metal layers.
[C23C 16/45504] Laminar flow -- The C23C 16/45504 subclass covers the use of laminar flow in chemical deposition or plating by decomposition, specifying methods where a smooth, non-turbulent fluid stream is employed to promote uniform metallic coating formation on a substrate. It falls under the broader categories of chemistry, coating metallic material, and chemical deposition or plating by decomposition.
[C23C 16/45506] Turbulent flow -- C23C 16/45506 addresses turbulent flow in chemical deposition or plating by decomposition, specifying how intentionally turbulent fluid dynamics are employed to enhance mass transport, coating uniformity and adherence of metallic layers. It applies to processes that use high agitation or flow turbulence to achieve desired coating characteristics.
[C23C 16/45508] Radial flow -- C23C 16/45508 - Radial flow refers to a configuration where the plating solution moves radially outward or inward across the surface of a workpiece, often achieved by rotating electrodes or pipe arrangements, to promote uniform metal deposition in chemical deposition or plating by decomposition processes.
[C23C 16/4551] Jet streams -- Jet streams refers to the use of high-velocity gas or liquid jets to transport reactive species onto a substrate, causing chemical decomposition that deposits a metallic coating. The method is employed in processes such as plasma spraying or jet plating to form thin, uniform metallic films on various surfaces.
[C23C 16/45512] Premixing before introduction in the reaction chamber -- The entry covers processes in which the reactant components are premixed before being fed into the reaction chamber for chemical deposition or metallic plating by decomposition. It pertains to coating metallic materials where the mixed precursor stream is introduced as a single feed, facilitating uniform film formation.
[C23C 16/45514] Mixing in close vicinity to the substrate -- The C23C 16/45514 entry covers methods in which the reacting chemicals are mixed very close to the workpiece surface during a chemical deposition or plating process that proceeds by decomposition of the plating reagents. It addresses the arrangement of mixing zones, delivery streams or reactors so that the generated metal or alloy species form directly on the substrate, improving uniformity and controlling film properties.
[C23C 16/45517] Confinement of gases to vicinity of substrate -- The classification covers techniques that keep reactive gases close to the substrate surface during chemical deposition or plating by decomposition, using barriers, curtains, or localized flow control to limit gas dispersion and enhance film uniformity and adhesion. It applies to processes where gas confinement is essential for coating formation.
[C23C 16/45519] Inert gas curtains
[C23C 16/45521] the gas, other than thermal contact gas, being introduced the rear of the substrate to flow around its periphery -- This CPC subclass deals with processes in which a gas that is not a thermal contact gas is fed to the rear side of a substrate so that it travels around the perimeter during chemical deposition or plating by decomposition, helping to control coating uniformity and edge coverage.
[C23C 16/45523] Pulsed gas flow or change of composition over time -- C23C 16/45523 covers coating processes in which the flow of reactive gases is pulsed or the gas composition is varied over time during chemical deposition or plating by decomposition. By intermittently changing the gas supply, the method controls the nucleation, growth rate and properties of the metallic film formed on a substrate.
[C23C 16/45525] Atomic layer deposition [ALD] -- Atomic layer deposition is a thin-film coating technique that builds up material one atomic layer at a time by alternating gas-phase reactants that chemisorb on a metallic surface and react to form a uniform, conformal layer. The process allows precise control of composition and thickness for metallic coatings.
[C23C 16/45527] characterized by the ALD cycle, e.g. different flows or temperatures during half-reactions, unusual pulsing sequence, use of precursor mixtures or auxiliary reactants or activations -- This CPC subgroup covers chemical deposition or plating by decomposition using atomic-layer-deposition cycles that are distinguished by variations such as different gas flows or temperatures during the half-reactions, unconventional pulsing sequences, the use of mixed precursors, or the addition of auxiliary reactants or activation steps. It focuses on process-level modifications that affect the ALD cycle rather than the material being deposited.
[C23C 16/45529] specially adapted for making a layer stack of alternating different compositions or gradient compositions -- A process or apparatus for chemical deposition or plating by decomposition that is specially designed to build a multilayer coating in which successive layers have different compositions or a continuous gradient of composition, enabling precise control of material properties across the stack. This includes equipment adapted to alternate feedstocks or adjust deposition conditions to create such compositional variations.
[C23C 16/45531] specially adapted for making ternary or higher compositions -- This CPC subclass covers equipment, methods or formulations that are specially adapted to produce metallic coatings containing three or more elements-ternary or higher-order alloys-by chemical deposition or plating through decomposition. It includes designs that enable precise control of multi-component metal layers during the plating process.
[C23C 16/45534] Use of auxiliary reactants other than used for contributing to the composition of the main film, e.g. catalysts, activators or scavengers -- C23C 16/45534 covers the use of auxiliary substances that are not incorporated into the final metallic coating but are added during chemical deposition or plating by decomposition, such as catalysts, activators or scavengers that modify the reaction. These agents improve film formation without becoming part of the main film composition.
[C23C 16/45536] Use of plasma, radiation or electromagnetic fields -- C23C 16/45536 covers methods of depositing metallic coatings by inducing chemical decomposition with plasma, radiation or electromagnetic fields. The subclass includes techniques that use these energy sources to drive plating reactions, enabling thin-film formation on substrates without traditional chemical reducing agents.
[C23C 16/45538] Plasma being used continuously during the ALD cycle -- This CPC subclass covers processes in which a plasma is applied continuously throughout the atomic layer deposition (ALD) cycle to effect chemical deposition or plating of metallic materials. It addresses plasma-enhanced reactions that decompose precursor gases, enabling uniform metallic coating formation.
[C23C 16/4554] Plasma being used non-continuously in between ALD reactions  C23C16/56  takes precedence
[C23C 16/45542] Plasma being used non-continuously during the ALD reactions -- This CPC entry covers atomic-layer-deposition of metallic coatings in which plasma is introduced in discrete pulses rather than continuously, allowing precise control of surface reactions during each ALD cycle. The intermittent plasma assists the decomposition of precursors and improves film quality while fitting within the chemical deposition by decomposition subclass.
[C23C 16/45544] characterized by the apparatus -- C23C 16/45544 designates the apparatus used in chemical deposition or plating by decomposition of metallic materials, covering equipment such as plating baths, rollers, electrodes and control systems that enable the formation of metallic coatings. The subclass falls under the coating metallic material group in the CPC.
[C23C 16/45546] specially adapted for a substrate stack in the ALD reactor -- The C23C 16/45546 entry covers designs or features that are specifically adapted to hold or manipulate a stack of substrates within an atomic-layer-deposition (ALD) reactor. It relates to chemical deposition or plating processes that use successive surface reactions to build up thin films, focusing on the mechanical or structural adaptations that enable uniform coating of multiple layered substrates. This subclass falls under the broader category of coating metallic material by decomposition.
[C23C 16/45548] having arrangements for gas injection at different locations of the reactor for each ALD half-reaction -- The subclass concerns atomic-layer-deposition reactors that use separate gas-injection points so that the precursor and reactant streams can be introduced at different locations for each half-reaction cycle, allowing precise control of film growth on metallic substrates. It falls under chemical deposition or plating by decomposition of metallic coatings.
[C23C 16/45551] for relative movement of the substrate and the gas injectors or half-reaction reactor compartments -- The subclass C23C 16/45551 covers processes in which the workpiece or substrate is moved relative to the gas injectors or separate half-reaction reactor compartments during chemical deposition or plating by decomposition, enabling controlled interaction of the reactant gases with the surface. This relative motion may be used to achieve uniform coating, gradient thickness, or selective deposition in vapor-phase metallisation techniques.
[C23C 16/45553] characterized by the use of precursors specially adapted for ALD -- A CPC subclass for chemical deposition or plating by decomposition of metallic coatings in which atomic-layer-deposition (ALD) processes employ precursors that have been specially engineered for that purpose. The entry falls under chemistry, coating metallic material, and focuses on the use of tailored ALD precursors.
[C23C 16/45555] applied in non-semiconductor technology -- C23C 16/45555 covers chemical deposition or plating methods that create metallic coatings through decomposition reactions, specifically for applications outside semiconductor devices. It includes processes that form protective, conductive or decorative metal layers on various substrates used in general industrial, automotive or consumer products. This entry falls under the broader class of coating metallic material in the Cooperative Patent Classification.
[C23C 16/45557] Pulsed pressure or control pressure -- C23C 16/45557 falls under the CPC group for chemical deposition or plating by decomposition of metallic materials. It covers coating methods that employ pulsed or precisely controlled pressure to influence the deposition of metallic layers, improving uniformity, adhesion or microstructure.
[C23C 16/45559] Diffusion of reactive gas to substrate -- It covers processes in which a reactive gas diffuses onto a substrate during chemical deposition or plating to form metallic coatings. The entry addresses control of diffusion parameters such as gas composition, temperature and pressure to achieve the desired coating properties.
[C23C 16/45561] Gas plumbing upstream of the reaction chamber -- The CPC entry C23C 16/45561 covers the arrangement of gas supply lines and associated piping that deliver reactive gases to the area before the reaction chamber in processes where a metallic coating is formed by chemical decomposition. It relates to the upstream plumbing that conditions, distributes or pre-heats the gas for deposition.
[C23C 16/45563] Gas nozzles -- The C23C 16/45563 entry defines gas nozzles used to deliver reactive gases in chemical deposition or plating by decomposition, where the nozzle's geometry, flow control, heating or distribution features are engineered to ensure uniform metallic coating on a substrate. It focuses on designs that influence gas-to-surface interaction during vapor-phase coating processes.
[C23C 16/45565] Shower nozzles -- The C23C 16/45565 subclass pertains to shower-type nozzles employed in chemical deposition or plating processes that rely on decomposition of a plating solution. It covers the design and operation of nozzle assemblies that atomize or direct the reactive fluid onto a workpiece to form metallic coatings.
[C23C 16/45568] Porous nozzles -- The CPC subclass C23C 16/45568 covers porous nozzles employed in chemical deposition or plating processes that involve decomposition of a vapor-phase precursor. These nozzles release the reactive species through a porous structure to achieve uniform metallic coating on substrates. The classification pertains to coating metallic material via this specific nozzle technology.
[C23C 16/4557] Heated nozzles -- C23C 16/4557 covers heated nozzles that supply vaporised precursor material in chemical deposition or plating processes. The classification applies to nozzle designs that are externally or internally heated to control temperature and flow of gases or liquids during metallic coating formation, such as in CVD or PVD techniques.
[C23C 16/45572] Cooled nozzles -- C23C 16/45572 covers cooled nozzles used in chemical deposition or plating processes for metallic coatings. The invention relates to nozzle designs that incorporate cooling means to control temperature and improve deposit uniformity during the coating of metallic materials.
[C23C 16/45574] Nozzles for more than one gas -- This subclass covers devices that deliver multiple gases simultaneously to a plating bath or reaction zone, enabling co-deposition or reactive plating processes. It includes multi-channel or dual-gas nozzles used for chemical vapor deposition, electrolytic plating, or other decomposition-based coating methods.
[C23C 16/45576] Coaxial inlets for each gas -- The subclass C23C 16/45576 covers apparatus or methods that use separate coaxial gas inlets to deliver distinct reactant gases during a chemical deposition or plating process by decomposition, allowing precise control of each gas stream as it contacts the substrate. This design is applied in metallic coating operations where multiple gases must be introduced simultaneously but independently.
[C23C 16/45578] Elongated nozzles, tubes with holes -- This subclass pertains to metallic coating processes in which an elongated nozzle or tubular component containing one or more holes is coated by chemical deposition or plating that occurs through decomposition of a precursor, forming a metallic layer on the shaped part.
[C23C 16/4558] Perforated rings -- The C23C 16/4558 subclass covers processes for forming metallic rings that contain perforations by means of chemical deposition or plating through decomposition reactions, such as electrolytic or electroless plating that creates a ring with holes for filtration, flow control or structural purposes. This falls under the broader chemistry area of coating metallic material.
[C23C 16/45582] Expansion of gas before it reaches the substrate -- The CPC entry C23C 16/45582 covers methods in which a reactive gas is allowed to expand or decompress before it contacts the substrate during chemical deposition or plating by decomposition. This expansion improves uniformity and control of the resulting metallic coating, often used in vapor-phase or plasma-enhanced processes. It falls under the broader categories of chemistry, coating metallic material, and chemical deposition by decomposition.
[C23C 16/45585] Compression of gas before it reaches the substrate -- C23C 16/45585 covers techniques that compress a reactive gas stream before it contacts the substrate during chemical deposition or plating by decomposition. By increasing pressure, the gas density and flow are controlled, influencing film uniformity, adhesion and deposition rate.
[C23C 16/45587] Mechanical means for changing the gas flow -- C23C 16/45587 refers to mechanical devices that alter the flow of gases during chemical deposition or plating by decomposition, such as valves, nozzles, or flow-control mechanisms used in metallic coating processes. These means are intended to regulate gas distribution, pressure or direction to achieve uniform metal layers on substrates.
[C23C 16/45589] Movable means, e.g. fans -- C23C 16/45589 refers to the inclusion of movable components, such as fans or agitators, within chemical deposition or plating apparatuses. These devices provide airflow, stirring or other mechanical motion to improve the distribution of reactive gases or liquids, thereby enhancing uniformity and quality of metallic coatings applied by decomposition.
[C23C 16/45591] Fixed means, e.g. wings, baffles -- This CPC subclass relates to chemical deposition or plating by decomposition in which stationary structures such as wings, baffles or other fixed means are employed to direct, shape or confine the metal coating as it forms on a substrate.
[C23C 16/45593] Recirculation of reactive gases -- This subclass covers processes that recycle reactive gases used in chemical deposition or plating by decomposition, improving efficiency, reducing waste, and maintaining coating quality. It includes methods, apparatuses and control strategies for capturing, purifying and re-using gases generated or consumed during the plating operation.
[C23C 16/45595] Atmospheric CVD gas inlets with no enclosed reaction chamber -- This subclass covers chemical vapor deposition methods that introduce precursor gases to a metal substrate under ambient pressure without a closed reactor; the inlet system delivers the gases directly to the surface, relying on an open or localized atmosphere for the decomposition and metal coating.
[C23C 16/45597] Reactive back side gas -- C23C 16/45597 covers the use of reactive gases that are generated on the opposite side of a workpiece during a chemical deposition or plating process by decomposition. These gases participate in forming a metallic coating, often to improve adhesion or modify composition. The classification falls under coating metallic material in the chemistry sector.
[C23C 16/458] characterised by the method used for supporting substrates in the reaction chamber -- C23C 16/458 covers coating metallic materials by chemical deposition or plating where the classification is defined by the method used to support the substrates inside the reaction chamber, such as fixtures, carriers, or holders that position and secure the workpieces during the decomposition-driven process.
[C23C 16/4581] characterised by material of construction or surface finish of the means for supporting the substrate -- The subclass C23C 16/4581 refers to deposition or plating processes in which the support for the substrate is defined by the material it is made from or by a particular surface finish, influencing the chemical decomposition-based coating. It applies to methods that explicitly specify the construction material or surface treatment of the means that hold the workpiece.
[C23C 16/4582] Rigid and flat substrates, e.g. plates or discs  C23C16/4581  takes precedence -- The subclass C23C 16/4582 covers methods for chemically depositing metallic coatings on rigid, flat substrates such as plates or discs, using decomposition-based plating processes. It lies within the broader area of coating metallic material by chemical deposition, focusing on solid, planar surfaces rather than flexible or irregular shapes.
[C23C 16/4583] the substrate being supported substantially horizontally -- C23C 16/4583 covers chemical deposition or plating processes in which the workpiece (substrate) is held essentially flat, i.e., supported substantially horizontally during the reaction. This positioning is typical for batch or continuous vapour-phase plating where uniform coating is achieved on a horizontally oriented surface.
[C23C 16/4584] the substrate being rotated -- The C23C 16/4584 subclass covers coating processes in which the workpiece or substrate is rotated during chemical deposition or plating by decomposition, such as electroless or chemical vapor deposition. Rotating the substrate promotes uniform film thickness, improves mass transport, and reduces localized buildup of reaction products.
[C23C 16/4585] Devices at or outside the perimeter of the substrate support, e.g. clamping rings, shrouds -- Devices positioned at, or outside, the edge of a substrate holder used in chemical deposition or plating by decomposition, such as clamping rings and shrouds that secure or isolate the workpiece during the coating process.
[C23C 16/4586] Elements in the interior of the support, e.g. electrodes, heating or cooling devices -- This CPC subclass covers coating of metallic materials where the substrate incorporates internal components such as electrodes, heating or cooling devices. It applies to processes that use these interior elements to facilitate chemical deposition or plating by decomposition.
[C23C 16/4587] the substrate being supported substantially vertically -- The code C23C 16/4587 designates a chemical deposition or plating-by-decomposition process in which the workpiece is held substantially vertical, i.e., supported in a mainly upright position, during the coating operation. This orientation is used to influence film uniformity, drainage of electrolytes, or to suit specific line-of-sight deposition geometries.
[C23C 16/4588] the substrate being rotated -- This CPC subclass covers chemical deposition or plating processes in which the workpiece is rotated while the coating is formed by decomposition of a precursor. Rotating the substrate promotes uniform mass-transfer and consistent layer thickness, improving coating quality and reducing localized buildup.
[C23C 16/46] characterised by the method used for heating the substrate -- This CPC subgroup pertains to metallic coating processes carried out by chemical deposition or plating through decomposition where the distinguishing factor is the way the substrate is heated. It includes methods such as induction, flame, resistive or other heating techniques used to raise the substrate temperature during the coating operation.
[C23C 16/463] Cooling of the substrate -- The CPC subclass C23C 16/463 addresses methods for cooling the substrate during chemical deposition or decomposition plating processes. It includes techniques such as water, air or cryogenic cooling applied to the workpiece to control temperature, improve coating uniformity and reduce thermal stress.
[C23C 16/466] using thermal contact gas -- C23C 16/466 covers methods of metallic coating in which a gas generated by thermal contact is employed as the reactant that decomposes to deposit metal onto a substrate. The approach is used in chemical deposition or plating processes where heat-induced gas evolution supplies the metallic species for film formation. It falls under the broader category of chemical deposition or plating by decomposition within coating metallic material.
[C23C 16/48] by irradiation, e.g. photolysis, radiolysis, particle radiation -- The C23C 16/48 subclass of the Cooperative Patent Classification covers chemical deposition or plating processes that rely on the decomposition of a precursor material through irradiation. It includes methods such as photolysis, radiolysis and the use of particle radiation to induce metallic coating formation on a substrate.
[C23C 16/481] by radiant heating of the substrate -- This subclass covers methods of depositing or plating a metallic coating in which the substrate is heated by radiant energy to trigger chemical decomposition of a metal-containing precursor, forming a metal film directly on the surface without the use of electrodes or plasma.
[C23C 16/482] using incoherent light, UV to IR, e.g. lamps -- C23C 16/482 covers processes for chemically depositing or plating metallic surfaces that are driven by broad-band incoherent radiation such as ultraviolet, visible or infrared lamps. The method uses light energy to decompose plating solutions and form a metal coating without the need for lasers or other coherent sources.
[C23C 16/483] using coherent light, UV to IR, e.g. lasers -- C23C 16/483 covers methods of depositing or plating metallic materials by decomposing precursors with coherent light such as lasers, spanning ultraviolet to infrared wavelengths. The classification addresses processes that use directed optical energy to drive chemical reactions for metal coating formation.
[C23C 16/484] using X-ray radiation -- C23C 16/484 pertains to chemical deposition or plating of metallic materials that is achieved by using X-ray radiation to decompose precursors or to reduce metal ions onto a substrate. The classification includes X-ray-induced sputtering, photochemical reduction and related techniques for forming metallic coatings.
[C23C 16/485] using synchrotron radiation -- C23C 16/485 covers processes that employ synchrotron radiation to induce chemical deposition or plating by decomposition of a precursor material onto a metallic substrate. The high-intensity, tunable X-ray beam enables precise control of film composition and thickness, often used for advanced coating applications.
[C23C 16/486] using ion beam radiation -- C23C 16/486 covers the use of ion-beam radiation to effect chemical deposition or plating by decomposition of a metallic material onto a substrate. It pertains to processes where energetic ions decompose precursors, forming metallic coatings through a controlled, beam-driven reaction. This falls within the broader CPC class for coating metallic material.
[C23C 16/487] using electron radiation -- A process for depositing metallic coatings in which an electron beam or other electron radiation decomposes a metal-containing precursor, causing metal reduction and film formation on a substrate. It is classified under CPC C23C 16/487, the subsection of chemical deposition or plating by decomposition that uses electron radiation.
[C23C 16/488] Protection of windows for introduction of radiation into the coating chamber -- The C23C 16/488 subclass concerns methods and apparatus for protecting the windows through which radiation-such as light, ultraviolet or electron beams-is introduced into a coating chamber during chemical deposition or plating by decomposition. It includes shielding, cooling or material choices that prevent window damage from reactive vapours, thermal load or sputtering.
[C23C 16/50] using electric discharges -- C23C 16/50 refers to processes that form metallic coatings by decomposing a precursor material through electric discharges such as arcs, sparks, or plasma jets. The technique is used to deposit layers of metal, alloys or composites onto substrates without using conventional chemical baths, and includes methods like plasma spraying, arc-jet deposition and spark discharge plating.
[C23C 16/503] using DC or AC discharges -- The subclass C23C 16/503 covers chemical deposition or plating processes that create metallic coatings by using direct-current (DC) or alternating-current (AC) electrical discharges, such as plasma or electro-arc techniques, to decompose plating solutions and deposit metal onto a substrate.
[C23C 16/505] using radio frequency discharges -- C23C 16/505 refers to the use of radio-frequency discharges to generate the reactive species needed for chemical deposition or plating of metallic coatings. The subclass includes RF-produced plasmas that decompose precursors and deposit metal films on substrates, typically in vapor-phase processes such as plasma-enhanced chemical vapor deposition.
[C23C 16/507] using external electrodes, e.g. in tunnel type reactors -- The CPC subclass C23C 16/507 covers processes that deposit metallic coatings by chemical decomposition where external electrodes are employed, such as in tunnel-type reactors. It falls under chemical deposition or plating by decomposition within the coating metallic material group.
[C23C 16/509] using internal electrodes -- C23C 16/509 relates to chemical deposition or plating by decomposition in which the electric current is supplied by electrodes positioned inside the plating bath, rather than by external electrodes, to form metallic coatings. This subclass addresses internal-electrode methods used for producing uniform metallic layers on workpieces.
[C23C 16/5093] Coaxial electrodes -- C23C 16/5093 covers coaxial electrode configurations employed in chemical deposition or plating by decomposition. The code pertains to metallic coating processes where the anode and cathode are arranged along a common axis to achieve uniform metal film growth on substrates. It falls under the broader categories of chemistry, metallic material coating, and chemical deposition.
[C23C 16/5096] Flat-bed apparatus -- The C23C 16/5096 entry defines a flat-bed apparatus used for chemical deposition or plating by decomposition. In this equipment the substrate rests on a planar surface while reactive gases decompose to form a metallic coating, often employed in vacuum or atmospheric processes. It distinguishes flat-bed configurations from rollers, drums or other moving-band systems.
[C23C 16/511] using microwave discharges -- The CPC subclass C23C 16/511 covers processes for forming metallic coatings by chemical deposition where the reducing agent is generated through microwave discharges. It pertains to plating methods that decompose a metal-containing gas or solution using microwave energy to deposit a metal layer.
[C23C 16/513] using plasma jets -- C23C 16/513 pertains to methods that use plasma jets to deposit metallic coatings on a substrate. It is classified under chemical deposition or plating by decomposition, where a high-energy plasma generated from a gas stream reduces metal-containing compounds to form a metallic layer, a technique employed in advanced surface-engineering and thin-film manufacturing.
[C23C 16/515] using pulsed discharges -- C23C 16/515 covers the use of pulsed electrical discharges to decompose a source material and deposit a metallic coating on a substrate. The classification includes processes such as pulsed plasma or pulsed arc plating where the discharge is periodically switched on and off to control film growth. It falls within chemical deposition or plating by decomposition of metallic materials.
[C23C 16/517] using a combination of discharges covered by two or more of groups -- The CPC subclass C23C 16/517 covers processes for chemical deposition or plating by decomposition in which two or more discharge types-such as plasma, arc, corona or spark discharges-are employed together to generate the reactive species that form a metallic coating.
[C23C 16/52] Controlling or regulating the coating process -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Control of diamond crystallography -> C23C16/279 - Pulsed pressure or control pressure -> C23C16/45557
[C23C 16/54] Apparatus specially adapted for continuous coating -- C23C 16/54 covers machines designed specifically for continuous deposition of metallic coatings through chemical decomposition processes such as electroless plating. These apparatuses enable uninterrupted application of metal layers onto substrates, providing consistent thickness and efficient production in industrial coating operations.
[C23C 16/545] for coating elongated substrates -- C23C 16/545 relates to chemical deposition or plating by decomposition techniques used to apply a metallic coating onto elongated substrates such as wires, rods or tubes.
[C23C 16/56] After-treatment -- The subclass C23C 16/56 covers after-treatment steps applied to metallic coatings produced by chemical deposition or plating through decomposition. It includes processes such as heat treatment, annealing, aging, surface finishing or other modifications carried out after the initial coating has been formed to improve properties, relieve stresses or enhance performance.
[C23C 18/00] Chemical coating by decomposition of either liquid compounds or solutions of the coating forming compounds, without leaving reaction products of surface material in the coating -- **Definition:** This place covers:  **Glossary:** - Contact plating: Plating of metal surface with a more electropositive metal
[C23C 18/02] by thermal decomposition -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes, apparatus compositions or compounds for chemical coating by thermal decomposition.  Processes of chemical coating by thermal decomposition characterised by the deposition of material other than inorganic material and involving particles  Apparatus for deposition of particles in general  Process of chemical coating by thermal decomposition characterised by the deposition of metallic material including particles.
[C23C 18/04] Pretreatment of the material to be coated -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Coating on selected surface areas, e.g. using masks -> C23C18/06

[C23C 18/08] characterised by the deposition of metallic material -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Coating for the deposition of metallic material per se and coating for the deposition of aluminium per se through thermal decomposition.
[C23C 18/10] Deposition of aluminium only -- C23C 18/10 concerns processes that form a pure aluminium layer on a substrate by chemical coating, usually through decomposition of a liquid aluminium-containing precursor so that only aluminium remains on the surface without residual reaction products.
[C23C 18/12] characterised by the deposition of inorganic material other than metallic material -- **Definition:** This place covers:  processes and product thereof whereby an inorganic material is deposited through thermal decomposition of its reactant/precursor  apparatus for said process and manufacture of product
[C23C 18/1204] inorganic material, e.g. non-oxide and non-metallic such as sulfides, nitrides based compounds -- C23C 18/1204 relates to inorganic coating materials that are neither oxides nor metallic, such as sulfides and nitrides, which are applied by chemical decomposition of liquid or solution precursors. The process forms a coating without leaving reaction products of the substrate in the film. It falls under chemical coating by decomposition of liquid compounds.
[C23C 18/1208] Oxides, e.g. ceramics -- C23C 18/1208 pertains to chemical coatings formed by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions that contain oxide-forming ingredients, resulting in ceramic-type oxides applied to metallic surfaces. The process deposits the oxide coating without leaving reaction products of the substrate material, and is classified under the cooperative EPC/USPTO scheme for metallic coating methods.
[C23C 18/1212] Zeolites, glasses -- This subclass concerns the formation of inorganic protective layers of zeolite or glass on metallic substrates by decomposing liquid precursors or solutions, creating a coating without leaving reaction products of the underlying surface in the film.
[C23C 18/1216] Metal oxides  C23C18/1212  takes precedence -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes, compositions for chemical coating by thermal decomposition characterised by the deposition of metal oxides other than zeolites or glasses.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Coating of Zeolites, glasses -> C23C18/1212
[C23C 18/122] Inorganic polymers, e.g. silanes, polysilazanes, polysiloxanes -- The subclass C23C 18/122 covers coating methods that create inorganic polymer films, such as those formed from silanes, polysilazanes or polysiloxanes, by decomposing liquid precursors or solutions. The process deposits a polymer layer on the metal surface without leaving reaction products of the substrate in the coating.
[C23C 18/1225] Deposition of multilayers of inorganic material -- C23C 18/1225 covers chemical coating processes in which inorganic layers are built up by decomposing liquid precursors or solutions, forming successive thin films without leaving reaction residues on the substrate. The subclass specifically addresses the deposition of multilayered inorganic structures, such as alternating metal oxides or nitrides, created through successive decomposition steps to achieve engineered coating properties.
[C23C 18/1229] Composition of the substrate -- This subclass concerns the material makeup of the metallic substrate that receives a chemical coating applied by decomposition of liquid precursors. It covers the elemental or alloy composition, any additives, and surface conditioning of the substrate that affect the coating process and the final properties.
[C23C 18/1233] Organic substrates -- The CPC subgroup C23C 18/1233 concerns chemical coating of metallic surfaces by decomposition of liquid compounds or solutions that contain organic substrates, in which the coating-forming material breaks down on the metal without leaving any reaction products of the substrate in the finished coating.
[C23C 18/1237] Composite substrates, e.g. laminated, premixed -- Covers composite metal substrate structures such as laminated or premixed layers that serve as bases for chemical coatings applied by decomposition of liquid compounds, without leaving reaction products on the surface. The classification addresses the preparation and use of these multi-material substrates in processes that generate the coating in situ from solution or liquid precursors.
[C23C 18/1241] Metallic substrates
[C23C 18/1245] Inorganic substrates other than metallic -- C23C 18/1245 relates to chemical coating of inorganic, non-metallic substrates by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions of coating-forming substances, forming a layer without leaving reaction products of the substrate in the coating. It falls under the hierarchy CHEMISTRY → COATING METALLIC MATERIAL → COATING METALLIC MATERIAL, specifically addressing substrates other than metallic.
[C23C 18/125] Process of deposition of the inorganic material -- C23C 18/125 covers processes for depositing inorganic materials as metallic coatings by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions on a substrate, forming a coating without leaving reaction-product residues on the surface. It falls under chemical coating of metallic material in the CPC hierarchy.
[C23C 18/1254] Sol or sol-gel processing -- C23C 18/1254 relates to metallic coatings produced by sol or sol-gel techniques, where liquid precursors decompose and solidify into a continuous metal layer without leaving reaction products of the substrate in the coating. The method converts a solution or colloidal sol into a gel that ultimately forms the metallic coating.
[C23C 18/1258] Spray pyrolysis -- Spray pyrolysis is a chemical coating technique in which a liquid solution of coating precursors is atomized and directed onto a heated surface, causing rapid solvent evaporation and thermal decomposition of the precursors to form a uniform metallic coating while leaving no residue from the substrate.
[C23C 18/1262] involving particles, e.g. carbon nanotubes [CNT], flakes -- This subclass covers chemical coating methods in which a liquid or solution of coating-forming compounds decomposes on a metallic surface, leaving a coating that incorporates solid particles such as carbon nanotubes or flakes, without depositing reaction products of the substrate. It pertains to metallic material coatings formed by in-situ decomposition of the coating precursor.
[C23C 18/1266] Particles formed  in situ -- This subclass concerns metallic coating processes where the coating particles are generated directly on the substrate during the chemical decomposition of a liquid or solution of coating-forming compounds, rather than being added from an external source. The in-situ formed particles become part of the deposited layer as the reaction proceeds, typically by thermal or pyrolytic decomposition. It applies to methods that create the coating and its constituent particles simultaneously.
[C23C 18/127] Preformed particles -- C23C 18/127 covers coating metallic surfaces by applying preformed particles from liquid or solution precursors that decompose on the substrate, forming a coating without leaving reaction products of the surface material. The particles serve as the coating material in a chemical deposition process.
[C23C 18/1275] performed under inert atmosphere -- The C23C 18/1275 subclass covers processes for chemically coating metallic surfaces by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions of coating-forming substances, performed in an inert atmosphere to prevent unwanted reactions with the substrate. This method avoids leaving reaction products of the base material in the coating, ensuring a clean, uniform metallic layer.
[C23C 18/1279] performed under reactive atmosphere, e.g. oxidising or reducing atmospheres -- This subclass covers processes where a metallic surface is coated by thermally decomposing liquid or solution precursors in a reactive gas environment such as oxidation or reduction, ensuring the coating forms without residual reaction products from the substrate. The reactive atmosphere influences the chemistry, enabling formation of metallic or oxide layers directly from the precursor.
[C23C 18/1283] Control of temperature, e.g. gradual temperature increase, modulation of temperature -- C23C 18/1283 covers methods for controlling the temperature during chemical coating processes that proceed by the decomposition of liquid compounds or solutions, such as applying a gradual temperature rise or modulating the heat level to influence the coating formation. This sub-category falls under metallic material coatings in the broader chemistry classification.
[C23C 18/1287] with flow inducing means, e.g. ultrasonic -- It covers chemical coating of metallic substrates by decomposing liquid or solution precursors, where a flow-inducing device such as an ultrasonic vibrator is employed to promote uniform film formation and adhesion.
[C23C 18/1291] by heating of the substrate -- C23C 18/1291 covers methods for applying a chemical coating to a metal surface where the coating is formed by thermally decomposing liquid precursors or solutions on the substrate, without leaving reaction residues from the substrate in the coating. The process involves heating the substrate to drive the decomposition and deposit the coating.
[C23C 18/1295] with after-treatment of the deposited inorganic material -- The subclass C23C 18/1295 covers chemical coating methods in which a metallic or inorganic layer is formed by decomposing liquid or solution precursors, and thereafter the deposited inorganic material undergoes an additional treatment-such as heating, annealing, polishing, chemical conversion, or surface modification-to enhance its properties, adhesion, or durability. This after-treatment step is integral to the coating process and is applied after the initial deposition.
[C23C 18/14] Decomposition by irradiation, e.g. photolysis, particle radiation -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Process for deposition of metallic or inorganic material through decomposition by irradiation.
[C23C 18/143] Radiation by light, e.g. photolysis or pyrolysis -- C23C 18/143 covers the formation of metallic coatings by decomposing liquid or solution-borne coating compounds using light energy such as photolysis or pyrolysis. The process creates a coating while the original surface material remains unchanged and no reaction residues are incorporated.
[C23C 18/145] Radiation by charged particles, e.g. electron beams or ion irradiation -- This subclass covers the use of charged-particle radiation, such as electron beams or ion streams, to decompose liquid or solution coating precursors on metallic substrates, forming a chemical coating without leaving reaction products from the substrate material.
[C23C 18/16] by reduction or substitution, e.g. electroless plating -- **Definition:** This place covers:  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Contact plating -> C23C18/54  **Glossary:** - Electroless plating: Process of depositing a coating with the aid of a chemical reducing agent in solution and without the application of external electrical power
[C23C 18/1601] Process or apparatus -- **Definition:** This place covers:  - Process or apparatus for chemical coating by reduction or substitution, for example:
[C23C 18/1603] coating on selected surface areas -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Coatings whereby the electroless coating is patterned.
[C23C 18/1605] by masking -- A chemical coating applied via decomposition of a liquid or solution that leaves no reaction products on the substrate, created by using a mask to define the coated areas. The masking technique protects selected regions while the coating forms only on the exposed surface.
[C23C 18/1607] by direct patterning
[C23C 18/1608] from pretreatment step, i.e. selective pre-treatment -- The subclass C23C 18/1608 addresses chemical coating processes that begin with a selective pretreatment of a metallic surface before applying a coating formed by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions, ensuring the coating forms without leaving reaction-product residues on the substrate.
[C23C 18/161] from plating step, e.g. inkjet -- C23C 18/161 covers processes that form a metallic coating by chemically decomposing a liquid or solution of coating compounds during a plating step, for example using inkjet deposition. The method creates a metal layer without leaving reaction products of the substrate in the coating.
[C23C 18/1612] through irradiation means -- This subclass covers chemical coating of metallic surfaces by decomposing liquid or solution precursors with irradiation means such as UV light, lasers or electron beams, ensuring that no reaction products of the substrate remain in the resulting coating.
[C23C 18/1614] plating on one side -- C23C 18/1614 covers methods for chemically forming a metallic coating on only one side of a workpiece by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions that supply the coating metal, resulting in a metal layer that does not contain reaction products of the substrate material.
[C23C 18/1616] interior or inner surface -- C23C 18/1616 covers chemical coating processes in which a liquid or solution of coating-forming compounds is decomposed to form a coating on the interior or inner surfaces of metallic articles, without leaving reaction products of the substrate in the coating. The classification applies to methods that create protective or functional layers inside hollow or enclosed metal parts by in-situ decomposition of the coating material.
[C23C 18/1617] Purification and regeneration of coating baths -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Process whereby the electroless coating bath is purified or regenerated.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Control of the bath/process -> C23C18/1601
[C23C 18/1619] Apparatus for electroless plating -- This subclass covers devices used to perform electroless plating, a chemical deposition process where metal coats a substrate without external electric current, typically by reducing metal ions from a solution. The apparatus may include containers, agitation systems, heating elements, and means to control solution composition to ensure uniform metallic coating.
[C23C 18/1621] Protection of inner surfaces of the apparatus -- C23C 18/1621 pertains to methods for protecting the inner surfaces of apparatuses by applying a chemical coating that forms through decomposition of liquid compounds or solutions, leaving no reaction products of the substrate material in the coating.
[C23C 18/1623] through electrochemical processes -- C23C 18/1623 covers coating a metallic substrate by electrochemical means in which a liquid or solution of coating-forming compounds is decomposed on the surface, forming a chemical coating without leaving reaction-product residues of the substrate material. The process relies on anodic or cathodic reactions to deposit the coating directly from the electrolyte.
[C23C 18/1625] through chemical processes -- This subclass covers formation of metallic coatings by chemical decomposition of liquid precursors directly on the substrate, leaving no reaction products of the surface material in the coating. It includes processes where a solution or molten compound breaks down in situ to produce a pure metal layer. The focus is on chemical reactions rather than physical deposition methods.
[C23C 18/1626] through mechanical processes -- C23C 18/1626 concerns applying a metallic coating formed by decomposing liquid or solution compounds through mechanical actions such as spraying, brushing or rubbing, wherein no reaction products of the substrate remain in the coating. It falls within the broader class of chemical coating of metallic materials.
[C23C 18/1628] Specific elements or parts of the apparatus -- C23C 18/1628 refers to chemical coating of metallic surfaces by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions of coating-forming substances so that no reaction products of the substrate remain in the coating, and it concerns particular elements or parts of the coating apparatus.
[C23C 18/163] Supporting devices for articles to be coated -- C23C 18/163 covers devices that hold or support articles while they undergo chemical metallic coating by decomposition of liquid compounds, ensuring stable positioning and uniform coating application, such as fixtures, racks, pallets or similar support structures used in coating operations.
[C23C 18/1632] Features specific for the apparatus, e.g. layout of cells and of its equipment, multiple cells -- The subclass concerns design aspects of apparatus for chemical metallic coating by decomposition of liquids, focusing on the layout of coating cells and related equipment, including configurations with multiple cells. It classifies structural features of the coating system rather than the coating composition.
[C23C 18/1633] Process of electroless plating -- C23C 18/1633 covers electroless plating processes in which a metallic coating is formed by chemically decomposing liquid compounds or solutions containing the plating material, depositing metal onto a substrate without using external electric current and leaving no reaction products of the surface material in the coating.
[C23C 18/1635] Composition of the substrate -- C23C 18/1635 covers the composition of the substrate that receives a chemical metallic coating applied by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions of coating precursors, where no reaction products of the surface remain in the coating. It focuses on the material, alloying elements, or surface treatment of the underlying metal that affect coating performance.
[C23C 18/1637] metallic substrate
[C23C 18/1639] Substrates other than metallic, e.g. inorganic or organic or non-conductive -- The CPC entry C23C 18/1639 covers chemical coating processes in which a liquid or solution of coating-forming compounds is decomposed on a substrate that is not metallic, such as inorganic, organic or other non-conductive materials, and the resulting coating contains no reaction products from the substrate itself. This falls under the broader categories of chemistry and metallic material coating, specifically dealing with non-metal substrates.
[C23C 18/1641] Organic substrates, e.g. resin, plastic -- C23C 18/1641 covers the use of organic substrates such as resins or plastics as the underlying material when applying a metallic coating formed by thermal decomposition of liquid precursors. The process deposits the metal without embedding reaction by-products of the substrate in the coating, allowing a clean metallic layer on non-metallic bases.
[C23C 18/1642] semiconductor  semiconductor  H10P14/48
[C23C 18/1644] porous substrates -- C23C 18/1644 relates to methods of chemically applying metallic coatings to porous substrates by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions that contain the coating-forming material. The process creates a metallic layer without leaving reaction-product residues on the surface, enabling uniform coating of porous structures. This subclass falls under chemical coating by decomposition of liquid precursors within the broader CPC hierarchy for metallic material coatings.
[C23C 18/1646] Characteristics of the product obtained -- This subclass concerns the examination of the properties of a metallic coating produced by decomposing liquid or solution precursors on a metal surface, including composition, thickness, hardness, adhesion, microstructure and other physical or chemical attributes of the final product. It is used to classify patents that describe how the resulting coating is characterized after the deposition process.
[C23C 18/1648] Porous product -- The C23C 18/1648 entry pertains to porous products formed by a chemical coating process in which liquid compounds or solutions decompose on the substrate, creating a metallic coating without leaving reaction-product residues on the surface. It falls under the broader categories of chemistry, metallic material coating, and coating metallic material.
[C23C 18/165] Multilayered product  layered product  B32B -- The CPC code C23C 18/165 defines multilayered metallic coating products created by chemically decomposing liquid compounds or solutions onto a metal surface, forming layered structures without leaving reaction residues. It falls under the chemistry area for chemical coatings of metallic materials and is linked to the B32B group of processes for producing such multilayered coatings.
[C23C 18/1651] Two or more layers only obtained by electroless plating -- C23C 18/1651 refers to processes that create two or more coating layers on a metal by electroless plating, i.e., chemical deposition without external current, where the layers are built sequentially using successive chemical reactions. This subclass falls under chemical coating by decomposition of liquids or solutions, applied to metallic materials.
[C23C 18/1653] Two or more layers with at least one layer obtained by electroless plating and one layer obtained by electroplating -- This subclass refers to metallic coatings formed as two or more layers in which at least one layer is deposited by electroless (chemical) plating and another layer by electroplating, applied by decomposition of liquid compounds or solutions without leaving reaction residues on the surface.
[C23C 18/1655] Process features -- C23C 18/1655 falls under the CPC group for coating metallic material by chemical means, specifically when a liquid or solution of coating-forming compounds is decomposed on the surface and no reaction products of the substrate remain in the coating. The "process features" subclass captures particular steps, conditions or apparatus details employed in these decomposition-based coating processes.
[C23C 18/1657] Electroless forming, i.e. substrate removed or destroyed at the end of the process -- C23C 18/1657 covers electroless forming where the coating is produced by chemical decomposition of a liquid or solution of coating-forming compounds and the original substrate is removed or destroyed after deposition. No reaction products of the substrate remain in the final coating.
[C23C 18/1658] with two steps starting with metal deposition followed by addition of reducing agent -- This subclass covers chemical coating methods in which a metallic layer is first deposited from a liquid compound or solution, followed by the addition of a reducing agent that converts the deposited material into a coating, while avoiding the formation of reaction products on the substrate surface. It is a two-step process of metal deposition and reduction within the broader group of coating metallic materials by decomposition of liquids.
[C23C 18/166] with two steps starting with addition of reducing agent followed by metal deposition -- In the CPC, subclass C23C covers chemical coating of metallic materials by decomposition of liquid compounds. The group 18/166 specifies a two-step process where a reducing agent is first added to the solution, then metal is deposited on the substrate. This method avoids leaving reaction products of the substrate in the coating.
[C23C 18/1662] Use of incorporated material in the solution or dispersion, e.g. particles, whiskers, wires -- This CPC subclass relates to chemical metallic coatings applied by decomposition of liquid compounds or solutions, where the coating includes dispersed or incorporated material such as particles, whiskers or wires that become part of the coating. It covers the use of these incorporated constituents within the coating solution or dispersion.
[C23C 18/1664] with additional means during the plating process -- C23C 18/1664 covers metallic coatings produced by chemical deposition from liquid precursors that decompose on the workpiece, leaving no reaction residues, and specifies that the plating operation employs additional means such as extra equipment, reagents or steps to modify the process. It falls under chemistry for coating metallic material, focusing on enhanced plating techniques beyond the basic chemical decomposition method.
[C23C 18/1666] Ultrasonics -- C23C 18/1666 designates the use of ultrasonic energy to decompose liquid or solution-based coating precursors on metallic substrates, creating a chemical coating without leaving reaction by-products on the surface. The method applies high-frequency sound waves to induce the required decomposition and film formation.
[C23C 18/1667] Radiant energy, e.g. laser -- The entry concerns coating metallic surfaces by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions using radiant energy such as laser beams, producing a metallic layer without leaving reaction-product residues on the substrate. It falls under chemical coating processes that employ light or other electromagnetic radiation to trigger the coating reaction.
[C23C 18/1669] Agitation, e.g. air introduction -- This subclass covers processes for forming metallic coatings by chemical decomposition of liquid precursors where agitation of the reaction zone is employed, for example by introducing air, stirring or bubbling, to improve mixing, heat transfer or deposition rates. It applies to coating methods that do not leave reaction products of the substrate in the final film.
[C23C 18/1671] Electric field -- C23C 18/1671 relates to metallic coatings formed by chemical decomposition of liquid precursors in which an applied electric field is used to initiate or accelerate the reaction and direct the coating onto the substrate, ensuring that no reaction products of the base material remain in the coating.
[C23C 18/1673] Magnetic field -- The C23C 18/1673 subclass pertains to metallic coating processes that rely on chemical decomposition of liquid precursors, where a magnetic field is applied to influence the deposition, plasma behavior, or orientation of the forming metal layer without leaving reaction residues on the substrate. It covers methods that use static or dynamic magnetic fields to control coating characteristics during the coating-by-decomposition step.
[C23C 18/1675] Process conditions -- C23C 18/1675 covers the specific process conditions used in chemical coating of metallic surfaces by thermal or catalytic decomposition of liquid precursors, where the coating forms without leaving reaction products of the substrate in the film. It falls under the chemistry hierarchy for metallic material coatings.
[C23C 18/1676] Heating of the solution -- The subclass C23C 18/1676 covers processes in which the coating solution is heated prior to or during its application. Heating promotes the decomposition of the coating-forming compounds, enabling the formation of a metallic layer without leaving reaction products from the substrate. This technique is used to improve coating uniformity and adhesion in chemical deposition of metallic materials.
[C23C 18/1678] Heating of the substrate -- The subclass C23C 18/1678 covers processes in which the coated substrate is heated after applying a chemical coating formed by decomposition of liquid or solution compounds. It includes heating steps such as annealing, curing, drying, or sintering that complete the coating, promote adhesion, or remove volatile by-products, without leaving reaction products of the surface material in the final layer.
[C23C 18/168] Control of temperature, e.g. temperature of bath, substrate -- C23C 18/168 relates to techniques for regulating temperature in processes that chemically deposit metallic coatings, including heating or cooling the coating bath, the substrate, or other reaction zones to control coating formation and properties. This includes devices, sensors and control systems used to maintain the desired temperature during the coating operation.
[C23C 18/1682] Control of atmosphere -- C23C 18/1682 covers methods for controlling the atmosphere during chemical coating of metallic parts by decomposing liquid or solution-borne coating precursors, ensuring the surrounding gas composition (inert, reactive or vacuum) is managed to influence coating formation and prevent unwanted reactions.
[C23C 18/1683] Control of electrolyte composition, e.g. measurement, adjustment  regeneration of bath  C23C18/1617 -- The CPC subclass C23C 18/1683 relates to methods and apparatus for controlling the electrolyte in chemical metallic coating baths that decompose liquid precursors, covering measurement, adjustment, and regeneration of the bath to maintain proper composition during the coating process.
[C23C 18/1685] with supercritical condition, e.g. chemical fluid deposition -- This CPC subclass C23C 18/1685 covers the production of metallic coatings by chemically decomposing liquid compounds or solutions on a surface while operating under supercritical conditions, such as supercritical fluid deposition, where the reaction leaves no residue of the initial reaction products on the coated material.
[C23C 18/1687] with ionic liquid -- C23C 18/1687 covers methods of applying metallic coatings by chemically decomposing liquid precursors or solutions where the coating involves an ionic liquid as the reaction medium or component, forming a metallic layer without leaving reaction residues on the substrate.
[C23C 18/1689] After-treatment -- C23C 18/1689 covers after-treatment steps applied to metallic surfaces that have been chemically coated by decomposition of liquid or solution precursors. The after-treatment may include curing, heating, polishing, or other modifications performed after the coating is deposited to enhance adhesion, durability, or appearance. It falls under the broader group for chemical metallic coatings.
[C23C 18/1691] Cooling, e g. forced or controlled cooling -- This sub-class covers the application of cooling, for example forced or controlled cooling, during chemical deposition of metallic coatings formed by thermal decomposition of liquid precursors, where no reaction products from the substrate remain in the coating.
[C23C 18/1692] Heat-treatment -- C23C 18/1692 covers heat-treatment operations applied to metallic surfaces that have been chemically coated by decomposition of liquids or solutions. It includes annealing, curing, sintering or other thermal processes used to modify the structure, adhesion, hardness or other properties of the resulting coating. This sub-class is part of the broader category of chemical coatings on metallic materials.
[C23C 18/1694] Sequential heat treatment -- Sequential heat treatment refers to a series of controlled heating steps applied to a metallic substrate after it has been chemically coated by decomposition of liquid precursors. The process adjusts the microstructure, relieves residual stresses and enhances adhesion or functional properties of the coating without introducing additional reaction products.
[C23C 18/1696] Control of atmosphere -- C23C 18/1696 addresses the control of the surrounding atmosphere during chemical coating of metallic substrates by decomposition of liquid compounds or solutions. It includes methods for adjusting gas composition, pressure, temperature or flow to influence the deposition and quality of the resulting coating.
[C23C 18/1698] Control of temperature -- The code C23C 18/1698 covers techniques for managing temperature while chemically coating metallic surfaces through the decomposition of liquid precursors or solutions. It includes methods that regulate heating or cooling to achieve uniform film formation and avoid adverse thermal effects on the substrate.
[C23C 18/18] Pretreatment of the material to be coated -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Pretreatment not specific to a particular substrate as well as pretreatment of metallic substrate to be coated.  **Glossary:** - Sensitising in C23C18/28 and lower: pre-treatment to the activation step by activation of a reducing agent on the substrate surface for promoting the formation of metallic clusters on the substrate surface during the subsequent activation step, e.g. Sn based solution - Activating in C23C18/28 and lower: Formation of catalytic site on the substrate surface by reduction of metal ions and deposition of metallic clusters, thereby facilitating subsequent electroless plating steps, e.g. Pd, Ag, Au, based solution
[C23C 18/1803] of metallic material surfaces or of a non-specific material surfaces -- C23C 18/1803 covers chemical coatings formed by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions that contain the coating material, resulting in a coating that does not leave reaction products of the substrate. The process is applied to metallic surfaces as well as to surfaces that are not specifically defined, providing a general method for depositing metallic or other types of coatings via in-situ chemical transformation.
[C23C 18/1806] by mechanical pretreatment, e.g. grinding, sanding -- This subgroup covers chemical coating processes where the substrate is mechanically pretreated, such as by grinding or sanding, before applying a coating formed by decomposition of a liquid or solution, ensuring no reaction products remain on the surface.
[C23C 18/181] by formation of electrostatic charges, e.g. tribofriction -- C23C 18/181 refers to a chemical coating process for metallic substrates where the coating is deposited by generating electrostatic charges, for example through tribofriction, to attract and bind decomposed coating-forming compounds onto the surface.
[C23C 18/1813] by radiant energy -- C23C 18/1813 covers chemical deposition of metallic coatings from liquid precursors that are decomposed by radiant energy, such as laser or UV light, without incorporating reaction products from the substrate into the coating. It belongs to the CPC class C23C for coating metallic material, a sub-group of chemical coating processes.
[C23C 18/1817] Heat -- A heat treatment applied during chemical coating of a metal surface by thermal decomposition of liquid or solution-based coating precursors, where the coating forms without leaving reaction products of the substrate in the film. This subclass covers the use of temperature to drive the coating reaction and control film formation on metallic materials.
[C23C 18/182] Radiation, e.g. UV, laser -- This subclass covers the use of radiation, such as ultraviolet light or laser beams, to decompose liquid or solution-based coating precursors on metallic surfaces, forming a coating while leaving no reaction products of the substrate in the film. It falls under chemical coating of metallic materials by decomposition.
[C23C 18/1824] by chemical pretreatment -- The C23C 18/1824 subclass covers chemical pretreatment steps used before applying a metallic coating formed by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions on a substrate. It includes processes that modify the surface chemically, such as cleaning, etching or activating, to improve adhesion of the subsequent coating without leaving reaction residues on the metal.
[C23C 18/1827] only one step pretreatment -- C23C 18/1827 covers a single-step pretreatment for metallic substrates before applying a chemical coating formed by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions, where the process leaves no reaction residues of the substrate in the final coating. The pretreatment is performed in one operation and prepares the surface for subsequent coating.
[C23C 18/1831] Use of metal, e.g. activation, sensitisation with noble metals -- The subclass C23C 18/1831 covers processes that treat a metal substrate with noble metals to activate or sensitize its surface before applying a chemical coating formed by decomposition of a liquid or solution, ensuring that no reaction products from the substrate remain in the coating.
[C23C 18/1834] Use of organic or inorganic compounds other than metals, e.g. activation, sensitisation with polymers -- C23C 18/1834 pertains to metallic coating processes in which the coating is formed by decomposing liquid compounds, and the subclass specifically covers the use of organic or inorganic, non-metallic compounds-such as polymers-for activation, sensitisation, or similar preparatory functions, without leaving reaction products of the surface material in the final coating.
[C23C 18/1837] Multistep pretreatment -- Multistep pretreatment involves sequential surface cleaning, activation and conditioning before applying a metallic coating by decomposing liquid precursors, ensuring good adhesion and a uniform film without leaving reaction residues on the substrate.
[C23C 18/1841] with use of metal first
[C23C 18/1844] with use of organic or inorganic compounds other than metals, first -- The subclass C23C 18/1844 covers processes for chemically coating metallic surfaces by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions, where the coating material is derived from organic or inorganic substances that are not metals themselves, applied as the first layer on the metal substrate. This method forms a coating without leaving reaction products of the underlying metal in the finished film.
[C23C 18/1848] by electrochemical pretreatment -- This subclass covers chemical conversion coatings applied by decomposing liquid or solution compounds on a metallic surface after an electrochemical pretreatment of the substrate. The pretreatment prepares the metal for coating while ensuring that reaction products of the surface material do not remain in the final film.
[C23C 18/1851] of surfaces of non-metallic or semiconducting in organic material -- C23C 18/1851 covers methods for forming metallic coatings on non-metallic or semiconducting substrates by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions of the coating-forming material, ensuring that the substrate's reaction products are not incorporated into the coating. The process relies on chemical decomposition rather than physical deposition.
[C23C 18/1855] by mechanical pretreatment, e.g. grinding, sanding -- C23C 18/1855 covers chemically formed metallic coatings applied by decomposing liquid or solution precursors, where the substrate surface is first mechanically pretreated such as by grinding or sanding to improve adhesion before the coating is deposited.
[C23C 18/1858] by formation of electrostatic charges, e.g. tribofriction -- This subclass deals with metallic chemical coatings formed by decomposing liquid or solution precursors, where the coating material is attracted to the substrate through electrostatic charges generated, for example by triboelectric friction, rather than by reaction products.
[C23C 18/1862] by radiant energy -- A method of forming a metallic coating in which a liquid or solution of coating-forming compounds is decomposed by radiant energy such as laser, electron beam or plasma, depositing metal without leaving reaction-product residues on the substrate. This falls under chemical coating by decomposition of liquid compounds within the metallic coating class.
[C23C 18/1865] Heat -- The subclass C23C 18/1865 covers coating processes in which heat is applied to induce thermal decomposition of liquid or solution-borne coating precursors on metallic substrates, forming a metallic coating without leaving reaction products of the base material. The heating step drives the chemical transformation that produces the desired metallic layer directly on the surface.
[C23C 18/1868] Radiation, e.g. UV, laser -- C23C 18/1868 covers processes for applying metallic chemical coatings by decomposing liquid or solution precursors with radiant energy such as ultraviolet light or laser beams, producing a coating without residual reaction products on the substrate.
[C23C 18/1872] by chemical pretreatment -- A chemical pretreatment step applied to a metallic substrate before a coating is formed by the decomposition of liquid compounds or solutions, ensuring that no reaction products of the surface material remain in the final coating. This process prepares the surface for subsequent metallic coating applications and falls under the CPC class C23C 18/1872 within the broader chemistry and metallic coating categories.
[C23C 18/1875] only one step pretreatment -- This subclass covers metallic surface pretreatments carried out in a single step, where a liquid or solution of coating-forming compounds decomposes on the metal to form a coating and no reaction products of the substrate remain in the coating. It applies to one-step chemical coating processes.
[C23C 18/1879] Use of metal, e.g. activation, sensitisation with noble metals -- The CPC subclass C23C 18/1879 relates to chemical coating processes in which a metal, especially a noble metal, is applied to a surface to activate or sensitize it, serving as a catalyst or seed layer during decomposition of liquid coating precursors, while no reaction products of the substrate remain in the coating.
[C23C 18/1882] Use of organic or inorganic compounds other than metals, e.g. activation, sensitisation with polymers -- C23C 18/1882 covers methods of applying metallic coatings in which non-metallic organic or inorganic compounds, such as polymers, are used to activate or sensitize the substrate before or during deposition. The compounds do not become part of the final coating but facilitate film formation, adhesion, or uniformity.
[C23C 18/1886] Multistep pretreatment -- C23C 18/1886 covers multistep pretreatment processes applied to metallic surfaces before a chemical coating formed by decomposition of liquid compounds or solutions. The pretreatment prepares the substrate without embedding reaction products in the final coating, and falls under the broader class of coating metallic material.
[C23C 18/1889] with use of metal first -- This subclass deals with chemical coating of metallic surfaces where the coating is created by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions of coating-forming substances, with the metal substrate employed first in the process. The method avoids leaving reaction products of the substrate in the final coating.
[C23C 18/1893] with use of organic or inorganic compounds other than metals, first -- This subclass covers processes that form metallic coatings by chemically decomposing liquid or solution precursors that are organic or inorganic compounds other than metals, depositing the metal without leaving reaction products of the substrate in the coating. It focuses on coating formation through decomposition rather than by plating or alloying, and excludes the use of metallic compounds as the source material.
[C23C 18/1896] by electrochemical pretreatment -- The subclass C23C 18/1896 covers metallic substrates that receive a chemical coating formed by decomposition of liquid compounds or solutions after an electrochemical pretreatment step. The pretreatment modifies the surface electrochemically to improve adhesion or reaction before the coating is deposited, and no reaction products of the substrate remain in the final film.
[C23C 18/20] of organic surfaces, e.g. resins -- C23C 18/20 concerns chemical deposition of metallic coatings on organic substrates, such as resin surfaces, by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions that contain the coating material. The process forms a metallic layer without leaving reaction products from the substrate in the coating. This sub-class falls under coating metallic material within the broader chemistry category.
[C23C 18/2006] by other methods than those of  C23C18/22  -  C23C18/30 -- C23C 18/2006 refers to chemical metallic coatings formed by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions on a metal surface, where the process does not leave reaction products of the substrate in the coating, and employs methods other than those listed in subclasses 18/22 through 18/30.
[C23C 18/2013] by mechanical pretreatment, e.g. grinding, sanding -- This CPC subclass covers processes that chemically coat a metallic surface by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions, after a prior mechanical pretreatment such as grinding or sanding to prepare the surface. It resides in the coating metallic material group within chemistry.
[C23C 18/202] by formation of electrostatic charges, e.g. tribofriction -- C23C 18/202 refers to chemical coatings applied to metallic surfaces by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions, where the coating material is deposited through electrostatic charges generated by tribofriction, without leaving reaction products of the substrate in the coating.
[C23C 18/2026] by radiant energy -- C23C 18/2026 covers methods of applying metallic coatings that rely on radiant energy-such as lasers, infrared, or UV light-to decompose liquid precursors or solutions directly on a substrate, forming a coating without incorporating reaction products from the underlying surface material.
[C23C 18/2033] Heat -- This subclass covers methods that apply a metallic coating by thermally decomposing liquid precursors or solutions on a substrate, where the heat alone drives the reaction and no residual reaction products from the substrate remain in the coating. The technique is used for forming uniform metallic layers without chemical by-products on the surface.
[C23C 18/204] Radiation, e.g. UV, laser -- C23C 18/204 covers chemical coatings formed by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions on a metallic surface, where the process is driven by radiation such as ultraviolet light or laser beams. The method creates a coating without leaving reaction products of the substrate in the film.
[C23C 18/2046] by chemical pretreatment -- C23C 18/2046 covers processes in which a metallic surface is first chemically pretreat­ed to modify its condition before a coating is applied. The pretreatment uses chemical reactions that alter the substrate without leaving reaction products on the surface, preparing it for subsequent coating by decomposition of liquid coating precursors.
[C23C 18/2053] only one step pretreatment -- C23C 18/2053 covers a single-step pretreatment applied to metallic surfaces before a chemical coating formed by decomposition of liquid compounds or solutions, where the process leaves no reaction residues of the substrate in the final coating. This entry defines the one-step pretreatment method.
[C23C 18/206] Use of metal other than noble metals and tin, e.g. activation, sensitisation with metals  sensitising with tin  C23C18/285 , sensitising with noble metals  C23C18/30 -- C23C 18/206 relates to chemical metal-coating processes in which a non-noble metal or tin is applied to the substrate to activate or sensitize the surface before the deposition of a coating formed by decomposing a liquid precursor, and where no reaction products from the substrate remain in the finished coating.
