It encompasses activation or sensitisation steps using metals other than noble metals, with separate sub-classes for tin sensitisation and noble-metal sensitisation.
[C23C 18/2066] Use of organic or inorganic compounds other than metals, e.g. activation, sensitisation with polymers -- The C23C 18/2066 subclass covers methods for applying chemical coatings to metallic substrates by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions so that no reaction products of the base metal remain in the coating. It specifically includes the use of non-metallic organic or inorganic agents, such as polymer-based activators or sensitizers, to prepare the surface before deposition. This enables improved adhesion and functional performance of the coating.
[C23C 18/2073] Multistep pretreatment -- C23C 18/2073, Multistep pretreatment, refers to processes that prepare a metal surface for coating by applying a series of chemical cleaning, etching or activation steps using liquid compounds that decompose on the substrate, leaving no reaction residues on the final coating.
[C23C 18/208] with use of metal first -- This subclass covers chemical coating processes in which a metal layer is applied to the substrate before the in-situ decomposition of a liquid or solution coating precursor, so that the metal acts as the first constituent of the resulting coating.
[C23C 18/2086] with use of organic or inorganic compounds other than metals, first -- C23C 18/2086 covers methods for applying metallic coatings where the coating is formed by decomposing liquid or solution-based compounds, and the process employs organic or inorganic additives that are not metals themselves, serving as binders, catalysts or intermediates.
[C23C 18/2093] by electrochemical pretreatment -- C23C 18/2093 covers metallic coatings formed after an electrochemical pretreatment of the substrate, where the pretreatment creates a surface condition that facilitates the subsequent chemical coating by decomposition of liquid compounds or solutions, without leaving reaction products of the substrate in the final coating. This subclass falls under chemical coating of metallic materials in the Cooperative Patent Classification system.
[C23C 18/22] Roughening, e.g. by etching -- C23C 18/22 covers methods for roughening metallic surfaces, such as etching, before applying a chemical metallic coating formed by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions. The techniques create a textured substrate to improve coating adhesion while ensuring that reaction products of the base material do not remain in the final coating.
[C23C 18/24] using acid aqueous solutions -- C23C 18/24 covers methods of chemically coating metallic surfaces by decomposing liquid or solution-based coating precursors, where the decomposition is carried out with acidic aqueous solutions and no reaction products of the substrate remain in the coating.
[C23C 18/26] using organic liquids -- C23C 18/26 covers processes for metallic coating in which an organic liquid-such as an organometallic solution or a liquid precursor-is decomposed on the workpiece surface to form a metal layer, with the organic components volatilising or burning away so that no reaction products from the substrate remain in the coating.
[C23C 18/28] Sensitising or activating -- C23C 18/28 concerns processes that sensitize or activate a substrate to enhance adhesion of a metallic coating applied by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions, such as pretreatment steps that modify the surface chemistry before the coating forms.
[C23C 18/285] Sensitising or activating with tin based compound or composition -- This CPC subclass covers chemical coating methods that sensitize or activate a substrate using tin-based compounds or compositions before metallic deposition. The process involves decomposition of liquid or solution precursors to form a coating while avoiding residual reaction products on the surface.
[C23C 18/30] Activating -- C23C 18/30, titled "Activating", covers the pretreatment of metallic substrates in which a liquid compound or solution is chemically decomposed on the surface to prepare it for a coating, while ensuring that no reaction products from the substrate remain in the resulting film. This process is used to improve adhesion of subsequent metallic or inorganic coatings.
[C23C 18/31] Coating with metals -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Coating with metals through electroless plating process.
[C23C 18/32] Coating with nickel, cobalt or mixtures thereof with phosphorus or boron -- C23C 18/32 pertains to chemical deposition of nickel, cobalt or their alloys containing phosphorus or boron onto metallic surfaces. The method involves decomposition of liquid precursors or solutions to form a coating without leaving residual reaction products on the substrate. It falls under the broader class of metallic material coatings in the CPC system.
[C23C 18/34] using reducing agents -- C23C 18/34 concerns chemical metallic coating processes in which liquid precursors or solutions are decomposed to form a metal layer, and a reducing agent is used to convert the coating-forming compound to metal without leaving reaction residues on the substrate.
[C23C 18/36] using hypophosphites -- C23C 18/36 covers the use of hypophosphite compounds as reducing agents in chemical (electroless) deposition of metal coats on substrates, forming a coating by decomposing solution components without incorporating reaction by-products of the substrate. The method typically produces a uniform metallic layer, often nickel-phosphorus, through autocatalytic reduction of metal ions.
[C23C 18/38] Coating with copper -- C23C 18/38 relates to chemical methods for depositing copper onto a surface by decomposing liquid or solution precursors, forming a copper coating without leaving reaction-product residues of the substrate in the final layer.
[C23C 18/40] using reducing agents -- C23C 18/40 covers chemical coating of metallic substrates by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions, where a reducing agent is used to promote the formation of a coating while preventing reaction-product residues from remaining on the surface.
[C23C 18/405] Formaldehyde -- C23C 18/405 refers to the use of formaldehyde as a coating material applied by chemical decomposition of a liquid or solution, producing a metallic coating that does not leave reaction products of the substrate on the surface.
[C23C 18/42] Coating with noble metals -- C23C 18/42 - Coating with noble metals relates to chemical methods that form a metallic layer of a noble metal on a substrate by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions of the coating-forming material, producing a coating that contains no residual reaction products from the surface material.
[C23C 18/44] using reducing agents -- C23C 18/44 covers processes that employ reducing agents to induce the decomposition of liquid or solution-borne coating precursors on metallic substrates, forming a chemical coating while avoiding reaction products of the surface material in the final layer.
[C23C 18/48] Coating with alloys -- Chemical coating in which an alloy is formed on a surface by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions that contain the alloy-forming constituents, resulting in a metallic layer that adheres without leaving reaction products of the substrate, and where the coating is produced by in-situ generation of the alloy from the precursor mixture.
[C23C 18/50] with alloys based on iron, cobalt or nickel -- This CPC subclass covers chemical coating processes in which a liquid or solution of coating-forming compounds is thermally decomposed on a metallic substrate, forming a coating that contains alloys based on iron, cobalt or nickel, with no reaction products of the substrate remaining in the coating.
[C23C 18/52] using reducing agents for coating with metallic material not provided for in a single one of groups -- C23C 18/52 covers chemical deposition of metallic coatings by decomposing liquid compounds or solutions in the presence of reducing agents, where the metallic material applied is not supplied as a single element or a defined alloy group. The process forms a metallic layer without leaving reaction products of the substrate in the coating.
[C23C 18/54] Contact plating, i.e. electroless electrochemical plating -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Plating of metal surface (e.g. Ni, Cu) with a more electropositive metal (e.g. noble metal).
[C23C 2/00] Coating by applying the coating material in the molten state -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Metallic coatings obtained by dipping or immersing a substrate into a molten bath of the coating material, where the substrate itself remains essentially unchanged, as well as any methods and/or apparatuses specifically used thereof.  **Glossary:** - Metallic material: Metals and metals alloys, also including inorganic materials such as oxides, carbides, nitrides, borides, silicides and their mixtures
[C23C 20/00] Chemical coating by decomposition of either solid compounds or suspensions of the coating forming compounds, without leaving reaction products of surface material in the coating -- This subclass covers methods for applying metal or alloy coatings by chemically decomposing solid precursors or suspensions directly on a substrate, forming the coating without any residual reaction by-products from the surface. It includes processes such as thermal decomposition, pyrolysis, and laser-induced breakdown of the coating material.
[C23C 20/02] Coating with metallic material -- C23C 20/02 relates to methods of applying a metallic coating by chemically decomposing solid compounds or suspensions of coating-forming materials so that the metal deposits on the substrate without leaving reaction-product residues on the surface.
[C23C 2/003] Apparatus -- C23C 2/003 covers apparatus used to coat metallic objects by applying the coating material in its molten state, such as furnaces, spray guns, rollers and supporting handling equipment that deliver and solidify the molten coating on the substrate.
[C23C 2/0032] specially adapted for batch coating of substrate -- C23C 2/0032 covers methods and equipment specially adapted for batch coating of a substrate where the coating material is applied in a molten state. The classification falls under chemistry, specifically metallic material coatings, and pertains to processes that treat multiple parts together rather than continuous lines. It is used to identify technologies such as batch dip-coating or spray-plating of metals in molten form.
[C23C 2/00322] Details of mechanisms for immersing or removing substrate from molten liquid bath, e.g. basket or lifting mechanism -- It covers processes for applying a metallic coating by immersing a substrate in a molten bath and specifies mechanisms for lowering or raising the workpiece, such as baskets, hooks or other lifting devices. The entry details the design and operation of handling equipment used during molten-state coating.
[C23C 2/0034] Details related to elements immersed in bath -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Elements that are immersed within the bath, such as walls, baffles, pumps, elements supporting the substrate during coating or elements for moving the substrate through the bath. Non-moving immersed elements are classified here.
[C23C 2/00342] Moving elements, e.g. pumps or mixers -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Elements that are immersed within the bath which are in motion relative to the bath, such as pumps (i.e. the internal impeller moves relative to the bath), mixers, impellers, rollers or bearings.
[C23C 2/00344] Means for moving substrates, e.g. immersed rollers or immersed bearings -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Elements that are immersed within the bath and act to force movement of the substrate through the bath, such as rollers or portions thereof, e.g. bearings.
[C23C 2/00348] Fixed work supports or guides -- This subclass covers coating processes in which the workpiece is held on a stationary support or guided by a fixed structure while a molten metallic coating material is applied, such as dip-coating, spraying or brushing where the substrate does not move relative to the equipment.
[C23C 2/0035] Means for continuously moving substrate through, into or out of the bath  C23C2/00344  takes precedence -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Elements that act upon the substrate to be coated to move the substrate through the bath, such as take-up rollers or supply rollers.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Rollers immersed within the bath -> C23C2/00344
[C23C 2/0036] Crucibles -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Crucibles and heating devices. This area also covers the vessel for a holding bath.
[C23C 2/00361] characterised by structures including means for immersing or extracting the substrate through confining wall area -- **Glossary:** - Wall: Any portion of the receptacle which confines the bath is located below the upper surface of the bath and may include a side wall as well as a floor of the receptacle which the substrate passes through
[C23C 2/00362] Details related to seals, e.g. magnetic means -- This subclass covers features of seals used in molten-metal coating processes, such as magnetic sealing devices that prevent leakage or contamination during application of the coating. It includes details on the design and operation of magnetic or other sealing means integrated with the coating apparatus.
[C23C 2/0038] characterised by the pre-treatment chambers located immediately upstream of the bath or occurring locally before the dipping process -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Pre-treatment chamber(s), and elements thereof, that are directly associated with the hot-dipping or immersion apparatus, such as specific structure of pretreatment chamber(s), chamber mechanisms, transportation mechanism, seals, or heat or atmospheric conditions.  **Glossary:** - Locally: The same physical location, e.g. plant, so as to exclude pre-treatment chamber(s) which treat a substrate which then require shipping the pre-treated substrate from one location to another
[C23C 2/004] Snouts -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Fixed enclosures between the furnace and the molten metal bath.
[C23C 20/04] with metals -- A chemical coating applied by thermal or chemical decomposition of solid or suspended compounds that incorporates metallic elements into the finished layer, without leaving reaction products of the underlying surface. This includes processes where metals are generated in situ or deposited as part of the coating matrix.
[C23C 2/006] Pattern or selective deposits -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes or devices for conducting patterned or selective deposition on the substrate.
[C23C 20/06] Coating with inorganic material, other than metallic material -- This CPC subclass concerns methods for depositing inorganic, non-metallic coatings on a substrate by chemically decomposing solid compounds or suspensions of coating-forming substances, with no reaction products of the substrate remaining in the coating. It is situated under chemistry → coating metallic material → chemical coating by decomposition of solids or suspensions.
[C23C 2/0062] without pre-treatment of the material to be coated, e.g. using masking elements such as casings, shields, fixtures or blocking elements -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods or devices for forming patterned or selective deposition by means external to the substrate, e.g. using masking elements such as casings, shields, fixtures or blocking elements.
[C23C 2/0064] using masking layers -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Pattern or selective deposition done by means of applying a masking layer to the substrate.
[C23C 20/08] with compounds, mixtures or solid solutions, e.g. borides, carbides, nitrides -- This subclass covers chemical coating processes in which a solid compound or a suspension decomposes on the substrate, leaving a coating formed from compounds, mixtures or solid solutions such as borides, carbides or nitrides, without residual reaction products of the substrate material. It is part of the metallic-material coating group in the CPC hierarchy.
[C23C 2/02] Pretreatment of the material to be coated, e.g. for coating on selected surface areas -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Pre-treatment of the material to be coated, an operation being considered as pre-treatment when it is specially adapted for, but quite distinct from, the coating process concerned and constitutes an independent operation.  For example:  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Fluxes or coverings on molten baths -> C23C2/30
[C23C 2/022] by heating -- The subclass C23C 2/022 covers processes for forming a metallic coating by heating the coating material while it is in the molten state, such as flame-spraying or other thermal-spray techniques where the melted metal is heated and introduced onto a substrate to create a bonded coating.
[C23C 2/0222] in a reactive atmosphere, e.g. oxidising or reducing atmosphere  C23C2/024  takes precedence -- C23C 2/0222 covers processes for applying a molten metallic coating to a substrate while the coating solidifies in a reactive atmosphere, such as oxidising or reducing conditions. The classification deals with controlling the chemical environment during solidification to affect coating properties. It is subordinate to C23C2/024, which has priority over this subgroup.
[C23C 2/0224] Two or more thermal pretreatments
[C23C 2/024] by cleaning or etching -- This subclass covers coating processes in which the substrate is cleaned or chemically etched before or during the application of a molten metallic coating. The cleaning/etching step removes contaminants, oxides or surface irregularities to enhance adhesion and uniformity of the deposited layer. It includes mechanical, chemical and plasma-based cleaning methods.
[C23C 2/026] Deposition of sublayers, e.g. adhesion layers or pre-applied alloying elements or corrosion protection -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Application of complete or partial layers onto the substrate to be coated prior to entry into the bath. Examples of these layers are adhesion layers that promote adhesion between the substrate and the bath material, pre-applied alloying elements that mix with the bath material in the coating, and layers that protect the substrate from corrosion prior to entry into the bath.
[C23C 2/04] characterised by the coating material -- C23C 2/04 covers processes for coating metallic articles by applying a coating material while it is molten, where the novelty lies mainly in the coating material itself. The subclass includes methods such as spray, dip or roller coating that use a liquid-to-solid transition of the coating, and it is defined by the composition, formulation or specific characteristics of the material being deposited.
[C23C 2/06] Zinc or cadmium or alloys based thereon -- The CPC subclass C23C 2/06 covers methods for applying a metallic coating in the molten state where the coating material is zinc, cadmium or alloys of these metals, such as hot-dip or spray processes that form a continuous metallic layer on a substrate.
[C23C 2/08] Tin or alloys based thereon -- C23C 2/08 covers the use of tin or tin-based alloys as coating materials applied in the molten state, such as hot-dip tin plating, tin-based hot-dip galvanising, and similar processes that dip a substrate into liquid tin or an alloy to form a protective or decorative metallic layer.
[C23C 2/10] Lead or alloys based thereon -- C23C 2/10 covers the use of lead or lead-based alloys as the coating material applied in a molten state onto metallic substrates. The subclass includes processes for melting, transferring and solidifying lead coatings, as well as the preparation of lead-based alloy formulations for such molten-application methods. It is part of the broader group dealing with metallic coating techniques.
[C23C 2/12] Aluminium or alloys based thereon -- This group covers processes and compositions where aluminium or its alloys are used as the molten coating material applied to a substrate. It includes methods of forming protective or functional metallic layers by melting aluminium-based feedstock and depositing it onto surfaces. Used in protective, decorative or wear-resistant coatings.
[C23C 2/14] Removing excess of molten coatings -- The CPC subclass C23C 2/14 covers methods for eliminating surplus coating material after it has been applied in a molten state. It includes techniques such as wiping, scraping, draining or otherwise removing the excess molten metal or alloy to achieve a uniform final thickness.
[C23C 2/16] using fluids under pressure, e.g. air knives -- A method for coating metallic substrates in which the molten coating material is applied by directing a pressurised fluid, such as an air-knife jet, onto the surface. The fluid stream spreads and directs the melt, enabling uniform coating of the metal part. This approach falls under CPC C23C 2/16.
[C23C 2/18] Removing excess of molten coatings from elongated material -- C23C 2/18 covers techniques for removing surplus molten coating from elongated items such as wires, rods or tubes after application, including wiping, brushing, scraping, air-jet or centrifugal methods to achieve a uniform layer and prevent buildup.
[C23C 2/185] Tubes; Wires
[C23C 2/20] Strips -- The class covers methods for coating metal strips by applying the coating material while it is molten, so that it adheres to the moving strip and solidifies into a continuous layer. It includes hot-dip, spray or roller techniques that form protective or functional metallic coatings on the strip surface.
[C23C 22/00] Chemical surface treatment of metallic material by reaction of the surface with a reactive medium -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods, compositions and apparatus for chemical surface treatment of metallic material by reaction of the metallic surface with a reactive liquid to form conversion or passivation coatings thereon.  This group covers also suspensions containing reactive liquids and non-reactive solid particles.  Apparatus for treating metallic material to form conversion coatings thereon ( C23C22/00 ).  General methods or special ones for forming conversion coatings on metallic materials that do not have an appropriate subgroup ( C23C22/00 ).  Conversion coatings ( C23C22/00 - C23C22/47 ).  C23C22/02 . using non-aqueous solutions  C23C22/05 . using aqueous solutions  C23C22/70 . using melts  Passivation, oxidation coatings ( C23C22/48 - C23C22/58 ).  Conversion coatings characterized by the process ( C23C22/73 ).  Pretreatment of the material to be coated ( C23C22/78 ).  After-treatment ( C23C22/82 ).  Regeneration of the coating bath ( C23C22/86 ).  **Glossary:** - Metallic material: covers metals and alloys (attention is drawn to the Note following the title of subclass C22C ). - Phosphate coatings: Phosphate coatings are processes of chemical conversion on a metal surface to produce thin adherent phosphate compound coatings. The phosphate crystals formed on the surfaces of materials can be iron, zinc, or manganese phosphates. Among these phosphates, manganese phosphate is more suitable for wear applications. Phosphate coatings are usually applied to carbon steel, low-alloy steel, and cast iron. They can also be applied to zinc, cadmium, aluminum, and tin. Phosphate processes are hard to apply on high alloys for these alloys are likely immune to the phosphoric acid. In short, phosphating is one of the most useful non-metallic conversion coatings. - Chromate coatings: Chromate coatings, similar to phosphate coatings, are processes of chemical conversion. But the chromate coatings are formed by the reaction of water solutions of chromic acid or chromium salts. The coatings can be applied to aluminum, zinc, cadmium, and magnesium. The coatings usually have good atmospheric corrosion resistance. Chromate coatings are widely used in protecting common household products, such as screws, hinges, and many hardware items with the yellow-brown appearance. - Oxide coatings: The oxide coatings are in fact corrosion products which is a thin, usually less than 2.5 µm oxide with good adhesion. The oxide treatments are done by heat, chemicals, or electrochemical reactions. - Bluing-type oxidations: gun -bluing -type oxidations are done by heating the metals, generally steel, at 370ºC in a steam atmosphere. Chemical baths produce coatings similar to a gun bluing coating by immersion techniques. - Black oxide or blackening coatings: Black oxide or blackening coatings is a conversion coating for steel, copper, zinc, powder metals and silver solder, and most for stainless steel by treating with hot caustic soda (blackening agent). Some pastes can be rubbed on surfaces to produce similar results.
[C23C 22/02] using non-aqueous solutions -- C23C 22/02 denotes the use of non-aqueous solutions for chemically treating metallic surfaces in coating processes. It falls under the CPC hierarchy for chemistry-related coating of metallic material, specifically covering reactions where the surface is contacted with a reactive, non-water based medium to achieve a protective or functional layer.
[C23C 22/03] containing phosphorus compounds -- The CPC subclass C23C 22/03 covers chemical surface treatments of metal where a phosphorus-containing compound is employed as the reactive medium to form a coating. It pertains to processes that use phosphorus reagents to create protective or functional metal layers.
[C23C 22/04] containing hexavalent chromium compounds -- The CPC entry C23C 22/04 covers chemical surface treatments of metal where the coating contains hexavalent chromium compounds, typically applied by reacting the metal surface with a reactive medium that introduces Cr(VI). Such processes are used for corrosion-resistant or decorative metal coatings.
[C23C 22/05] using aqueous solutions -- This subclass relates to chemical surface treatment of metals in which the reactive medium is an aqueous solution, such as water-based baths or sprays that form protective or functional coatings on the metal surface. It covers processes that rely on water as the primary reacting agent.
[C23C 22/06] using aqueous acidic solutions with pH less than 6 -- C23C 22/06 covers processes that treat metal surfaces by contacting them with aqueous acidic solutions having a pH below 6, effecting a chemical reaction that modifies the surface for coating or corrosion resistance. The method is used to clean, etch, or activate the metal before further coating steps.
[C23C 22/07] containing phosphates -- C23C 22/07 covers chemical treatments that form phosphate layers on metal surfaces, where the reactive medium contains phosphates. Such processes are used to improve corrosion resistance, adhesion or lubricity of the coated metallic material.
[C23C 22/08] Orthophosphates -- C23C 22/08 refers to the use of orthophosphate compounds to chemically convert the surface of a metal into a protective phosphate coating. The process involves reacting the metal with an orthophosphate-containing solution, forming a thin inorganic layer that enhances corrosion resistance, lubrication and paint adhesion. It is classified under chemical surface treatments of metallic materials.
[C23C 22/10] containing oxidants -- This subclass covers chemical surface treatments of metal parts where the reactive medium includes oxidising agents. The process modifies the metal surface by reactions that involve oxidation, such as forming oxide layers or converting the surface to a different chemical state. It falls under the broader category of coating metallic material in the CPC system.
[C23C 22/12] containing zinc cations -- C23C 22/12 covers chemical surface treatments of metal objects in which the reactive medium contains zinc cations, applying zinc ions to modify, protect or enhance the metal surface. This subclass is part of the coating metallic material group within the chemistry section.
[C23C 22/13] containing also nitrate or nitrite anions -- C23C 22/13 covers chemical surface treatments of metals where the reactive medium used for the coating contains nitrate or nitrite anions, employed to modify the metal's surface properties such as corrosion resistance or appearance. The classification applies to processes that involve reacting the metal with such anionic solutions to form a protective or functional coating.
[C23C 22/14] containing also chlorate anions -- A chemical surface-treatment process for metallic articles in which the reactive medium contains chlorate anions, used to modify or form a coating on the metal through a reaction at the surface. This includes methods where chlorates act as oxidising agents or participants in the coating formation.
[C23C 22/16] containing also peroxy-compounds -- C23C 22/16 covers chemical surface treatments of metals where the substrate is reacted with a reactive medium that includes peroxy-compounds to form a protective or functional coating. The peroxy agents act as oxidizers or initiators, enabling the formation of oxide, oxide-metal or polymeric layers on the metallic surface.
[C23C 22/17] containing also organic acids -- Code C23C 22/17 pertains to chemical surface treatment of metallic materials where the reactive medium also contains organic acids. It covers processes that modify or coat metal surfaces by reacting them with solutions, suspensions or gases that include organic acids to improve corrosion resistance, adhesion or other surface characteristics. This entry lies within the CPC hierarchy for coating metallic material.
[C23C 22/18] containing manganese cations -- C23C 22/18 covers chemical surface treatments of metals in which the reactive medium contains manganese cations. The manganese ions become incorporated into the coating, altering properties such as corrosion resistance, hardness or catalytic activity. This subclass falls under coating metallic material in the CPC hierarchy.
[C23C 22/182] containing also zinc cations
[C23C 22/184] containing also nickel cations
[C23C 22/186] containing also copper cations -- C23C 22/186 designates chemical surface treatments of metallic substrates where the reacting medium contains copper cations, resulting in a copper-bearing coating on the metal. This subclass falls under the broader category of coating metallic material in the CPC system.
[C23C 22/188] containing also magnesium cations -- This subclass covers chemical surface treatments of metals where the reactive medium contains magnesium cations, such as conversion or plating processes that incorporate magnesium ions into the coating. It includes methods that use magnesium-containing solutions to form protective or functional layers on metallic substrates.
[C23C 2/22] by rubbing, e.g. using knives -- C23C 2/22 is a CPC subgroup dealing with coating metallic parts by applying a molten coating material using a rubbing action, such as employing knives or similar tools to spread the melt over the surface. It falls under the broader class for coating metallic material by molten-state application.
[C23C 22/20] containing aluminium cations -- This subclass deals with chemical surface treatments of metals in which the reactive medium contains aluminium cations, forming conversion or protective coatings such as anodic films. It is used for processes that modify the metal surface by reacting with Al-based species to improve corrosion resistance, adhesion or aesthetic properties.
[C23C 22/22] containing alkaline earth metal cations -- C23C 22/22 covers chemical surface treatments of metals where the reactive medium includes alkaline-earth-metal cations. The process modifies the metallic surface through reactions that incorporate these cations to form protective or functional coatings. It falls under the broader class for coating metallic material by chemical means.
[C23C 2222/00] Aspects relating to chemical surface treatment of metallic material by reaction of the surface with a reactive medium -- This group covers processes where the surface of a metal or alloy is chemically altered by contacting it with a reactive liquid, gas, or plasma to form a conversion coating, passivation layer, or other functional film. It includes treatments such as acid pickling, anodizing, chemical etching and other reactions that modify surface composition or properties without mechanical action.
[C23C 2222/10] Use of solutions containing trivalent chromium but free of hexavalent chromium -- This CPC subgroup covers chemical surface treatments of metal that employ coating solutions containing trivalent chromium while excluding all hexavalent chromium. It specifies methods that use Cr(III) chemistry to form protective or decorative layers without the toxic Cr(VI) species.
[C23C 2222/20] Use of solutions containing silanes -- The code C23C 2222/20 covers processes that treat metal surfaces by applying solutions that contain silanes, which chemically bond to the metal to form protective or functional layers. It pertains to chemical surface treatment where the silane reacts with the metallic substrate, often to improve corrosion resistance, adhesion, or other surface properties.
[C23C 22/23] Condensed phosphates -- The class C23C 22/23 covers the application of condensed phosphates in chemical surface treatments of metals, where the reactive phosphate medium forms a conversion coating on the substrate. Such coatings are used to improve corrosion resistance, provide lubrication, or promote adhesion of subsequent paints or finishes.
[C23C 22/24] containing hexavalent chromium compounds -- The CPC subclass C23C 22/24 covers chemical surface treatments of metals that employ hexavalent chromium compounds as the reactive medium. It includes processes where Cr(VI) species react with the metal to form protective or decorative coatings, typically for corrosion resistance, coloration or other functional surface properties.
[C23C 22/26] containing also organic compounds -- C23C 22/26 covers chemical surface treatments of metal where the reactive medium contains organic compounds, such as organic acids, solvents, or other organic reagents that react with the metal surface to modify its properties or prepare it for further processing.
[C23C 22/27] Acids -- The C23C 22/27 subclass covers surface treatments of metals in which acids act as the reactive medium, providing cleaning, etching, pickling, passivation or activation of the metallic substrate. It includes procedures that employ mineral, organic or mixed acids to modify surface composition, roughness or reactivity before further processing.
[C23C 22/28] Macromolecular compounds -- The C23C 22/28 subclass covers the use of macromolecular compounds, such as polymers or oligomers, in chemical surface treatments of metallic substrates. It includes processes where a reactive medium forms a polymeric film on the metal by reaction with the surface, providing corrosion resistance, lubrication, or functional coatings. This falls under the broader category of coating metallic material through chemical treatment.
[C23C 22/30] containing also trivalent chromium -- The subclass C23C 22/30 covers methods and compositions for chemically treating metal surfaces with a coating that includes trivalent chromium, a less toxic form of chromium used to enhance corrosion resistance, adhesion or coloration of the coating.
[C23C 22/32] containing also pulverulent metals -- C23C 22/32 refers to chemical surface treatments of metallic substrates in which the coating incorporates finely divided, or pulverulent, metals applied by reacting the metal surface with a reactive medium. This subclass falls under the broader categories of chemistry and metallic material coating.
[C23C 22/33] containing also phosphates -- C23C 22/33 covers chemical surface treatments of metal where the coating is applied by reacting the metal with a reactive medium and the resulting layer includes phosphate compounds, providing corrosion resistance or other functional properties. This sub-class falls under coating metallic material within the broader chemistry classification.
[C23C 22/34] containing fluorides or complex fluorides -- The subclass includes methods for chemically treating metal surfaces by reacting them with fluoride-containing or complex-fluoride reagents, forming fluoride layers, etching, or imparting corrosion resistance and other surface properties. It covers processes where the reactive medium is primarily composed of fluorides or their complexes.
[C23C 22/36] containing also phosphates -- C23C 22/36 covers chemical treatments that form a coating on metal surfaces by reacting the substrate with a reactive medium that includes phosphates. The process creates phosphate-based conversion layers that improve corrosion resistance, adhesion, or lubricity of the metal. It falls within the broader class of coating metallic materials.
[C23C 22/361] containing titanium, zirconium or hafnium compounds -- A CPC subclass for chemical surface treatments of metal where a reactive medium containing titanium, zirconium or hafnium compounds is applied to form a coating on the metallic substrate. It covers processes that generate protective or functional layers by reacting these elements with the metal surface.
[C23C 22/362] containing also zinc cations -- The CPC subclass C23C 22/362 covers chemical surface treatments of metallic material where a reactive medium forms a coating and the process involves zinc cations, either as part of the medium or incorporated into the resulting layer. Such treatments are used for corrosion protection, plating or conversion coatings that benefit from the presence of zinc.
[C23C 22/364] containing also manganese cations -- C23C 22/364 covers chemical surface treatments of metals in which a reactive medium is used to form a coating that incorporates manganese cations. It is a sub-category of coating metallic material within the broader chemistry class, describing processes that embed manganese ions during the reaction.
[C23C 22/365] containing also zinc and nickel cations -- This CPC subclass covers chemical surface treatments of metals where the reaction medium contains zinc and nickel cations, resulting in a coating that incorporates both metals. Such processes are used to modify the substrate's properties, often for enhanced corrosion resistance or specific functional characteristics.
[C23C 22/367] containing alkaline earth metal cations -- The CPC entry C23C 22/367 covers chemical surface-treatment methods for metallic substrates in which a reactive medium interacts with the metal surface, and the treatment composition includes alkaline-earth-metal cations. It falls under the hierarchy Chemistry → Coating Metallic Material → Coating Metallic Material → Chemical surface treatment of metallic material by reaction of the surface with a reactive medium.
[C23C 22/368] containing magnesium cations -- C23C 22/368 classifies chemical surface treatments of metals in which the reactive medium includes magnesium cations. The process involves reacting the metal surface with a magnesium-containing solution or bath to alter properties such as corrosion resistance, hardness, or adhesion of subsequent coatings. It is used in various industrial coating and pretreatment operations.
[C23C 22/37] containing also hexavalent chromium compounds -- The CPC subclass C23C 22/37 covers chemical surface treatments of metals in which the reactive medium contains hexavalent chromium compounds, used to form protective or decorative layers on metallic substrates. It falls under the broader groups for coating metallic material in the chemistry section.
[C23C 22/38] containing also phosphates -- This CPC subclass covers chemical surface treatments of metallic substrates where the reactive medium contains phosphates. It relates to forming a phosphate-containing coating on the metal to enhance corrosion resistance, adhesion or lubricity.
[C23C 2/24] using magnetic or electric fields -- C23C 2/24 covers methods for applying a metallic coating in the molten state that employ magnetic or electric fields to control the coating process. It includes techniques such as electromagnetic stirring, induction heating, or field-assisted spray where the fields influence the flow, orientation, and solidification of the molten metal to achieve desired coating properties.
[C23C 22/40] containing molybdates, tungstates or vanadates -- A chemical surface treatment of metallic material in which the surface reacts with a medium containing molybdate, tungstate or vanadate compounds, forming protective or functional conversion layers on the metal. This process is used to improve corrosion resistance, adhesion or other surface properties. It falls under the coating of metallic materials in the CPC hierarchy.
[C23C 22/42] containing also phosphates -- A process for chemically treating a metallic surface with a reactive medium that incorporates phosphate compounds, producing a phosphate-containing coating or conversion layer. It falls under coating metallic material in the CPC chemistry section, specifically C23C 22/42.
[C23C 22/43] containing also hexavalent chromium compounds -- A chemical surface-treatment process for metallic articles that involves reacting the metal with a reactive medium, where the treatment formulation includes hexavalent chromium compounds as part of the coating composition. This entry covers such processes within the coating of metallic materials.
[C23C 22/44] containing also fluorides or complex fluorides -- C23C 22/44 covers chemical surface treatments of metallic material where a reactive medium containing fluorides or complex fluorides is used to create a coating, fitting within the coating metallic-material group of the CPC.
[C23C 22/46] containing oxalates -- C23C 22/46 defines chemical surface treatments of metals in which oxalate compounds are employed as the reactive medium to form a coating on the metallic substrate. The process involves reacting the metal surface with oxalate-based solutions, precipitating a protective layer that can improve corrosion resistance, adhesion or other functional properties of the coated material.
[C23C 22/47] containing also phosphates -- C23C 22/47 covers chemical surface treatments of metals that involve reacting the substrate with a medium containing phosphates, producing a phosphate-based coating. The process is used to enhance corrosion resistance, improve paint adhesion or impart lubricity by forming a thin inorganic film on the metal surface.
[C23C 22/48] not containing phosphates, hexavalent chromium compounds, fluorides or complex fluorides, molybdates, tungstates, vanadates or oxalates -- The subclass C23C 22/48 covers chemical surface treatments of metals where the surface is reacted with a liquid or gaseous medium, but the treatment composition must not contain phosphates, hexavalent chromium compounds, fluorides or complex fluorides, molybdates, tungstates, vanadates or oxalates.
[C23C 22/50] Treatment of iron or alloys based thereon -- C23C 22/50 covers chemical surface treatments applied to iron and its alloys, where the metal is reacted with a chemically active medium to form protective or functional layers. Methods include conversion coatings, passivation, and other reactions that alter the surface composition or structure for corrosion resistance, adhesion improvement, or other functional properties.
[C23C 22/52] Treatment of copper or alloys based thereon -- C23C 22/52 covers chemical surface treatments that form a coating on copper or copper-based alloys by reacting the metal surface with a reactive medium. This subclass falls under the broader category of coating metallic material within the chemistry section of the CPC.
[C23C 22/53] Treatment of zinc or alloys based thereon -- The CPC subclass C23C 22/53 covers methods for chemically treating zinc or zinc-based alloys, or items made from them, to alter surface properties. It includes processes that react the metal surface with a reactive medium such as acids, oxidizers, or other chemicals to achieve cleaning, passivation, corrosion resistance, or preparation for further coating. This subclass falls under the broader category of chemical surface treatments for metallic materials.
[C23C 22/54] Treatment of refractory metals or alloys based thereon -- The CPC subclass C23C 22/54 covers processes for chemically treating the surfaces of refractory metals or their alloys, such as tungsten, molybdenum or niobium, by reacting them with a suitable medium to modify or improve properties like corrosion resistance, hardness, or adhesion. These treatments typically involve oxidation, nitriding, carbiding or other reactive surface reactions.
[C23C 22/56] Treatment of aluminium or alloys based thereon -- C23C 22/56 relates to chemical surface treatments applied to aluminium and its alloys, where a reactive medium modifies the metal to create protective or functional layers. Methods include anodizing, conversion coatings, and other chemical reactions that alter the surface composition or structure.
[C23C 22/57] Treatment of magnesium or alloys based thereon -- C23C 22/57 concerns chemical surface treatments applied to magnesium and its alloys, where the metal is reacted with a suitable medium to form protective or functional layers. Techniques include conversion coatings, anodizing, and other chemical reactions that enhance corrosion resistance, adhesion, or other surface properties.
[C23C 22/58] Treatment of other metallic material -- C23C 22/58 covers chemical surface treatments applied to metallic substrates that are not otherwise specified, where the metal is reacted with a suitable reactive medium to alter its surface properties, such as cleaning, passivation, or functionalisation.
[C23C 2/26] After-treatment -- The CPC subclass C23C 2/26 covers after-treatment steps applied to metallic coatings that have been deposited in the molten state. It includes processes such as annealing, tempering, quenching, surface polishing, or any other post-application operations intended to modify the coating's microstructure, hardness, adhesion, or surface finish.
[C23C 22/60] using alkaline aqueous solutions with pH greater than 8 -- The subclass C23C 22/60 covers chemical surface treatment of metals using alkaline aqueous solutions whose pH is greater than 8. It includes processes where the basic solution reacts with the metal to clean, etch, passivate or otherwise modify the surface properties.
[C23C 2/261] in a gas atmosphere, e.g. inert or reducing atmosphere -- The subclass C23C 2/261 concerns the application of a molten coating material to a metallic substrate while the workpiece is placed in a controlled gas atmosphere, such as an inert or reducing gas, to limit oxidation or other undesirable reactions during the coating process. This approach is used to achieve uniform, high-quality metallic coatings in environments that protect the molten metal and the underlying surface.
[C23C 22/62] Treatment of iron or alloys based thereon -- C23C 22/62 covers chemical surface‐treatment methods applied specifically to iron and its alloys. It includes processes that react the metal's surface with a reactive medium-such as gases, liquids, or plasmas-to modify properties like corrosion resistance, hardness, lubricity or adhesion, for example phosphating, pickling, oxidation or conversion-coating treatments.
[C23C 22/63] Treatment of copper or alloys based thereon -- C23C 22/63 covers chemical surface treatments applied to copper and copper-based alloys, where the metal's exterior reacts with a reactive medium to form a coating or modify its properties. It falls within the broader category of coating metallic material in the Cooperative Patent Classification system.
[C23C 22/64] Treatment of refractory metals or alloys based thereon -- C23C 22/64 covers chemical surface treatments applied to refractory metals or their alloys, where the metal is reacted with a chemically active medium to form a coating or modify the surface. The methods include oxidation, nitriding, sulfidation or deposition of compounds that improve corrosion resistance, wear resistance or high-temperature performance.
[C23C 2/265] by applying solid particles to the molten coating -- C23C 2/265 defines a method for applying a metallic coating in its molten form in which solid particles are added to the melt during the coating process. The approach is used to modify the composition, structure or properties of the resulting solidified coating by incorporating these particles before the melt solidifies.
[C23C 22/66] Treatment of aluminium or alloys based thereon -- C23C 22/66 covers chemical surface treatments applied specifically to aluminium and its alloys, where the metal surface is altered by reacting with a suitable chemical medium. It includes processes such as etching, anodizing, conversion-coating and other reactions that modify surface properties for corrosion resistance, adhesion or aesthetic purposes.
[C23C 22/67] with solutions containing hexavalent chromium -- A surface treatment that chemically modifies a metal by immersing it in a solution that contains hexavalent chromium, forming a protective or functional coating through reaction with the reactive medium.
[C23C 22/68] using aqueous solutions with pH between 6 and 8 -- The subclass refers to chemical surface treatments of metallic materials in which the reactive medium is an aqueous solution whose pH is controlled to a neutral-to-slightly alkaline range, typically pH 6 to 8. This pH window is used to influence corrosion resistance, adhesion or the formation of protective or functional coatings on the metal surface.
[C23C 22/70] using melts -- The CPC entry C23C 22/70 covers processes that form coatings on metal surfaces by reacting the substrate with a molten medium. It includes the use of liquid metals, slags, salts, glasses or other melts that chemically interact with the surface to create a protective or functional layer, often for corrosion resistance, wear protection or functional modification.
[C23C 22/72] Treatment of iron or alloys based thereon -- The CPC subclass C23C 22/72 covers chemical surface treatments applied to iron and its alloys, where the metal's surface reacts with a reactive medium to modify its properties. This includes processes such as oxidation, carburizing, nitriding, and other chemical reactions that form protective or functional coatings on the material.
[C23C 22/73] characterised by the process -- C23C 22/73 covers chemical surface treatments of metallic objects where the metal is reacted with a specific reactive medium to form a coating, the defining feature being the particular process steps employed. The subclass includes methods using acids, bases, oxidizing agents or other reactive substances to modify the surface chemistry and create a protective or functional film.
[C23C 22/74] for obtaining burned-in conversion coatings -- C23C 22/74 defines methods for producing burned-in conversion coatings on metallic substrates by reacting the surface with a chemically active medium, forming a tightly bound inorganic layer that enhances corrosion resistance, adhesion, and surface durability.
[C23C 22/76] Applying the liquid by spraying -- C23C 22/76 concerns the application of a liquid coating to a metallic surface by spraying, where the liquid reacts with the surface to form a chemical treatment layer. It falls within the chemistry subclass for coating metallic material and addresses the process of depositing the reactive medium in a sprayed form.
[C23C 22/77] Controlling or regulating of the coating process -- The CPC subclass C23C 22/77 pertains to methods and apparatus that monitor, adjust, or otherwise regulate the parameters of metallic coating processes, such as temperature, flow rate, composition, deposition speed or other operating conditions, in order to achieve specific coating qualities or performance.
[C23C 22/78] Pretreatment of the material to be coated -- This CPC subclass concerns pretreatment of metallic substrates before applying a coating; it covers chemical surface treatments where the metal is reacted with a reactive medium to modify the surface prior to coating. It falls under chemical coating of metallic material.
[C23C 2/28] Thermal after-treatment, e.g. treatment in oil bath -- C23C 2/28 covers the post-coating heat treatment of metallic surfaces, such as heating the coated part in an oil bath to improve adhesion, hardness or corrosion resistance. The step follows solidification of the molten coating and may involve controlled temperature and time to achieve the desired material properties.
[C23C 22/80] with solutions containing titanium or zirconium compounds -- The CPC subclass C23C 22/80 covers chemical surface treatments of metallic objects in which the reactive medium is a solution that includes titanium or zirconium compounds, used to form protective or functional coatings on the metal surface.
[C23C 22/82] After-treatment -- C23C 22/82 - After-treatment covers additional chemical processes applied to a metallic surface after an initial coating or reaction, such as finishing, modification, or protective steps that enhance the coating's properties.
[C23C 22/83] Chemical after-treatment -- C23C 22/83 addresses chemical after-treatment applied to metallic surfaces following a primary coating step. It includes reactions with a reactive medium that modify the coating or substrate to improve adhesion, corrosion resistance, hardness or appearance, such as passivation, conversion coatings and post-etching.
[C23C 22/84] Dyeing -- The CPC subclass C23C 22/84 "Dyeing" covers methods for imparting colour to metal surfaces by applying dye-containing solutions that react with or adsorb onto the treated metallic substrate. It includes procedures where the metal has been pre-treated (e.g., anodised, etched or sensitised) and the dye is fixed through chemical bonding, precipitation or physical absorption to achieve decorative or functional coloration.
[C23C 2/285] for remelting the coating -- The CPC subclass C23C 2/285 relates to metallic coatings where the coating material is applied in its molten state and subsequently remelted to improve adhesion, uniformity or repair damage. It falls under the hierarchy Chemistry → Coating Metallic Material → Coating Metallic Material → Coating by applying the coating material in the molten state, covering processes that re-heat an existing metal coating to achieve the desired surface properties.
[C23C 22/86] Regeneration of coating baths -- The CPC code C23C 22/86 concerns processes for regenerating metallic coating baths, involving chemical treatment that removes degradation products, replenishes depleted components and restores the bath's functional performance for continued use on metal surfaces. These methods fall under chemical surface treatment of metallic material by reaction with a reactive medium.
[C23C 2/29] Cooling or quenching -- C23C 2/29 relates to the cooling or quenching step applied to metallic coatings that have been deposited in a molten state. It covers techniques for rapidly reducing temperature to control solidification, microstructure and mechanical properties of the coating. The classification is used for processes that follow the molten-state application of a metallic material in coating operations.
[C23C 2/30] Fluxes or coverings on molten baths -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Fluxes or covering materials for molten baths, e.g. fluxes materials used in hot dipping process  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Removing excess of molten coatings from elongated material by rubbing -> C23C2/22  **Glossary:** - Covering: A chemical compound and/or composition, usually immiscible with the melt and having a lower density, i.e. not a physical object.
[C23C 2/32] using vibratory energy applied to the bath or substrate -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Application of vibrations using physical, magnetic or other means to the bath or to the substrate. An example of subject matter covered by this group is the use of ultrasonic energy to a substrate to cause vibrations of the substrate to enhance wettability of the substrate.
[C23C 2/325] Processes or devices for cleaning the bath -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes for cleaning of the bath and the devices that perform the cleaning.  "Cleaning" is intended to cover removal, by chemical or physical means, of impurities within the bath, such as devices which skim material from the surface of the bath or which remove a portion of the bath for treatment to remove impurities before returning the treated portion to the bath.
[C23C 2/34] characterised by the shape of the material to be treated -- C23C 2/34 covers coating of metallic items where the process is defined by the shape of the material being treated, applied using a coating material in a molten state. It pertains to methods that adjust the coating technique according to the geometry of the workpiece, such as pipes, sheets or complex profiles, within the broader field of chemical coating of metals.
[C23C 2/36] Elongated material -- C23C 2/36 covers coating processes applied to elongated metallic bodies such as wires, rods, strips or tubes by introducing the coating material in the molten state. The classification pertains to methods where the molten coating flows over or adheres to the surface of these continuous or shaped forms, enabling protective or functional metal layers.
[C23C 2/38] Wires -- The CPC subclass C23C 2/38 covers processes for coating metallic wires by applying a molten coating material, such as dipping, drawing or extrusion of the wire through a melt. It includes methods that form a continuous metallic sheath on the wire surface during manufacture, typically for electrical or mechanical improvement.
[C23C 2/385] Tubes of specific length -- C23C 2/385 concerns coating metallic tubes in the molten state when the tubes are of a predetermined length. It covers methods that apply the molten coating material to tubes whose length is specified to achieve consistent coverage and properties along the entire tube.
[C23C 2/40] Plates -- C23C 2/40 is a CPC subclass within chemistry dealing with metallic-material coatings applied in the molten state, specifically for producing plates that receive a metallic layer via casting, spraying or dipping of the molten coating material.
[C23C 24/00] Coating starting from inorganic powder -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Coating methods where the material to be coated is applied in powder form on the surface of the substrate to be coated, e.g. cold spray methods.  Also methods where the coating material is applied in form of a slurry as long as said methods result in obtaining a coating, and not in a modification of the surface of the substrate or in a diffusion into the substrate.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Spraying of the coating material in molten state, starting from a powder -> C23C4/00 - Solid state diffusion of only non-metal elements into metallic material surfaces -> C23C8/00 - Solid state diffusion of only non-metal elements into metallic material surfaces using solids, e.g. powders, pastes -> C23C8/60 - C23C8/78 - Solid state diffusion of only metal elements or silicon into metallic material surfaces using solids, e.g. powders, pastes -> C23C10/28 - C23C10/58 - Solid state diffusion of at least one non-metal element other than silicon and at least one metal element or silicon into metallic material surfaces -> C23C12/00 - Manufacture of composite layers, workpieces or articles by sintering metallic powder -> B22F7/00 - Friction welding -> B23K20/12 - Coating mortars, concrete, artificial stone or ceramics, using a powder as coating material -> C04B41/4545 - C04B41/4549 - Coating mortars, concrete, artificial stone or ceramics, with vitreous materials -> C04B41/5022  **Glossary:** - Metallic material: Metals or metal alloys, optionally comprising hard particles, e.g. oxides, carbides or nitrides
[C23C 24/02] by application of pressure only -- C23C 24/02 refers to methods of producing metallic coatings from inorganic powders that rely solely on the application of pressure, without heat or chemical reactions. The process typically involves compacting the powder onto a substrate to create a dense, adherent layer, often used in cold-spraying or powder-pressing techniques. This subclass falls under the broader categories of chemistry, coating metallic material, and coating starting from inorganic powder.
[C23C 24/04] Impact or kinetic deposition of particles -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Cold spray methods, i.e. spraying methods in which the sprayed particles are not significantly melted before reaching the substrate.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Spraying of the coating material in molten state, starting from a powder -> C23C4/00
[C23C 24/045] by trembling using impacting inert media -- This subclass covers the formation of a metallic coating from an inorganic powder by a trembling process in which inert media impact the substrate, embedding the powder particles to build up a metallic layer without melting the base material.
[C23C 2/405] Plates of specific length -- C23C 2/405 in the CPC relates to metallic coating processes where the coating material is applied in the molten state, specifically covering plates of a defined length. It is classified under chemistry - coating metallic material - coating by applying the coating material in the molten state.
[C23C 24/06] Compressing powdered coating material, e.g. by milling -- C23C 24/06 refers to methods that densify an inorganic powder-based metallic coating before it is applied, typically by compressing the particles through milling or similar mechanical actions. The process creates a more cohesive, uniform coating material, improving its adherence and performance on the substrate. This classification falls under coating metallic materials derived from inorganic powders.
[C23C 24/08] by application of heat or pressure and heat -- C23C 24/08 relates to processes for forming metallic coatings from inorganic powder where the coating is fixed by applying heat alone or by combining pressure and heat. The classification covers methods such as sintering, hot pressing, or thermal spray that transform the powder into a solid metallic layer on a substrate. It falls under the broader categories of chemistry, coating metallic material, and coating starting from inorganic powder.
[C23C 24/082] without intermediate formation of a liquid in the layer -- This subclass covers processes for forming metallic coatings from inorganic powder where the layer is built without first creating a liquid film; the powder is applied and then solidified by heating, plasma, or other energy directly. It falls under coating metallic material in chemistry.
[C23C 24/085] Coating with metallic material, i.e. metals or metal alloys, optionally comprising hard particles, e.g. oxides, carbides or nitrides -- The C23C 24/085 subclass covers processes for applying a coating composed of a metal or metal alloy, which may be mixed with hard particles such as oxides, carbides or nitrides. It pertains to metallic coatings formed from inorganic powders and includes techniques for depositing these composite layers onto substrates.
[C23C 24/087] Coating with metal alloys or metal elements only -- C23C 24/087 concerns coating processes that apply a layer composed exclusively of metal alloys or pure metal elements, using inorganic powder as the feedstock. The subclass covers techniques such as thermal spraying that deposit metallic coatings for protective or functional purposes.
[C23C 24/10] with intermediate formation of a liquid phase in the layer -- C23C 24/10 covers methods for applying a metallic coating that starts from an inorganic powder and involves the transient formation of a liquid phase within the deposited layer. The liquid phase aids particle consolidation or alloying before solidification, improving adhesion and coating quality.
[C23C 24/103] Coating with metallic material, i.e. metals or metal alloys, optionally comprising hard particles, e.g. oxides, carbides or nitrides -- C23C 24/103 pertains to coating processes that apply a metallic material or alloy to a substrate, where the coating may incorporate hard particles such as oxides, carbides or nitrides, and the metal is supplied as an inorganic powder. It falls under the chemistry category for metallic coating technologies.
[C23C 24/106] Coating with metal alloys or metal elements only -- C23C 24/106 classifies coating processes that use inorganic powders to apply a layer consisting solely of metal alloys or pure metal elements, without any non-metallic components. It falls under the chemistry hierarchy for metallic material coatings, covering techniques that deposit only metallic constituents as the coating.
[C23C 2/50] Controlling or regulating the coating processes  C23C2/14  takes precedence
[C23C 2/51] Computer-controlled implementation -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Control or regulation of the coating process, wherein the control or regulation is performed responsive by a computer.  Examples include standard PID controllers, "fuzzy" logic controllers and artificial intelligence or machine-learning implemented control of the coating process.
[C23C 2/52] with means for measuring or sensing -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Control or regulation of the coating process wherein at least one variable is measured or sensed.  "Measured or sensed" includes both electronic and mechanical detection of variables, as well as "measuring or sensing" by an operator of the coating process, such as visual inspection of the variable of the coating process.
[C23C 2/521] Composition of the bath -- C23C 2/521 designates the composition of the molten bath employed in metallic coating processes where the coating material is applied in a liquid state. The subclass covers the chemical formulation, additives, and physical characteristics of the bath that influence coating quality and performance. It resides within the broader category of coating metallic material in the chemistry field.
[C23C 2/522] Temperature of the bath -- The CPC subclass C23C 2/522 covers metallic‐material coating processes that involve immersing the workpiece in a molten bath, with particular emphasis on the temperature of that bath. It addresses the selection, control and effects of bath temperature on coating formation, thickness, adhesion and microstructure.
[C23C 2/523] Bath level or amount -- The CPC subclass C23C 2/523 covers aspects related to the level or quantity of the molten bath used in metallic coating processes, such as monitoring, adjusting, or specifying the bath height, volume, or amount during application. It pertains to methods and apparatus for controlling these parameters to achieve consistent coating quality. This subclass falls under coating metallic material applied in the molten state.
[C23C 2/524] Position of the substrate -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Measuring or sensing the position of the substrate, which includes at least the location of the substrate with respect to fixed portions of the coating apparatus and any change in the location of the substrate over time, e.g. vibration of the substrate.
[C23C 2/5245] for reducing vibrations of the substrate -- The C23C 2/5245 subclass covers metallic coating processes in which the molten coating material is formulated or applied so that it reduces vibrations of the underlying substrate, typically by incorporating damping agents, specific alloy compositions or micro-structures that absorb mechanical energy during solidification. This is used to improve stability and performance of coated metal parts.
[C23C 2/525] Speed of the substrate -- The subclass C23C 2/525 covers the speed at which a metallic substrate is moved while a coating material is applied in the molten state, such as in hot-dip or molten-metal spraying processes. It addresses how substrate velocity influences coating thickness, uniformity, adhesion and production efficiency, and includes methods for measuring, controlling or optimizing that speed.
[C23C 2/526] for visually inspecting the surface quality of the substrate -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Using image processing techniques to investigate the surface quality of the substrate.
[C23C 2/54] of the mixing or stirring the bath -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods or devices for controlling or regulating the mixing or stirring of the bath.
[C23C 2/542] using static devices separate from the substrate, e.g. a fixed plate -- C23C 2/542 covers coating of metallic objects with molten material using a static apparatus that remains separate from the workpiece, such as a fixed plate positioned near the substrate. The device does not move with the part, allowing the molten coating to be transferred onto the surface.
[C23C 2/544] using moving mixing devices separate from the substrate, e.g. an impeller of blade -- C23C 2/544 covers methods for applying molten metallic coatings in which the coating material is mixed by a moving device that is not part of the substrate, such as an impeller or blade, to achieve uniform distribution during deposition. This approach is used to improve coating quality on metallic parts.
[C23C 26/00] Coating not provided for in groups -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Any method of coating a metallic surface and/or of coating a substrate with a metallic material which is not already described in any of groups C23C2/00 - C23C24/00  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Applying liquids or other fluent materials to surfaces in general -> B05 - Making metal-coated products by extrusion -> B21C23/22 - Connecting objects or parts, e.g. coating with sheet metal otherwise than plating -> B21D39/00 - Working of metal by the action of a high concentration of electric current on a workpiece using an electrode -> B23H - Plating by soldering or welding -> B23K - Metallising of glass -> C03C17/36 - Metallising mortars, concrete, artificial stone, ceramics or natural stone -> C04B41/00 - Paints, varnishes, lacquers -> C09D - Enamelling of, or applying a vitreous layer to, metals -> C23D5/00 - Treating metal surfaces or coating of metals by electrolysis or electrophoresis -> C25D - Electrolytic stripping of metallic layers or coatings -> C25F5/00 - Single-crystal film growth -> C30B - Manufacture of printed circuits -> H05K - Manufacture of semiconductor devices -> H10
[C23C 26/02] applying molten material to the substrate -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Any method of coating a metallic surface with a molten material or molten metallic material to a substrate which is not already described in any of groups C23C2/00 - C23C24/00 , e.g. brazing, arc welding, laser welding, friction welding, laser alloying
[C23C 28/00] Coating for obtaining at least two superposed coatings either by methods not provided for in a single one of groups -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Multi-layered coatings, where the different layers composing the coating have been deposited by at least two different methods as disclosed in group C23C2/00 - C23C26/00 or by a combination of one method from C23C and one method from C25D .  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Deposition of sublayers, e.g. to promote adhesion of the coating, prior to the deposition of a coating by PVD -> C23C14/024 - C23C14/025 - Deposition of sublayers, e.g. to promote adhesion of the coating, prior to the deposition of a coating by CVD -> C23C16/0272 - C23C16/029  **Glossary:** - Metallic material: Metals and metals alloys, not including inorganic materials such as oxides, carbides, nitrides, borides, silicides and their mixtures, with the exception where said inorganic materials are embedded in a metal matrix as hard particles, e.g. Cermets and MMC. - Inorganic non-metallic materials: Oxides, carbides, nitrides, borides, silicides and their mixtures, enamels, phosphates and sulphides.
[C23C 28/02] only coatings of metallic material -- C23C 28/02 refers to processes that create at least two superposed metallic coatings, where each layer is applied using a method that is not encompassed by a single group's procedures. The subclass is limited to metallic-material coatings applied sequentially with distinct techniques, enabling the formation of layered metal films with combined properties.
[C23C 28/021] including at least one metal alloy layer -- C23C 28/021 pertains to methods for producing at least two superposed metallic coatings by employing separate deposition techniques that are not combined into a single step, with at least one of the layers being a metal alloy.
[C23C 28/022] with at least one MCrAlX layer -- This subclass concerns metallic coating systems that contain at least one layer of an MCrAlX alloy, where M is a metallic element such as nickel, cobalt or iron and X is a non-metallic element like silicon, boron or carbon. It applies to processes that create two or more superposed metallic layers by techniques not covered in other groups.
[C23C 28/023] only coatings of metal elements only
[C23C 28/025] with at least one zinc-based layer -- This CPC sub-group relates to metallic coatings that consist of at least two superposed layers, where one of the layers is zinc-based. The required structure is achieved by methods that are not described in any single group of the CPC, thereby covering combined or sequential processes for multi-layer metallic finishes.
[C23C 28/026] including at least one amorphous metallic material layer -- A CPC subclass for coating metallic materials where at least two layers are applied in succession using processes not described in a single group, and where one of the layers is an amorphous metallic material. It falls under the chemistry hierarchy for metallic coating technologies.
[C23C 28/027] including at least one metal matrix material comprising a mixture of at least two metals or metal phases or metal matrix composites, e.g. metal matrix with embedded inorganic hard particles, CERMET, MMC. -- C23C 28/027 designates metallic coatings that incorporate a metal matrix formed from a mixture of two or more metals or metal phases, such as metal-matrix composites, cermets, or alloys containing embedded inorganic hard particles, used in multilayer coating systems where the layers are applied by distinct processes.
[C23C 28/028] Including graded layers in composition or in physical properties, e.g. density, porosity, grain size -- C23C 28/028 refers to coatings that contain graded layers, where the composition or physical characteristics such as density, porosity or grain size vary through the thickness. This subclass covers methods for producing at least two superposed layers that cannot be obtained by a single method, typically used in metallic coating applications.
[C23C 28/04] only coatings of inorganic non-metallic material -- The subclass C23C 28/04 covers the application of inorganic non-metallic coatings onto metallic substrates when at least two distinct layers are applied using separate processes that are not combined in a single group. It falls under the chemistry section for coating metallic material and specifies methods for obtaining superposed inorganic coatings.
[C23C 28/042] including a refractory ceramic layer, e.g. refractory metal oxides, ZrO 2 , rare earth oxides -- C23C 28/042 relates to metallic coating processes that produce at least two superposed layers using methods not covered by other groups, specifically where a refractory ceramic layer such as metal oxides, ZrO₂ or rare-earth oxides is applied on the metal surface. This subclass falls under coating metallic material within the broader chemistry field.
[C23C 28/044] coatings specially adapted for cutting tools or wear applications -- C23C 28/044 covers metallic coatings designed for cutting tools or wear applications where at least two layers are applied in a superposed manner, using methods that are not covered by a single group's procedures. The classification targets specialized multilayer coatings that enhance performance and durability in aggressive machining environments.
[C23C 28/046] with at least one amorphous inorganic material layer, e.g. DLC, a-C:H, a-C:Me, the layer being doped or not -- C23C 28/046 covers metallic substrates that receive at least two superimposed coatings, where one of the layers is an amorphous inorganic material such as diamond-like carbon, hydrogenated amorphous carbon or metal-doped amorphous carbon. The classification applies whether the amorphous layer is doped or undoped and when the multilayer structure cannot be achieved by a single coating step.
[C23C 28/048] with layers graded in composition or physical properties -- C23C 28/048 covers metallic coatings that are applied as multiple superposed layers in which the composition or physical properties change gradually from one layer to the next. The graded structure is created by varying the material or process parameters during deposition, yielding a coating with tailored corrosion resistance, hardness, or thermal performance.
[C23C 28/30] Coatings combining at least one metallic layer and at least one inorganic non-metallic layer -- This subclass covers coatings that consist of at least two superposed layers, one metallic and one inorganic non-metallic, applied by different processes. It includes methods for forming such combined layers where the metallic and inorganic phases are not provided in a single step, enabling functional or protective properties that arise from the layered structure.
[C23C 28/32] including at least one pure metallic layer -- C23C 28/32 covers metallic coatings that consist of at least two superposed layers when the layers are produced by methods not defined in a single group, and where one of the layers is a pure metal. It falls under the chemistry hierarchy for coating metallic material and addresses multilayer metallic film structures.
[C23C 28/321] with at least one metal alloy layer -- C23C 28/321 covers processes for applying metallic coatings that contain at least one metal-alloy layer, aimed at producing at least two superposed coating layers by using methods that are not specified together in a single group. It falls under the chemistry subclass for metallic material coatings.
[C23C 28/3215] at least one MCrAlX layer -- C23C 28/3215 covers a metallic coating comprising at least one layer of an MCrAlX alloy, where M is a metal such as nickel or cobalt and X is an optional element like silicon or boron. The layer is part of a superposed coating structure produced by separate deposition methods that are not combined in a single process. Such coatings are employed to improve oxidation, corrosion or wear resistance.
[C23C 28/322] only coatings of metal elements only -- This CPC subclass (C23C 28/322) concerns methods for producing at least two superposed metallic layers where each layer is applied by a technique not covered in a single CPC group, and the coatings consist solely of metal elements.
[C23C 28/3225] with at least one zinc-based layer -- The subclass C23C 28/3225 covers metallic coating processes that produce at least two superposed layers, where one of the layers is zinc-based, and the layers are applied by methods not specified in a single group, typically for corrosion protection or decorative purposes.
