[C23C 28/323] with at least one amorphous metallic material layer -- This CPC subclass concerns multilayer metallic coatings that incorporate at least one amorphous metal layer and are produced by methods not covered by a single coating group. It is located under chemistry → coating metallic material and addresses the creation of two or more superposed layers with at least one amorphous metallic material.
[C23C 28/324] with at least one metal matrix material layer comprising a mixture of at least two metals or metal phases or a metal-matrix material with hard embedded particles, e.g. WC-Me -- C23C 28/324 covers metallic coating structures that include at least one layer of metal-matrix material formed from a mixture of two or more metals or metal phases, or a metal matrix containing hard particles such as tungsten-carbide-metal (WC-Me). The code is applied to processes that produce two or more superposed metallic coatings where the combined layers are not achievable by a single method described in other groups.
[C23C 28/325] with layers graded in composition or in physical properties -- C23C 28/325 covers metallic coatings that consist of at least two superposed layers created by separate processes rather than a single method, where the layers are graded either in chemical composition or in physical properties such as hardness, thickness or conductivity. The classification applies to coatings designed to achieve a gradual transition between layers for improved performance.
[C23C 28/34] including at least one inorganic non-metallic material layer, e.g. metal carbide, nitride, boride, silicide layer and their mixtures, enamels, phosphates and sulphates -- The CPC subclass C23C 28/34 covers processes for producing multilayer metallic coatings in which at least one layer consists of an inorganic non-metallic material. Examples of such layers include metal carbides, nitrides, borides, silicides, as well as mixtures, enamels, phosphates or sulphates, applied by methods not combined within a single group.
[C23C 28/341] with at least one carbide layer -- C23C 28/341 covers metallic coatings that incorporate at least one carbide layer as part of a multilayer coating structure, where the layers are applied using methods that are not covered by a single group of processes. The classification is used for patents describing composites where a carbide layer is combined with other metallic layers to achieve specific surface properties.
[C23C 28/343] with at least one DLC or an amorphous carbon based layer, the layer being doped or not -- C23C 28/343 covers metallic substrates that receive a multilayer coating in which at least one of the layers is a diamond-like carbon (DLC) or an amorphous carbon layer, regardless of whether the carbon layer is doped. The classification applies to processes that produce two or more superposed coatings where this carbon-based layer is part of the stack, and the method is not covered by other groups.
[C23C 28/345] with at least one oxide layer -- The C23C 28/345 subclass concerns metallic coatings that incorporate at least one oxide layer and are applied as two or more superposed layers, where the individual layers are deposited by methods that are not combined in a single group of processes. This classification is used for inventions that achieve a multilayer metallic coating with an oxide component through distinct, sequential coating techniques.
[C23C 28/3455] with a refractory ceramic layer, e.g. refractory metal oxide, ZrO 2 , rare earth oxides or a thermal barrier system comprising at least one refractory oxide layer -- This subclass deals with methods that create at least two superposed coatings on a metallic substrate where one of the layers is a refractory ceramic, such as a metal oxide like ZrO₂, rare-earth oxides or other high-temperature oxides, often forming a thermal-barrier system. It is part of the broader group for metallic material coatings that employ multiple layers not covered by a single method.
[C23C 28/347] with layers adapted for cutting tools or wear applications -- C23C 28/347 covers metallic coating compositions that are applied in multiple superposed layers, each layer being tailored for cutting-tool or wear-resistance purposes, and that are produced by methods not combined in a single group of coating processes. This subclass is used when at least two distinct coatings are required for the final performance.
[C23C 28/36] including layers graded in composition or physical properties -- C23C 28/36 covers metallic coating processes that produce at least two superposed layers whose composition or physical characteristics vary gradually through the thickness, such as graded or functionally graded coatings, using methods not defined in other CPC groups.
[C23C 28/40] Coatings including alternating layers following a pattern, a periodic or defined repetition -- The C23C 28/40 class covers coatings that are built from at least two superposed layers arranged in a regular pattern, periodic sequence, or defined repetition, where the method of creating the layered structure is not specified in any other group. It pertains to metallic material coatings that employ alternating layers to achieve specific functional or structural characteristics.
[C23C 28/42] characterized by the composition of the alternating layers -- C23C 28/42 covers metallic coatings formed by at least two superposed layers created with methods not defined in a single group, where the defining feature is the specific composition of the alternating layers. The subclass is used when the material make-up of each layer governs the technical treatment and performance of the multilayer coating.
[C23C 28/44] characterized by a measurable physical property of the alternating layer or system, e.g. thickness, density, hardness -- The CPC subclass C23C 28/44 pertains to metallic coatings that consist of at least two superimposed layers produced by separate processes, where the invention is defined by a measurable physical property of the layers or the multilayer system, such as thickness, density or hardness. This property is used to control or evaluate the performance of the coating.
[C23C 30/00] Coating with metallic material characterised only by the composition of the metallic material, i.e. not characterised by the coating process -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Coatings obtained by any of the methods of group C23C2/00 - C23C26/00 but characterized either by the peculiarity of their compositions or of their structures, e.g. columnar thermal barrier coatings, metal matrix composite coatings, two/multi-phase metallic coatings, quasicrystalline coatings, etc.
[C23C 30/005] on hard metal substrates -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Essentially coated cutting tools where the coating has been obtained by any of the methods of group C23C2/00 - C23C26/00 .  **Glossary:** - Hard metal substrates: Includes cemented carbide substrates
[C23C 4/00] Coating by spraying the coating material in the molten state, e.g. by flame, plasma or electric discharge -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Coating processes in which melted or partially melted materials are sprayed, i.e. propelled, onto a surface, as well as apparatuses specifically used thereof.  The material to be deposited is typically fed into the spray gun in powder, wire or rod form where it is rapidly heated and melted or partially melted by electrical (plasma or arc) or chemical means (combustion flame, detonation), before being accelerated towards the substrate to be coated.  The obtained coatings are characterized by a lamellar grain structure resulting from the rapid solidification of small globules, flattened from striking a cold surface at high velocities.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Build-up welding -> B23K , e.g B23K5/18 , B23K9/04  **Glossary:** - Metallic material: Metals and metals alloys, also including inorganic materials such as oxides, carbides, nitrides, borides, silicides and their mixtures
[C23C 4/01] Selective coating, e.g. pattern coating, without pre-treatment of the material to be coated -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Masking elements such as casings, shields, fixtures or blocking elements.  Stripping foreign matter from cavities by means of gas or water jets.
[C23C 4/02] Pretreatment of the material to be coated, e.g. for coating on selected surface areas -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Pre-treatment of the material to be coated, an operation being considered as pre-treatment when it is specially adapted for, but quite distinct from, the coating process concerned and constitutes an independent operation.  For example:
[C23C 4/04] characterised by the coating material -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Spraying the coating material characterised by the coating composition that is not covered by the subgroups
[C23C 4/06] Metallic material -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Metals and metal alloys compositions mixed with inorganic hard particles such as oxides, borides, carbides, nitrides and/or silicides.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - MCrAl(Y) alloys where M is nickel, cobalt or iron as coating material with or without non-metal elements, e.g. silicon. -> C23C4/073 - Pure metals or metal alloys as coating material -> C23C4/08 - Pure oxides, borides, carbides, nitrides, silicides or their mixtures as coating material -> C23C4/10 - Pure oxide compositions as coating material -> C23C4/11
[C23C 4/067] containing free particles of non-metal elements, e.g. carbon, silicon, boron, phosphorus or arsenic -- This subclass of C23C covers metallic coatings applied by spraying the material in a molten state and that contain dispersed free particles of non-metal elements such as carbon, silicon, boron, phosphorus or arsenic to alter the coating's characteristics. It is part of the coating-by-spray (flame, plasma or electric discharge) group.
[C23C 4/073] containing MCrAl or MCrAlY alloys, where M is nickel, cobalt or iron, with or without non-metal elements -- **Definition:** This place covers:  MCrAl or MCrAlY alloys, also when further elements are present in said alloys, e.g. Si, ..., and/or hard particles.
[C23C 4/08] containing only metal elements -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Pure metals or metal alloys compositions.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - MCrAl(Y) alloys where M is nickel, cobalt or iron as coating material with or without non-metal elements, e.g. silicon. -> C23C4/073
[C23C 4/10] Oxides, borides, carbides, nitrides or silicides -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Compositions including mixtures of any two or more of oxides, borides, carbides, nitrides and/or silicides, or pure borides, carbides, nitrides or silicides compositions.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Pure oxides compositions as coating material -> C23C4/11
[C23C 4/11] Oxides -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Pure oxides compositions
[C23C 4/12] characterised by the method of spraying -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Coating processes characterised by the method of spraying being not covered by the subgroups.
[C23C 4/123] Spraying molten metal -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes and apparatuses in which the material to be deposited is melted in a furnace, then the molten material is slowly poured through a conical tundish into a small-bore ceramic nozzle. The molten material exits the furnace as a thin free-falling stream and is broken up into droplets by an annular array of gas jets, and these droplets then proceed downwards, accelerated by the gas jets to impact onto a substrate.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Dipping in a molten bath -> C23C2/00 - Casting molten material on a substrate -> C23C6/00 - Continuous casting of metals -> B22D11/00
[C23C 4/126] Detonation spraying -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes and apparatuses where oxygen and fuel is fed into a barrel along with a charge of powder of the material to be deposited. A spark is used to ignite the gas mixture and the resulting detonation heats and accelerates the powder to supersonic velocity down the barrel, to deposit on the substrate.  Schematic diagram of a detonation process:
[C23C 4/129] Flame spraying -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes and apparatuses in which the spray material, in form of a powder or a wire, is fed continually into a fuel gas-oxygen flame where it is typically melted by the heat of combustion. A powder feed carrier gas transports the powder particles into the combustion flame, and the mixed gases transport the material towards the prepared workpiece surface.  Schematic diagram of a wire flame process:  © Sulzer Metco  Schematic diagram of a powder flame process:  © Sulzer Metco
[C23C 4/131] Wire arc spraying -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes and apparatuses using two metallic wires, usually of the same composition, as the coating feedstock. The two wires are electrically charged with opposing polarity and are fed into the arc gun at matched, controlled speeds. When the wires are brought together at the contact point, the opposing charges on the wires create enough heat to continuously melt the tips of the wires. Compressed air is used to atomize the now molten material and accelerate it onto the workpiece surface to form the coating.  Schematic diagram of a wire arc process:  © Sulzer Metco
[C23C 4/134] Plasma spraying -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes and apparatuses where an electric arc is generated between an anode and a cathode. This ionizes the flowing process gases into the plasma state. Powdered feedstock material is injected into the plasma jet, melting the powder particles and propelling them to the surface of the workpiece.  Schematic diagram of a plasma spray process:  © Sulzer Metco
[C23C 4/137] Spraying in vacuum or in an inert atmosphere -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Coating by spraying in vacuum or in an inert gas chamber the coating material in the molten state, for example:  Spraying at below atmospheric pressure  Spraying using inert gas shrouds or in enclosures filled with inert gas
[C23C 4/14] for coating elongate material -- The C23C 4/14 subclass addresses methods of applying a metallic coating to elongated items such as wires, rods or tubes by spraying the coating material while it is molten, using techniques like flame, plasma or electric discharge. This falls within the broader chemistry domain of metallic material coating, specifically covering spraying processes that produce a continuous protective or functional layer on long, thin substrates.
[C23C 4/16] Wires -- This subclass deals with methods of applying a metallic coating to wires by spraying the coating material in its molten state, using techniques such as flame spraying, plasma spraying or electric-discharge spraying, and includes the associated preparation, deposition and finishing steps.
[C23C 4/18] After-treatment -- C23C 4/18 covers after-treatment steps applied to metallic coatings that have been deposited by spraying the material in a molten state, such as flame, plasma or electric-discharge techniques. The classification addresses processes performed subsequent to the initial spray to modify, finish or improve the coating's properties.
[C23C 4/185] Separation of the coating from the substrate -- The CPC subclass C23C 4/185 covers techniques for detaching or removing a metallic coating that has been applied to a substrate by spraying the material in a molten state, such as flame, plasma, or electric-discharge spraying. It includes processes that separate the coating from the underlying part without damaging the substrate, enabling recycling, repair, or re-coating.
[C23C 6/00] Coating by casting molten material on the substrate -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes and apparatuses involving pouring molten, i.e. liquid, material onto a substrate to form a coating.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Dipping in a molten metal bath -> C23C2/00 - Spraying molten metals -> C23C4/123 - Casting molten macromolecular compounds, i.e. polymers, on a substrate -> B05C5/00 , B05D7/00 - Enamelling of, or applying a vitreous layer to, metals -> C23D5/00  **Glossary:** - Material: Metals and metals alloys, also including inorganic materials such as oxides, carbides, nitrides, borides, silicides and their mixtures
[C23C 8/00] Solid state diffusion into metallic material surfaces -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The diffusion of non-metal elements such as carbon, oxygen, nitrogen, but also boron, phosphor, sulfur, selenium or tellurium into a metal or metal alloy surface by contact with either a reactive gas (e.g. oxygen, hydrocarbons, nitrogen), a liquid (e.g. salt melts) or a solid (e.g. powders, pastes).  Coatings obtained by oxidising, carburising, nitriding, carbo-nitriding and/or boronising a metal or metal alloy surface.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Diffusion of only metal elements or silicon into a metallic surface -> C23C10/00 - Diffusion of at least one non-metal element other than silicon and at least one metal element or silicon into metallic material surfaces -> C23C12/00 - Coating by evaporation, by sputtering or by ion implantation of the coating forming material -> C23C14/00 - Reactive after treatment of PVD coatings with sulfur, selenium and/or tellurium -> C23C14/5866 - Electroless plating -> C23C18/00 - Conversion or passivation coatings obtained by reaction of the metallic surface with a reactive liquid, e.g. chromate, phosphate and/or silicate conversion coatings -> C23C22/00 - Conversion coatings obtained by electrolytic surface reaction, e.g. anodisation, phosphatising, chromatising -> C25D11/00 - Process or apparatus specially adapted for the manufacture or treatment of semiconductors devices, e.g. doping of semiconductors -> H10P  **Glossary:** - Ferrous surfaces: Surfaces containing a majority of iron per weight, such as but not limited to steel and cast iron
[C23C 8/02] Pretreatment of the material to be coated -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Cleaning or etching treatments  Physical treatments such as roughening, grinding or polishing  Deposition of sublayers, i.e. adhesion layers, masking layers
[C23C 8/04] Treatment of selected surface areas, e.g. using masks -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Masking elements such as casings, shields, fixtures or blocking elements, as well as masking layers or tapes.  Treatments on selected surface areas also not involving masking elements.
[C23C 8/06] using gases -- C23C 8/06 covers coating processes that use gases to introduce selected elements into the surface of a metallic substrate by solid-state diffusion, forming protective or functional layers such as nitrides, carbides or oxides. The gases act as carriers of the coating species and diffuse into the metal at elevated temperature, enabling the formation of a uniform, adherent coating without melting the base material.
[C23C 8/08] only one element being applied -- The C23C 8/08 subclass covers solid-state diffusion processes that apply a single elemental material onto a metallic surface to form a coating. It includes methods in which only one element, not an alloy or compound, is introduced by diffusion to modify the substrate's properties, falling under the broader coating-metallic-material group.
[C23C 8/10] Oxidising -- Oxidising in this context refers to solid-state diffusion processes that form oxide layers on metal surfaces, typically by heating the metal in an oxygen-containing atmosphere or by electrochemical means. The resulting oxide films alter surface properties such as corrosion resistance, hardness, and electrical behavior, and are used in protective and functional coatings for metallic components.
[C23C 8/12] using elemental oxygen or ozone -- C23C 8/12 covers methods that apply elemental oxygen or ozone to metallic surfaces to promote solid-state diffusion for coating purposes. It falls under the chemistry hierarchy for metallic material coatings, emphasizing diffusion-based surface treatment.
[C23C 8/14] Oxidising of ferrous surfaces -- C23C 8/14 relates to the chemical process of oxidising ferrous (iron-containing) surfaces, a specific type of solid-state diffusion treatment applied to metallic substrates. It falls within the broader category of coating metallic materials in the chemistry section, focusing on creating oxide layers that modify surface properties such as corrosion resistance or adhesion. This classification is used to index patents dealing with methods and compositions for controlled oxidation of iron-based surfaces.
[C23C 8/16] using oxygen-containing compounds, e.g. water, carbon dioxide -- This subclass covers methods that form oxide or oxy-compound layers on metal surfaces by solid-state diffusion of oxygen-containing compounds such as water vapor or carbon dioxide, providing protective or functional coatings.
[C23C 8/18] Oxidising of ferrous surfaces -- C23C 8/18 covers processes that intentionally oxidize iron-containing surfaces to form protective or functional oxide layers, typically by exposing the metal to oxygen or oxidising agents at elevated temperature, allowing a solid-state diffusion of oxygen into the substrate to improve wear resistance, corrosion protection, or adhesion of subsequent coatings.
[C23C 8/20] Carburising -- This subclass covers the carburising of metallic workpieces, i.e., the solid-state diffusion of carbon or carbon-containing gases into the surface to form a hardened layer. It includes methods, atmospheres, temperature regimes and treatment steps used to enrich the surface with carbon for improved wear resistance.
[C23C 8/22] of ferrous surfaces
[C23C 8/24] Nitriding -- Nitriding is a solid-state diffusion process that introduces nitrogen into the surface of metallic materials, primarily steel, to form hard nitride layers. The treatment enhances surface hardness, wear resistance, fatigue strength and corrosion performance, making it a key method for coating metallic components.
[C23C 8/26] of ferrous surfaces -- C23C 8/26 covers methods for applying coatings to ferrous surfaces by solid-state diffusion. Techniques include case hardening, carburizing, nitriding and other diffusion treatments that introduce alloying elements into iron or steel without melting the substrate.
[C23C 8/28] more than one element being applied in one step -- C23C 8/28 covers coating metallic surfaces by solid-state diffusion in which two or more different elements are introduced simultaneously in a single step, producing a combined alloy or composite layer. The entry applies to processes such as mixed-powder pack cementation, diffusion-based alloying, or other techniques where multiple diffusants are co-deposited onto the substrate in one operation.
[C23C 8/30] Carbo-nitriding -- Carbo-nitriding is a solid-state diffusion treatment in which carbon and nitrogen atoms simultaneously penetrate the surface of a metallic workpiece, forming a hard, wear-resistant compound layer. The process is applied to steel and other alloys to increase surface hardness, fatigue strength and corrosion resistance without melting the base material. It falls under CPC class C23C 8/30 within the coating metallic material subgroup.
[C23C 8/32] of ferrous surfaces -- C23C 8/32 pertains to solid-state diffusion processes that form a coating on ferrous surfaces, such as iron or steel, by diffusing metallic material into the substrate to create a bonded layer. These methods are used to improve wear resistance, corrosion protection, or surface hardness.
[C23C 8/34] more than one element being applied in more than one step -- C23C 8/34 relates to solid-state diffusion coating of metallic substrates in which two or more elements are deposited in separate, successive steps, allowing each element to diffuse into the surface and form a combined alloyed layer. This subgroup is used for multi-element, multi-stage diffusion processes.
[C23C 8/36] using ionised gases, e.g. ionitriding -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Treatment of the metallic surface with ionised gases, leaving reaction products of surface material in the coating, e.g. ionnitriding..
[C23C 8/38] Treatment of ferrous surfaces -- C23C 8/38 covers methods for treating ferrous metal surfaces by solid-state diffusion of elements such as carbon, nitrogen or other alloying agents, including carburizing, nitriding and related processes that modify hardness, wear resistance or corrosion behaviour. The classification applies to techniques where the diffusing species penetrates the substrate without melting, often performed in gas, plasma or solid media.
[C23C 8/40] using liquids, e.g. salt baths, liquid suspensions -- The entry covers methods that deposit metallic coatings by diffusing material from a liquid medium, such as molten salt baths or liquid suspensions, into the surface of a metal substrate. It addresses solid-state diffusion processes where the liquid acts as the carrier for the coating element.
[C23C 8/42] only one element being applied -- C23C 8/42 covers solid-state diffusion methods in which a single metallic element is introduced onto a metal surface to form a coating, typically by heating the substrate so the element diffuses into the lattice and creates a modified surface layer.
[C23C 8/44] Carburising -- C23C 8/44 covers carburising, a solid-state diffusion treatment in which carbon atoms are introduced into the surface layer of a metallic workpiece to raise hardness and wear resistance. The method typically heats the component in a carbon-rich environment so carbon diffuses inward, forming a hardened case while preserving the toughness of the core.
[C23C 8/46] of ferrous surfaces -- C23C 8/46 relates to coating ferrous surfaces by solid-state diffusion, where metallic or non-metallic elements are introduced into the surface of iron or steel to form a thin alloyed layer. The process modifies hardness, wear resistance or corrosion protection without applying a separate coating layer.
[C23C 8/48] Nitriding -- C23C 8/48 covers nitriding, a solid-state diffusion process that introduces nitrogen into the surface of a metal to form hard nitrides, improving wear resistance, fatigue strength and corrosion resistance. The method is used to create protective or functional coatings on steels and other alloys.
[C23C 8/50] of ferrous surfaces -- C23C 8/50 covers solid-state diffusion techniques for applying metallic coatings specifically to ferrous substrates. It addresses processes where alloying elements diffuse into iron or steel surfaces to form a protective or functional layer without melting the base metal.
[C23C 8/52] more than one element being applied in one step -- The C23C 8/52 subclass relates to solid-state diffusion processes in which two or more metallic elements are introduced onto a substrate in a single operation, forming an alloyed or composite coating without separate application steps for each element. It covers methods such as multi-component pack cementation or diffusion-bonding where the elements migrate simultaneously to modify the surface properties.
[C23C 8/54] Carbo-nitriding -- Carbo-nitriding is a solid-state diffusion heat-treatment in which carbon and nitrogen atoms diffuse together into the surface of a steel or other alloy, forming a hard, wear-resistant compound layer. It typically uses temperatures below the melting point and gaseous or plasma atmospheres containing hydrocarbon and nitrogen sources.
[C23C 8/56] of ferrous surfaces -- C23C 8/56 refers to processes that form coatings on ferrous surfaces by solid-state diffusion of metallic elements into the substrate. It includes techniques where metal atoms migrate into the iron or steel surface to create an alloyed or protective layer without melting. The classification is used for patents dealing with diffusion-based metallurgical treatments of iron-based materials.
[C23C 8/58] more than one element being applied in more than one step -- C23C 8/58 covers methods for forming metallic coatings where more than one elemental species is introduced to the substrate in separate application steps, typically using solid-state diffusion to incorporate each element into the metal surface. The classification addresses sequential multi-element diffusion processes for producing alloyed or composite coatings on metallic materials.
[C23C 8/60] using solids, e.g. powders, pastes -- This subgroup deals with methods of applying metallic coatings where the coating material is supplied in solid form such as powders or pastes, rather than liquids. It includes processes like diffusion of solid particles into a substrate surface, often followed by heating to form a metallic layer.
[C23C 8/62] only one element being applied -- C23C 8/62 relates to coating metallic material by solid-state diffusion of a single element into the substrate surface. The process introduces only one elemental species, forming a thin layer or alloy at the interface to modify properties such as hardness, wear resistance or corrosion behaviour. This subclass is used for treatments like carburizing, nitriding or boriding where one diffusing element is applied.
[C23C 8/64] Carburising -- It covers processes of introducing carbon into the surface of a metallic workpiece by heating in a carbon-rich environment to form a hardened case layer; the diffusion occurs in the solid state without melting and is widely used for steels to improve wear resistance and fatigue strength.
[C23C 8/66] of ferrous surfaces -- The CPC subclass C23C 8/66 relates to solid-state diffusion treatments applied to ferrous (iron-based) surfaces. It covers processes such as carburising, nitriding, carbonitriding or other diffusion-based methods that modify the surface composition and properties of steel or cast iron without using a liquid or gaseous coating medium. This subclass falls under the broader categories of chemistry, coating metallic material, and solid-state diffusion into metallic material surfaces.
[C23C 8/68] Boronising -- C23C 8/68 covers boronising, a solid-state diffusion heat treatment in which boron is introduced into the surface of a metallic workpiece to form hard boride layers that increase wear and corrosion resistance. The process typically involves heating the part in a boron-rich environment such as a furnace packed with boron compounds or using gas or plasma sources.
[C23C 8/70] of ferrous surfaces -- C23C 8/70 covers methods for coating ferrous (iron-based) surfaces by solid-state diffusion, where atoms or compounds migrate into the metal substrate without melting, forming a protective or functional layer directly on the steel or iron surface. This subclass pertains to diffusion-based metallic coatings applied to ferrous materials.
[C23C 8/72] more than one element being applied in one step -- This subgroup covers processes where two or more different elements are simultaneously introduced onto a metal surface by solid-state diffusion, forming a mixed-metal coating in a single operation. It falls under coating metallic material within chemistry.
[C23C 8/74] Carbo-nitriding -- Carbo-nitriding is a solid-state thermochemical diffusion treatment applied to metallic surfaces, especially steels, in which both carbon and nitrogen atoms simultaneously penetrate the substrate to form a hardened, wear-resistant compound layer. The process combines carburizing and nitriding, enhancing surface hardness, fatigue strength and corrosion resistance while retaining the bulk material's core properties.
[C23C 8/76] of ferrous surfaces -- The C23C 8/76 subclass deals with applying coatings to ferrous surfaces by solid-state diffusion, where metal atoms migrate into the substrate and form a hardened, corrosion-resistant layer. It covers processes that modify steel or iron parts without melting, using heat or mechanical activation to achieve metallurgical bonding.
[C23C 8/78] more than one element being applied in more than one step -- C23C 8/78 relates to solid-state diffusion coating processes in which two or more different elements are introduced onto a metallic substrate in separate, sequential steps, such as layered or alternating deposition followed by diffusion. The classification covers methods that apply each element in a distinct stage to form a multi-element coating on the metal surface.
[C23C 8/80] After-treatment -- The C23C 8/80 entry concerns after-treatment steps applied to metallic surfaces that have undergone solid-state diffusion. It includes processes such as heat-treatment, annealing, surface polishing or other modifications performed after the primary diffusion coating to adjust hardness, stress, corrosion resistance or other surface properties.
[C23D] ENAMELLING OF, OR APPLYING A VITREOUS LAYER TO, METALS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes for enamelling or for applying glass layers on metal.  Enamelling is here only the coating of metals with vitreous powders in dry form, in dispersion or mixed with a polymeric binder (e.g. transfer sheets) that will disappear during burning without leaving byproducts. The heat treatment is here to melt the powder and eventually to burn the carrier, when present.  The coating of metal with glass can be done by the same processes as enamelling, by coating with molten glass.
[C23D 1/00] Melting or fritting the enamels -- C23D 1/00 covers processes in which an enamel is melted or fritted as a preliminary step before it is applied to a metal substrate. The classification includes heating the enamel powder or frit to a liquid or semi-solid state, thereby forming a glassy coating when it cools on the metal surface. It is used for enamelling techniques that involve a vitreous layer on metallic articles.
[C23D 1/02] Granulating the melt -- Granulating the melt refers to breaking a molten enamel or frit into small granules while it is still liquid, creating a particulate form that can be cooled, stored, or re-melted for later use in coating metallic substrates. This step follows the melting or fritting of the enamel and facilitates controlled application in subsequent enamelling processes.
[C23D 11/00] Continuous processes -- C23D 11/00 covers continuous methods for applying a vitreous, enamel-type coating to metal surfaces, including processes that keep the workpiece or coating material in nonstop motion. It includes techniques such as roller, dip, spray, extrusion or other uninterrupted feed systems used to produce coated metal articles.
[C23D 13/00] After-treatment -- C23D 13/00 refers to after-treatment steps carried out on metals that have received a vitreous (glass-like) coating or enamel. The subclass includes operations such as heat-treating, polishing, sealing, aging or other processes applied after the primary coating to improve adhesion, durability, appearance or other functional properties. It sits under chemistry → coating metallic material → enamelling of, or applying a vitreous layer to, metals.
[C23D 13/02] Removing defects by local re-melting of the enamel -- The code C23D 13/02 covers after-treatment methods for metallic enamel coatings in which localized re-melting is used to eliminate imperfections such as cracks, pits or unevenness, restoring a uniform vitreous layer on the metal surface.
[C23D 15/00] Joining enamelled articles to other enamelled articles by processes involving an enamelling step -- The C23D 15/00 subclass covers methods for joining two enamel-coated metal items where the joining operation includes an additional enamelling step, such as re-applying or fusing vitreous layers during assembly. It encompasses processes that create a continuous enamel surface across the joint of the articles.
[C23D 17/00] De-enamelling -- C23D 17/00 relates to the removal of enamel or vitreous coatings from metal surfaces. It covers processes and equipment used to strip, peel or otherwise de-enamel metallic articles, including chemical, mechanical and thermal methods. This subclass falls under chemistry, coating metallic material and enamelling of metals.
[C23D 3/00] Coating with the enamels -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Pre-treatment of metals when they are specific to enamelling.
[C23D 5/00] Coating with enamels or vitreous layers -- The CPC subclass C23D 5/00 concerns the application of enamel or vitreous (glass-like) coatings onto metal surfaces, encompassing processes and equipment used to create a bonded, protective or decorative layer of ceramic material on metals.
[C23D 5/005] by a method specially adapted for coating special objects -- This subgroup covers processes that use specially adapted techniques to apply enamel or vitreous layers to particular objects such as pipes, wires, intricate shapes or other items where conventional enamel methods are unsuitable. It includes equipment or procedures tailored to the geometry, size or material of the object being coated.
[C23D 5/02] by wet methods -- C23D 5/02 covers the application of enamel or other vitreous layers to metal objects using wet processes such as dips, sprays, brush-coating, or flow-over of liquid suspensions, solutions or pastes, where the coating is deposited in a fluid state before drying or firing. This subclass groups methods that rely on liquid media rather than dry or powder techniques.
[C23D 5/04] by dry methods -- C23D 5/04 pertains to the application of enamel or glass-like (vitreous) layers onto metal surfaces using dry techniques. These methods include powder spraying, electrostatic powder deposition, and subsequent heating or sintering to fuse the coating without a liquid carrier. The classification captures processes where the coating material is applied in a solid or powdered form rather than as a wet slurry.
[C23D 5/06] producing designs or letters -- C23D 5/06 covers processes for creating decorative designs, letters or symbols on metal by applying enamel or vitreous layers. It includes techniques such as printing, stamping, drawing or otherwise forming patterns in the coating before it is fused to the metal surface, providing ornamental or identification markings.
[C23D 5/08] Applying enamels non-uniformly over the surface -- C23D 5/08 covers processes for applying enamel or other vitreous coatings to metal in a non-uniform manner, such as selective spraying, brushing or spotting that produces patterned or irregular coverage rather than a continuous film.
[C23D 5/10] with refractory materials -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Coating metals with ceramics -> C23C
[C23D 7/00] Treating the coatings, e.g. drying before burning -- C23D 7/00 covers methods for treating enamel or vitreous coatings on metal before firing, such as drying, preheating, or other conditioning steps that improve adhesion or reduce defects. These processes are applied after the coating is applied and before the final burning stage to ensure uniformity and quality of the finished surface.
[C23D 9/00] Firing the enamels -- This subgroup covers the heating step that fuses enamel coatings on metal workpieces, specifying temperature ranges, dwell times and equipment such as kilns or ovens. It includes post-application treatments that transform the vitreous layer into a durable glassy film bonded to the substrate.
[C23D 9/02] Non-electric muffle furnaces -- C23D 9/02 refers to non-electric muffle furnaces employed to fire enamel or vitrified layers on metal surfaces. These furnaces create a sealed, high-temperature chamber without electric heating elements, enabling controlled vitrification in coating applications.
[C23D 9/04] Non-electric tunnel ovens -- Non-electric tunnel ovens are continuous furnaces that use combustion gases rather than electricity to fire vitreous enamel layers on metal workpieces, delivering uniform heat for enamel sintering in coating and metallurgical processes.
[C23D 9/06] Electric furnaces -- C23D 9/06 covers electric furnaces used to fire vitreous enamel coatings on metal substrates. The subclass defines furnaces powered by electricity, including batch, continuous and vacuum types, designed to achieve the temperatures required for enamel melting and bonding. It falls under the broader categories of chemistry, metallic coating and enamelling processes.
[C23D 9/08] Supporting devices for burning-bars -- Supporting devices for burning-bars include fixtures, holders or supports that position and stabilize the metal workpiece while the enamel layer is fired in a furnace, ensuring even heat exposure and preventing distortion or damage during the vitrification process. These devices are used in the enamelling of metallic articles where precise control of the firing environment is required.
[C23D 9/10] Loading or unloading devices -- Loading or unloading devices are apparatuses used to introduce or remove metal workpieces, often coated with enamel, into and out of furnaces during the firing process. They facilitate handling of items while applying or drying vitreous layers and are employed in industrial coating operations involving metallic materials.
[C23F] NON-MECHANICAL REMOVAL OF METALLIC MATERIAL FROM SURFACE -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods, compositions and apparatus for etching of metallic materials by chemical means ( C23F1/00 - C23F1/44 ).  Regeneration of etching compositions, including apparatus for regenerating etching agents ( C23F1/46 ).  Methods, compositions and apparatus for chemical polishing (brightening) of metals ( C23F3/00 - C23F3/06 ).  Other non-mechanical processes for removing metallic material from surfaces, e.g. by plasma or sputter etching, and compositions therefor ( C23F4/00 - C23F4/04 ).  Simultaneous chemical and mechanical removal of metallic material from surfaces, e.g. by laser ablation ( C23F4/02 , C23F4/04 ).  Inhibiting corrosion of metallic material by applying inhibitors to the surface in danger of corrosion ( C23F11/00 - C23F11/188 ).  Inhibiting corrosion of metallic material by adding inhibitors to the corrosive agent ( C23F11/00 - C23F11/188 ).  Inhibiting corrosion of metals by anodic or cathodic protection ( C23F13/00 - C23F13/22 ).  Inhibiting incrustation in apparatus for heating liquids for physical or chemical purposes ( C23F14/00 ), in polymerisation reactors ( C23F15/005 ).  Corrosion inhibitors per se ( C23F11/12 - C23F11/18 ).  Incrustation inhibitors per se ( C23F14/02 ).  Other methods of preventing corrosion or incrustation, e.g. by removing the corrosive agent from the medium or rendering it non corrosive by neutralizing it ( C23F15/00 ).  Other apparatus for executing the methods mentioned above as far as they are specially adapted for treating metallic material, e.g. apparatus for regenerating etching agents; apparatus for anodic or cathodic protection, apparatus for executing the processes of the other groups, but only if they have at least one feature which is specifically designed for treating metallic material ( C23F1/00 , C23F3/00 ; C23F4/00 , C23F13/00 , C23F14/00 , C23F15/00 ).  Multi-step processes for surface treatment of metallic material involving at least one process provided for in class C23 and at least one process covered by subclass C21D or C22F or class C25 ( C23F17/00 ).  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Methods for preventing fouling -> B08B17/00 - Working of metal by electro-erosion -> B23H - Desurfacing by applying flames -> B23K7/00 - Working metal by laser beam -> B23K26/00 - Adding scale preventives or removers to water -> C02F5/00 - Polishing compositions -> C09G - Etching process and compositions for silicon or germanium -> C09K13/00 - Adding corrosion inhibitors to pickling solutions -> C23G - Electrolytic etching or polishing -> C25F  **Glossary:** - Metallic material: covers metals and alloys - Alloys: include: metallic composite materials containing a substantial proportion of fibres or other somewhat larger particles;ceramic compositions bonded by free metal, containing free metal bonded to carbides, diamond, oxides, borides, nitrides or silicides, e.g. cermets, or other metal compounds, e.g. oxynitrides or sulfides, other than as macroscopic reinforcing agents. - Applying corrosion inhibitors: Applying corrosion inhibitors to a metallic surface layer is not considered to be applying a protective coating. - Inhibiting corrosion: Inhibiting corrosion is a specific form of preventing corrosion, the words are not synonyms - Corrosion: Deterioration of a metallic material due to a change of valence state caused by reactions with its environment. - Incrustation: Accumulation of deposition /precipitation of undesired solid /dense products on a metallic surface in systems in which a fluid circulation takes place, preferably a water-based fluid, e.g. deposition /precipitation of compounds of calcium, magnesium, barium or strontium (carbonates/ sulphates, oxalates, phosphates, fluorides, silica, silicates, naphtelenates), iron /lead / zinc sulphide, zinc /cadmium carbonates (white rust).
[C23F 1/00] Etching metallic material by chemical means -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods, compositions and apparatus for etching of metallic materials by chemical means.  Regeneration of etching compositions, including apparatus for regenerating etching agents ( C23F1/46 ).  Selective etching /dealloying of an element /phase from an alloy in order to obtain a porous surface ( C23F1/00 ).  Selective etching of complex structures (i.e. metallic mutilayers) ( C23F1/44 ).  Local etching e.g. by using a photoresist mask ( C23F1/02 ).  Apparatus for photo-mechanical printing surface ( C23F1/08 ).  Emulsions compositions for etching of metallic material ( C23F1/42 ).  In the subgroup C23F1/10 , the expression "etching composition" is used with the meaning: "etching composition for specific metals" and covers: etching composition of specific metals, and not etching composition in general;  The subgroup C23F1/06 relates to "sharpening files" (old technology).  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Etching compositions of silicon or germanium -> C09K13/00 - Electrolytic etching -> C25F3/02 - Etching semiconductors -> H10P  **Glossary:** - Chemical Etching: Removal or dissolution of metallic material from a surface by chemical reaction between the metallic material and the etching agent - Chemical Milling: Removal of high amount of metallic material from a piece having big dimensions by chemical reaction between the metallic material and the etching agent
[C23F 1/02] Local etching -- C23F 1/02 covers the localized chemical removal of metal from a surface, where an etchant acts only on specific areas to create patterns, openings or relief features. Methods may use masks, resists or controlled application of the reagent to achieve selective metal dissolution without mechanical action. This class includes processes for producing engraved, printed or micro-structured metal parts.
[C23F 1/04] Chemical milling -- C23F 1/04 concerns chemical milling, the non-mechanical removal of metallic material from a surface by etching with chemical agents. It covers processes that dissolve or otherwise chemically attack metals to create patterns or reduce thickness, typically used in manufacturing and finishing of metallic components.
[C23F 1/06] Sharpening files -- The C23F 1/06 subclass concerns chemical sharpening of metal files, where etching or other non-mechanical means remove material to restore the cutting edges. It covers processes that dissolve or recess surface metal to regain sharpness without grinding, typically applied to maintain tool performance.
[C23F 1/08] Apparatus, e.g. for photomechanical printing surfaces -- C23F 1/08 covers devices used in photomechanical printing that chemically etch metallic surfaces to form images. The apparatus typically includes a plate or substrate holder, exposure system and chemical treatment zones that remove metal without mechanical action. These tools enable precise pattern creation for printing applications.
[C23F 1/10] Etching compositions -- C23F 1/10 classifies chemical etching compositions employed to remove metallic material from surfaces without mechanical action. It includes acidic, alkaline or complexing solutions designed to dissolve or selectively attack metals in processes such as printed-circuit fabrication or surface patterning.
[C23F 11/00] Inhibiting corrosion of metallic material by applying inhibitors to the surface in danger of corrosion or adding them to the corrosive agent -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Inhibiting corrosion of metallic material by applying inhibitors to the surface in danger of corrosion.  Inhibiting corrosion of metallic material by adding inhibitors to the corrosive agent.  Preventing leaching /elution of a metallic element /phase from an alloy, e.g. in water systems ( C23F11/00 ).  Preventing leaching /elution of a metallic element /phase from an alloy, e.g. in water systems ( C23F11/08 , C23F11/10 ).  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Adding corrosion inhibitors to pickling solutions -> C23G  **Glossary:** - Applying corrosion inhibitors: Applying corrosion inhibitors to a metallic surface layer is not considered to be applying a protective coating. - Adding corrosion inhibitors: Adding corrosion inhibitors to a corrosive agent (composition) is always in a small amount, which makes a big difference between a corrosion inhibiting composition and a protective coating composition
[C23F 11/02] in air or gases by adding vapour phase inhibitors -- This subclass covers methods of protecting metal surfaces from corrosion by introducing vapor-phase inhibitors into the surrounding air or gas, allowing the inhibitor to adsorb onto the metal and form a protective layer. It belongs to the non-mechanical removal of metallic material category, under coating metallic material, and pertains to inhibiting corrosion by adding inhibitors to the corrosive environment.
[C23F 11/04] in markedly acid liquids -- C23F 11/04 covers methods of protecting metal surfaces from corrosion by applying corrosion inhibitors in strongly acidic liquids, such as acid baths or solutions, where the inhibitor is added to the liquid or directly treated onto the metal.
[C23F 11/06] in markedly alkaline liquids -- C23F 11/06 relates to corrosion-inhibition techniques that employ markedly alkaline liquids as the medium. It covers applying corrosion inhibitors to metal surfaces or adding them to the alkaline corrosive solution to prevent or reduce metal loss without mechanical action.
[C23F 11/08] in other liquids -- C23F 11/08 refers to chemical methods for preventing corrosion of metal surfaces by applying corrosion inhibitors in liquid media that are not otherwise specified, such as organic solvents or specialty fluids. The entry falls under Chemistry → Coating metallic material → Non-mechanical removal of metallic material from surface → Inhibiting corrosion by adding inhibitors to the corrosive environment.
[C23F 11/10] using organic inhibitors -- C23F 11/10 pertains to the use of organic corrosion inhibitors applied to metal surfaces or introduced into the corrosive medium to protect the material from deterioration, forming part of the non-mechanical removal of metallic material from surfaces within the coating metallic material subclass.
[C23F 11/12] Oxygen-containing compounds -- C23F 11/12 includes oxygen-containing compounds used to prevent or mitigate corrosion of metals, either by applying the inhibitor directly to the metal surface or by introducing it into the corrosive environment. These agents act chemically to form protective films or neutralize aggressive species, enabling non-mechanical removal of metallic material.
[C23F 11/122] Alcohols; Aldehydes; Ketones -- C23F 11/122 covers the use of low-molecular organic compounds - specifically alcohols, aldehydes and ketones - as corrosion-inhibiting agents applied to metallic surfaces. These compounds are employed to prevent or reduce corrosion of the metal.
[C23F 11/185] Refractory metal-containing compounds -- C23F 11/185 covers compositions that contain refractory metals and are used as corrosion inhibitors applied to metal surfaces or added to corrosive media. The classification falls under non-mechanical removal of metallic material from surfaces, specifically the inhibition of corrosion by surface-applied or additive inhibitors. It is part of the broader chemistry group for coating metallic material.
[C23F 11/187] Mixtures of inorganic inhibitors -- This class relates to mixtures of inorganic corrosion inhibitors that are applied to metal surfaces or introduced into a corrosive environment to protect the metal from degradation. It falls under non-mechanical removal of metallic material and addresses chemical methods for inhibiting corrosion.
[C23F 11/188] containing phosphates -- C23F 11/188 covers the use of phosphate-containing compounds as corrosion inhibitors applied to metal surfaces or added to the corrosive medium in order to prevent or slow corrosion, a non-mechanical chemical method of protecting metallic materials.
[C23F 1/12] Gaseous compositions -- This CPC subclass C23F 1/12 concerns gaseous compositions used for chemically etching metallic materials. It includes mixtures of gases, vapours or plasma-generating agents that remove metal from a surface without mechanical action, such as acid-vapour or plasma etching processes.
[C23F 1/14] Aqueous compositions -- Aqueous compositions cover water-based solutions formulated for chemically etching metallic surfaces, typically containing acids, salts, additives or inhibitors that facilitate the non-mechanical removal of metal coatings. These formulations are used in processes that dissolve or strip metal layers without mechanical force.
[C23F 1/16] Acidic compositions -- C23F 1/16 refers to acidic compositions employed to chemically etch metallic surfaces, removing material without mechanical action. These reagents dissolve or react with the metal to create patterns or clean areas, and are classified under the chemistry of coating metallic material and non-mechanical metal removal.
[C23F 1/18] for etching copper or alloys thereof -- C23F 1/18 covers chemical etching processes specifically directed at copper and its alloys, used to remove metal from a surface without mechanical action. It includes methods employing acidic, alkaline, or other reactive solutions to pattern or clean copper in applications such as printed circuit board fabrication and metal finishing.
[C23F 1/20] for etching aluminium or alloys thereof -- A process for chemically etching aluminium or its alloys, removing material from the surface without mechanical action. The method uses chemical reagents to dissolve or pattern the metal, typically for cleaning, surface preparation, or creating micro-structures. It falls within the coating metallic material group of the Cooperative Patent Classification.
[C23F 1/22] for etching magnesium or alloys thereof -- C23F 1/22 addresses chemical etching processes applied to magnesium or its alloys, where material is removed from the surface by chemical reaction rather than by mechanical means. It falls under the hierarchy of chemistry → coating metallic material → non-mechanical removal of metallic material from surface → etching metallic material by chemical means.
[C23F 1/26] for etching refractory metals -- This subclass covers chemical etching processes specifically for refractory metals such as tungsten, molybdenum, tantalum and niobium, where the metal is removed from a surface without mechanical action. It includes methods using acids, halogen-containing solutions or other reagents to selectively dissolve or pattern these high-melting-point metals.
[C23F 1/28] for etching iron group metals -- C23F 1/28 is a subclass of the Cooperative Patent Classification dealing with chemical etching of metallic surfaces, specifically targeting iron-group metals such as iron, cobalt and nickel. It covers non-mechanical methods that dissolve or remove these metals by reactive chemicals, typically acids or other etchants, to produce patterned or cleaned surfaces.
[C23F 1/30] for etching other metallic material -- This CPC group covers non-mechanical removal of metal from a surface by chemical etching when the metal is not one of the specific materials dealt with in other subclasses. It includes processes that use chemical reagents to dissolve or otherwise remove metallic substrates other than those defined in the more specific entries of the coating metallic material section.
[C23F 13/00] Inhibiting corrosion of metals by anodic or cathodic protection -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods, apparatuses and electrode materials for inhibiting corrosion of metals by anodic or cathodic protection, i.e. for applying a current and polarizing a metallic object /structure to be protected while the object /structure is in use.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Anodisation -> C25D11/02 - Reinforcing elements, e.g. for concrete : Anti-corrosion -> E04C5/015 - Coatings or treating compositions -> E04C5/017  **Glossary:** - Anodic protection (AP): Technique to control the corrosion of a metal surface by making it the anode of an electrochemical cell and controlling the electrode potential in a zone where the metal is passive. - Cathodic protection (CP): Technique to control the corrosion of a metal surface by making it the cathode of an electrochemical cell - Sacrificial anode: A piece of corrodible metal, attached to a metallic surface to be protected, that is preferentially consumed by electrolytic action. - Stray currents: Stray currents may originate from direct-current distribution lines, substations, or street railway systems, etc., and flow into a pipe system or other steel structure.
[C23F 13/005] Anodic protection -- The entry C23F 13/005 deals with anodic protection, a corrosion-inhibition technique that applies a controlled anodic current to maintain a metal's surface in a protective oxide state. It is used for alloys prone to passivation and falls under non-mechanical removal of metallic material from surfaces within the coating metallic material branch of chemistry.
[C23F 13/02] cathodic -- The CPC code C23F 13/02 relates to cathodic protection, a technique that prevents corrosion of metals by making the metal a cathode of an electrochemical cell, often using sacrificial anodes or an external current. This falls under chemistry, coating metallic material, and non-mechanical removal of metallic material from a surface.
[C23F 13/04] Controlling or regulating desired parameters -- C23F 13/04 pertains to methods and apparatus for controlling or regulating key parameters-such as voltage, current density, electrolyte composition, temperature, or flow rate-during anodic or cathodic protection processes that chemically remove metallic material from a surface. The entry covers monitoring and adjustment techniques that optimize corrosion inhibition and non-mechanical metal removal, ensuring effective coating or cleaning without physical abrasion.
[C23F 13/06] Constructional parts, or assemblies of cathodic-protection apparatus -- C23F 13/06 covers the structural components and complete assemblies used in cathodic-protection systems, including anodes, cathodes, connectors, and supporting frames that enable anodic or cathodic protection of metal surfaces. These parts are designed to inhibit corrosion by electrically managing the metal's environment rather than by mechanical means.
[C23F 13/08] Electrodes specially adapted for inhibiting corrosion by cathodic protection -- C23F 13/08 covers electrodes that are specifically designed for cathodic protection systems to prevent corrosion of metals. These electrodes supply a protective current that makes the metal surface a cathode, reducing anodic dissolution, and are used in pipelines, tanks and other structures exposed to aggressive environments.
[C23F 13/10] Electrodes characterised by the structure -- The C23F 13/10 subgroup covers electrodes whose defining feature is their physical structure-such as shape, composition, surface texture or internal geometry-used in electrochemical processes for non-mechanical metal removal or coating. These structured electrodes enable anodic or cathodic protection, helping to inhibit corrosion of metals by controlling the electro-chemical reactions at the surface.
[C23F 13/12] Electrodes characterised by the material -- The CPC subclass C23F 13/12 covers electrodes whose defining feature is the material from which they are made, intended for use in non-mechanical removal of metallic material and in anodic or cathodic corrosion-protection systems. It groups patents that specify the composition of electrodes for coating, plating or protective applications.
[C23F 13/14] Material for sacrificial anodes -- C23F 13/14 covers materials used as sacrificial anodes to protect metals by providing anodic or cathodic corrosion inhibition. These substances are applied to metal surfaces to remove metal ions without mechanical action, typically as part of coating systems.
[C23F 13/16] Electrodes characterised by the combination of the structure and the material -- C23F 13/16 refers to electrodes whose functional characteristics are defined by both their physical structure and the material from which they are made, employed in chemical processes that remove metal without mechanical action, such as anodic or cathodic corrosion-inhibition coatings.
[C23F 13/18] Means for supporting electrodes -- C23F 13/18 covers devices that hold or position electrodes used in non-mechanical removal of metallic material, such as anodic or cathodic corrosion-protection processes. The means for supporting electrodes may include frames, clamps, brackets or other structures that keep the electrodes stable during coating or cleaning operations.
[C23F 1/32] Alkaline compositions -- Alkaline compositions are chemical mixtures designed to etch metallic surfaces by dissolving metal without mechanical action, enabling controlled non-mechanical removal of material. In the CPC system they fall under class C23F 1/32, which covers chemical etching processes for metallic coatings and substrates.
[C23F 13/20] Conducting electric current to electrodes -- The CPC class C23F 13/20 covers techniques that apply an electric current to electrodes in order to provide anodic or cathodic protection of metal surfaces, thereby inhibiting corrosion. It includes non-mechanical, electrically driven processes used in coating and removal of metallic material from surfaces.
[C23F 13/22] Monitoring arrangements therefor -- The code C23F 13/22 pertains to devices and methods that monitor the operation or condition of anodic or cathodic corrosion-protection systems applied to metallic coatings, including sensors, measurement circuits, data-acquisition units and control arrangements that track parameters such as potentials, currents or coating integrity.
[C23F 1/34] for etching copper or alloys thereof -- C23F 1/34 pertains to non-mechanical removal of metallic material by chemical means, specifically covering processes for etching copper or its alloys from a surface.

[C23F 14/00] Inhibiting incrustation in apparatus for heating liquids for physical or chemical purposes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Inhibiting incrustation in apparatus for heating liquids for physical or chemical purposes, e.g. evaporators, distillations units, crystallisation units, etc. ( C23F14/00 ). [C23F 2213/00] Aspects of inhibiting corrosion of metals by anodic or cathodic protection -- C23F 2213/00 relates to techniques for preventing metal corrosion by employing anodic or cathodic protection, including the use of chemical inhibitors or electrical methods that suppress electrochemical reactions on metal surfaces. The ionic conductor facilitates ion transport for anodic or cathodic protection, enabling non-mechanical removal of metal from the surface.

[C23F 3/00] Brightening metals by chemical means -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods, compositions and apparatus for chemical polishing or chemical-mechanical (brightening) of metals.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Abrasive or related blasting, e.g. shot blasting -> B24C - Electrolytic polishing -> C25F3/16  **Glossary:** - Chemical Polishing: Removal of metallic material from a surface in order to make the surface more bright by chemical reaction between the metallic material and the polishing agent - Chemical-Mechanical Polishing (CMP): Removal of metallic material from a surface by combining abrasive polishing and chemical polishing, typically by applying a polishing composition or slurry to a polishing pad, establishing pressure-contact between the composition-or slurry-coated surface and the polishing pad while providing relative motion, typically rotational or orbital motion, between the surface and the polishing pad. The chemically- mechanically polishing compositions typically contains an abrasive material, such as silica, ceria, and/or alumina particles, in an acidic, neutral, or basic solution.

[C23F 4/00] Processes for removing metallic material from surfaces, not provided for in group -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Other non-mechanical processes for removing metallic material from surfaces, e.g. by plasma or sputter etching, and compositions therefor ( C23F4/00 ).  Removal of metallic material from surfaces, e.g. by evaporation /volatilisation /vaporisation (EP049312, GB998708, GB817017), e.g. CO2 or YAG lasers are utilized to thermally vaporize the metal layer, excimer laser for laser ablation, or in metal-halogen systems by laser stimulated halogen gas etching of metal substrates (US4622095, US5874011), or by using an UV light to produce a product which is either volatile or easily removed in solution (US4490211, US5318662) ( C23F4/02 ).  Removal of metallic material from surfaces, e.g. by physical dissolution /melting (EP0158536), by laser surface melting (EP1640109)( C23F4/04 ).  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Cleaning by radiant energy, e.g. by UV, laser, light beam -> B08B7/0035 - Cutting, scarfing or desurfacing by applying flames, e.g. laser flame cutting -> B23K7/00 - Working metal by laser beam, e.g. welding, cutting or boring metal parts by using plasma arc cutting torch, or a laser beam cutting head -> B23K26/00 - Physical treatment to alter the texture of the surface, e.g. by irradiation with laser or particle beam -> C23C16/0263 - Etching semiconductors, e.g. by plasma -> H10P  **Glossary:** - Laser- induced chemical etching: Removal or dissolution of very thin layers of metallic material from a surface (in a very small amount) by reaction between the metallic material and reactive species (in the presence of reactive gases or under clean conditions) enhanced by incidence of a laser beam, e.g. by reaction of chlorine gas with aluminium is formed aluminium chloride which desorbs resulting in an etching of aluminium surface, the etching process of aluminium is further enhanced by UV laser pulses incident to the surface. - Laser -induced ablation: Removal or dissolution of very thin layers of metallic material from a surface (in a very small amount) by evaporation or physical dissolution /dissociation under clean conditions by using an UV pulsed laser, e.g. an UV Excimer -Laser. - Laser-transmissive ablation: A very thin metal film is selectively removed by means of a single radiation pulse.
[C23F 4/02] by evaporation -- C23F 4/02 relates to non-mechanical methods that eliminate metal from a surface by evaporating the metal. The process involves heating the substrate so that the metallic layer transforms into vapor, which is then removed or condensed elsewhere, and is used when other listed removal techniques are not applicable.
[C23F 4/04] by physical dissolution -- This subclass covers methods for eliminating metallic material from a surface by physical dissolution, where the metal is removed through a solvent or chemical agent without mechanical action. [C23G] CLEANING OR DE-GREASING OF METALLIC MATERIAL BY CHEMICAL METHODS OTHER THAN ELECTROLYSIS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods, compositions and apparatus for stripping non-metallic inorganic coatings from metallic substrates.  **Glossary:** - Metallic material: covers metals and alloys - Pickling of metallic material: Chemical removal or dissolution of surface deposits of inorganic contaminants, such as rust (iron oxides), or scale from ferrous metals, copper or aluminium alloys, or corrosion products from metallic surfaces. Chemical stripping of non-metallic inorganic coatings from metallic substrates. - De-greasing of metallic material: Non-mechanical removal or dissolution of surface deposits of organic contaminants, such as oils, fats, greases, dust, finger-print contaminations, or similar hydrophobic compounds from metallic surfaces.

[C23G 1/30] using inhibitors -- The subclass C23G 1/30 covers methods that employ chemical inhibitors while cleaning or pickling metallic substrates with aqueous solutions or molten salts, aiming to limit corrosion or scale formation during the de-greasing process. It focuses on the addition of substances that suppress unwanted reactions in the cleaning medium.
[C23G 1/32] Heavy metals -- C23G 1/32 addresses the chemical cleaning or pickling of metallic surfaces using solutions or molten salts to remove heavy-metal contaminants. It falls under the broader category of coating metallic material and specifically covers non-electrolytic methods for de-greasing or cleaning metals, focusing on the treatment of alloys and substrates that contain lead, cadmium, mercury, chromium or similar toxic metals.
[C23G 1/34] Light metals -- C23G 1/34 covers processes for chemically cleaning or pickling light metals such as aluminium, magnesium and their alloys using liquid solutions or molten salts, excluding electrolytic methods. The methods are applied to remove scale, oxides or residues and prepare the surface for subsequent coating or treatment.
[C23G 1/36] Regeneration of waste pickling liquors -- The CPC subclass C23G 1/36 concerns processes for restoring spent pickling solutions or molten salts used to chemically clean or de-grease metallic workpieces. It includes methods that remove dissolved metals, acids and other contaminants so the liquors can be reused in further pickling operations, thereby reducing waste and improving resource efficiency.
[C23G 3/00] Apparatus for cleaning or pickling metallic material -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Apparatus for cleaning or pickling metallic material such as pieces, wafers, or articles by chemical means, e.g. with acidic, alkaline, neutral solutions or with molten salts.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Apparatus for cleaning or de-greasing metallic material with organic solvents -> C23G5/04  **Glossary:** - Pickling wires, strips or filaments continuously: pickling coiled wires, strips or filaments or pickling metallic material of continuous length, but not wafers, pieces or articles.
[C23G 3/02] for cleaning wires, strips, filaments continuously -- The CPC subclass C23G 3/02 covers apparatus used to clean or pickle metallic wires, strips or filaments in a continuous process, employing chemical methods other than electrolysis. It falls under the broader categories of chemistry, coating metallic material and cleaning or de-greasing of metallic material.
[C23G 3/021] by dipping -- This subclass covers machines that clean or pickle metal parts by immersing them in chemical solutions. The equipment typically uses a dip tank or conveyor that submerges the workpiece for a set time to remove oils, scale, or oxides without electrolytic action. It falls under coating metallic material cleaning, chemical methods other than electrolysis.
[C23G 3/022] the objects following a helicoidal path -- C23G 3/022 covers apparatus for chemically cleaning or pickling metallic items in which the workpieces are moved along a helicoidal (spiral) trajectory, such as through rotating drums or helical conveyors. The classification falls under the CPC section on coating metallic material and the subgroup for non-electrolytic cleaning methods.
[C23G 3/023] by spraying -- This subclass covers apparatus that clean or pickle metallic material using chemical methods applied by spraying, including spray nozzles, spray chambers and associated pumping or distribution systems that direct cleaning solutions onto metal surfaces. It focuses on equipment designed to deliver the chemical agents in a spray form for effective de-greasing or pickling.
[C23G 3/024] by a combination of dipping and spraying -- C23G 3/024 covers apparatus that cleans or pickles metal surfaces using a combined dip-and-spray process. It falls within the chemical-coating field, specifically methods for chemically degreasing metallic articles that are not based on electrolysis. This subclass addresses equipment that integrates immersion and spray actions in a single cleaning operation.
[C23G 3/025] Details of the apparatus, e.g. linings or sealing means -- The CPC subgroup C23G 3/025 covers the structural and material details of equipment used for chemically cleaning or pickling metallic objects, specifically elements such as internal linings, seals, gaskets and other sealing means that protect the apparatus or control the flow of cleaning agents.
[C23G 3/026] for guiding the objects -- A subclass for apparatus that cleans or pickles metallic parts by chemical (non-electrolytic) methods and incorporates means for guiding the objects during treatment. The guidance features keep workpieces correctly positioned as they pass through the cleaning medium, improving uniformity and efficiency. It belongs to the broader groups dealing with coating metallic material and chemical de-greasing.
[C23G 3/027] Associated apparatus, e.g. for pretreating or after-treating -- The CPC subclass C23G 3/027 covers devices that are used together with a cleaning or pickling system for metals, such as equipment for pre-treatment, post-treatment, rinsing, drying or waste handling. These associated apparatuses support the chemical de-greasing or pickling process but are not the primary cleaning unit themselves.
[C23G 3/028] for thermal or mechanical pretreatment -- C23G 3/028 covers apparatus that applies a thermal or mechanical pretreatment-such as heating, blasting, rolling or vibration-to metallic workpieces before they undergo chemical cleaning or pickling. The pretreatment prepares the surface, removes oxides or scale and enhances the effectiveness of subsequent non-electrolytic chemical de-greasing or cleaning steps.
[C23G 3/029] for removing the pickling fluid from the objects -- C23G 3/029 covers apparatus designed to eliminate residual pickling fluid from metal workpieces after chemical cleaning or de-greasing. The devices typically drain, rinse, or otherwise remove the acidic or alkaline solutions that remain on the surface, preventing corrosion and preparing the material for further processing. This sub-class falls under cleaning or pickling of metallic material by chemical methods, excluding electrolytic processes.
[C23G 3/04] for cleaning pipes -- C23G 3/04 relates to apparatus designed for the chemical cleaning or pickling of metallic pipes, excluding electrolytic methods. It includes devices that convey pipe sections and expose them to cleaning solutions or agents to remove scale, rust, or other contaminants, typically as part of a coating or surface-preparation process.
[C23G 5/00] Cleaning or de-greasing metallic material by other methods -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Other methods, compositions and apparatus for non-mechanical cleaning or de-greasing metallic material, e.g. by using gases, ion beams, plasma, freezing or cooling, supercritical fluids, melts (applying a coating which is a fondant for another coating), ultrasonics, by removing liquid contaminants by suction, by using reactive solids, followed by heating, two-phase cleaning mixtures, e.g. air under pressure in combination with an aqueous solution.
[C23G 5/02] using organic solvents -- C23G 5/02 covers processes for cleaning or de-greasing metallic surfaces that employ organic solvents rather than electrolytic methods. The methods are intended to remove oils, greases and other contaminants before coating or further treatment. It is classified under chemical cleaning techniques for metallic materials.

[C23G 5/06] using emulsions -- C23G 5/06 pertains to the cleaning or de-greasing of metallic items by chemical means that use emulsions, which are mixtures of water-based and oil-based phases. [C25] ELECTROLYTIC OR ELECTROPHORETIC PROCESSES -- C25 covers the production of chemical substances and materials by using an electric current, including electrolytic synthesis, electroplating, and electrophoretic deposition. The class comprises methods that employ electrolytic cells, electrolytes, and related apparatus to drive chemical reactions, separate components, or coat surfaces, and it includes variations such as pulsed or alternating current processes. It is used to classify patents involving electrochemical manufacturing and surface-treatment techniques.
[C25B] ELECTROLYTIC OR ELECTROPHORETIC PROCESSES FOR THE PRODUCTION OF COMPOUNDS OR NON-METALS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic or electrophoretic processes for the production of inorganic compounds, non-metals or organic compounds.  Cells or assemblies of cells and their constructions.  Electrodes, diaphragms.  Operating or servicing of cells.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Treatment of water, waste water, or sewage by electrochemical means, e.g. electrolysis electrodes therefor -> C02F1/46 - Separation or purification of peptides, e.g. of proteins, by electrophoresis -> C07K1/26 - Inhibiting corrosion of metals by anodic or cathodic protection -> C23F13/00 - Single crystal growth -> C30B  **Glossary:** - Monopolar electrode: A monopolar electrode is connected to a power source and thus acts either as an anode or as a cathode. - Bipolar electrode: A bipolar electrode is a floating conductor in contact with an ionically conductive phase. It is a field electrode, positioned in an electrical field between a monopolar anode and a monopolar cathode without being itself connected to a power source. Through the action of the electrical field, the side of the bipolar electrode that faces the cathode acts as an anode, and the side that faces the anode acts as a cathode. - Dimensionally-stable electrode: An electrode that is not intended to dissolve upon electrolysis (not a sacrificial electrode).
[C25B 1/00] Electrolytic production of inorganic compounds or non-metals -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic production of all those inorganic compounds or non-metals that do not fall within the scope of one of the subgroups of C25B1/00 .  Specific compounds like hydrogen, oxygen, silicon, ozone, alkali metal compounds, inorganic acid, per-compounds, etc. are classified in the subgroups of C25B1/00 , not in C25B1/00 .
