[C25B 11/051] Electrodes formed of electrocatalysts on a substrate or carrier -- **Glossary:** - Substrate: The substrate forms the bulk of the electrode and includes oxide layers, which are particularly common on valve metals. - Coating: The coating includes all layers on the substrate, i.e. the coating is not exclusively the electrocatalytic layer, which is usually on top and in contact with the electrolyte. The coating also includes intermediate layers, such as oxide layers that are not inevitable, but intentionally formed on the substrate.

[C25B 11/093] at least one noble metal or noble metal oxide and at least one non-noble metal oxide -- The CPC subclass C25B 11/093 covers electrodes that incorporate at least one noble metal or noble-metal oxide together with at least one non-noble metal oxide. Such mixed-metal electrodes are employed in electrolytic or electrophoretic processes for producing compounds or non-metallic products, where the combination influences conductivity, catalytic activity, or durability.

[C25B 1/13] Ozone -- The C25B 1/13 subclass refers to electrochemical processes that generate ozone. It includes methods and apparatuses that produce O₃ from oxygen or air by electric discharge or related electrolytic techniques, as part of the broader category of electrolytic production of inorganic compounds or non-metals.
[C25B 1/135] Carbon -- Group C25B1/135 is incomplete pending reclassification of documents from group C25B1/00 . Groups C25B1/00 and C25B1/135 should be considered in order to perform a complete search.
[C25B 1/14] Alkali metal compounds -- C25B 1/14 covers electrolytic methods used to produce inorganic compounds of alkali metals, including sodium, potassium, lithium, rubidium and cesium salts. The class addresses the preparation of these compounds by passing electric current through suitable electrolytes or molten salts, and includes variations in cell design, operating conditions and product recovery.
[C25B 1/16] Hydroxides -- The C25B 1/16 subgroup concerns electrolytic processes that produce inorganic hydroxides. It includes methods in which hydroxide ions are generated at the cathode, often from aqueous solutions or molten salts, to form solid or dissolved hydroxide compounds, and covers related conditions, electrodes, and electrolytes used to achieve these products.
[C25B 1/18] Alkaline earth metal compounds or magnesium compounds
[C25B 1/20] Hydroxides -- C25B 1/20 Hydroxides classifies electrolytic methods for producing inorganic hydroxide compounds, such as metal hydroxides, by passing electric current through aqueous solutions or melts. The subclass includes processes that generate hydroxide ions at electrodes and recover the solid hydroxide product, covering industrial routes to bases and precursors for further chemical synthesis.
[C25B 1/21] Manganese oxides -- The class pertains to electrolytic methods for producing manganese oxides such as MnO, MnO₂ and related compounds, involving the passage of electric current through manganese-containing electrolytes or melts. It includes the choice of electrodes, electrolyte composition and operating conditions that control the oxidation state of the manganese during synthesis.
[C25B 1/22] Inorganic acids -- C25B 1/22 relates to the electrolytic production of inorganic acids, covering methods that generate acids such as sulfuric, phosphoric or hydrofluoric acid by electrolysis of suitable salts or solutions. It falls under the chemistry section, specifically electrolytic or electrophoretic processes for producing inorganic compounds or non-metals. This subclass groups patents describing apparatus, conditions and electrolytes used to obtain these acids via electric current.

It is situated within the broader category of electrolytic processes for inorganic compounds in chemistry.
[C25B 1/245] Fluorine -- C25B 1/245 covers the electrolytic production of fluorine, a non-metal obtained by passing electric current through molten fluoride salts or other suitable electrolytes. The process falls under the broader categories of electro-/electrophoretic methods for making inorganic compounds, specifically within the chemistry section of the Cooperative Patent Classification system.
[C25B 1/26] Chlorine -- C25B 1/26 covers the electrolytic production of chlorine, describing processes that generate elemental chlorine by electrolysis of chloride-containing solutions, brines or molten salts. It is placed in the CPC hierarchy under CHEMISTRY - ELECTROLYTIC OR ELECTROPHORETIC PROCESSES - ELECTROLYTIC OR ELECTROPHORETIC PROCESSES FOR THE PRODUCTION OF COMPOUNDS OR NON-METALS - Electrolytic production of inorganic compounds or non-metals.
[C25B 1/265] Chlorates -- C25B 1/265 pertains to the electrolytic preparation of chlorate salts and related inorganic chlorate compounds. It includes processes where chloride ions are oxidized at an anode in aqueous solution to generate chlorate ions, followed by isolation or utilization of the resulting chlorates.
[C25B 1/27] Ammonia -- Group C25B1/27 is incomplete pending reclassification of documents from group C25B1/00 . Groups C25B1/00 and C25B1/27 should be considered in order to perform a complete search.
[C25B 1/28] Per-compounds -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic production of per-compounds (see Glossary of terms).  **Glossary:** - per-compounds: When an element can bond with oxygen in multiple ways to form different polyatomic ions (also called oxyanions), the prefixes "hypo-" and "per-" are used in conjunction with the suffixes "-ite" and "-ate" and a portion (x) of the name of the primary element to designate the oxyanion: (1) a "hypo-x-ite" ion has one fewer oxygen atom than (2) an "x-ite" ion, while an "x-ite" ion has one fewer oxygen atom than (3) an "x-ate" ion, and an "x-ate" ion has one fewer oxygen atom than (4) a "per-x-ate" ion (per-compound). For example, ClO - is hypochlorite, ClO 2 - is chlorite, ClO 3 - is chlorate, and ClO 4 - is perchlorate.
[C25B 1/29] Persulfates -- The subclass C25B 1/29 covers electrolytic processes that produce persulfate salts such as sodium, ammonium or potassium persulfate by oxidation of sulfate ions in aqueous solution. These compounds are strong oxidising agents used in polymerisation, bleaching, etching and other industrial applications. The entry limits the scope to the specific electrolytic preparation methods rather than the downstream use of the persulfates.
[C25B 1/30] Peroxides -- C25B 1/30 designates electrolytic processes for making inorganic peroxide compounds, such as hydrogen peroxide or metal peroxides, by passing electric current through suitable electrolytes. It is part of the hierarchy covering electrolytic or electrophoretic methods for producing non-metals and inorganic compounds.
[C25B 13/00] Diaphragms -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Structural material used to separate the electrodes of an electrolytic or electrophoretic cell to form two or more compartments and allow the flow of an electrolytic solution or the migration of particular ions while preventing the intermixing of the products formed at the surface of the electrodes.
[C25B 13/02] characterised by shape or form -- C25B 13/02 designates diaphragms used in electrolytic or electrophoretic processes for producing compounds or non-metals where the distinguishing feature is the diaphragm's shape or form. It covers membranes, plates or other separator structures whose geometry affects the process performance.

[C25B 1/32] Perborates -- C25B 1/32 covers the electrolytic preparation of perborate compounds, a class of inorganic peroxyborates used as bleaching agents and oxidizers. The subclass falls within the broader category of electrolytic or electrophoretic processes for producing inorganic compounds.
[C25B 1/33] Silicon -- C25B 1/33 covers electrolytic methods for producing silicon, an inorganic non-metal, from molten salts or other electrolytes. The classification includes processes that generate silicon metal or silicon-based compounds by applying an electric current, often involving reduction of silica or silicon dioxide. It falls under the broader CPC groups dealing with electrolytic production of inorganic compounds and non-metals.
[C25B 1/34] Simultaneous production of alkali metal hydroxides and chlorine, oxyacids or salts of chlorine, e.g. by chlor-alkali electrolysis -- The code C25B 1/34 covers electrolytic processes that simultaneously generate alkali-metal hydroxides together with chlorine, its oxyacids or chlorine salts, such as the classic chlor-alkali electrolysis. It is used for patents describing combined production of these inorganic compounds in a single electrolytic cell.
[C25B 1/36] in mercury cathode cells -- This subclass concerns electrolytic processes that use a mercury cathode, where the cathodic surface is a liquid mercury pool or a mercury-amalgam. It covers the production of inorganic compounds or non-metallic elements by reduction at the mercury surface, such as in chlor-alkali, sodium or other metal-mercury cell operations.
[C25B 1/42] Decomposition of amalgams -- The CPC subclass C25B 1/42 covers electrolytic processes that decompose amalgams-mixtures of mercury with other metals-by using electric current to separate the metallic component from mercury, facilitating recovery of the metal or purification of the mercury.
[C25B 1/44] with the aid of catalysts -- This subclass covers electrolytic processes that produce inorganic compounds or non-metals with the assistance of a catalyst, whereby the catalytic agent is used in the electrolytic cell to lower the required energy, increase reaction rate or improve product selectivity.
[C25B 1/46] in diaphragm cells -- This subclass covers the use of diaphragm cells for electrolytic production of inorganic compounds or non-metallic elements, where the cell contains a porous separator that isolates the anode and cathode compartments while allowing ion migration. It addresses methods and apparatus employing such diaphragms to control product distribution and improve efficiency in processes such as chlorine-alkali or metal extraction.

[C25B 9/73] of the filter-press type -- **Glossary:** - Filter-press type cells: Filter-press type cells generally consist of a stack of vertical frames that define electrolysis chambers in which electrodes are arranged vertically.
[C25B 9/75] having bipolar electrodes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Stacks of a plurality of cells with bipolar electrodes, as in a filter press.  **Glossary:** - Monopolar electrode: A monopolar electrode is connected to a power source and thus acts either as an anode or as a cathode. - Bipolar electrode: A bipolar electrode is a floating conductor in contact with an ionically conductive phase. It is a field electrode, positioned in an electrical field between a monopolar anode and a monopolar cathode without being itself connected to a power source. Through the action of the electrical field, the side of the bipolar electrode that faces the cathode acts as an anode, and the side that faces the anode acts as a cathode.
[C25B 9/77] having diaphragms -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Cells with a diaphragm, e.g. membrane or separator, which is a permeable barrier between electrodes.
[C25C] PROCESSES FOR THE ELECTROLYTIC PRODUCTION, RECOVERY OR REFINING OF METALS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic production or recovery (electrowinning) of metals and alloys from solutions or melts.  Electrorefining of metals and alloys in solutions or melts.  Constructional parts, cells or assemblies of cells for the electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metals or alloys.  Servicing or operating of cells for the electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metals or alloys.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Removing metallic impurities from waste water or sewage by electrolytic methods -> C02F1/461 - Inhibiting corrosion of metals by anodic or cathodic protection -> C23F13/00 - Single crystal growth -> C30B
[C25C 1/00] Electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metals by electrolysis of solutions -- This subclass covers processes that obtain, reclaim or purify metallic elements by passing electric current through solutions containing metal ions, causing the metal to deposit on electrodes. It includes the design of electrolytic cells, bath compositions, operating conditions and methods for controlling deposition quality and product purity.
[C25C 1/02] of light metals -- The C25C 1/02 subclass covers electrolytic methods for producing, recovering or refining light metals such as aluminium, magnesium, calcium, and lithium from aqueous solutions, focusing on the specific electrochemical steps and conditions used for these light-metal processes.
[C25C 1/04] in mercury cathode cells -- C25C 1/04 covers electrolytic metal production, recovery or refining that employs mercury cathode cells, where the metal forms an amalgam with liquid mercury at the cathode and is later separated by stripping or distillation. The subclass captures both batch and continuous cell designs used for metals such as zinc, copper and cadmium.
[C25C 1/06] or iron group metals, refractory metals or manganese -- C25C 1/06 pertains to electrolytic processes used to produce, recover or refine iron-group metals, refractory metals or manganese from aqueous solutions, covering methods such as electrodeposition, electro-refining and related solution-based techniques.
[C25C 1/08] of nickel or cobalt -- This subclass covers electrolytic methods in which nickel or cobalt are deposited, recovered or purified from aqueous solutions by applying an electric current, including electrowinning, plating and subsequent refining steps. It falls under processes for the electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metals.
[C25C 1/10] of chromium or manganese
[C25C 1/12] of copper -- C25C 1/12 covers processes that produce, recover or refine copper through the electrolysis of aqueous solutions. The class details the specific electrolytic techniques, cell designs and operating conditions used to deposit copper metal from copper-containing electrolytes, typically involving cathodic deposition and anodic dissolution. It is a subcategory of broader electro-metal refining methods within the chemistry section of the CPC system.
[C25C 1/14] of tin -- The subclass C25C 1/14 covers electrolytic methods that are directed specifically at the production, recovery or refining of tin from aqueous solutions. It includes processes in which tin ions are deposited on a cathode or otherwise separated by electrolysis, and any related steps for purifying tin obtained by this technique.
[C25C 1/16] of zinc, cadmium or mercury -- C25C 1/16 relates to electrolytic processes used to produce, recover or refine zinc, cadmium or mercury from aqueous solutions. The subclass includes methods where the metal ions are deposited on a cathode by electrolysis, covering electrode configurations, electrolytes and operating conditions specific to these metals.
[C25C 1/18] of lead
[C25C 1/20] of noble metals -- This CPC group covers electrolytic methods for extracting, purifying or recovering noble metals such as gold, silver, platinum and palladium from aqueous or other solutions, including cathodic deposition, anode dissolution and related solution-phase cell operations used to refine these metals.
[C25C 1/22] of metals not provided for in groups -- This subclass covers electrolytic methods for producing, recovering or refining metals that are not specifically covered in other groups of the CPC C25C 1 series. It includes any solution-based electrolysis steps applied to such metals, regardless of the electrode material or cell design. The class is used when a metal has no dedicated subgroup elsewhere.
[C25C 1/24] Alloys obtained by cathodic reduction of all their ions -- This subclass covers processes where an alloy is produced directly from an aqueous solution containing the ions of each component, with all ions simultaneously reduced at the cathode to deposit the alloy. It includes electrolytic recovery or refining methods that form the alloy in situ without separate plating steps.
[C25C 3/00] Electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metals by electrolysis of melts -- **Glossary:** - Melt: molten salt or ionic liquid or fused bath
[C25C 3/02] of alkali or alkaline earth metals
[C25C 3/04] of magnesium
[C25C 3/06] of aluminium -- C25C 3/06 refers to processes that produce, recover or refine aluminium by electrolytic electrolysis of molten metal. It falls under the chemistry section, specifically the sub-category for electrolytic or electrophoretic processes and the broader group dealing with electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metals.
[C25C 3/08] Cell construction, e.g. bottoms, walls, cathodes -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Constructional parts, or assemblies thereof, of cells; servicing or operating of cells for the production of alloys or metals other than aluminium -> C25C7/00
[C25C 3/085] characterised by its non electrically conducting heat insulating parts -- This CPC subgroup covers electrolytic processes that melt metals for production, recovery or refining and are distinguished by the use of heat-insulating parts that do not conduct electricity, providing thermal management without affecting the electrical circuit.
[C25C 3/10] External supporting frames or structures -- C25C 3/10 relates to external supporting frames or structures used in the electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metals from molten baths. It covers devices that hold, brace or secure the melt-containing cell, crucible or furnace, providing mechanical stability during electrolysis.
[C25C 3/12] Anodes -- C25C 3/12 covers the design, materials and fabrication of anodes used in the electrolytic processing of molten metals, including those employed for the production, recovery or refining of metals by melt electrolysis. The subclass addresses features such as anode composition, geometry, surface treatment and methods for mounting or supporting the anode within the electrolytic cell.
[C25C 3/125] based on carbon -- **Glossary:** - Söderberg anode: An electrode used in metallurgy, which continuously forms in an electrical furnace when a mixture of coke and coal-tar pitch is added to a heated steel casing and is baked as it passes through. It emerges into the furnace where it is continuously consumed.
[C25C 3/14] Devices for feeding or crust breaking -- The C25C 3/14 subclass covers apparatus used in the electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metals from molten baths that introduce material into the melt or break through solidified crusts on its surface. It includes feeders, plungers, rakes, rotary or reciprocating devices and any mechanisms that mechanically disrupt a solidified layer to maintain continuous electrolysis. The focus is on equipment that ensures the melt remains accessible for metal deposition or dissolution.
[C25C 3/16] Electric current supply devices, e.g. bus bars -- C25C 3/16 covers devices that deliver electric current to electrolytic cells used for metal production, recovery or refining, such as bus bars, connectors and other distribution components. These supply the necessary power for melt electrolysis and related processes.
[C25C 3/18] Electrolytes -- The C25C 3/18 entry covers the electrolytes employed in melt-electrolysis processes for producing, recovering or refining metals. It includes molten salts, ionic liquids and other conductive media that dissolve metal oxides or alloys and facilitate ion transport during high-temperature electrolysis.
[C25C 3/20] Automatic control or regulation of cells -- The C25C 3/20 subclass covers technologies that automatically control or regulate the behavior of electro-cells used in the electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metals from molten salts or melts. It includes sensor-based feedback systems, process-control algorithms and instrumentation that adjust current, voltage, temperature or melt composition to maintain optimal cell performance. This subclass falls under the broader category of electrolytic processes for metal refining.
[C25C 3/22] Collecting emitted gases -- This subclass covers methods and apparatus for collecting gases emitted during the electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metals from molten baths. It includes techniques for capturing, treating or recycling vapours, fumes and off-gases generated in melt electrolysis to improve environmental control and metal recovery.
[C25C 3/24] Refining -- C25C 3/24 addresses refining of metals by electrolytic treatment of molten metal baths. The classification includes processes that use electric current to dissolve, separate, or remove impurities from a melt, thereby obtaining a higher-purity metal product. Techniques may involve cathodic deposition, anode dissolution, or selective extraction within the molten electrolyte.
[C25C 3/26] of titanium, zirconium, hafnium, tantalum or vanadium -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic production of the metal (titanium, hafnium, tantalum, vanadium) by the direct reduction of the metal ion at the electrode.  Reduction of the metal oxide by another metal (usually calcium) which is itself electrolytically reduced from the electrolyte (usually calcium chloride), although the reduction step of the metal ions is chemical rather than electrolytic.
[C25C 3/28] of titanium -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic production of titanium by the direct reduction of the metal ion at the electrode.  Reduction of titanium oxide by another metal (usually calcium) which is itself electrolytically reduced from the electrolyte (usually calcium chloride), although the reduction step of the titanium ions is chemical rather than electrolytic.
[C25C 3/30] of manganese
[C25C 3/32] of chromium
[C25C 3/34] of metals not provided for in groups -- C25C 3/34 designates electrolytic melt processes used to produce, recover or refine metals that are not otherwise enumerated in the more specific CPC groups. It covers general methods of electrolysis of molten baths for such unspecified metals.
[C25C 3/36] Alloys obtained by cathodic reduction of all their ions -- The subclass C25C 3/36 covers electrolytic processes in which every metal ion present in a molten electrolyte is simultaneously reduced at the cathode, producing an alloy directly rather than separating the metals individually. It falls under the broader category of electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metals from melts.
[C25C 5/00] Electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metal powders or porous metal masses -- The C25C 5/00 group covers electrolytic methods used to produce, recover or refine metal powders and porous metal structures, as opposed to bulk metal forms. It includes processes that generate fine particulate metal or open-cell metallic matrices through electrolysis, deposition, or dissolution-re-precipitation techniques.
[C25C 5/02] from solutions -- C25C 5/02 refers to electrolytic processes that obtain metal powders or porous metal structures directly from liquid solutions. It includes methods where metal ions in an electrolyte are reduced to form fine particles or a porous deposit, covering recovery, precipitation, and collection of the metal product from the solution.
[C25C 5/04] from melts -- Electrolytic processes that generate metal powders or porous metal masses by using molten metal as the source material. The method involves electrolytic reduction or dissolution of the melt to form fine particles or a porous structure, rather than starting from solid or aqueous feedstocks.
[C25C 7/00] Constructional parts, or assemblies thereof, of cells -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Constructional parts, or assemblies thereof, of cells; servicing or operating of cells for the production of aluminium -> C25C3/06 - C25C3/22
[C25C 7/002] of cells comprising at least an electrode made of particles  C25C7/005 ,  C25C7/02  -  C25C7/06  take precedence -- The C25C 7/002 subclass covers constructional parts of electrolytic cells in which at least one electrode is formed from particulate material, such as metal powders that are sintered, compressed or otherwise aggregated. It pertains to cell components used in the electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metals, and is subordinated to the more specific particle-based electrode groups C25C 7/005 and C25C 7/02-C25C 7/06.
[C25C 7/005] of cells for the electrolysis of melts  C25C7/02  -  C25C7/06  take precedence
[C25C 7/007] of cells comprising at least a movable electrode  C25C7/002 ,  C25C7/02  -  C25C7/06  take precedence -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Movable electrodes, be it electrodes that move in space or electrodes that move around an axis, such as rotary electrodes.
[C25C 7/02] Electrodes -- The code C25C 7/02 covers constructional parts or assemblies that function as electrodes in cells used for the electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metals. It includes the design, structure and mounting of anode and cathode components within electrochemical cells. This subclass falls under processes for electrolytic metal production in the CPC hierarchy.
[C25C 7/025] used in cells for the electrolysis of melts -- C25C 7/025 covers constructional parts or assemblies that are installed in cells used for the electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metals from molten melts. These components may include electrodes, containers, separators or supporting structures specifically designed to withstand high-temperature molten electrolyte environments. The class is part of the broader CPC hierarchy for electrolytic or electrophoretic processes in chemistry.
[C25C 7/04] Diaphragms -- C25C 7/04 covers diaphragms used as structural components or assembled parts in electrochemical cells for the electrolytic production, recovery or refining of metals. These diaphragms separate anode and cathode compartments, providing mechanical support while allowing ion transport. The classification applies to designs, materials and configurations of such cell elements.
[C25C 7/06] Operating or servicing -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Operating or servicing of cells, when generally applied to a cell or in a process of C25C .
[C25C 7/08] Separating of deposited metals from the cathode
[C25D] PROCESSES FOR THE ELECTROLYTIC OR ELECTROPHORETIC PRODUCTION OF COATINGS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electroforming.  Electroplating, baths therefor.  Electroplating characterized by the process; pretreatment or after-treatment of workpieces.  Electroplating characterized by the article coated.  Electrolytic coating other than with metals.  Electrolytic coating by surface reaction, reforming conversion layers.  Electrophoretic coating.  Electrolytic or electrophoretic production of coating containing embedded materials, e.g. particles, whiskers, wires.  Constructional parts, or assemblies thereof, of cells for electrolytic coating.  Electrolytic coating plants.  Processes and equipment for servicing or operating cells for electrolytic coating
[C25D 1/00] Electroforming -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electroforming processes, i.e. processes involving the reproduction or formation of objects by electrodeposition or electrophoresis in which, typically, the deposit does not permanently remain with the base upon which deposition is made.  Apparatuses and devices especially designed for electroforming.  Electrolytic baths especially formulated for electroforming.  Electroformed products
[C25D 1/003] 3D structures, e.g. superposed patterned layers -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electroforming processes for building high-aspect-ratio structures extending from the surface of the base, wherein it would be inappropriate to describe the product obtained as a coated product in the sense of C25D7/00 and wherein the 3-D structure and the base will typically form the final product, e.g. a metal spring electroformed on a base by successive masking and deposition steps. However, the high-aspect-ratio structures may finally be removed from the base as well.  **Glossary:** - LIGA (German acronym): Lithographie, Galvanoformung, Abformung process
[C25D 1/006] Nanostructures, e.g. using aluminium anodic oxidation templates [AAO] -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electroforming of nanostrutures, e.g. electroforming of nanowire arrays using AAO templates.
[C25D 1/02] Tubes -- The C25D 1/02 subclass addresses the electrolytic or electrophoretic formation of tubular metal parts. It covers processes, conditions and equipment used to produce tubes by depositing metal onto a mandrel or within a cavity, forming solid or hollow cylindrical coatings.
[C25D 1/04] Wires -- The C25D 1/04 sub-group deals with the electroforming of wire-shaped products, covering processes and apparatus for depositing metal onto a conductive template to produce wires, including the control of parameters specific to wire formation.
[C25D 1/06] Wholly-metallic mirrors -- C25D 1/06 covers wholly-metallic mirrors made by electroforming, where a metal coating is deposited electrolytically onto a form or substrate and then separated to create a solid metal reflective surface. The mirrors consist entirely of metal without backing layers, and the classification includes processes for forming, shaping and finishing such electro-deposited metal mirrors.
[C25D 1/08] Perforated or foraminous objects, e.g. sieves -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Perforated objects, e.g. nozzle plates and foraminous objects, e.g. metal foams.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Moulds; Masks; Masterforms , e.g. mandrels, stampers -> C25D1/10  **Glossary:** - Foraminous: A material such as metal screen, netting, fabric, foam, etc. that has openings, holes, punctures, etc. penetrating through its entire depth
[C25D 1/10] Moulds -- C25D 1/10 covers moulds employed in electroforming, the electrolytic or electrophoretic technique for creating metal coatings. It addresses the design, material and preparation of moulds that define the shape of the deposited coating during the electrolytic production process.
[C25D 11/00] Electrolytic coating by surface reaction, i.e. forming conversion layers -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic coating by surface reaction with formation of conversion layers, which often serve as passivation layers. However, certain processes are directly classified in the relevant subgroups C25D11/02 - C25D11/38 , e.g. anodisation of refractory metals are classified in C25D11/26 .
[C25D 11/005] Apparatus specially adapted for electrolytic conversion coating  apparatus in general for electrolytic coating  C25D17/00 -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Apparatus specially adapted for electrolytic conversion coating.
[C25D 11/02] Anodisation -- C25D 11/02 relates to anodisation, an electrolytic surface-reaction process that forms conversion oxide layers on metals such as aluminium. The subclass covers the chemical and electrochemical steps used to produce protective or decorative coatings by anodic oxidation in an electrolyte.
[C25D 11/022] Anodisation on selected surface areas -- The CPC subclass C25D 11/022 covers anodising methods that are applied only to predetermined areas of a metal workpiece, producing a conversion coating by an electrolytic surface reaction limited to those selected regions. It falls under the broader group of electrolytic or electrophoretic processes for coating production within the chemistry field.
[C25D 11/024] Anodisation under pulsed or modulated current or potential -- Anodisation carried out with a pulsed or otherwise modulated electrical current or voltage, where the anodic oxidation of a metal surface is performed in discrete or varying intervals rather than continuously, to control film growth, composition, and properties of the resulting conversion coating.
[C25D 11/026] Anodisation with spark discharge -- C25D 11/026 covers anodisation processes that employ a spark discharge to create conversion-type coatings on metal surfaces. The method uses controlled electrical sparks in an electrolytic bath to form protective or decorative oxide layers, representing a specific variant of electrochemical coating formation within the broader class of electrolytic or electrophoretic processes.
[C25D 11/028] Borodising,, i.e. borides formed electrochemically -- This subclass covers electrochemical formation of boride conversion layers on metal surfaces, known as borodising. It includes processes where boron is deposited by electrolytic means to create hard, corrosion-resistant coatings applied through surface-reaction methods.
[C25D 11/04] of aluminium or alloys based thereon
[C25D 11/045] for forming AAO templates -- C25D 11/045 covers electrochemical methods that produce anodic aluminum oxide (AAO) templates, i.e., conversion-layer coatings formed on aluminum surfaces by anodisation. The processes involve electrolytic reactions that generate a porous oxide film used as a nanoscale mask or scaffold for subsequent material deposition or patterning.
[C25D 11/06] characterised by the electrolytes used -- C25D 11/06 covers electrolytic coating processes that are distinguished primarily by the type of electrolyte employed. It includes methods where acids, bases, salts or mixed solutions are used to form conversion layers on metal surfaces through surface reactions. The classification is used for patents describing how the electrolyte composition controls coating properties and deposition mechanisms.
[C25D 11/08] containing inorganic acids -- C25D 11/08 covers electrolytic coating processes in which a conversion layer is formed on a metal surface by a surface-reaction type electrolyte, specifically using inorganic acids to produce protective or decorative films.
[C25D 11/10] containing organic acids -- C25D 11/10 designates electrolytic coating processes that create conversion layers on metal surfaces by surface-reaction mechanisms using electrolytes that contain organic acids. The classification covers any method where the organic-acid component influences film formation, composition or properties during the electrolytic or electrophoretic deposition.
[C25D 11/12] Anodising more than once, e.g. in different baths -- This subgroup covers methods where a metal surface is anodised in multiple successive steps, often using different electrolytic baths to achieve layered or graded oxide films. It includes processes that repeat the anodising operation to modify thickness, composition, or properties of the conversion coating.
[C25D 11/14] Producing integrally coloured layers -- C25D 11/14 covers electrolytic processes that create conversion-type coatings through surface reactions, where the coating itself is intrinsically coloured rather than being tinted after application. The method integrates colour formation into the metal-oxide layer during electrolysis, producing a uniform, durable finish. It is used for decorative and protective treatments of metal parts.
[C25D 11/16] Pretreatment -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Pretreatment of the substrate surface, e.g. by desmutting.  **Glossary:** - Desmutting: Removal of smut layer formed after etching a metal or an alloy
[C25D 11/18] After-treatment, e.g. pore-sealing -- **Definition:** This place covers:  After-treatment of electrolytic coated surface, e.g. physical or mechanical after-treatments.
[C25D 1/12] by electrophoresis -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrophoretic forming processes, i.e. processes involving the reproduction or formation of objects by electrophoretic deposition in which, typically, the deposit does not permanently remain with the base upon which deposition is made.  Apparatus for performing an electrophoretic forming process.  Products obtained by such processes.  Baths for electroforming by electrophoresis.
[C25D 11/20] Electrolytic after-treatment -- Electrolytic after-treatment refers to post-coating processes that use an electric current to modify an existing coating through surface-reaction conversion layers, such as anodizing or chromate passivation. The technique improves properties like corrosion resistance, adhesion or wear performance by forming a thin, chemically altered film on the coated substrate. It is classified under CPC C25D 11/20.
[C25D 11/22] for colouring layers -- C25D 11/22 covers electrolytic coating processes that create conversion layers on a substrate through surface-reaction mechanisms, specifically when the resulting layer is intended to provide colour. It falls under chemistry, electrolytic or electrophoretic processes, and the production of coatings by electrolysis, focusing on coloured conversion films applied to metals or other materials.
[C25D 11/24] Chemical after-treatment -- C25D 11/24 covers chemical after-treatments applied to conversion layers formed by electrolytic surface reactions, such as rinsing, sealing, chromating or other chemical modifications that improve corrosion resistance, adhesion or other properties of the coating. It pertains to the post-electrolysis step that enhances or stabilises the electrolytically produced conversion film.
[C25D 11/243] using organic dyestuffs -- C25D 11/243 covers electrolytic conversion-coating processes in which organic dyestuffs are used to form the coating layer on a metal surface. During the anodic reaction the dye molecules become incorporated into the conversion film, providing coloration, corrosion resistance or other functional properties. The class is applied to decorative or protective finishes produced by such dye-based electrolytic treatments.
[C25D 11/246] for sealing layers -- Code C25D 11/246 designates processes that apply sealing layers as part of electrolytic conversion coatings. It covers methods where a surface reaction forms a thin protective film to close pores or improve corrosion resistance after the primary conversion layer is generated.
[C25D 11/26] of refractory metals or alloys based thereon
[C25D 11/28] of actinides or alloys based thereon -- C25D 11/28 covers electrolytic coating processes in which the metal being deposited or the substrate contains actinide elements or alloys derived from them. The classification applies to conversion-layer formation by surface reaction on such actinide-based materials.
[C25D 11/30] of magnesium or alloys based thereon
[C25D 11/32] of semiconducting materials -- C25D 11/32 covers electrolytic coating processes that create conversion layers on semiconducting materials through surface reactions, such as anodic oxidation that forms protective or functional oxide, nitride or similar films on semiconductor substrates.
[C25D 11/34] of metals or alloys not provided for in groups -- C25D 11/34 covers electrochemical coating processes in which a surface-reaction conversion layer is formed on metals or alloys that are not specifically listed in other groups, such as uncommon or newly developed alloys, using electrolytic or electrophoretic methods to produce protective or functional films.
[C25D 11/36] Phosphatising -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic conversion processes comprising the formation of an adherent phosphate coating on a metal substrate by immersion thereof in a suitable aqueous phosphate solution and precipitation of insoluble metal phosphate compounds upon variation of the pH in the vicinity of the substrate, wherein part of the metal substrate reacts with the solution to form the coating. A metal source other than the substrate may be added to the solution (e.g. precipitation of zinc phosphate on steel substrate), thereby limiting the actual contribution of the metal of the substrate to the formation of the coating.  Articles obtained by such processes.
[C25D 11/38] Chromatising -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes of coating by electrochemical reaction of hexavalent chromium with a metal surface in the presence of other components, or "activators," in an acid solution. The hexavalent chromium is partially reduced to trivalent chromium during the reaction, with a concurrent rise in pH, forming a complex mixture consisting largely of hydrated basic chromium chromate and hydrous oxides of both chromium and the basis metal. The typical substrate metals to which a chromate conversion coating is applicable are Al, Cd, Cu, Mg, Ag and Zn. Processes are known for Sn as well.  Processes of anodic chromating wherein the coating formed is a mixture of a chromate and an oxide of the coated metal.  Articles obtained by such processes.
[C25D 1/14] of inorganic material -- The C25D 1/14 subclass covers electroforming processes in which the deposited coating is an inorganic material, such as metals, alloys or inorganic compounds, rather than an organic polymer. It includes methods for producing solid metal parts or layers by electrodeposition from aqueous or non-aqueous electrolytes.
[C25D 1/16] Metals -- This subclass covers electroforming operations in which a metal is deposited from an electrolytic bath to form a coating or freestanding part. It includes the preparation of metal-containing solutions, control of current density, temperature and additives, and the techniques used to achieve desired thickness, shape and properties of the metallic deposit.
[C25D 1/18] of organic material
[C25D 1/20] Separation of the formed objects from the electrodes -- C25D 1/20 covers techniques for detaching objects produced by electroforming from the electrodes that served as their substrates. It includes mechanical, chemical, thermal or other methods used to separate the formed parts without damaging their shape or surface coating.
[C25D 1/22] Separating compounds -- C25D 1/22 relates to electroforming processes in which the deposited metal or alloy is subsequently separated from the electrolyte or other compounds present. It covers methods such as mechanical, chemical or electro-chemical removal of residual ligands, binders, solvents or mixed-metal phases to obtain a pure coating. The classification is used for patents describing post-deposition purification steps in the production of metal parts by electrolytic or electrophoretic techniques.
[C25D 13/00] Electrophoretic coating characterised by the process -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes wherein charged particles or molecules suspended or dissolved in a liquid medium, possibly forming a colloid, migrate under the influence of an electric field and are deposited onto an electrode by coagulation.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Electrolytic or electrophoretic production of coating containing embedded materials -> C25D15/00 - Compositions for electrophoretic coating of polymers -> C09D5/44  **Glossary:** - Electrocoating, electropainting, e-coat: Processes called "electrocoating", "electropainting", "e-coat", etc., wherein the first step is the protonation/deprotonation of the low molecular weight organic compound in the bath, followed by the deprotonation and deposition at the cathode (i.e. cataphoretic process with concomitant reduction of H+ at the cathode according to 2H+ + 2e- --> H2) or protonation and deposition at the anode (i.e. anaphoretic process with concomitant oxidation of water at the anode according to H2O --> ½ O2 + 2e-). Strictly speaking, such processes should be called "electrolytic" instead of "electrophoretic" because the films are not formed by coagulation, but by reaction at the working electrode. However, C25D13/00 and C09D5/44 use the expression "electrophoretic coating with polymers" for historical reasons, as generally does the patent and non-patent literature.
[C25D 13/02] with inorganic material -- C25D 13/02 relates to electrophoretic coating processes in which the deposited layer contains inorganic material. It is situated within the class of electrolytic-or-electrophoretic processes for producing coatings, a sub-category of chemistry.
[C25D 13/04] with organic material -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The electrophoretic deposition of low molecular weight organic compounds, i.e. non polymeric and non polymerizable compounds.
[C25D 13/06] with polymers -- C25D 13/06 pertains to electrophoretic coating processes in which the coating material includes polymers, either as the electrophoretically suspended particles or as binders within the coating bath. The subclass addresses the formulation and application of polymer-based electrophoretic films.
[C25D 13/08] by polymerisation -- C25D 13/08 covers electrophoretic coating processes in which the coating material is formed by polymerisation during deposition. It includes methods where monomers, oligomers or pre-polymers in the electrophoretic bath polymerise in situ, producing a cured polymeric film on the substrate as a result of the electric field-driven migration. This subclass is used for patents describing polymerisation-based electrophoretic deposition of protective or functional coatings.
[C25D 13/10] characterised by the additives used -- This CPC subclass deals with electrophoretic coating processes that are defined by the particular additives incorporated into the coating bath or formulation, such as surfactants, binders, pigments or other functional agents that influence conductivity, stability, film formation or performance. It covers inventions where the choice, amount or combination of these additives is the distinguishing technical feature of the coating method.
[C25D 13/12] characterised by the article coated -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Articles coated by electrophoretic deposition.
[C25D 13/14] Tubes -- C25D 13/14 covers electrophoretic coating processes where the coating is applied to tubular substrates. It includes methods for forming uniform pigment or polymer films on the interior or exterior of tubes by moving charged particles in a suspension under an electric field.
[C25D 13/16] Wires
[C25D 13/18] using modulated, pulsed, or reversing current -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrophoretic processes using a modulated, pulsed or reversing current, including dielelectrophoretic processes.  **Glossary:** - Dielectrophoresis: Motion of matter as induced by its polarization in an inhomogeneous electric field, usually into regions of highest field strength, and most evident with neutral matter. The direction of the motion is independent of the sign of the field. - Electrophoresis: Motion of charged matter induced by an electric field. The direction of the motion here is dependent on the sign of the field.
[C25D 13/20] Pretreatment -- C25D 13/20 covers the preparatory steps applied to a substrate before it receives an electrophoretic coating, such as cleaning, surface activation, or the application of a conductive or adhesion-promoting layer. These pretreatment actions are performed to ensure uniform deposition and strong bonding of the electrically-driven paint during the coating process.
[C25D 13/22] Servicing or operating -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Equipment and processes for servicing and operating; covering aspects such as heating, cooling, filtering, agitating and process control.  Apparatus specially adapted for the electrophoretic coating process.  Multistep processes.  Details of processes of electrophoretic coating with polymers not classified elsewhere.
[C25D 13/24] Regeneration of process liquids -- This subclass covers methods for restoring the composition of the electrolytic or electrophoretic bath used in coating production, including removal of degradation products, replenishment of depleted components, and filtration or chemical treatment that enable the process liquid to be reused.
[C25D 15/00] Electrolytic or electrophoretic production of coatings containing embedded materials, e.g. particles, whiskers, wires -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The coated products obtained by such processes.
[C25D 15/02] Combined electrolytic and electrophoretic processes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes involving the formation of a matrix containing supplemental embedded substances (see the definition of C25D15/00 ) wherein said supplemental substances are not only passively entrapped in the matrix but are actively involved in an electrophoretic or electrolytic deposition process, e.g. processes wherein the formation of the matrix by electroplating and the migration of the supplemental substances to the cathode by electrophoresis take place concomitantly.  The coated articles obtained by such processes.
[C25D 17/00] Constructional parts, or assemblies thereof, of cells for electrolytic coating -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Constructional parts, or assemblies thereof, of cells for electrolytic coating.  Electrolytic coating plants.
[C25D 17/001] Apparatus specially adapted for electrolytic coating of wafers, e.g. semiconductors or solar cells -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Apparatus specially adapted for electrolytically coating wafers, such as fountain platers, plating jigs for wafers, etc.  **Glossary:** - Wafer: A thin slice of conductor or semiconductor material
[C25D 17/002] Cell separation, e.g. membranes, diaphragms -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Means such as membranes or diaphrams for dividing the plating cell into a plurality of regions having different bath compositions, e.g. anolyte chamber and catholyte chamber.
[C25D 17/004] Sealing devices -- C25D 17/004 covers sealing devices employed in the constructional parts or assemblies of electrolytic-coating cells. It pertains to components that prevent fluid or gas leakage between cell sections during electrolytic or electrophoretic coating processes, ensuring the integrity of the coating environment.
[C25D 17/005] Contacting devices -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Means for electrically contacting the substrate, e.g. electrodes, pins, brushes, etc., e.g. ensuring a uniform current supply to the substrate.
[C25D 17/007] Current directing devices -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Means made of a conductive material in contact with the plating bath, showing an electric potential, thereby modifying the electric field and the current density field in the plating bath.  Those means are often electrically connected to a power supply, as in the case of thief electrodes, auxiliary electrodes, etc., but not necessarily, as in the case of bipolar electrodes.  The current directing device conducts current density lines, contrary to the current shielding device in the sense of C25D17/008 , which acts as an obstacle.
[C25D 17/008] Current shielding devices -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Shielding means, not connected to an electric circuit, for modifying the current density field in the electroplating cell and the current density distribution over the substrate surface, e.g. "diaphragms", "screens", "shields", virtual anodes, for example, to avoid edge effects, etc.  Insulating spacers for avoiding short-circuits and arcing between the substrate and the counter-electrode.  The current shielding device influences the current density field in the plating bath by constituting an obstacle to the current lines in a first region, which normally implies concentrating the current lines in a second region.  The current shielding device is not necessarily made of a dielectric material, but should it be made of a conductive material, it should not act as a current conducting device in the sense of C25D17/007 .  An electrolyte flow directing device (e.g. baffle, damping device, hydrodynamic diffuser, etc.) placed between anode and cathode and aiming at modifying the hydrodynamics of the cell, will normally influence the electric current density distribution as well as the hydrodynamics and is as such also considered as a current insulating device.
[C25D 17/02] Tanks -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Tanks characterized by their construction material, their shape or by integrated equipment, e.g. sealing devices, windows, integrated cooling or heating devices, etc.
[C25D 17/04] External supporting frames or structures -- This subclass covers external frames or structural elements that support or hold the cell components in electrolytic coating processes, including supports for electrodes, cathodes, anodes, and bath containers. It includes assemblies that provide rigidity, alignment, or mounting for the coating cell but not the internal cell parts themselves.
[C25D 17/06] Suspending or supporting devices for articles to be coated -- A suspending or supporting device for articles to be coated is any rack, hook, fixture or similar component that holds parts in place while they undergo electrolytic or electrophoretic coating, ensuring proper positioning and separation in the coating bath. It includes designs for supporting structures used in plating, anodizing or electrophoretic deposition cells.
[C25D 17/08] racks -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Racks, for supporting, not suspending.
[C25D 17/10] Electrodes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Counter-electrodes, auxiliary electrodes, thief electrodes, including aspects relating to their composition.
[C25D 17/12] Shape or form -- C25D 17/12 covers the shape or form of constructional parts and assemblies that make up electrolytic coating cells. It pertains to the geometric design of electrodes, anodes, cathodes or other cell components used in electrolytic or electrophoretic deposition processes.
[C25D 17/14] for pad-plating -- This subclass covers pad-plating, an electrolytic coating technique where a conductive pad contacts the workpiece to transfer metal from the plating bath. It falls under processes for the electrolytic production of coatings and specifically relates to constructional parts or assemblies of cells used for electrolytic coating.
[C25D 17/16] Apparatus for electrolytic coating of small objects in bulk -- C25D 17/16 covers apparatus designed to electrolytically coat many small items simultaneously, concentrating on the structural components or assembled units of the coating cells. It includes the design of cell parts such as electrodes, holders, and fluid distribution systems that enable bulk processing of miniature workpieces. This subclass falls under processes for electrolytic or electrophoretic production of coatings within the chemistry section.
[C25D 17/18] having closed containers -- C25D 17/18 refers to the constructional parts or assemblies of electrolytic-coating cells that include closed containers, i.e., sealed chambers used to hold the electrolyte, workpiece, or both during the electrolytic or electrophoretic deposition of a coating. This subclass falls under processes for the electrolytic or electrophoretic production of coatings within the broader chemistry section.
[C25D 17/20] Horizontal barrels -- Horizontal barrels are constructional parts of electrolytic-coating cells, designed as cylindrical containers oriented horizontally to hold workpieces and electrolyte during coating. Their shape promotes uniform fluid flow and consistent deposition of metal layers across the coated surfaces.
[C25D 17/22] having open containers -- C25D 17/22 covers constructional parts or assemblies of electrolytic-coating cells that incorporate open containers, such as tanks or baths without sealed lids. These open-container designs facilitate the introduction and removal of coating suspensions and are used in processes that apply metallic or polymeric films by electrolysis or electrophoresis.
[C25D 17/24] Oblique barrels -- C25D 17/24 covers oblique barrels, which are specially shaped cylindrical components used in electrolytic or electrophoretic coating cells. These barrels are mounted at an angle to guide electrolyte flow or particle deposition, forming part of the cell's construction or assembly.
[C25D 17/26] Oscillating baskets -- C25D 17/26 refers to oscillating baskets that form part of the cell structure or assemblies used in electrolytic or electrophoretic coating processes. These baskets are designed to move back-and-forth during deposition, ensuring uniform film formation on workpieces immersed in the coating bath. The class falls under chemistry, specifically electrocoating technologies.
[C25D 17/28] with means for moving the objects individually through the apparatus during treatment -- The C25D 17/28 subgroup pertains to components or assemblies of electrolytic-coating cells that include mechanisms for transporting workpieces individually through the treatment zone, such as conveyors, belts, rollers or robotic carriers, enabling separate control of each object during coating.
[C25D 21/00] Processes for servicing or operating cells for electrolytic coating -- C25D 21/00 covers methods used to maintain, service, and operate the electrolytic cells employed in electrocoating processes. It includes procedures for cleaning, repairing, adjusting parameters, and managing the cell during production to ensure consistent coating quality. The classification falls under chemistry, specifically electrolytic or electrophoretic processes for producing coatings.
[C25D 21/02] Heating or cooling -- C25D 21/02 relates to methods of heating or cooling the electrolytic cell, its bath or surrounding equipment while the cell is in operation. The entry covers temperature-control techniques used to maintain optimal conditions, improve coating quality and efficiency, or manage energy consumption during electro-coating processes.
[C25D 21/04] Removal of gases or vapours -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes and equipment for the removal of gases or vapours emanating from the electrolytic coating bath, e.g. using a suction hood.
[C25D 21/06] Filtering -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes and equipment for filtering particles, not ions.
[C25D 21/08] Rinsing -- C25D 21/08 pertains to rinsing steps used in the servicing or operation of electrochemical cells that apply electrolytic or electrophoretic coatings. It covers methods of removing residual electrolyte, debris or contaminants from the workpiece or cell components between coating cycles. The aim is to improve coating quality and cell performance.
[C25D 21/10] Agitating of electrolytes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes and equipment for moving vigorously the aqueous solution for electrolytic coating or for displacing the supports of the article to be treated.
[C25D 21/11] Use of protective surface layers on electrolytic baths -- C25D 21/11 covers the application of protective coatings or surface layers to the interior walls or components of electrolytic baths used in electrodeposition. Such layers guard the bath against degradation, contamination and wear, thereby extending service life and improving coating quality.
[C25D 21/12] Process control or regulation -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes and equipment (architectures, mechanisms and algorithms) for maintaining the output of the electrolytic coating process within a desired range, using open-loop or feedback control. Control and regulation implies that an action is taken during the electrolytic coating process, which results in the modification of a process variable.
[C25D 21/14] Controlled addition of electrolyte components -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes and equipment (architectures, mechanisms and algorithms) for maintaining the composition of the electrolyte within a desired range during the electrolytic coating process.
[C25D 21/16] Regeneration of process solutions -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes and equipment for replenishing and/or purifying spent solutions.  The regeneration can be carried out continuously (using e.g. circulation loops) or in the batch mode.
[C25D 21/18] of electrolytes -- C25D 21/18 covers the selection, composition and use of electrolytes in processes that service or operate electrolytic cells for applying coatings. It includes the chemical formulation of the bath, additives that modify conductivity or deposition quality, and methods for maintaining electrolyte conditions during coating operations.
[C25D 21/20] of rinse-solutions -- C25D 21/20 covers the formulation and use of rinse-solutions employed during the maintenance, cleaning or operation of electrolytic or electrophoretic coating cells. It includes liquids that remove residual particles, acids, bases or other contaminants from cell surfaces or workpieces between coating cycles, ensuring uniform deposition and preventing defects.
[C25D 21/22] by ion-exchange -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Regenerations of process solutions by ion exchange, filtering ions, not particles
[C25D 3/00] Electroplating: Baths therefor -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Baths for electroplating, e.g. solutions, melts.  **Glossary:** - Electroplating: Electrodeposition on a substrate of a firmly adhering metal or metal alloy
[C25D 3/02] from solutions -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic solutions for electroplating, aqueous as well as nonaqueous.  **Glossary:** - Solution: A homogeneous mixture comprising metal cations dissolved in a molecular solvent, e.g. water or an organic solvent.
[C25D 3/04] of chromium
[C25D 3/06] from solutions of trivalent chromium -- A subclass of electroplating baths that employ solutions containing trivalent chromium as the source of chromium for coating deposition. It covers the composition, preparation and use of these baths for producing chromium-based layers by electrolytic or electrophoretic methods.
[C25D 3/08] Deposition of black chromium -- The CPC subclass C25D 3/08 covers the electrolytic deposition of black chromium coatings. It specifies bath compositions, operating conditions and post-treatment steps used to produce a dark-metallic, corrosion-resistant layer on metal parts, typically for decorative or wear-resistant applications. This falls under the broader group of electroplating baths within electro-phoretic coating processes.
[C25D 3/10] characterised by the organic bath constituents used -- C25D 3/10 covers electroplating baths that are defined primarily by the organic compounds present in the solution, such as organic solvents, complexing agents or additives that influence plating characteristics. This subgroup distinguishes these baths from those based on inorganic constituents.
[C25D 3/12] of nickel or cobalt -- This subclass covers electroplating baths that use nickel or cobalt as the metal source to deposit these metals onto a workpiece. It includes bath compositions containing inorganic nickel or cobalt salts, complexing agents and other additives, as well as the operating conditions and formulations specific to such nickel or cobalt plating processes.
[C25D 3/14] from baths containing acetylenic or heterocyclic compounds -- This subclass refers to electroplating baths that contain acetylenic or heterocyclic compounds, which are used as additives or components to influence the composition, structure or properties of the deposited coating. It falls under processes for the electrolytic production of coatings within the broader chemistry classification.
[C25D 3/16] Acetylenic compounds -- C25D 3/16 covers the use of acetylenic compounds as components of electrolytic baths for electroplating. It includes any organic additives containing carbon-carbon triple bonds that are incorporated to modify deposit properties, improve brightness, or control grain structure during the plating process. This subclass is part of the broader category of electroplating baths within the CPC hierarchy.
[C25D 3/18] Heterocyclic compounds -- C25D 3/18 covers heterocyclic compounds that are incorporated into electroplating baths for the electrolytic or electrophoretic deposition of coating layers. The entry pertains to chemicals containing ring structures with at least one non-carbon atom, used as complexing agents, brighteners or additives to control deposit properties in coating processes.
[C25D 3/20] of iron -- C25D 3/20 concerns electrolytic baths formulated specifically for depositing iron as a metallic coating. It covers the composition, preparation and use of iron plating solutions, including additives that control deposit properties such as brightness, hardness or corrosion resistance. The classification is applied to processes that produce iron coatings by electroplating in industrial or laboratory settings.
[C25D 3/22] of zinc
[C25D 3/24] from cyanide baths -- C25D 3/24 covers electrolytic coating processes that employ cyanide-based plating baths, wherein metal ions are complexed with cyanide to form stable solutions for electrodeposition. It includes the preparation, composition, and use of such baths for depositing metals such as copper, nickel, or alloy layers onto workpieces.
[C25D 3/26] of cadmium
[C25D 3/28] from cyanide baths -- C25D 3/28 covers electroplating processes that use cyanide-based plating baths, detailing the composition, preparation and operation of these baths for depositing metal coatings. The classification includes variants of cyanide solutions, additives, and parameters specific to cyanide chemistry in electrolytic coating production.
[C25D 3/30] of tin -- C25D 3/30 covers electrolytic baths formulated for the deposition of tin onto a workpiece, including the composition of the solution, additives, and operating parameters used in tin-plating processes. The classification is applied to methods that produce tin coatings for purposes such as corrosion protection, solderability or decorative finishes.
[C25D 3/32] characterised by the organic bath constituents used -- C25D 3/32 covers electroplating processes where the bath composition is defined by the organic constituents employed. It includes baths that use organic solvents, complexing agents, surfactants or other organic additives to control plating conditions, metal-ion solubility, deposit properties or bath stability.
[C25D 3/34] of lead
[C25D 3/36] characterised by the organic bath constituents used -- The C25D 3/36 subclass pertains to electroplating baths whose defining characteristic is the type of organic constituents present, such as solvents, complexing agents or additives that affect the deposition process. It classifies electrolytic coating processes where the organic bath composition is the primary distinguishing feature.
[C25D 3/38] of copper
[C25D 3/40] from cyanide baths -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Copper electroplating baths containing cyanide ions, e.g. baths containing Cu+ ions as copper source.
[C25D 3/42] of light metals -- C25D 3/42 relates to electroplating baths that contain light metals such as aluminum, magnesium or lithium. It covers the preparation, composition and additives of electrolytic solutions used to deposit these metals as coatings on various substrates.
[C25D 3/44] Aluminium -- C25D 3/44 covers electroplating baths that contain aluminium as the plating metal. It relates to processes for the electrolytic or electrophoretic production of aluminium coatings, specifying the composition, preparation and use of such baths in depositing aluminium onto workpieces.
[C25D 3/46] of silver -- C25D 3/46 is a subgroup of the CPC class for electroplating baths that specifies baths where silver is the metal to be deposited. It covers compositions, additives and operating conditions used in electrolytic or electrophoretic processes for applying silver coatings onto substrates.
[C25D 3/48] of gold -- The subclass C25D 3/48 concerns electrolytic baths formulated for depositing gold onto a workpiece, covering the composition of the gold-containing solution, any additives or modifiers, and the operating parameters used in the gold-plating process. It is situated within the broader category of electroplating processes for producing metallic coatings.
[C25D 3/50] of platinum group metals -- C25D 3/50 covers electroplating baths that use platinum-group metals as the plating material. The subclass details the composition, preparation and use of solutions containing platinum, palladium, rhodium, iridium or ruthenium for depositing metallic coatings by electrolytic or electrophoretic methods. It is part of the broader hierarchy of chemical processes for producing coated surfaces.
[C25D 3/52] characterised by the organic bath constituents used -- C25D 3/52 covers electroplating processes whose baths are defined by the organic constituents present, such as solvents, complexing agents, brighteners or other organic additives that control metal deposition, bath stability and coating properties. The classification applies to any plating operation where the organic composition of the bath is a distinguishing feature.
[C25D 3/54] of metals not provided for in groups -- C25D 3/54 covers electroplating baths and related solutions used for depositing metals that are not specifically listed in the other groups of this subclass, including their electrolyte compositions, additives and operating conditions. It addresses the formulation and use of such baths for unusual or less-common plating metals.
[C25D 3/56] of alloys -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic baths for plating alloys.
[C25D 3/562] containing more than 50% by weight of iron or nickel or cobalt -- C25D 3/562 classifies electrolytic or electrophoretic plating baths that contain more than 50 percent by weight of iron, nickel or cobalt. These high-metal-content solutions are used to deposit metallic coatings in processes covered by the broader chemistry and electrolytic-coating hierarchy.
[C25D 3/565] containing more than 50% by weight of zinc -- C25D 3/565 is a CPC subclass for electroplating baths used in electrolytic or electrophoretic coating processes, in which the bath formulation contains more than 50 % by weight of zinc. It falls under the hierarchy CHEMISTRY → ELECTROLYTIC OR ELECTROPHORETIC PROCESSES → PROCESSES FOR THE ELECTROLYTIC OR ELECTROPHORETIC PRODUCTION OF COATINGS → Electroplating: Baths therefor.
[C25D 3/567] containing more than 50% by weight of platinum group metals -- C25D 3/567 designates electrolytic or electrophoretic plating baths in which more than 50 % of the total weight consists of platinum-group metals such as platinum, palladium or rhodium. These baths are used to deposit high-performance, corrosion-resistant or catalytic layers on substrates.
[C25D 3/58] containing more than 50% by weight of copper -- This subclass refers to electroplating baths in which copper makes up more than 50 % of the bath's weight. It is part of the electro-electrophoretic coating production hierarchy, specifically covering electrolytic processes for coating deposition.
[C25D 3/60] containing more than 50% by weight of tin -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic baths for plating tin alloys, including tin-phosphorous (Sn-P) alloys.
[C25D 3/62] containing more than 50% by weight of gold -- The subclass C25D 3/62 relates to electrolytic plating baths in which gold makes up more than 50 % of the metal content by weight. These baths are formulated for the electroplating of gold-rich metallic layers onto workpieces, falling under the broader category of processes for the electrolytic production of coatings.
[C25D 3/64] containing more than 50% by weight of silver -- C25D 3/64 designates electroplating baths whose composition includes silver as the predominant metal, with the silver content exceeding fifty percent by weight of the total metal portion. Such baths are used for depositing silver-rich layers on substrates via electrolytic or electrophoretic methods.
[C25D 3/66] from melts -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic baths based on melts, fused baths or ionic liquids.  **Glossary:** - Melt: molten salt or ionic liquid or fused bath
[C25D 3/665] from ionic liquids -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic baths based on ionic liquids or deep eutectic solvents, which are liquid at a temperature typically, lower than 100°C, in particular Room Temperature Ionic Liquids (RTILs).  **Glossary:** - Ionic liquid: System composed primarily of one type of discrete anion or cation - Deep eutectic solvent: Eutectic mixture containing a variety of anionic and/or cationic species
[C25D 5/00] Electroplating characterised by the process -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electroplating processes, i.e. processes of electrolytic coating the substrate with a firmly adhering metallic layer, including the preparation of the workpieces for subsequent electroplating.  **Glossary:** - Electroplating: Electrodeposition on a substrate of a firmly adhering metal or metal alloy
[C25D 5/003] Electroplating using gases, e.g. pressure influence -- **Definition:** This place covers:
[C25D 5/007] Electroplating using magnetic fields, e.g. magnets -- C25D 5/007 covers electroplating processes in which magnetic fields-generated by permanent magnets or electromagnets-are applied to the plating bath to influence metal ion transport, deposition rate, or coating morphology. The magnetic field may be used to improve uniformity, refine grain structure, or reduce defects in the resulting coating.
[C25D 5/009] Deposition of ferromagnetic material -- C25D 5/009 covers electroplating processes in which ferromagnetic metals such as iron, nickel or cobalt are deposited as a coating. The subclass is part of the broader class for electrolytic or electrophoretic production of coatings, focusing on magnetic material deposition for functional or protective purposes.
[C25D 5/011] Electroplating using electromagnetic wave irradiation  using locally applied electromagnetic radiation  C25D5/024
[C25D 5/013] Wavelengths other than ultraviolet [UV], visible or infrared [IR], e.g. X-rays or microwaves
[C25D 5/02] Electroplating of selected surface areas -- C25D 5/02 covers methods for electroplating that target specific regions of a workpiece rather than the whole surface. It includes techniques such as masking, selective activation or localized current control to deposit metal only on designated areas. The classification falls under electroplating processes within electrolytic or electrophoretic production of coatings.
[C25D 5/022] using masking means -- The subclass C25D 5/022 covers electroplating processes in which masking means are employed to selectively protect portions of a workpiece from metal deposition. By applying removable or permanent masks, only the intended areas receive the coating, allowing precise patterning, edge definition and prevention of unwanted plating.
[C25D 5/024] using locally applied electromagnetic radiation, e.g. lasers -- C25D 5/024 covers electroplating processes in which locally applied electromagnetic radiation, such as laser beams, is used to initiate, control or limit metal deposition on a workpiece. The radiation provides selective energy to a specific area, enabling patterned or targeted coating without affecting surrounding surfaces.
[C25D 5/026] using locally applied jets of electrolyte -- This subclass covers electroplating processes where the electrolyte is delivered to the workpiece via jets applied locally, such as localized flow or spray techniques that confine the plating bath to a small area. It is used to deposit metal selectively or to improve mass transport in restricted zones.
[C25D 5/028] one side electroplating, e.g. substrate conveyed in a bath with inhibited background plating -- This CPC subclass C25D 5/028 is nested under chemistry → electrolytic or electrophoretic processes → processes for the electrolytic or electrophoretic production of coatings. It pertains to electroplating in which only one side of a workpiece is plated, such as when a substrate is conveyed through a plating bath while background plating is inhibited.
[C25D 5/04] Electroplating with moving electrodes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes of electroplating with moving electrodes, e.g. moving counter-electrodes.
[C25D 5/06] Brush or pad plating -- C25D 5/06 relates to brush or pad plating, an electrolytic coating method where a rotating or moving brush or felt pad serves as the anode and contacts the workpiece to deposit metal. This technique is used for localized or selective plating and falls under processes for the electrolytic production of coatings within the chemistry section.
[C25D 5/08] Electroplating with moving electrolyte e.g. jet electroplating -- **Definition:** This place covers:  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Using locally applied jets of electrolyte -> C25D5/026
[C25D 5/10] Electroplating with more than one layer of the same or of different metals -- C25D 5/10 pertains to electroplating processes that produce a coating consisting of two or more successive layers, which may be of the same metal or of different metals. The classification covers methods in which the multilayer structure is built during the electrolytic deposition, including variations in bath composition, current regime, and layer thickness to achieve desired functional or protective properties.
[C25D 5/12] at least one layer being of nickel or chromium -- C25D 5/12 covers electroplating processes in which the deposited coating includes at least one layer of nickel or chromium, often as part of a multi-layer stack. The classification falls under chemical methods for electrolytic or electrophoretic production of coatings, specifically those characterized by the plating process itself.
[C25D 5/14] two or more layers being of nickel or chromium, e.g. duplex or triplex layers -- This subclass covers electroplating processes where two or more coating layers are made of nickel, chromium, or combinations of the two, such as duplex or triplex structures. It focuses on producing multilayer metal films of nickel and/or chromium to achieve enhanced corrosion resistance, hardness, or other functional properties.
[C25D 5/16] Electroplating with layers of varying thickness -- **Definition:** This place covers:
[C25D 5/18] Electroplating using modulated, pulsed or reversing current -- This subclass covers electroplating methods in which the electric current applied to the bath is varied in a controlled manner, such as by using pulses, modulation, or periodic reversal. Such techniques are employed to improve coating uniformity, reduce stress, refine grain structure, or enhance other material properties compared with constant-current plating.
[C25D 5/20] Electroplating using ultrasonic waves -- C25D 5/20 covers electroplating processes in which ultrasonic energy is applied to the plating bath, using high-frequency sound waves to agitate the solution, improve metal ion transport, and enhance coating uniformity. The ultrasonic action can reduce surface defects, accelerate deposition rates, and enable plating of intricate geometries. This subclass falls under electrolytic processes for producing metal coatings.
[C25D 5/22] Electroplating combined with mechanical treatment during the deposition -- The subclass covers electroplating operations in which a mechanical treatment-such as brushing, rolling, vibrating, or impact- is applied to the workpiece while the metal coating is being deposited, influencing the deposit's structure, adhesion or properties. It lies within the broader category of electrolytic or electrophoretic processes for producing coatings.
[C25D 5/34] Pretreatment of metallic surfaces to be electroplated -- The subclass C25D 5/34 deals with processes that prepare metal parts for electroplating by removing impurities, oxides, and surface films. It includes cleaning, degreasing, acid or alkaline pickling, mechanical abrasion, and electrolytic or chemical pretreatments that enhance adhesion of the subsequent coating.
