[C25D 5/36] of iron or steel -- This CPC subclass covers electrolytic or electrophoretic processes that deposit a coating on iron or steel substrates, specifying the bath composition, operating conditions and plating parameters used to plate these ferrous materials. It includes methods for preparing, treating and coating iron or steel surfaces by electroplating.
[C25D 5/38] of refractory metals or nickel -- C25D 5/38 relates to electroplating processes in which the deposited coating consists of a refractory metal such as tungsten, molybdenum, tantalum, or nickel. It includes the specific electrolytic baths, current densities and operating conditions required to achieve uniform, adherent layers of these metals on a workpiece.
[C25D 5/40] Nickel -- C25D 5/40 covers electroplating processes in which nickel is deposited as a coating. It includes the preparation of nickel plating baths, the conditions for electrodeposition, and any additives or steps specific to achieving nickel layers. The subclass is used for inventions that focus on the method, apparatus, or composition of nickel electroplating.
[C25D 5/42] of light metals -- This subclass covers electroplating methods where the metal deposited is a light metal such as aluminum, magnesium, calcium, or titanium, including the preparation of baths, control of parameters, and achieving coating adhesion. It falls under processes for the electrolytic or electrophoretic production of coatings.
[C25D 5/44] Aluminium -- C25D 5/44 covers electroplating processes in which aluminium is deposited as a coating, detailing the electrolytic or electrophoretic methods, bath compositions, operating conditions and auxiliary steps used to achieve a metallic aluminium layer on a substrate. It pertains to the specific chemistry and technique of aluminium plating within the broader electroplating field.
[C25D 5/46] of actinides -- C25D 5/46 covers electroplating processes in which actinide elements are used as the metal source or coating material. It relates to the electrolytic or electrophoretic deposition of actinide layers onto a substrate, including bath composition, anodic or cathodic conditions, and other process parameters. This subclass falls under electroplating characterised by the process in the CPC hierarchy.
[C25D 5/48] After-treatment of electroplated surfaces -- C25D 5/48 covers methods applied after electroplating to modify or improve the surface, such as cleaning, polishing, passivation, heat treatment, or conversion coating to enhance corrosion resistance, adhesion, or appearance.
[C25D 5/50] by heat-treatment -- This subgroup pertains to electroplating processes in which the deposited coating is subjected to heat-treatment to alter its structure or properties, such as hardness, stress relief, grain size or metallurgical phase. It is a narrow division of processes for the electrolytic production of coatings.
[C25D 5/505] of electroplated tin coatings, e.g. by melting -- C25D 5/505 covers electrolytic methods for applying tin coatings in which the tin is introduced as a melt rather than from a solution, i.e., the coating is formed by plating from molten tin during the electroplating process. This sub-group falls under processes for electrolytic production of coatings within the broader chemistry hierarchy.
[C25D 5/52] by brightening or burnishing -- C25D 5/52 covers electroplating operations in which the deposited coating is subjected to brightening or burnishing treatments, typically to improve surface smoothness and reflectivity. It belongs to the class of electrolytic or electrophoretic processes for producing coatings, under the broader chemistry heading for electroplating methods.
[C25D 5/54] Electroplating of non-metallic surfaces -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electroplating on non-metallic surfaces, e.g. graphite, ceramics, etc.  For example:  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Semiconductors -> C25D7/12  **Glossary:** - Direct electroplating: Electroplating process comprising the deposition of catalytic cluster seeds on a non-metallic substrate prior to electroplating.
[C25D 5/56] of plastics -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electroplating of plastics and polymers, for example:  **Glossary:** - Direct electroplating: Electroplating process comprising the deposition of catalytic cluster seeds on a non-metallic substrate prior to electroplating.
[C25D 5/60] Electroplating characterised by the structure or texture of the layers -- C25D 5/60 includes electroplating processes in which the coating is defined by the structure or texture of the deposited layers, such as grain orientation, multilayer architecture, porosity or surface relief, rather than merely by its chemical composition. It covers methods for controlling crystallographic texture, layer thickness distribution and other physical characteristics of the plated film.
[C25D 5/605] Surface topography of the layers, e.g. rough, dendritic or nodular layers -- C25D 5/605 covers the surface topography of electroplated layers produced in electrolytic coating processes, specifying features such as rough, dendritic or nodular textures. It classifies patents that address how these micro-structures affect the appearance, performance or further treatment of the coating.
[C25D 5/611] Smooth layers -- C25D 5/611 pertains to electroplating processes that produce smooth coating layers, covering methods and conditions that minimize surface roughness, such as controlled current density, bath composition, temperature, agitation, and substrate preparation to achieve uniform, defect-free metallic films. It is used to classify technologies aimed at high-quality, low-texture electroplated surfaces.
[C25D 5/615] Microstructure of the layers, e.g. mixed structure -- C25D 5/615 covers the microstructural characteristics of electroplated layers, including mixed or composite structures, within the broader category of electrolytic or electrophoretic coating processes. It addresses how the internal grain size, phase distribution, or layered architecture of the deposited metal or alloy is formed and analyzed.
[C25D 5/617] Crystalline layers -- This subclass covers electroplating methods that intentionally produce a crystalline coating on the workpiece. It includes processes where deposition parameters such as temperature, current density, or electrolyte composition are controlled to obtain crystalline metal or alloy layers. The focus is on the formation of a distinct crystalline microstructure rather than amorphous or mixed phases.
[C25D 5/619] Amorphous layers -- C25D 5/619 pertains to electroplating processes that produce amorphous, non-crystalline metal or alloy layers on a substrate. The classification covers methods where the deposited coating lacks a defined crystal structure, including parameters such as bath composition, current density and temperature that favor amorphous formation. It is used for applications requiring uniform magnetic, corrosion-resistant or wear-resistant properties.
[C25D 5/623] Porosity of the layers -- C25D 5/623 covers the porosity of metallic or alloy layers produced by electrolytic or electrophoretic deposition, focusing on the presence, formation, measurement, control or reduction of pores, voids and other discontinuities within the coating. It relates to how porosity affects the coating's integrity, protective performance and mechanical properties. This subgroup falls under processes for the electrolytic production of coatings within the broader chemistry hierarchy.
[C25D 5/625] Discontinuous layers, e.g. microcracked layers -- In electroplating processes, the classification C25D 5/625 covers the formation of discontinuous coating layers, such as those intentionally or unintentionally containing micro-cracks, gaps, or isolated islands rather than a uniform film. It includes methods that produce or control these microcracked structures to achieve specific functional properties or to manage stress, adhesion, or permeability in the deposited coating.
[C25D 5/627] Electroplating characterised by the visual appearance of the layers, e.g. colour, brightness or mat appearance -- C25D 5/627 covers electroplating methods whose distinguishing feature is the visual appearance of the deposited layer, such as specific colours, brightness levels or a matte finish. It pertains to electrolytic or electrophoretic coating processes where the aesthetic quality of the coating is the primary parameter for classification. This subclass falls under the chemistry section of the CPC, within electrolytic or electrophoretic processes for producing coatings.
[C25D 5/67] Electroplating to repair workpiece -- C25D 5/67 pertains to electroplating techniques applied to restore or repair a workpiece by depositing a metal coating through an electrolytic process. It includes methods that target damaged or worn areas to improve appearance, corrosion resistance or mechanical performance.
[C25D 7/00] Electroplating characterised by the article coated -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes of electroplating to form a specific electroplated article. However, certain aspects are directly classified in the relevant subgroups C25D7/003 - C25D7/126 .
[C25D 7/001] Magnets
[C25D 7/003] Threaded pieces, e.g. bolts or nuts
[C25D 7/005] Jewels; Clockworks; Coins -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electroplated jewels, clockworks, coins.
[C25D 7/006] Nanoparticles -- C25D 7/006 covers the use of nanoparticles as the material deposited in electroplating processes where the coating is defined by the type of article being plated. It includes methods for suspending, stabilizing and delivering nanoscale particles to the substrate, and the resulting coatings that exhibit enhanced hardness, wear resistance, corrosion protection or other functional properties due to the nanoscale structure.
[C25D 7/008] Thermal barrier coatings -- C25D 7/008 covers electroplating processes in which the coating applied functions as a thermal-barrier layer, protecting the substrate from high-temperature exposure. The classification applies to methods that deposit such barrier coatings by electrolytic or electrophoretic means onto metals, alloys, ceramics or similar articles, emphasizing the nature of the coating rather than the substrate material.
[C25D 7/02] Slide fasteners -- C25D 7/02 covers electroplating processes specifically applied to slide fasteners, such as zippers, where the coating is deposited on the fastener's elements (e.g., metal teeth, polymer tapes). The class includes methods for applying metallic or alloy layers, post-treatment steps, and related surface-finishing techniques aimed at improving durability, corrosion resistance, or aesthetic appearance of the fastener.
[C25D 7/04] Tubes -- This CPC subclass C25D 7/04 covers electroplating processes applied to tubes, where conductive or protective layers are deposited on the interior, exterior, or both surfaces of tubular articles for corrosion protection, conductivity enhancement, or decorative effect.
[C25D 7/06] Wires -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electroplated wires, strips or foils, apparatuses and processes for electroplating wires, strips or foils.
[C25D 7/0607] Wires -- **Definition:** This place covers:
[C25D 7/0614] Strips or foils -- **Definition:** This place covers:
[C25D 7/0621] In horizontal cells -- The CPC subclass C25D 7/0621 covers electroplating processes in which the article being coated is a horizontal cell, such as flat plates, sheets or other horizontally oriented components. It pertains to the production of metal or alloy coatings on these surfaces by electrolytic or electrophoretic methods.
[C25D 7/0628] In vertical cells -- C25D 7/0628 covers electroplating processes performed in vertical cells, where the electrolytic bath and electrodes are arranged so that the workpiece stands upright during deposition. The vertical orientation facilitates drainage of gases and promotes a uniform coating on the article.
[C25D 7/0635] In radial cells -- C25D 7/0635 covers electroplating arrangements that employ radial cells, in which the work-pieces are positioned around a central electrode to create a radially outward flow of plating solution. This design is used when the type of article being coated dictates a geometry that promotes uniform deposition across all surfaces.
[C25D 7/0642] Anodes -- The subclass C25D 7/0642 concerns the anodes employed in electrolytic plating processes, detailing their composition, shape, surface treatment and preparation as the source of metal ions for coating a workpiece. It falls under the broader category of electroplating methods that are defined by the material being deposited onto the article.
[C25D 7/065] Diaphragms -- Diaphragms are partition elements used in electroplating cells to separate the anode and cathode compartments while permitting ionic conduction, thereby controlling solution mixing and bath composition during the coating of a workpiece. They may be porous, non-porous or semi-permeable and are positioned to support uniform current distribution and product quality.
[C25D 7/0657] Conducting rolls -- C25D 7/0657 covers conducting rolls employed as electrodes in electroplating lines, where the roll itself supplies the electric current that reduces metal ions onto a moving substrate. The rolls are typically made of conductive materials or coated with conductive layers to ensure uniform current distribution and consistent coating thickness as the material passes through the plating bath.
[C25D 7/0664] Isolating rolls -- C25D 7/0664 covers isolating rolls employed in electroplating processes in which the workpiece is separated from the plating bath by a rotating roll. These rolls support, transport or isolate the coated article and may be conductive or insulated, helping to control deposition and prevent short-circuits. The classification is used for apparatus where the roll itself defines the coated article's geometry or separation.
[C25D 7/0671] Selective plating -- C25D 7/0671 refers to electroplating processes where metal deposition is intentionally confined to specific regions of a workpiece. Techniques such as masking, localized activation, patterned electrodes or chemical inhibition are used to achieve selective coating of the article.
[C25D 7/0678] using masks -- The C25D 7/0678 entry covers electroplating operations in which a mask or resist is applied to the workpiece to define the areas that receive the metal coating. It includes methods for positioning, shaping or removing the mask during the electrolytic deposition to achieve patterned or selective plating. This classification is used for processes that rely on masking to control the coating geometry.
[C25D 7/0685] Spraying of electrolyte -- This subclass covers methods of applying electrolyte to a workpiece by spraying, used in electroplating where the coating material is delivered as a fine mist or aerosol onto the surface. It includes techniques such as pneumatic or air-assisted spraying, atomisation with high-pressure nozzles, and related equipment for uniform electrolyte distribution.
[C25D 7/0692] Regulating the thickness of the coating -- This CPC subclass covers electroplating processes in which the thickness of the deposited coating is controlled, describing methods, parameters and equipment used to regulate layer thickness during electrolytic or electrophoretic deposition.
[C25D 7/08] Mirrors -- The CPC subclass C25D 7/08 covers electroplating processes in which the article being coated is a mirror, i.e., a reflective surface produced by depositing a metallic layer onto a substrate such as glass or polymer to create a reflective coating. This falls under the broader categories of chemistry, electrolytic or electrophoretic processes, and specifically the production of coatings by electrolytic or electrophoretic methods.
[C25D 7/10] Bearings -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electroplated antifriction means as balls or rollers, designed to receive a rotating shaft, or to be used in connection with a pivoted, sliding, or rotary element.
[C25D 7/12] Semiconductors -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Details of processes of electroplating semiconductor substrates or devices, such as silicon wafers.
[C25D 7/123] Semiconductors first coated with a seed layer or a conductive layer -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Details of processes of electroplating semiconductor substrates or devices, such as silicon wafers, including a seed layer or a conductive layer deposited prior to electroplating.  **Glossary:** - Seed layer: A thin conductive film providing a low resistance conduction path for the plating current that drives the electroplating process, and functioning as a nucleation layer for metal film growth during electroplating. The seed layer acts as the plating base and an underlying adhesion or barrier layer and is typically deposited using sputtering, evaporation, chemical vapour deposition or electroless plating.
[C25D 7/126] for solar cells -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Details of processes of electroplating peculiar to the manufacture of solar cells, including a seed layer or a conductive layer deposited prior to electroplating.  **Glossary:** - Seed layer: A thin conductive film providing a low resistance conduction path for the plating current that drives the electroplating process, and functioning as a nucleation layer for metal film growth during electroplating. The seed layer acts as the plating base and an underlying adhesion or barrier layer and is typically deposited using sputtering, evaporation, chemical vapour deposition or electroless plating.
[C25D 9/00] Electrolytic coating other than with metals -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes of electrolytic coating with other materials than metals.  Apparatuses specially adapted for electrolytic coating other than with metals.  Articles electrolytically coated other than with metals.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Electrolytic coated by surface reaction, i.e. forming conversion layers -> C25D11/00 - Electrophoretic coating -> C25D13/00 - Electrolytic or electrophoretic production of coatings containing embedded materials -> C25D15/00
[C25D 9/02] with organic materials -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes of electrolytic coating with organic materials, e.g. by electrografting.  Articles obtained by such processes.  **Glossary:** - Electrografting: Electrochemical modification of conducting and semi-conducting surfaces, wherein activated moieties are formed in the vicinity of the electrode from electroactive molecules present in the electrolyte, leading to the formation of strong chemical bonds between the molecules and the electrode.
[C25D 9/04] with inorganic materials -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic coating with inorganic materials, upon partial reduction/oxidation of the source of material to a lower/higher valence state to be deposited or upon variation of the conditions, e.g. variation of the pH further to the electrolysis of water at the working electrode, thereby inducing precipitation of the material.
[C25D 9/06] by anodic processes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic coating with inorganic materials by anodic processes, e.g. an anodic coating process comprising the formation of a film comprising nickel in an average valence state between +2 and +4 from a solution containing NiSO4.
[C25D 9/08] by cathodic processes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic coating with inorganic materials by cathodic processes, e.g. a process comprising the electro-reduction of SiCl4 to silicon on a copper substrate.
[C25D 9/10] on iron or steel -- This subclass covers processes where iron or steel substrates are coated by electrolysis using non-metallic materials such as oxides, ceramics, polymers or composite films rather than metallic deposition. It includes methods like anodizing, electrophoretic painting and other electrolytic treatments that form protective or functional non-metal coatings on ferrous substrates.
[C25D 9/12] on light metals -- C25D 9/12 covers electrolytic processes for applying non-metallic coatings to light metals such as aluminium, magnesium, titanium and their alloys. It includes methods that use an electrolyte to deposit protective or functional films on these substrates, excluding metallic plating.
[C25F] PROCESSES FOR THE ELECTROLYTIC REMOVAL OF MATERIALS FROM OBJECTS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electrolytic cleaning, degreasing, pickling or descaling  Electrolytic etching or polishing  Polishing or etching using a plasma which is generated at the surface of the workpiece by a voltage applied thereto in an electrolyte  Electrolytic stripping of metallic layers or coatings  Constructional parts, or assemblies thereof, of cells for electrolytic removal of material from objects, servicing or operating  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Working of metal by the action of electric current on a workpiece, electrochemical machining, electrolytic grinding, electro-erosion -> B23H - Non-mechanical removal of metallic material from surfaces -> C23F - Inhibiting corrosion of metals by anodic or cathodic protection -> C23F13/00 - Constructional parts or assemblies thereof, of cells for both electrolytic coating and removal -> C25D17/00 - Wafer treatment -> H10P - Processes specially adapted for treatment of semi-conductors or solid state devices, e.g. electrolytic etching -> H10P50/00 , H10P50/20 , H10P52/00 , H10P95/70
[C25F 1/00] Electrolytic cleaning, degreasing, pickling or descaling -- **Glossary:** - Electrolytic cleaning: removing impurities from a surface by electrolytic action - Electrolytic degreasing: removing grease from a surface by electrolytic action - Electrolytic pickling or de-scaling: removing oxide or scale from a surface by electrolytic action - Melt: molten salt or ionic liquid or fused bath
[C25F 1/02] Pickling -- Pickling is an electrolytic surface treatment in which a workpiece is immersed in an acidic or electrolytic solution to dissolve oxides, rust, or other contaminants, thereby cleaning, degreasing, or descaling the metal. It is classified under CPC code C25F 1/02 within the hierarchy of chemistry, electrolytic or electrophoretic processes, and processes for the electrolytic removal of materials from objects.
[C25F 1/04] in solution -- C25F 1/04 covers electrolytic cleaning, degreasing, pickling or descaling performed with the object immersed in an electrolyte solution. The classification pertains to processes that remove surface contaminants by passing an electric current through the solution, effecting dissolution or conversion of material. It falls under electrochemical material removal within the chemistry domain.
[C25F 1/06] Iron or steel -- The C25F 1/06 subgroup pertains to electrolytic cleaning, degreasing, pickling or descaling operations that are applied specifically to iron or steel workpieces, using an electrolytic process to remove contaminants, scale or oil from the metal surface.
[C25F 1/08] Refractory metals -- C25F 1/08 covers electrolytic cleaning, degreasing, pickling or descaling operations applied to refractory metals such as tungsten, molybdenum, niobium and tantalum. The subclass includes methods where these high-melting-point metals are placed in electrolyte baths and subjected to an electric current to dissolve oxides, contaminants or surface scale, enabling subsequent machining or finishing.
[C25F 1/10] Actinides -- C25F 1/10 covers the use of actinide elements-such as uranium, thorium, plutonium and other trans-uranic metals-in electrolytic cleaning, degreasing, pickling or descaling processes. The subclass includes methods where actinide-containing electrolytes, electrodes or additives facilitate the removal of contaminants from metal objects.
[C25F 1/12] in melts -- This CPC subgroup deals with electrolytic cleaning, degreasing, pickling or descaling that is carried out in a molten electrolyte, such as a molten salt or metal melt, to remove material from an object's surface. It falls under the hierarchy of chemistry → electrolytic or electrophoretic processes → processes for the electrolytic removal of materials from objects.
[C25F 1/14] Iron or steel -- C25F 1/14 covers electrolytic cleaning, degreasing, pickling or descaling processes applied to iron or steel. It falls under the CPC group for electrochemical removal of material from objects, specifically for iron or steel substrates. This classification is used for patents describing electrolytic treatments of steel and iron surfaces.
[C25F 1/16] Refractory metals -- C25F 1/16 relates to electrolytic cleaning, degreasing, pickling or descaling operations that use refractory metals such as tungsten, molybdenum, tantalum or niobium as electrodes or as the treated objects.C25F 1/16 relates to electrolytic cleaning, degreasing, pickling or descaling operations that use refractory metals such as tungsten, molybdenum, tantalum or niobium as electrodes or as the treated objects.
[C25F 1/18] Actinides -- C25F 1/18 covers electrolytic cleaning, degreasing, pickling or descaling operations that specifically involve actinide elements such as uranium, thorium, plutonium and related compounds. The subclass addresses processes for removing contaminants, oxides or scale from surfaces containing these radioactive metals, often in nuclear fuel handling or waste-treatment contexts.
[C25F 3/00] Electrolytic etching or polishing -- **Glossary:** - Electrolytic etching: dissolving by - electrolytic action or - a plasma which is generated at the surface of the workpiece by a voltage applied to the electrodes in the electrolyte, such that a rough surface is obtained - Electrolytic polishing: dissolving by - electrolytic action or - by a plasma which is generated at the surface of the workpiece by a voltage applied to the electrodes in the electrolyte, such that a smooth surface is obtained
[C25F 3/02] Etching -- C25F 3/02 covers electrolytic etching, a process that removes material from a workpiece by passing an electric current through an electrolyte to dissolve the surface. It is used for cleaning, patterning, or surface finishing of metals and other conductive objects, often as a step in manufacturing or micro-fabrication.
[C25F 3/04] of light metals -- This subclass concerns electrolytic methods for etching or polishing light metals such as aluminium, magnesium and their alloys. It covers the use of electrolytic cells, solutions and operating parameters that remove material from the metal surface to achieve fine texture, cleaning or decorative effects.
[C25F 3/06] of iron or steel -- This subclass covers electrolytic etching or polishing processes that are specifically applied to iron or steel, where the metal acts as the anode and material is removed by anodic dissolution in an electrolyte. The technique is used to achieve fine surface finishing, cleaning, or patterning of iron or steel workpieces.
[C25F 3/08] of refractory metals
[C25F 3/10] of actinides
[C25F 3/12] of semiconducting materials -- **Glossary:** - Semiconducting material: the material as such, not a workpiece which is a semiconductor (e.g. a wafer)
[C25F 3/14] locally -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Locally electrolytic etching where the portions to be etched are determined only by a mask or a template
[C25F 3/16] Polishing -- C25F 3/16 covers electrolytic polishing, a process in which an object serves as the anode in an aqueous electrolyte and a controlled current removes surface material to produce a smooth, bright finish. The method is used for metals, alloys and some semiconductor surfaces, reducing roughness without mechanical abrasion. It falls under processes for the electrolytic removal of materials from objects.
[C25F 3/18] of light metals -- C25F 3/18 covers electrolytic etching and polishing processes specifically applied to light metals such as aluminium, magnesium, titanium and their alloys. The methods use an electrically powered electrolyte to remove material from the metal surface for cleaning, surface preparation or finishing.
[C25F 3/20] of aluminium -- C25F 3/20 covers electrolytic etching or polishing techniques directed at aluminium. It includes processes that remove material from aluminium surfaces by anodic dissolution in an electrolyte, typically for finishing, cleaning or micro-structuring.
[C25F 3/22] of heavy metals
[C25F 3/24] of iron or steel -- C25F 3/24 covers electrolytic etching or polishing methods applied to iron or steel, where electric current removes material from the metal surface. It falls under processes for the electrolytic removal of materials from objects within the broader chemistry and electrolytic/electrophoretic processes categories.
[C25F 3/26] of refractory metals -- C25F 3/26 covers electrolytic etching or polishing techniques applied to refractory metals such as tungsten, molybdenum or niobium. The subclass deals with the removal of material from these high-temperature-resistant metals by controlled anodic dissolution in an electrolytic bath.
[C25F 3/28] of actinides
[C25F 3/30] of semiconducting materials -- **Glossary:** - Semiconducting material: the material as such, not a workpiece which is a semiconductor (e.g. a wafer)
[C25F 5/00] Electrolytic stripping of metallic layers or coatings -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Removing an entire layer or coating, even when this layer or coating is already partially damaged (e.g. removing NiCrAlY from a turbine blade to be reworked)
[C25F 7/00] Constructional parts, or assemblies thereof, of cells for electrolytic removal of material from objects -- C25F 7/00 relates to the structural components and assemblies of electrolytic cells used for removing material from objects, such as parts of plating or stripping equipment. It covers housings, electrodes, separators and other mechanical elements that form the cell architecture for electro-etching or electro-cleaning processes.
[C25F 7/02] Regeneration of process liquids -- C25F 7/02 covers methods and apparatus for renewing or treating the electrolytic solutions used in processes that remove material from objects, including the design of cell components or assemblies that facilitate such regeneration.
